About the Author                                        444

CHAPTER 1                                                                                                                                                                                                      A New Dawn

I woke up to the morning sun peeking through my window. The gentle sounds of the little stream and chirping birds sound outside. The wind blew in through the open window and brushed my short, leafy hair, bringing a smile to my face. Another day... I wonder what it might bring, I thought  as I sat up in bed. As I stretched in my bed I chuckled “Alright Deta.... time to get up!”

Throwing on my favorite light gray shirt and green pants, both made from scrat fur, I reached for my satchel, pulling it over my shoulder and checking to make sure the leaf-shaped flap was clamped shut. Our clan crest, the Celeste Randeth, glittered as the sun caught it.

After getting ready, I left my room and headed to the kitchen to prepare breakfast. As I walked in that direction, I heard a soft voice calling. "Deta, how is your morning?" It was Vomete, my mother. Her long hair was made of vines and leaves, as all Randeths' hair was. She was made of stones and moss, with eyes of gold. Her demeanor was sweet, frail, and loving. Her voice was always soft and gentle, with a slight quiver to it, yet had a calming quality to it, like a soothing lullaby.

         "Good to see you and welcome home! I'm doing fantastic of course. Did you have another long night?" I replied.

Vomete smiled gently, as she had for many years before. "You know how it goes... One does not care for all of nature simply." With that, she walked to her chair in the meeting room, not far from the kitchen, her green robe fluttering. She sat down and scrubbed the dirt from her clothes.

Her reply brought a smile to my face, "That's true, but you do a wonderful job at it!" As I waved my hand over the windowsill garden, six carrots grew instantly, and I picked and prepared them. "A little dirty there, huh?" I continued preparing the food as we spoke.

Vomete chuckled and said, "Even though we are one with nature, we don't need to be dirty," giving a small cough as her health was in decline as of late.

"Very true," I replied with a smile, hoping to bring her some joy. "Alright, breakfast is ready—"

Out of the blue, we heard a knock on our door. We both stared at each other in confusion, as it was rare for anyone to venture this far into the forest.

She shook her head, then suggested, "Why don't you answer it, Deta?"

As I walked to the door, I changed my appearance to look like a human. This is to conceal my identity as the appearance of my kind tends to frighten most travelers. My hand quivered as I reached for the door knob, wondering who in the world of Entine it could be. The apprehension quickly vanished when I saw a little human girl, about five years old, standing there. Her clothes hung in tatters, and her face was streaked with dirt and smeared with fresh cuts, each one a testament to her struggle. Her long brown hair was a tangled mess, matted with twigs and leaves that clung stubbornly to it.

Concerned, I exclaimed, "Oh dear! Are you alright? Please come in!" The girl hesitated before slowly entering. "Let's get you cleaned up. Vomete, can you bathe her?" Vomete rose from her seat, causing the little girl to jump, thinking Vomete was a pile of rocks.

Curious, I asked the girl, "How did you get so deep into the forest? It's not safe out there." I worried about what could have happened to her parents. Vomete and I often helped people leave the forest safely, as it was filled with dangerous creatures. Not only were there wolves in the woods, but mythical creatures such as the eagle-bear, Sklerps (a creature made of acidic ooze with metallic horns), Basilisk-folk and other monsters. Without guidance, people could be seriously hurt.

The little girl answered me saying, "I was playing and got lost. I tried to find my way back but I fell down a hill. I haven't seen my momma in two days..."

Two days?! I thought to myself, stunned. Eyes widened and mouth slightly agape. Trying to console her, I said, "Don't worry, little one. Go see Vomete and take a nice bath. I'll make you some food, and then we'll take you back home, alright?" I gave her a comforting smile, and the girl smiled back softly. "Okay, thank you, mister!" she said before running off to the back, where the sound of rushing water could be heard.

After some time, I managed to prepare something despite my limited knowledge gathered from human books. When the girl emerged, she was all clean and happy. Her long brown hair shone, and her cuts had been bandaged. Vomete followed her out.

With bright-eyed eagerness, she asked, "What are we eating?" I replied with a smile, "Well, I made some sugar rice!" Though I found it off putting, the child surprised me by eating it all. Humans are strange, I thought. Vomete, on the other hand, smiled and praised me.

"You have made it well, my son." Happy to hear her approval, I chuckled and reluctantly finished the weird human food. As we ate, Vomete asked the little girl for her name, “Maggie!” She said with a smile and her cheeks full of food. We both chuckled at this.

I then asked “So Maggie, can I ask you a question?” she nodded as she ate more food, then questioned her what sound a duck makes.

She thought for a moment and responded with “Quack?” with a tilt to her head. Vomete coughed and chuckled knowing this joke. Looking at Vomete confused, she looked at me as I smiled and mimicked a duck call. Maggie erupted in laughter as Vomete and I giggled and snickered.

After our meal, I slipped on my old brown shoes and said, "Alright, let's get you home." The little girl's energy brought a smile to my face as we made our way out the door.

We stepped outside, I gave Vomete a small hug Before I surveyed the front yard with a sweeping gaze. The small stream meandered lazily through the garden, its clear waters revealing darting fish that shimmered in the sunlight. Blossoms of every hue spilled across the flower garden, their vibrant colors mingling in a riotous dance of petals. The house, nestled snugly beneath the looming cliff, remained a secret from anyone peering down from above, its presence concealed by the rugged overhang.

Breathing in the fresh air, I exclaimed, "Ah, this is a beautiful day." Turning to Maggie , I asked, "Are you ready?" She seemed nervous, but I didn't blame her.

"Here, take my hand," I offered, extending my hand to her. "We can take the shortcut so we don't have to go through the scary part."

Her smile was warm as she reached out, her fingers gently closing around mine. Together, we strolled along a winding path, the crunch of gravel beneath our feet. Ahead, a stone archway emerged, its ancient stones draped in a lush cascade of green vines. I raised my hand, feeling the tingle of magic as my palm turned green, and exclaimed, "Exitum!", causing the vines to recede and the archway to reveal a portal beneath.

Maggie, taken aback by the sudden opening of the portal, let go of my hand, taking a few steps back. "Hey, it's okay. This will help us go to your mother," I reassured her.

She looked with uncertainty at the portal, then back to me. "Okay..." Taking my hand once again, we walked through the portal.

Walking through the portal felt like a warm hug, comforting and peaceful. Emerging on the other side, we found ourselves in a field of grass and flowers. Maggie was mesmerized by the colorful blooms, and I couldn't help but chuckle. "Pretty, right?"

She nodded excitedly. "It's very pretty!"

Pointing to a gray smudge in the distance, I explained to her, "And do you see that little gray bit over there? That's the human kingdom."  This was the most common place I would see humans go to after leaving the forest.

Her eyes sparkled with excitement. "Home!" she exclaimed, her grip on my hand loosening as she dashed ahead. Her infectious enthusiasm made my heart skip a beat, and I couldn’t help but sprint after her, laughter bubbling up and filling me with pure, joyful energy.

As we walked, Maggie’s boundless energy began to wane. Eventually, she sank down amidst the flowers, her cheeks flushed from running. Looking at her with a gentle smile, I asked, "Are you tired?" She nodded, her voice soft but earnest. "Yeah... I ran so fast, and now my legs need a rest." I smiled back and replied, "Alright, let’s take a small break." We both settled into the soft bed of flowers, savoring the gentle warmth of the breeze and the soothing embrace of the sun.

We sat in the field for about an hour when the little girl got up and turned her back to me. "What are you doing?" I asked, sitting up and looking at her. Turning around, she revealed a flower crown she had made.

 "Here! I made this for you!" She promptly placed it on my head, and we both giggled.

"Alright, let's get going, hm? Your mother is waiting," I said, smiling. "Okay, mister!" She replied, grinning from ear to ear.

As we approached the kingdom gates, Maggie had gotten tired so I picked her up to give her a rest and she fell asleep in my arms. I continued to walk late into the afternoon. "Hey, little one... time to wake up," I said softly. She groggily opened her eyes and exclaimed.

"Home!" Eager to get down, she squirmed in my arms. "Hold on, wait a sec. I'll put you down," I chuckled.

Setting Maggie down, we approached the gates, where two stern guards in red tinted armor adorned with the kingdom’s lion crest stood. Their faces were hard and unyielding, etched with lines of stern discipline and disdain. One guard's eyes were narrow slits, glaring at us with a mix of suspicion and contempt, while his thick brows furrowed into a permanent scowl. The other’s face was set in a grim, unrelenting expression, his jaw clenched tightly as if daring anyone to challenge his authority. Their stern, unblinking states seemed to pierce through any pretense of civility.

"Hold your ground! Stay where you are!" one of them barked, his voice a harsh command that brooked no argument.

I tried to reason with them, "Uh, gentlemen... I don't mean any harm. I just came to help—" But before I could finish, the guards began closing in, their faces unchanging and menacing. One moved deliberately from the left, his glare fixed on me with unwavering hostility, while the other advanced from the right, his expression a cold mask of authority. "What? Wait! Hey, this isn't right!" I protested, but one guard abruptly jabbed the tip of his spear to my throat, his eyes a chilling mix of anger and indifference. "Quiet! Or you'll die where you stand, criminal!" he growled.

Swallowing my fear, I complied, my heart racing as I followed them, Maggie clinging to my side, her eyes wide with worry.

As we walked through the bustling town, I could feel the weight of curious gazes pressing on us. Whispers fluttered like restless birds around us, but their voices were lost in the din of the crowded streets. My eyes were drawn to the curious steel contraptions clattering by, each one pulled by horses and rattling with a noise that clashed with the smooth hum of magic and the lush greenery I was used to.

Our journey led us to an imposing castle, its grandeur striking against the cityscape. A maid came out alongside a knight and upon seeing Maggie, they snatched her up. While the maid embraced her, the other knight gave me a hard look of disdain. Walking in, tall pillars rose like sentinels, and archways loomed high above, framing the grandeur of the structure. Inside, the air was cool and solemn. Statues lined the hallways, their stone eyes gazing down with a timeless, unspoken authority. At the end of the grand hall, a raised platform held the council chamber. Nine figures sat in high-backed chairs, their robes cascading around them like waves of shadow. Among them, one cloaked figure stood in proximity to the regal couple seated on elaborate thrones. The King and Queen, were unmistakably the focal point of the room’s austere elegance.

The king's gaze cut through the room, his eyes cold and narrowed. His lips tightened into a thin line as he spoke, "What is the meaning of this?"

A man in a red robe stood up, he was on a pedestal just as high as the king’s throne. His face was flushed with anger "Do you not know we are in a meeting? This better be good or you will be stripped of your privileges!"

I flinched at the sudden outburst, my heart pounding as the harsh words were directed at me and the knights. "My king!" One of the knights stammered as he tried to keep his composure. "I greatly apologize for the intrusion, but we have captured this strange man outside the walls, and he had the princess herself!"

A collective gasp rippled through the room. The king’s eyes widened, momentarily breaking from their sternness. I then tried to plead my case to say I had no idea that the girl was the princess and was just trying to do the right thing.

"SILENCE!" The King roared, and the room fell silent for a few moments before a human in a white cloak next to the king spoke up.

From her voice, I could tell it was a woman. "Sire... if I may."

The king nodded. "Of course, mage..."

The woman nodded and stood up revealing a staff as tall as her with a bright blue stone at its top "This, my king, is one of the mythical Randeths," she declared.

The men were incredulous, insisting that Randeths were nothing more than myths to delight children. The king cleared his throat, silencing them. "What brings you to this conclusion, Zula, for the man before us seems human to me?"

She smiled. "As you know, the Randeth are typically made of stones and moss, they are also made of wood, and other foliage, and typically use plant magic."

The man in the red cloak interrupted, "Yes, we know this, so how is this man a Randeth? He clearly is human!" The man continued to yell, “Furthermore, what does this have anything to do with the princess!”

The Mage, Zula, looked at him disdainfully. "Allow me to finish speaking, Modius" She then turned to the room as a whole. "Randeths will often protect forests and aid travelers to their homes when they become lost in their territory. They are peaceful and often take the form of humans or wildlife to seem less threatening. Observe."

She extended her staff to me, the light blue stone at the end of it began to glow and I could feel my spell being countered and reverted to my original form for a moment. The room stared in awe. "The second he entered, I felt his presence, and Randeths would have no reason to kidnap a child."

The Queen looked unamused. "Guard. You have said he has stolen my daughter. Yet we do not see her. "

The men began to murmur, and I saw the guard's nervous expression. "Apologies, my queen!" The maid from earlier then entered, holding Maggie’s hand.

"Hi Momma!" she chirped with delight.

The Queen’s eyes softened, but the relief that flickered across her face seemed almost practiced, too polished. "Maggie... Did this man kidnap you?" Her voice was gentle, but there was a curious lack of urgency, as if the question was more a formality than a genuine concern. She clasped her hands loosely in her lap, a touch too casual for a mother who had feared the worst. Maggie started to explain, but the Queen’s warm smile lacked depth, her eyes flicking to me before resting on her daughter with a serene, almost detached expression.

When she finished, Modius spoke again. "He could have placed a spell over her! This could be the making of magic, to appear as though he was not guilty!"

Zula silenced him with a glowing blue strap across his mouth. I looked at her staff, and the crystal on top was glowing. "If there was magic on her, council member Modius, it would have disappeared. I have made sure that all magic is disabled upon entering here. After all that was your request."

Modius’ voice cut through the tension, his brow furrowed in confusion. “Why didn’t you just dispel the illusion?” he asked, his tone sharp with suspicion.

She looked at him, her lips curling into a faint smile that hinted at a deeper understanding. “If I had,” she said, her voice steady, “you would have seen the truth, but your eyes would have refused to believe it. Whats real would have seemed more impossible than the illusion.”

The Queen’s expression remained composed as she asked, "So... she is telling the truth?" Her voice was calm, almost measured.

The King inquired, "And this is a Randeth?"

Zula nodded. "Yes. Your daughter is telling the truth, and this..." she pointed her staff at me, "is a Randeth from myths of old!"

The men burst into conversation. As they did so I gave their confusion some thought. I guess it makes sense we seemed like a myth to them—Randeths lived so much longer than humans and don't normally interact aside from helping out of the woods. Vomete is over a myriad years old, which was old even for our standards…

"It is settled then…" the King stated, as he turned to look at me.  "Sir, we apologize, for we know from our myths that Randeths are peaceful and we know that you mean no harm."

I chuckled, the sound coming out with a playful hiccup, "Well, I'm just glad everything worked out."

This made the King smile, all the sternness and hostility gone. "You have done me a great service, I would like to have you stay as a guest for dinner."

"Really? Umm…" I scratched the back of my head. Vomete shouldn't be too mad if I stay for dinner, right? Not like anything will happen. "Well.. sounds good to me. I would be honored to join you and your family for dinner"

The King let out a rich, full-bodied laugh. "Good! Now.." He snapped his fingers and three maids came up to him and whispered something. He seemed to think about it then nodded. "See that he is properly cared for until dinner.." They bowed and walked away then the King turned to me and smiled. "Enjoy your stay. I will be seeing you later this evening."

Before I could respond, the maids arrived, each bringing their own distinct presence. The tallest among them approached first. “Come, sir,” she said, her voice calm and reassuring as she brushed back a strand of her long brown hair.

The second tallest offered a gentle nod, her short hair bobbing with her. “Let us show you to your room,” she added, her tone smooth and inviting.

The smallest and youngest looking maid, chimed in eagerly,  “Yes, please come.” The lighting hinted at a tinge of red in her hair as she spoke, her voice carried a surprising depth of sincerity.

They spoke quickly and with voices similar to one another. Though they seemed pleasant, their smiles seemed a little too... sharp. As if it were unnatural for them to smile at this moment. I let out a nervous chuckle.  

As we walked through the halls of the castle, our steps echoed around us. As my anxiety grew I tried to think of conversation. “So, uh… could I ask you three a question?”

Without batting an eye the two shortest turned to me while now walking backwards and asked in unison what my question was. I gave an awkward smile and asked “So, back there with all those people… what was that all about?”

The youngest spoke first, a smile plastered across her face, “It is to represent the Council of Seven Gods that speak to the Ruler of the Heavens!”

The next one picked up without a moment of silence “The different members of the council each represent something different with the color of their cloaks symbolizing them.”

I tilted my head. “Cloak colors? What do you mean?”

The oldest then responded, “You probably didn't notice when they were yelling at you, but here are the colors and what they represent: Life, Time, Wisdom, Energy, Spirit, Conflict and Guidance. Their colors are gold, brown, blue, green, silver, red and white respectively”

The youngest nodded. “Yes, and the council members represent a corporal form of those! Nature, Architecture, History, Nutrition, Connections, War and Religion”

The second oldest then chimed in, “For instance, the council member over History would need to know everything about the past of the kingdom and share his knowledge with the King to prevent previous mistakes. The one representing Conflict makes sure all threats are eradicated. He was the one who kept yelling at you in court.”

At that point we had made it to a large green door, to which the oldest opened, revealing a lofty room. My desire to ask more questions soon dissipated as I looked into the room.  The space was grand, with towering walls that made the room feel both imposing and empty. The bed, with its ornate design, looked almost too perfect to be real.

"Wow! This is amazing!" I looked around the room in awe, not sure how to process it.

"We hope you enjoy your stay," the eldest maid said, adjusting her starched apron with a quick, practiced flick.

"We will be awaiting your requests," the second maid added, her voice carrying a faint hint of impatience as she fidgeted with the edge of her lacy cap.

"And will be waiting outside your room. Farewell," the third maid finished, her gaze lingering for a moment longer as she smoothed down her uniform.

As the three of them departed, I let out a long sigh of relief, the door clicked shut behind them. The faint smell of lavender and lemon zest lingered in the air, a testament to their meticulous attention to detail.

"Oh thank goodness they are gone." Rock formed out of my arm and wood encased the other. "I didn't know how much longer I could hide these..." My hair then changed slowly back into vines and leaves. "Ah, much better..." I then thought back to the courtroom. "I'm impressed she knew what I was that fast.” Even though she revealed my form I still felt the desire to hide my form until we left. Though I guess since I was caught, there isn't much use in hiding it now.

I saw at the other end of the room a door and went to investigate to find it led to a bathroom made of quartz and gold. "What in the world? This… is too much..." I left the bathroom alone and closed the door. "Well let's see... dinner isn't for many more hours so... I guess I could head into town?"

I peeked out the front door of my room and saw the maids standing there with no emotion at all. As I tried to sneak past they all turned to me at the same time which caused me to jump "Ah!"

"Hello!" "Are you well?" "Where might you be off to?" They all had the same voice which was starting to become creepy. "Um, I was just going to head to town to look around-"

"Let us accompany you." "Yes let's" "Yes." I already knew that there was no saying no. "Well.. alright... you want to show me around?" They all nod simultaneously and begin to lead the way.

As we walked in town people began to whisper to which I could only assume they were taking notice of my arms and vines as I hadn’t bothered to recast my concealment spell.

The two older maids walked at my sides, their steps slightly out of sync. The first maid walked very composed, while scanning the surroundings with a sharp gaze.

The second kept glancing around anxiously, making sure we stayed together. Her eyes darted from me to the other two maids and back.

The last one from what I could tell was more void than the others, her expression almost seemed doll-like with her unwavering smile,  as she kept looking straight ahead.

After walking aimlessly for what seemed like hours, I asked hesitantly "So... where are you three taking me?"

The first maid asked with a precise tone, "Where would you like to go?"

The second maid nodded eagerly and added, "Yes, tell us."

The third smiled, “We will take you there.”

I thought the situation was incredibly awkward, but I glanced around and led the way into a building. The door creaked as it opened, revealing a dimly lit room filled with a thick haze of smoke and the raucous chatter of its patrons. The walls were lined with dark wood paneling, scarred from years of use, and the air was heavy with the scent of beer and unwashed bodies. Rough-hewn tables and mismatched chairs were scattered haphazardly across the floor, each one occupied by burly men engaged in animated conversations or laughter. The atmosphere was rowdy and rough, with a palpable tension that made me uneasy.

I spotted an open table near the back, away from the main cluster of activity, and we made our way over. The table was grimy, the surface stained with who knows what, but it was a small refuge from the chaotic energy of the room. I turned to the maids, trying to mask my own discomfort with a reassuring smile.

"Here, sit down," I said, gesturing to the chairs. The maids exchanged uneasy glances, their apprehension evident, but they took their seats. I could see the tension in their posture, their fingers fidgeting with their skirts as they tried to acclimate to the unwelcoming environment.

A few moments later, a burly man approached us with four large mugs of a yellow-orange liquid in his rough hands. His face was rugged, with a weathered complexion and a scruffy beard. His eyes scanned us briefly before he plopped the mugs down on the table.

"Uh... sir, we didn’t—" I began, attempting to clarify our order, but his glare cut me off. His expression was a stern mask of impatience, and I realized he was in no mood for small talk.

"Drink up," he muttered curtly before turning on his heel and lumbering back to the bar. The clinking of glass and the murmur of voices quickly filled the silence he left behind.

I look at the drinks and then at the maids, "Umm.. are these for us?" They seemed confused and nodded, "Oh, well then. Let's drink up!"

After our drinks were done I noticed the maid's faces were beet red and they seemed wobbly. I could not understand why, as I felt fine. I noticed a man walk our way. Right before he passed, I waved him over with my hand. "Excuse me, is something wrong with them?"

He looked at the maids with confusion in his brow. "The King's maids? They are drunk,.. does the King have business with you?"

"Oh, well I'm supposed to be meeting with him this evening." I chose not to mention that I was dining with the King and his family, as the people in this bar looked intimidating and I feared it might put me in danger. "What is being drunk?"

He rolled his eyes. "Well, just don't let those maids get in trouble. Being drunk normally allows others to do… unholy things." He walked off.

"What? Unholy?" I turn to the maids "Are you three alright?"

The three maids exchanged quick glances, the two older ones immediately putting on forced smiles. "Oh yes, we are fine! Perfectly fine," they said in unison, their voices unnaturally cheerful.

However, the ginger-haired maid broke the facade, her eyes dropping to the ground as she hesitated. Her voice was softer, more vulnerable, as she admitted, "I feel hot... and dizzy."

A wave of heat rolled through the room, thickening the air. Sweat beaded on foreheads, and people moved as if wading through molasses. I could feel the unnatural warmth seeping into my scalp, my leaves drooping and curling inward, losing their usual vibrant luster. Was someone using magic?

The other two maids were shocked and exchanged worried looks. "Rose?" they asked in concern.

“Rose?” I asked confused as I looked around expecting to see someone else at the table, but their gaze rested on the youngest maid. “Your name is Rose?”

The redheaded maid blinked her eyes and rubbed them at the mention of that name and tried to reassure, "Oh, I'm fine! Perfectly fine!" The temperature began to return to normal, as she smiled.

The other two maids then did the same thing before whispering to each other, "It seems the spell has been interrupted…We need to save Rose..."

Did they say ‘spell’? Were they enchanted somehow? I thought, my brow furrowed in confusion. Are they trying to keep her magic secret…? The maids had spoken so softly that I almost didn’t hear it. I then interrupted, “Are you ladies sure you’re okay?”

They each nodded, and Rose changed the subject, not realizing what the other two were talking about, "Oh! It's time to meet the

King! Follow us, sir!"

As we walked towards the castle, the two taller maids slowed down and walked beside me, their faces still red,trying to keep their balance. Even though they kept telling me they were okay, the way they stumbled over their own feet told me otherwise. I opened my mouth to offer my assistance again, but before I could, the brunette maid pleaded with me, "Please sir... listen to us."

The eldest maid added, "We serve the King but are under the Queen's charge, and by her royal decree, no one is permitted to possess magic except those approved by the King." They exchanged worried glances before speaking in hushed tones. "We have no magic of our own," she admitted, her voice barely above a whisper. "But Rose… she’s been showing signs." She glanced nervously at the youngest, whose fiery locks seemed to shimmer with a faint, untrained energy.

"If the Queen ever finds out..." The second’s voice faltered, the unspoken words hanging heavy in the air. “Everyone knows the Queen's stance—uncontrolled magic was a threat to her power. To protect her throne, she wouldn’t hesitate to strip Rose of her emerging gift, publicly humiliate her, and then…” she gulped, “Execute her without mercy.”

The brunette maid implored me to take Rose away from there if the King gave me a chance. I tried to ask why such an extreme measure would be taken. They explained to me that the Queen loves to exercise her power. The King would stop her but he doesn't know she does this. They then asked me again to take Rose away.

I was hesitant. "Uh... are you sure? How can you trust a stranger? I mean, what if I'm a bad guy?"

"Please, sir..." they pleaded, their voices trembling with a mix of desperation and fear. The oldest maid's hands clutched the edge of her apron, knuckles white, while the younger one twisted a loose thread around her finger, eyes darting nervously “she isn't safe here."

Just then, two guards approached us, their polished armor catching the flickering torch light from the corridor. Their voices, barely more than whispers, said, “The Queen has requested your presence in the King's dining hall.”

The maids exchanged glances, their faces betraying a mix of curiosity and apprehension. The brunette maid, her expression clouded with something like quiet desperation, glanced back at me. Her eyes were filled with a silent plea, a hint of worry lingering in their depths before she and her companions turned and began to walk away, their footsteps echoing softly against the cold stone floor.

"Sir, if you follow us, we will show you the way," one of the knights said, their voice steady and authoritative, though not unkind. I gave a nod of acknowledgement and fell into step behind them.

The hallway we traversed was grand, its high ceiling adorned with intricate tapestries and the walls lined with ancient portraits of regal ancestors. As we approached the dining hall, the air grew warmer, filled with the scent of rich, roasted meats and fragrant herbs. The grand doors to the dining hall loomed before us, heavy and imposing, but they swung open effortlessly as the guards ushered us inside.

We entered a space that was nothing short of monumental—a room vast enough to host an entire army. Its grandeur was accentuated by the sheer simplicity of the furnishings: a single long table stretched down the center, surrounded by an array of high-backed chairs. At the far end of the table, the King, Queen, and the princess, Maggie, were seated in a commanding trio. Their presence was regal and imposing, a stark contrast to the otherwise unadorned room.

A few seats away, the mage, Zula, sat in quiet contemplation, her gaze fixed on some distant thought. The three maids from earlier stood in a discreet line near the Queen, their earlier composure replaced by a more formal and attentive demeanor. The youngest maid, the one who had glanced back at me with such concern, now stood with a careful poise, her eyes darting between the Queen and the other nobles.

The scene was set, the atmosphere charged with a palpable tension as we awaited whatever may occur.

The King welcomed us warmly, "Ah, there you are! Come, sit down!" He gestured towards a chair on the other side of the table from Zula, and I smiled and took a seat.

Approaching the table, I noticed a thin man with an impressive bushy black mustache holding a scroll. Humans are quite amusing, I thought to myself, they hold high positions yet insist on growing their hair in such strange ways.

After sitting down, I greeted the King and Queen with a smile and a respectful tone, "Thank you for inviting me to join you." However, the Queen's demeanor had changed. Now, she stared at me with palpable hostility, her eyes sharp and unyielding, brimming with a fierce aggression that was impossible to ignore. “Did I do something wrong?”

“Quite the contrary, you saved my daughter! Allowing you to dine with us is the least we could do. However, we do have something important to discuss." The King's smile was wide and sincere as he spoke. The man with the bushy mustache approached the King and handed him the scroll, which the King proceeded to open and place on the table.

As I gazed at the scroll I saw it was a map of the catacombs. The King interrupted my thoughts with a question, "Oh! I almost forgot, what is your name Randeth?" I realized I had not introduced myself and responded, "Oh, apologies. My name is Deta."

The room fell silent as everyone turned to look at me. "Did...I say something?" I asked, confused.

The King cleared his throat and shook his head, "No, no. Deta, hm? Your parents must have been Detations?"

Before I could ask what they were, the Queen interjected, "It doesn't matter. Just tell him what you want, dear."

With a nervous chuckle, the King agreed "I suppose so. Deta, we would like to ask for your help. There is something immense lurking beneath our city, something stirring deep in the dungeon. The ground shakes at times, and the air feels heavy with its presence. We’ve sent soldiers below to investigate, but none have returned since their descent five moons ago. The creature, whatever it is, remains unseen.”

The Queen interjected, “Dear. We have our guardian down there, the serpent is probably hunting whatever it is that is bothering you, the knights simply got in the way.”

The King smiled at his wife then turned to me. “Yes, but the season for when it wakes has long passed. Without it awake I fear things from beneath the land may be making their way to us. Randeth, would you please find it and drive it away?"

"Fight a monster?" I repeated in disbelief. The King explained, "Our Mage has informed us that your race has incredible magic abilities and we hoped that you could lend us your strength. Additionally, someone has stolen something precious from us and escaped down there. An amulet with fine carvings and a Soul Stone, It is incredibly-"

My eyes widened in shock not hearing the rest of what he said. "A soul stone..? How did..." I murmured under my breath. A Soul Stone is what keeps my kind alive, its name being quite literal. If someone were to take it they could harness a Randeth's powers… at the cost of the Randeth’s life to which the soul belonged.

Interrupting my thoughts, the King sighed, "Of course, we understand if you cannot. You have already done a tremendous service by returning our daughter."

The princess then pleaded with me, "Can you help us, mister? Please?" Her innocent request and the knowledge of the soul stone at risk made it impossible for me to refuse. "Alright...I'll help," I said, smiling at Maggie.

The King was overjoyed, "Thank you, young Deta! Find those you want to take with you, and when you return, you and your party will be greatly rewarded!"

He hesitated, his gaze shifting between the maids with a sense of growing unease. The request from the maids echoed in his mind, their voices soft but insistent, weaving a tapestry of obligation and concern. His eyes lingered on the ginger-haired maid, a tangle of apprehension and determination knotting in his chest.

A tight smile formed on his lips as he finally spoke, his voice a blend of formality and unspoken hope. "Of course, your majesty." He took a deep breath, the weight of his decision palpable. "Might I, for my first recruitment, ask for the ginger-haired maid?" He paused, the silence stretching painfully as he gauged their reactions, his heart pounding with the unspoken plea for understanding.

"And—" he added, his voice softening with earnest resolve, "it would greatly help me to have someone who knows the kingdom, to be able to find the rest of my party."

The room seemed to hold its breath, the tension thick with his silent hope and the potential for change.

Before the King could answer, the Queen interrupted, raising her voice. "You are choosing one of the princess's keepers to join your quest? How absurd!" Her words cut through the air, sharp and deliberate, my mind struggling to catch up with the intensity of her message.

The King promptly stepped in to calm his belligerent wife. "Darling, it's alright. She has two others, and he is freeing our kingdom of something we cannot do on our own." He chuckled in an attempt to ease the tension.

The Queen scoffed and turned away. "Do as you wish," she muttered under her breath.

Just as the King was about to speak again, a loud explosion echoed through the castle walls. "What was that?" I asked urgently, my voice slightly strained as I glanced around.

The King raised his hand and smiled,"No need to worry. We have our loyal knights on hand for these matters," he said, his tone carrying a practiced reassurance. I found myself relaxing, the knot of anxiety in my chest loosening. It was clear this was a routine he handled with ease.

 CHAPTER 2                                                                                                                          Wild Chase

Beans’ View

We heard an explosion in the town square. Bluma, the demon knight, and I, Beans, were ready for action. Bluma wore a striking ensemble of bright red and gold armor that seemed to catch the light just right, drawing your eye to the fine details. The smooth red breastplate fit her form with an effortless grace, with delicate gold etchings that traced soft patterns down her arms and legs. Her pauldrons curved outward slightly, lined with gold that gleamed. There was something about the way it all came together—refined, powerful, and undeniably captivating, like the armor was made to reflect the confidence she carried.

Her four golden eyes shone brightly against the deep black of her sclera. Cascading down her back was her fiery red hair which danced with every movement. Standing at an impressive seven feet tall, she was adorned with two smoky brown horns elegantly curving from her head, adding a majestic quality to her appearance.

What sets her apart most dramatically is her face, which lacks both mouth and nose, resembling a festival mask in its purity and simplicity. Her visage is dominated solely by those mesmerizing eyes, creating a captivating aura. While this might be disconcerting to some, to me, it only enhances her enigmatic allure.

And I, a Dwarf and her squire, stood by her side. I have round blue eyes and scruffy blonde hair, with freckles scattered across my clean shaven face and down my arms. I'm in my mid forties which may seem old to humans but for a Dwarf I am a young adult. We have been working together for seven years, and we knew each other inside and out in more ways than one.

However, a knight can never fall in love with their squire, that's something we keep secret, if anyone were to find out, we wouldn't be able to see each other again.

I had just finished preparing Bluma's sword. "Here you go, ma'am! Your sword is as sharp as an Entian's glare!" I said, handing the sword to Bluma. It was made of a black metal that was almost indestructible called a sklerp horn. Legends say that a Randeth blessed a deer’s womb causing the sklerp to be born.  Her sword had a golden handle and hilt with the kingdom's crest molded into its stump. It was an oddly light-weight sword but would never fail its handler when used correctly. Bluma had spent many years mastering it. She nodded and patted my head. We have worked together for so long that we had developed an unspoken language, and knew each other's every move.

Bluma put the sword into its sheath on her side, and the two ran out of the barracks and to the town square. There was chaos and confusion as the local inn and bar had been set ablaze. "Gather," Bluma said softly, and I saluted her. "Yes, ma'am!" I replied, knowing exactly what she meant.

Bluma darted into the inn, her eyes scanning the dim interior for anyone who might still be trapped. Meanwhile, I wove through the frantic crowd outside, alongside the other knights and squires.  We gently guided panicked townsfolk away from the inn, our calm voices and firm hands working to stem the rising tide of chaos. As Bluma stepped inside, her eyes landed on the source of the chaos, one of them twitching involuntarily. An elvish bard—who had been explicitly told not to get drunk—had, predictably, gotten drunk. She could only assume he was once again the main culprit behind this outburst of propaganda. When intoxicated, his inability to control his powers was a frustratingly familiar issue. And since he was a frequent visitor to our kingdom, enforcing magic control laws on him proved nearly impossible.She proceeded to walk over to the passed-out drunk and grab him by the scruff of his hair with one hand and, with the other, grasped onto his harp.

Bluma dragged the limp body out of the building, while some town mages came to extinguish the fire. Seeing her walk out of the flames unharmed was magical so I ran up to Bluma and upon seeing the sleeping drunk bard groaned and sighed, "Again? How many times till he learns to stop drinking? He should know he can't handle the alcohol." Bluma rolled her eyes and groaned with her lower two eyes looking at me and the other two gliding between the Elf and the jailblock.

"Discipline," I said in agreement. I sighed then stated, "I suppose you're right. Maybe a few nights locked up will do him some good. I'll put this harp back into the barracks to prevent any more mishaps like last time." I chuckled while Bluma shook her head. Kneeling down she handed the harp to me then as she was standing up she let her hand follow up my arm and fall off my shoulder with a small flick of her finger causing a rush to my face but I quickly composed myself.

After dropping off the harp, I made my way to the castle. The towering stone walls loomed overhead, their surfaces worn smooth by time but still imposing. Ornate banners, bearing the kingdom’s crest, hung between the archways, their deep reds and golds a stark contrast to the cool gray stone. The scent of polished wood and burning torches filled the air as I stepped inside, my boots clicking softly against the gleaming floors.

The halls stretched endlessly before me, lined with tall windows that let in thin beams of morning light. Servants bustled about, their hurried footsteps echoing faintly, but none paid me any mind. I passed intricately carved wooden doors, each leading to unknown chambers filled with royal secrets I had no business knowing. My stomach twisted with unease, but I kept moving, my hands gripping the straps of my bag tightly.

As I turned a corner, I spotted a man made of plants and one of the princess’s maids speaking with a guard. My heart lurched as the guard suddenly pointed in my direction. My breath hitched. The only time things like this happened was when foreign royalty visited.

Oh no.

My pulse pounded in my ears. Am I supposed to bow? Speak formally? What if he spoke another language? What if I said the wrong thing and insulted him? What if I was supposed to guide him somewhere? I didn't know how to do that! What if—what if he needed something important, something royal, and I messed it up?

My hands were clammy, my legs stiff and useless as the two figures walked toward me. My thoughts spiraled further. What if this was a test? What if the princess was watching, and she expected me to handle this properly? Was I supposed to introduce myself? Could I just run? No, no, that would definitely be worse.

Deta’s View

Seeing the small squire, I smiled, hoping he could help us. "Hey there! Could you please help us with something?" I smiled again. "I was told you were a squire and could lead me to a strong knight!"

 The squire stood a few feet away from us, clutching his bag as if someone might try to steal it. His mouth opened and closed as if he were trying to find the right words. When he opened again, this time taking in a deep breath, a high-pitched shrill echoed in the halls, the sound slowly growing louder until it sounded like a choked burp, which echoed in the vastness of the room. I thought the man was screaming, until his face started turning a deep shade of red.

“Are you-” I started to speak but the man interrupted.

“I am a knight!” He blurted, his face crimson. “Follow me!” He then dashed off before we could respond.

I looked at Rose a bit confused, and she too was lost so we decided to chase after the mysterious knight. “Hey! Wait up!” I called out in vain as he continued to run.

Rose and I chased after the knight hoping to ask him for assistance in dealing with the beast below the kingdom. We followed him around a corner as he disappeared..

“Where could he have gone?” Rose asked anxiously, her brow furrowing as she scanned the area. Her hands fidgeted with the hem of her dress.

“I don't know but we will find him! This is probably a test to see if we are worth his time!”

Rose looked unsure, her gaze darting around as she shifted from one foot to the other. She didn’t say anything, but her uneasy stance said it all, “Are you sure? Would a knight do that?”

I shrugged not knowing. “Well, we will find out!” I smiled which made Rose roll her eyes but smile so and we went searching.

Rose and I had decided to split up to cover more ground. I tried to navigate through the bustling crowd, but with everyone pushing and shoving, it was nearly impossible to search. This place was so new, I didn’t even know where to begin looking. I felt a knot of anxiety tightening in my chest. The mix of unfamiliar scents and the constant chatter of vendors made it hard to concentrate. My hands were slightly clammy, and I found myself gripping my bag more tightly than usual. The bustling environment was overwhelming, making it difficult to focus on anything specific. I glanced back to see where Rose had gone, but the mass of people made it impossible to pick her out.

Eventually, I caught sight of Rose through the sea of faces, her distinctive red hair barely visible above the crowd. I maneuvered through the busy streets, my eyes locked on that small glimpse of her, determined to close the distance. After putting my hand on her shoulder she turned towards me and asked, “Any luck?” I sighed and shook my head. Just as we were about to give up and start looking for other help we heard a huge crash on the other end of the district.

As Rose and I hurried towards the commotion, I saw a couple of knights gathered around a cart crash and two men being dragged away by a knight. As we got closer I began to recognize the knight from before in the group, I approached him and asked, "Hey, what's going on? Is everything okay?"

"Oh yes! Everything is just fi—" but he stopped short when I realized he was the knight we were looking for. “Wait, you were the knight we were looking for! We finished your test!”

He raised an eyebrow unsure what we meant “What test?”

I smiled “You know, how you had us chase you around town and-” But Rose cut me off.

“Sorry to interrupt but, are you even a knight?” she asked, a little timid but direct. “I do find it odd a knight would run away from someone seeking aid. Especially that quick.”

Embarrassed, Beans chuckled nervously and said, "Oh, no, sorry, I'm not actually a knight. I'm just a squire to the great demon knight!"

It was then we saw a figure standing behind him. As my eyes slowly traveled upward, I noticed the deep red and gold-trimmed armor she wore, the colors too vivid, too alive, for something so terrifying. My breath caught as I reached their face—or what should have been a face. Instead, there were no features, just a smooth, mask-like surface with four intense, cold eyes, each with a golden sheen set against an eerie black background. Those eyes seemed to pierce right through me, as if they could see every hidden fear. A shiver ran down my spine, and an overwhelming sense of dread washed over me. My gaze drifted to the dark hilt of the sword under their hand, the smoky brown horns on their head adding to the menacing aura that surrounded them, making every second feel heavier, like the air itself was thick with danger.

Realizing my mistake, I said, "Oh, I see. Sorry about that. We just wanted to ask if you could help us. We're in search of a knight, and we were told you knew someone."

Bluma looked down at Beans and chuckled quietly. Beans could tell that Bluma was bound to tease him about that later. He then clarified that he wasn't a knight but a squire then gestured with his whole body to Bluma and said, "She's the strongest knight in the kingdom!" He smiled wide, while Bluma just stared at us, her expression inscrutable.

"Oh!" I then turned to the demon knight and asked, "May we ask you to join our group then? The Ki—" but before I could finish, she cut me off, "No." She turned away and started walking, which caught me off guard. "H-hey! Where are you going?"

As I was going to go after her, Beans grabbed my arm firmly and brought me to a sudden stop. "Leave her be, please. She's loyal only to the Royal family and will only listen to their words.” Continuing he asked “What do you need a knight for? Don't you have many of your own?"

I raised an eyebrow, and then Rose chimed in with a small chuckle, "He's not a prince, but is a guest to the kingdom. A Randeth no less."

Beans was taken aback and released Deta's arm. "A Randeth? Aren't they just legends, like Entians?" he exclaimed.

Rose smiled and reassured him, "No, they're quite real and friendly."

I chuckled, feeling a bit flattered. "I try my best to be friendly, but I'm not a prince," I said. "The King has tasked me with putting together a team, so I-"

But Beans interrupted me, putting his fist into his hand. "The King needs you to form a team? Alright, I'll tell Blu - er, I mean the Demon Knight. I'm sure she'd love to join now that you have the King's charge!"

I felt a rush of excitement. "Really? You mean it?"

Beans nodded enthusiastically. "Yep! Just give me a moment!" He exclaimed before running off to find the Demon Knight. As he disappeared, I turned to Rose.

"Isn't this great, Rose?" I exclaimed, excitement bubbling up inside me. But then I noticed her cheeks turning pink, her eyes darting away from mine. She fidgeted slightly, her fingers twisting together. "Rose? Are you okay?" I asked, my voice softening as I tried to make sense of her sudden discomfort.

Rose patted her face with her hands and shook her head. "Oh yes, I'm fine. I'm just not used to hearing my name," she explained.

I raised an eyebrow in surprise. "Really? Have you never been called by your name before? Not even by the other maids?"

She shook her head no, “We typically aren't together and don't sleep in the same dorms. So it is rare for me to hear it”

This was strange for me to hear, however, I didn't dwell on it and instead, I smiled kindly. "Well, get used to it because I plan on calling you by your first name often, Rose."

Wonder filled Rose's eyes, and her face lit up with a bright smile, eyes sparkling with pure delight which made me smile. "I guess I will, Deta," she said.

Just as I was about to speak again, someone shoved me to the side, causing me to lose my balance and fall over. "Excuse me!" The person exclaimed as they rushed past me.

Rose bent down and helped me up "Are you all right, sir!?"

I stood up and brushed myself off. "Ya, ya I'm okay." I then smiled. "You know you can call me Deta right?"

She blushed slightly but nodded. Just then, an anxious older gentleman ran up to us, visibly upset. "Please help me, that man stole my family's heirloom!" he pleaded.

My eyes widened and looked at the man running away to the older man, "Of course! We will get your heirloom back for you!" I then turned to my companion. "Let's go, Rose!" She nodded and we both ran off to catch the man.

The man ran quickly and looked behind him to see us chasing him then looked straight ahead again. Once he exited the kingdom's gates, he took a sharp left behind the pillar adjoining the gate to the kingdoms' outer wall. "We can't lose him!" I declared, trying to catch up to him.

As I rounded the corner, the bustling noise of the market faded into a sharp, startling sound. A massive creature suddenly loomed before me, its powerful legs propelling it upwards. I stumbled back, momentarily disoriented. "Whoa there!" I blurted out, trying to steady myself. The creature, I soon realized, was a robust horse, and atop it was a man dressed in dark, worn clothing.

Before I could gather my thoughts or say anything more, the man let out a fierce shout. The horse, spurred by the sound, reared up on its hind legs and then surged forward, galloping swiftly across the open field. Dust billowed in their wake, and I could only watch as they disappeared into the distance.

Rose appeared beside me just as the man and horse became a distant blur. Her face fell as she took in the scene. “We can’t catch him, Deta…” she said quietly, her shoulders slumping in defeat.

As we walked back into the city, I looked up and saw a strange building with horses inside. It looked like they were trapped yet free to roam. "Wait a minute," I said, "maybe we can still catch him."

Rose looked at me, doubting. "How?" she asked.

I smiled and approached the nearest horse.Rose looked confused as I walked towards the stable. "Hey there!" I greeted the horse with a smile.

The horse rolled its eyes and turned away. "Oh goodie, another peasant wishing to ride one of us. Go away. The great Rubert has no time for you." It said,

I chuckled, "Rubert, is it? Do you think I could borrow a small portion of your time?"

Rubert looked at me with a skeptical tilt of his head. He stamped his front hoof and snorted, the sound echoing slightly. “You can understand me, peasant?” he said, his voice condescending. His ears flicked back and forth, whether from annoyance or bafflement, I couldn’t quite tell..

I nodded and replied, "I can indeed, and I was wondering if I could ask for your help. A thief stole someone’s prized heirloom, and we need your help catching up to him."

Rubert thought about it for a moment and muttered to himself, "A chase... hmm... that would be more exciting than this…"

I smiled with anticipation. “For every second we wait here the farther away the thief gets farther. A noble steed, such as yourself, wouldn’t want to miss out on the chance of becoming a hero… right?” I said, unsure, hoping that would convince him.

The horse stamped his feet, "I say, that sounds quite exciting! I am all for assisting you!"

A mixture of relief and joy washed over me as now Rose and I could continue the chase. Hopefully, the thief hadn't gotten too far ahead of them.

"Lad, why on earth are you talking to the horse?" A Dwarf with a long black beard, covered in straw and dirt, walked up to me. The man wore overalls that had some cuts and stains. "What are you, crazy?" they asked with raised eyebrows.

I gave out a nervous laugh, "Oh no no. You see, my magic allows me to communicate with animals."

He jumped back, his arms raised in front of him,  eyes wide. “Magic!?” He drew a knife, his voice trembling. “What do you want from me? Magic users bring nothing but trouble! Were you the one who set the tavern on fire?”

“No!” I stammered, holding up my hands in a placating gesture. “I just wanted to ask if we could borrow one of your horses.”

"We!? There are more of you!?" His grip tightened on his knife.

Rose walked up behind me and chirped, "We are assisting knights in capturing a thief that has escaped the kingdom's walls."

The Dwarf seemed to back down and think for a moment. "Hmm... that would give my stables quite the reputation. Very well! You may choose any horse." He paused, his gaze narrowing. "But be warned, Rubert is quite stubborn. He doesn't often like being ridden." With a gruff nod, he turned and walked away, muttering something under his breath about stubborn horses and careless riders. His boots echoed off the stone as he disappeared into the shadows of the stable.

Smiling, I turned to Rose and said, “Thank you so much!”

Her eyes lit up as a warm smile graced her lips. Before she could say anything, I scooped her into a hug. When I pulled back, I noticed a mix of surprise and blush on her cheeks.

“Oh, I’m sorry!” My stone body quaked as I realized that I may have overstepped and became embarrassed. “Sorry… I tend to be a bit of a hugger…”

Rose giggled, covering her mouth as if to hide her amusement, and said, "You're fine. Shall we get going?" She looked up at the signs above the horses' stables to read their names. "Well, Rubert is probably not an option as he-" Before she could finish, I had already mounted Rubert's back, ready to go. Rose seemed surprised at how quickly I had climbed onto the horse, despite the old man’s warning.

"Want to come on?" I asked with a nervous titter. Rose nodded and I held Rubert steady as she managed to climb on. "All right, Rubert! Let’s go!" I shouted, and Rubert nodded. From behind me, I could hear a small gasp from Rose as the horse nodded in response to my command.

As we neared the man, he rushed through the portal. "Rubert! Hurry!" I urged as the portal flickered, its edges curling in as if being pulled shut. Rubert’s hooves pounded the ground, muscles coiling and stretching as he raced toward the closing gap. His breath came in short bursts, nostrils flaring, just as he leaped through, the portal sealing behind him with a soft snap.

On the other side, the air turned cool and earthy. Tall trees rose around us, their branches casting long shadows over the forest floor. Rubert slowed, his sides heaving, and ahead, the mouth of a dark cavern stretched open, quiet and waiting.

I slid off Rubert’s back and reached my hand out to assist Rose. 

"Thank you very much" Rose said, tucking a loose strand of hair behind her ear with a quick motion.

When we both had dismounted, Rubert turned to me and declared, "I shall wait for the two of you here. None shall remove me."

I smiled and replied, "Thank you, Rubert."

Rubert tilted his head, his brow furrowing slightly. "But might I ask, where did your female friend go?"

I spun around, scanning the area. Rose had vanished. My heart thudded. "Rose...?" I called, my voice rising, a prickle of unease crawling up my spine. "Where did you go?"

CHAPTER 3                                                                                                    Subterranean Dwelling

Rose’s View

As Deta chatted with Rubert, I glanced around at my surroundings in awe of the beauty around me. It had been a longtime since I’d left the castle and never without my sisters. My gaze rested on the cavern, its gloomy darkness sending a chill through me, though we had yet to enter it. A soft breeze blew toward me and.. I could have sworn I heard something. Like a soft moan or cry, coming from the depth of a cave. My brow furrowed, unsure if the thing I had heard was human or just a figment of my mind. Inching closer to the cavern, I listened, straining to possibly hear it again. Only silence greeted me. Relieved, I turned to return to Deta when, all of a sudden, I felt a hand clamp over my mouth, yanking me into the shadows of the cavern. Panic surged through my core as I struggled, dragging my boots in the dirt, trying to get Deta’s attention, but whoever had grabbed me held tight. My strength waned as I was dragged deeper into the darkness, my thoughts reeling with fear and confusion.

The further we went, the darker it became, like the shadows were swallowing me whole. The damp air pressed against my skin, chilling me as the cave seemed to close in. I fought back harder, but each movement felt like I was hitting a wall—my captor was too powerful. Tears of frustration trickled down my cheeks, my energy dwindled down to nothing once more, my body trembling from overexerting itself. A sharp pain shot through my neck and the world around me faded into nothing.

When I finally came to, I found myself restrained to a post, thick ropes biting into my wrists, the side of my neck throbbing from where it had been struck. My surroundings came into focus slowly—a campfire flickered nearby, casting long shadows. Three large men stood around, their faces illuminated by the flames. A gag had been shoved into my mouth, making it impossible to call out, and every attempt to move sent sharp pains through my bound hands. As I shifted, I felt something sharp behind me. Pain shot through my fingers, but I couldn’t let that stop me—I had to get free. My movements must’ve caught the attention of one of the men because his gaze flicked towards me.

An old man in ragged clothes rose slowly from where he sat. "Well, well, well... looks like the lady's awake," he rasped, his voice like gravel. The other two men turned to me, grinning like they knew something I didn’t.

"She sure is, John," one of them added, coughing as he settled by the fire.

Fear knotted in my stomach as I tried to inch backward, but the pole kept me pinned. As I wriggled in my bonds, my hands once again brushed against something sharp. Hope flared inside me as I started sawing at the ropes, praying they’d give before the men noticed.

The old man’s chuckle sent chills down my spine. "Oh, little girl, you’re not going anywhere. Best sit still, or we’ll have to punish you." He lifted his hands, and a faint blue glow enveloped them.

Out of nowhere, three glowing blue projectiles shot from his hands and streaked toward me. Terror gripped me as I struggled to raise my arms to protect myself, screaming despite the gag.

Just as the magic was about to hit, the rope snapped. My hands now free, I raised them to shield myself. There were three loud bangs as the projectiles collided with some invisible force. Dust filled the air, and I heard the old man laugh—until it cleared.

All three men stood in shock. A soft white glow shimmered around me. A magical shield had formed, and I peeked through my arms, barely believing what I saw. Was this me? Did I do this?

The old man’s face twisted in anger. "A magic user, eh? You’ll regret that." He motioned to the other two, and they rose, pulling out daggers as they stepped toward me.

Deta’s View

While I searched the bushes on the surface, Rose’s scream ripped through the air, echoing from the cave and snapping my focus. Without hesitation, I rushed towards the cave entrance and saw three flashes of blue light accompanied by three loud bangs. "Rose!! I'm coming!" I yelled as I passed by Rubert and entered the dim cavern.

As I sprinted through the cave, I noticed a large ditch blocking my path.Even in the dim light, my eyes caught the outline of a path to leap over it, and I pressed forward without breaking stride. As I got closer,a strange clicking sound came from somewhere just out of view. I turned my head, trying to determine the source of the sound, but then tripped over a rock just as I came to the ditch. "Oh, shoot!!" I exclaimed, trying to regain my balance but failed and fell in.

What I thought was a small ditch turned out, as luck would have it, to be a large hole.. I tumbled for what felt like minutes before hitting a body of water.

I panicked, realizing that I hadn’t taken a good breath before plunging into the water. As someone made partially of stone, I felt the weight of the water drag me further and further down. My limbs, heavy and unyielding, scraped along the bottom as I stumbled through the dark depths.

After a few tense moments, I managed to find a shallow spot where I could push off the sandy floor and wade towards a small land mass that loomed above the surface. I dragged myself onto the shore, the gritty sand grating against me and sticking to my wet clothes.

Collapsing onto the ground, I let out a long sigh. “Oh gosh… that wasn’t fun”

Catching my breath, I looked around. The walls were steep and slick, leaving no way to climb back up. I was stuck on a small patch of sand, surrounded by dark, rippling water. A few skeletal remains were scattered about the sandy dune. Apparently, I was not the first victim this pit had claimed.

A flicker of movement caught my eye—a narrow alleyway where water flowed in a steady stream. "Well, that's better than nothing," I muttered, making my way toward it. Stepping into the current, the water quickly rose around me, but with stone for skin, I didn’t swim so much as walk beneath the surface. My heavy body pressed against the pull of the water, slow but steady.

I kept one hand pressed against the wall. Each step felt deliberate, my fingers trailing along the rough stone to keep balance as the water tugged at me. Whenever the current grew stronger, I tightened my grip, around the stone begging i wouldn't get swept away.

As I made my way through the underwater passage, I noticed an incline in the floor. Yes! The surface! I thought with relief, my tense shoulders easing just a fraction. Climbing up the incline, I emerged into a much larger room, feeling a tingling sensation at having escaped the underwater passage. I exhaled slowly, my body began to absorb the water from my drenched clothes. The moisture seeped into my wooden frame, easing the cracks, while the stone held onto the lake’s lingering chill.

"Oh, thank heavens... no more water..." I shook my head to get rid of the water in my eyes and looked around. As my eyes adjusted to the dim light, I realized the room was larger than the last, though it wasn't much of an improvement. Bones, scattered in pieces, littered the ground, mixed with broken chunks of wood. The air felt still and heavy, the remnants of a struggle clear, but now all that remained was the quiet, echoing off the walls."Oh, how lovely..."

I surveyed the room and saw a passageway, but it was on the other side of the pool I had come out of. On the side I was on, there were two passages and a staircase leading up. "I'll stay on this side," I muttered to myself, turning toward the staircase. “Maybe these will lead somewhere. I have to find Rose.”

The staircase carved straight into the rock of the underground cave. The steps were rough and uneven, blending into the natural stone walls. Each tread seemed to merge with the rock, creating a sense of an endless climb. The stone was marked with veins of minerals, catching the faint light as I ascended. The air grew cooler and damper with every step, the silence of the cavern pressing in around me.

"I...hate...stairs..." I huffed, the stairs seemed to go on forever, sapping my energy like a Scorp feeding on a Sklerp. But as I got higher up, I noticed a door. "Yes! This is exactly what I..."

The door creaked open into a small, dimly lit room. Moss clung to the walls, mingled with patches of what appeared to be dried blood. The air was thick with a metallic tang and damp red moss clung to the walls adding to the smell, like water left to fester in a forgotten corner. Tables with scattered boxes stood in the corners, but my gaze drifted to the figure bound to the wall.

She had a light muscular build and was chained up off the ground, covered in cuts, bruises, and blood. The bones were sticking out of her arms and legs, jagged and wrong, skin stretched too tight around the breaks. Every shallow breath made her twitch, the motion tugging at torn flesh, sending fresh jolts of pain through her ruined limbs. Blood, sticky and half-dried, clung to her skin, pulling at open wounds with every shift. Her fingers trembled, curling in on themselves as if trying to hold onto something—anything—to ground herself against the agony.

"Ma'am...?" I hesitantly approached her. "Can you hear me?"

There was no response. Her head hung forward, chin resting against her collarbone, strands of matted hair sticking to the sweat and blood caked across her face. Her eyes were shut, lids twitching slightly, as if trapped in some distant nightmare. Shallow, uneven breaths shuddered through her cracked lips, each one barely lifting her chest.

“She must have passed out..” My stomach churned as I realized the extent of the torture this poor woman had endured. I couldn't imagine the pain she must have been in. Whatever the reason may have been for this woman’s imprisonment, it could not justify this level of suffering.

I recalled my training with Vomete, remembering a spell to heal wounds. Taking a deep breath, I focused my energy, concentrating on casting the spell. My arms glowed a deep green and with trembling hands, I touched the woman's broken leg, watching as the bones retracted and reformed under my touch. I hesitated for a moment before placing my hand on her chest, feeling the shallow rise and fall of her breath. The glow from my hands intensified and, to my relief, the woman's breathing grew stronger.

Her eyes snapped open, wild and unfocused, pupils blown wide with something between rage and desperation. With a sudden, violent jerk, she lunged at me, the chains biting into her skin as they yanked her back. A guttural, animalistic snarl tore from her throat. I stumbled away, my arms instinctively raising, the glow flickering out.

"Hey! I'm here to help you!" I said quickly, my voice tight with urgency. "I just need to heal your wounds!"

She didn't seem to hear me. She thrashed and writhed, her body twisting against the restraints, muscles straining despite the jagged bones jutting from her limbs. Her breath came in ragged, shuddering gasps, her face contorted in raw, mindless fury. I took another step back—too fast. My foot caught the leg of a table, sending it crashing to the ground as I landed hard beside it.

Heart pounding, I scanned the room, desperate for something—anything— that could either free her or at least stop her from tearing herself apart. That’s when I saw it: a small box on the floor, a bottle of red liquid nestled inside.

Sometime ago, there had been some travelers lost in the woods. They held bottles like these to their lips whenever one of them was injured. Perhaps they were healing drinks of some kind? I grabbed one and approached her again. She was still struggling when I opened the bottle and splashed it on her face. I could see the fury in them begin to settle, her tense body allowing itself to droop just a little. Only when she relaxed did I dare to inch closer, another bottle uncorked and my hand cupped ready to assist her with taking it.

By the time she drank all the bottles, her body had mostly recovered, save for a few bruises. "Thank you," she said, finally able to speak.

"It's no problem," I replied, relieved that she was okay. "What's your name?" Once we got her out of the chains, We sat in heavy silence, the weight of unspoken words thick between us. Finally, she exhaled softly and spoke.

Her name was Gwen. She didn’t remember much about her past, or so she claimed, but there were things she held back—hesitations that flickered across her face, small pauses where words seemed to catch in her throat. Whatever she did remember, some part of her wasn’t ready to share.

She was around five foot seven inches with dark skin and wild, matted hair full of rocks and sticks. Additionally, she had deep blue eyes. I was struck by her unique dark skin tone, one I had never encountered before in a human. But when I asked about it, her expression hardened immediately.

"What does it matter?" she snapped, her voice sharp and defensive.

I flinched at the sudden edge in her tone. She shot me a glare, her eyes narrowing with annoyance. Her posture stiffened, and she crossed her arms tightly, as if trying to protect herself from something more than just my questions. She approached the nearest box and threw off its lid, and being unsure what to do I copied.

We rummaged through the boxes and, unsure of what we were looking for, I tried to speak to her “So… Gwen? What are we looking for exactly?”

She groaned. “My things.. What else do you think, Tree Face?”

“Your things? Got it.” I gave out a nervous chuckle. “Um, I hate to ask this but, I lost my friend down here.. I think she was kidnapped-”  But before I could finish, she found her belongings in one of the boxes and let out a sigh of relief when she uncovered her metallic shirt made of chains and a bag. Humans really are confusing creatures, I thought.

After putting some things into the bag and donning some slightly large pants and her shirt, she turned to me "Alright," she stood up and brushed her hair back. "As thanks for helping me escape those chains, I will help you in finding your friend. However, I have no intention of becoming a captive again," she glared at me, sending shivers down my spine. "Do you get that?"

I bobbed my head., "Yes, I assure you that I have no such intentions. I just want to find my friend." I let out a nervous chuckle, hoping to ease the tension between us.

She didn't look convinced. My eyes darted around the room, landing on a rusted sword jutting from a corpse. I gestured toward it. "Uh, maybe we should take that? Just in case—"

Before I could finish, Gwen stepped forward, planted a foot on the body, and yanked the sword free with a sickening squelch. I swallowed hard, deciding not to push my luck.

We left the room and headed back the way I’d come. As we turned the corner to go down the last flight of stairs, I spotted a giant spider drinking from the lake below, its body about the size of a small deer. I turned to warn Gwen about disturbing it, but my foot slipped on the damp steps.

The next thing I knew, I was tumbling down the rest of the stairs.

This caught the spider's attention, and it ran in my direction. “Food! Die! Die!” I heard the spider yell in a scratchy, high-pitched, hissing voice that rang through my ears.

Before I could react, the spider was on me, sinking its fangs into my arm. The pain spread like fiery cracks, chipping away at my stone and wooden arm and leaving a relentless, deep ache. While stuck on the ground underneath the spider's weight, I managed to grab a long piece of wood from off the ground and fight back against the creature, smacking its leg and causing it to screech out in pain. “I'm not food! Get away from me!”

The spider’s weight pressed down onto me, making it difficult to move. I could hear the scuffle of Gwen’s approach, the ring of metal as she drew her sword, and her frustrated grunt as she missed her target.

The spider, now furious with me, tried to bite down again and shot some green liquid from its fangs, but it bounced off my stone flesh and burnt some of the wood of my arm. I cried out and hit its leg again, breaking it, causing the creature to screech and stumble. This gave Gwen the chance to attack the creature again. She slashed on the spider’s abdomen, but its hide was so thick that the sword slid down its side.

The creature screeched out in pain as its deep blue blood spewed out. I threw the spider off and tried to get up, but it bit my arm again with so much force that when it pulled, it tore my forearm off. I took a few steps back as a sharp agony tore through me, making me drop the long stick.

My fear flipped to fury as the pain consumed me, the vines on my skin twisted and grew, forming a whip in my hand. Sharp thorns sprouted along its length, ready to strike, I lashed out at the creature, the barbed vines striking with a satisfying crack.

Gwen then took her sword and slashed at its large abdomen again, causing its organs to fall out and be exposed. It screeched and tried to escape, but I would not let it. Not an ounce of sympathy remained as  I used my thorn whip to grab it by its liver and pull it back to us. Gwen took the opening and speared the thing through its head, causing blood to splatter all over her, and the creature fell limp.

I took a deep breath, feeling the tension settle like cracks forming in my frame. My body was sturdy, but even stone could break under enough pressure. This was the first time I had truly been in danger—real danger—and if I continued down this path through the cave, it wouldn’t be the last.

I exhaled slowly, letting the weight of the moment pass like wind through the trees. Fear never helps as Vomete would say. I had to stay steady. I wasn’t just some lost wanderer stumbling through danger—I had a purpose.

Shaking off the lingering dread, I straightened and let a small, familiar smile return. "Alright," I muttered to myself. "Let’s keep moving."

 My fingers flexed, seeking something solid to hold onto. When I turned to Gwen to see if she was alright, I saw that she’d turned white as snow and shaking. Before I could speak, her deep blue eyes rolled back into her skull, and she collapsed onto the ground unconscious.

After an hour, she finally stirred. I glanced over from where I crouched by the small, flickering fire, prodding the embers in a futile attempt to keep them alive. The dim orange glow cast restless shadows against the damp stone walls, the smoke curling upward in thin, lazy trails.

A thin blanket, rough and smelling faintly of dust and old fabric, was draped over her shoulders. She sat with her back pressed against the wall, her breath slow but uneven. The fire cracked weakly, struggling against the cold air that seeped through the cracks in the stone. Tending fires wasn’t my strength, and the flames seemed to mock my efforts, shrinking every time I thought I had them under control.

I turned around when I heard her stir and was relieved to see that she was awake. "Gwen! I'm so glad to see you're okay." I smiled, but she seemed confused.

"What about your arm? How did it regenerate?"

I was a little taken aback by her question, but then I remembered that most people considered my kind to be a mere fairy tale, as the deep voiced child who worked with the demon knight had mentioned. "Oh, it's just one of my abilities. After a certain amount of time, I can piece my body back together with the materials around me."

She looked at me with a puzzled expression. She gave me a puzzled look, her eyes narrowing as she studied me. Then, her expression shifted —understanding dawning as she put the pieces together.

Without saying anything, she got up, wadded up her blanket and stuffed it back into her bag.. "I see you went through my things," she remarked, sounding a little annoyed.

"Sorry about that," I apologized sheepishly. "I didn't know what to do, so I was hoping you had some supplies or something."

She let out a deep sigh and shook her head. "Whatever. Let's just focus on finding your friend and getting out of here,"

We packed up our camp and made our way to a narrow set of stairs that turned a corner, leading into a larger chamber thick with cobwebs. Another stairway was visible on the other side. Memories of our last battle crept in, and I let out a sigh before glancing at Gwen, who looked a little shaky.

"Are you alright?" I asked, catching the tension in her stance.

She scoffed, her voice flat. "I'm fine. Let's just burn these webs and get moving."
