With that, she took a small stick out of her bag and flicked it against the wall, igniting it. She then dropped the stick onto the webs on the floor, causing them to burn slowly.

"Uh... okay?" I was hesitant about burning the webs, as that could disturb more giant spiders, but agreed to go along with it. Looking around the room, I noticed that the entrance on the other side was blocked by cobwebs that would eventually burn on their own. There didn't seem to be much else we could do, so I let out a sigh."Can I get one of those sticks?"  

Gwen nodded and passed me a stick, and I struck it against a web-free surface, igniting it as she had. I placed the burning stick on a cobweb as the webs began to burn away, revealing two dead animal bodies. One of them was lying on its side, and when it was exposed, Gwen flinched in surprise thinking they were more spiders.

After burning through enough webs, the doorway finally cleared. I couldn't help but chuckle, a smile creeping across my face. "Alright! We can continue onward!" I exclaimed.

Gwen nodded, her lips pressing into a thin line as she glanced away, and we stepped into the next room, which was also covered in cobwebs much to our disappointment.

This time, Gwen stepped forward, taking the lead. I looked at her confused as she flashed a grin. "Last time you led, you lost an arm," she joked with a slight grin.

I smiled and said with a slight laugh. “That's not fair!”

Unfortunately, our banter had drawn unwanted attention. Two younger spiders emerged from the darkness, their eyes glinting menacingly. I quickly warned Gwen, and we both fell into battle stances. The spider closest to Gwen lunged at her, aiming for her face, but with practiced movement, she seized its leg and hurled it aside.

"Not these pests again!" she yelled, her face scrunching in disgust, as she got ready to fight them again.

The spider closest to me leapt, trying to bite me, but I managed to block its attack with my arm once again. The pain was less intense than before, spreading slower but it still left a persistent, deep ache.

"I hate these things," I muttered to myself. Remembering my thorn whip, I summoned it, using it to lash out at the spider.

I watched as Gwen charged at the webspinner, but her foot caught on a hidden web, causing her to stumble and miss her strike. Seeing an opening, the creature attacked, but Gwen jerked back, narrowly avoiding its fangs.

The other spider lunged at me again, its movements sharp and fluid, as if it were gliding over the ground. Each step was calculated, its legs skittering across the stone with unnerving precision. Remembering its previous attack, I sidestepped just in time, pulling my arm out of harm’s way. I retaliated by releasing a cloud of poison from my hand. The mist enveloped the spider, making it stagger and falter, its legs twitching erratically as it struggled against the poison’s effects.

“Die, you filthy beast!” Gwen shouted and I watched as she drove her sword into the spider’s head. The blade pierced through its immature hide, causing the spider to go limp and stop struggling.

My attention snapped back to my enemy as its fangs sank into my arm. Pain jolted through me, making me hesitate. I had no chance to strike back before the spider tore deeper into my forearm.

Gwen turned her attention to the spider that held me. She charged forward, and with her sword managed to smack the spider off of my arm.

“Thank you for-”

“Shut it!” Gwen seized the opportunity and, with grim determination, drove her sword into the spider’s abdomen. Her blade hit vital organs, and the creature convulseMy attention snapped back to my enemy as its fangs sank into my arm. Pain jolted through me, making me hesitate. I had no chance to strike back before the spider tore deeper into my forearm.d before stiffening.

She extended her sword toward me, her hand trembling slightly. "Could you clean the blood off?" she asked.

Confused, I hesitated. "Are you alright?" I asked softly.

She nodded her head, offering a faint smile. "I’m fine… I just don’t want to pass out again."

Realization dawned on me, and I smiled as I sat down, pulling a rag from my bag to wipe the blade clean. "There, the blood’s gone." I held the sword out by the blade's tip, offering it back to her. She took the hilt with a grateful nod.

Yawning, I glanced around. "It’s getting late... I think." We both chuckled, though weariness weighed on our voices. Gwen scanned the area, her gaze sharp, but no enemies remained in sight.

She sighed in relief. "Maybe, but we still need to find your friend."

Suddenly, soft music drifted through the air. Its quiet, melodic notes felt dreamlike, as if we were floating on a cloud. A strange warmth settled over me, my limbs growing heavy, my thoughts sluggish. My eyelids drooped, and I yawned again.  

"Where is that music coming from?" I asked, my voice thick with exhaustion.  

Gwen looked around, but her legs buckled beneath her, and she sank to the ground, stifling another yawn. "I don’t know," she murmured, her words slow and drowsy.  

The next thing I knew, I was on the floor, my body refusing to move. Gwen lay asleep in front of me, her breathing deep and steady. A shadow loomed over her—a figure crouched at her side, tying her hands behind her back. He wore leather armor, his long white hair falling over his shoulders. Around his waist, a strip of white fur contrasted against his purple pants, and large leather boots planted him firmly on the ground. A small harp swung from his side, its strings still quivering.

"There we go," he muttered, tightening the bindings with practiced ease.

As I woke up more and focused, I could see he had pale gray skin and long pointed ears. I sprang to my feet, summoning vines and roots to trap him. He struggled, but one arm remained free. He drew a dagger and hurled it at me, grazing my side. I winced, grabbing at the chipped stone.

"I'm done with all this stupid fighting!” I growled, advancing. I tore out one of the long thin roots from the floor, which gave off a faint glow after straightening itself, and struck him across the head.

The commotion stirred Gwen from her enchanted sleep. She too had been bound by roots, but broke free of them with ease. Grabbing her sword from the ground, she slashed at the man, leaving a deep wound in his upper arm. His expression twisted in pain, realizing he had underestimated us.

"Please don’t kill me!" he pleaded, his voice shaking. Gwen narrowed her eyes, unconvinced.

I turned to the man. "Why were you trying to tie up my friend?"

recognizing him, Gwen stepped forward, fury building in her eyes. "Rinn," she spat.

He laughed weakly, his bravado crumbling. "Gwen! I see those wounds healed quick!"

She punched the side of his face then grabbed his throat pinning him in the air.

Rinn chuckled, speaking between faint gasps. “I take it… the creature behind you… used the potions? I'm surprised you remember me” He let out another weak laugh.

Gwen tightened her grip. “Those potions almost saved you, but I can’t forget the man who made my life hell for seven years!” Her voice shook with anger, her fingers closing tighter around his throat.

“What do you mean?” I asked in confusion. I had never heard of potions before. Was that the name of the colored water?

Gwen’s knuckles cracked as she squeezed harder. “Those potions you gave me? Restoration potions. They heal injuries, sure—but they also have this nasty little side effect of making people forget what’s been done to them.” Her tone dripped with venom. “Guess that worked out real well for you, huh?”

Rinn’s face began to pale. His hands clawed weakly at her arm, but she didn’t budge.

“Gwen, let him go,” I said, my voice softer than I meant it to be.

She shot me a glare, her eyes wild with fury. “No! He deserves to die! He ruined my life!”

I stepped closer, my chest tight, my mind spinning. Was I stopping her for the right reasons? Or was I just scared? I met her furious gaze, searching for anything—hesitation, doubt, some sign that she didn’t really want to go through with it. For a moment, I thought she might just ignore me and finish it anyway. But after what felt like an eternity, her grip loosened, and she let him go, though her anger still smoldered in the air between us.

The elf, Rinn, gasped for air, trembling. "Thank you, young creature. I—"

Before he could finish, I punched him square in the face. A sharp crack rang out as my fist connected, flames briefly flickering across my knuckles. Rinn's head snapped to the side, and he staggered back, clutching his face. Blood dripped from his nose, pooling at his upper lip before he wiped it away with a shaky hand. He groaned, spitting a fleck of red onto the ground, his breathing uneven.

"If you ever harm Gwen again, I’ll make sure you regret it. Do I make myself clear?"

Rinn, stunned and dazed, nodded weakly, his fingers still pressed against his nose, as if unsure whether it was broken.

"Now tie him up," I instructed Gwen. "We'll let others deal with him. For now, we need him alive."

"Why should we?" she snapped, her eyes narrowing in immediate refusal.

I hesitated, choosing my words carefully. "He probably knows this place better than we do. If we keep him alive, we can use him as a guide. After that… we'll figure out what to do with him." My voice was steady, but tension lingered beneath it.

With a curt nod, Gwen bound him, taking little care as to how deep the ropes cut into his wrists. She picked up Rinn’s harp and tossed it to me. "Catch, Bushy Hair.",

I caught it, tucking it into my satchel. "We should also bandage his wound. If he bleeds out he won't be of much help."

“Oh.. how noble of you..” Rinn said with a roll of his eyes only to have Gwen punch him in the wound causing him to give a sharp recoil and fall silent.

With Rinn securely tied, we moved onward. Our footsteps echoed in the stillness, and as we ventured further into the room, we found another exit to the left.

CHAPTER 4                                                                                                                   Hungry Guests

Upon going through the west exit, we found a long sandy pass leading to a large underground lake. The beach stretched along the side of the cave, and a little path veered off to the middle of the lake. I sighed as we walked along the sandy passageway.

Rinn gave a grin. "So, might I ask, what are you, fire hand boy? I've never seen a creature like you before."

Gwen tugged at the rope, causing him to stumble a bit. "Stay quiet, monster," she said with scorn, then looked at me.

I hadn’t hardly heard them as I stared, transfixed, at my hand, which was still set ablaze. I questioned how I, being a Randeth—a being of nature—could somehow create fire. I then remembered something Vomete told me when I was a young boy.

We were out in the garden, and the fire lily was struggling. Vomete extended her hand and set it aflame. The fire caused the lily to sprout up and appear much healthier, but I was stunned.

"Vomete? How can you use fire? Doesn't it hurt the forest?"

Vomete smiled and patted my head. "Oh Deta, fire is more than destruction. It brings life and light to barren lands." She moved the fire closer for me to observe. "Fire is something only a few Randeths can use, and it only shows when passion and protection meet."

This left me puzzled. "What do you mean, Vomete?" I asked, still too young to grasp it. She chuckled softly. "When you're older and have more experience, you'll understand."

Gwen’s voice then shook me back to the present. "You okay, Deta?" she asked. "You’ve been quiet for almost an hour."

I turned to her, my body tensing in slight surprise.. "Oh! Sorry! Just lost in my thoughts." I glanced back at my hand, and the fire had faded. I tried to summon it again but couldn't. "But yeah, I’m fine," I reassured her. I then looked at Rinn. "To answer your earlier question, I am a Randeth."

Rinn scoffed. "A Randeth? Do you think I’m a child? Randeths don’t exist! They're just fables. If you were truly a Randeth, you could shift into a forest elk, which I doubt you can!"

I sighed, rolling my eyes at Rinn's dismissive tone. "Believe what you want," I said, waving my hand before turning down a corridor and moving on.

As we continued, the path led us back into the cave system, eventually opening into a larger chamber. The sound of dripping water echoed off the walls, and the faint shimmer of an underground lake stretched out before us. A slim beach ran along one side, leading to another room deeper in the cavern. "Finally, some progress," I muttered, my voice carrying through the cavern. "Now we're one step closer to finding Rose!"

Rinn smirked, his eyes gleaming with mockery. “Rose? You collecting a polyg—”

Before he could finish, Gwen’s fist slammed into his gut, cutting him off. “Shut up, or I’m throwing you in the lake,” she growled, her voice sharp with fury.

The room had three exits: one continued forward, another path led upwards, and a staircase descended. As we approached the center of the chamber, we heard a faint squeaking sound.

Gwen let out an exasperated sigh. “If it’s not giant spiders, it’s rats! What’s next? A bear?” She threw her hands up in frustration, clearly fed up. “Honestly, I’d take anything other than these little pests.”

I couldn’t help but chuckle at her comment, but Rinn scoffed once more.
“It’s a cave, girl. You should be smart enough to know that by now,” he said, rolling his eyes.

Gwen shot him a wicked grin, her eyes narrowing. “Yeah, well, I’m starting to think you’re the biggest pest in here. At least the rats know when to shut up.”

Rinn smirked, trying to brush off her comment. “Nice try, but—”

Before he could finish, Gwen’s eyes narrowed and her hand shot out, grabbing him by the collar. “Shut. Up.” Her tone was lethal, and she pulled him closer, letting the threat linger.

Rinn’s bravado faltered for a second, but he quickly recovered, his jaw tightening. He met her gaze, unwilling to back down.

“Well, which way should we go?” Gwen asked, dropping her grip on him but still glaring like she could tear him apart if he said one more word.

Before I could answer, a heavy clunking sound shattered the silence, each step reverberating through the ground like distant thunder. It wasn’t just footsteps—it was something massive forcing its way forward, uncaring of what lay in its path. The air grew thick, charged with an unnatural weight as the shadows ahead twisted and split apart.

Then it emerged.

A towering humanoid figure, clad in ancient, rusted metal. Its armor was jagged, uneven, as if pieced together from the remains of something long forgotten. Chains dangled from its limbs, swaying with a metallic rattle, and the deep grooves in its helmet suggested something inside had been struggling—maybe for a long time. It moved strangely, its steps uneven, its entire frame shifting in ways that felt...wrong.

I didn't wait to see what it wanted.

My arm extended, the stone and wood of my body shifting and groaning as the vines embedded in my form sprang to life. They twisted together, growing, stretching, until they formed a long, whip-like weapon. Sharp thorns jutted from its surface, glistening like fangs in the dim light. The weapon pulsed, brimming with raw energy, aching for release.

I wasn’t about to hesitate.

With a sharp crack, I lashed the whip forward, the air shrieking as the thorns sliced through it, striking the armored figure’s arm.

“Who are you?” I said, my voice quieter than I meant, but steady. The whip coiled around its limb, thorns biting deep into the metal. I yanked hard, and with a sickening screech, a chunk of rusted plating tore free, clattering to the ground.

What spilled out wasn’t blood.

Rats. A writhing, churning mass of them poured from the gap in the armor, their slick bodies squirming over one another, their beady eyes glinting in the dim light. They seethed and twitched, some vanishing back inside the hollow suit while others scrambled over the ground. The thing lurched but did not fall, the armor adjusting, shifting as the creatures within worked in grotesque harmony to keep it moving.

My breath hitched. This wasn’t a person. It wasn’t even a creature. It was a swarm.

Gwen charged at the humanoid, Rinn trailing behind her. With a sharp swing, she unsheathed her sword and sliced clean through its neck. The severed head hit the ground with a sickening thud, and from the gaping hole in the helmet, a torrent of rats spilled out, writhing and screeching as they poured onto the floor like a living flood.

"Rats!" Gwen recoiled, her voice thick with disgust.

Before she could react further, the displaced rodents turned on her, their eyes gleaming as they leaped, teeth snapping. She sidestepped them with a scowl, but the grotesque puppet of armor lurched forward, swinging its massive mace in a deadly arc. Gwen barely dodged, the weapon smashing into the stone floor with a thunderous impact that sent dust and debris flying.

In the chaos, Rinn seized his chance. He turned on his heel and bolted.

Gwen caught the movement instantly. With a sharp yank, she pulled on the rope binding him, jerking him backward. He crashed onto the ground with an undignified grunt, arms flailing.

Meanwhile, I grabbed my staff, bracing myself as the fallen rats turned their attention toward me. They leaped, their gnashing teeth flashing in the dim light. I swung hard, smashing them mid-air, but more swarmed at my feet, clawing at my legs, trying to burrow into the crevices of my wooden skin. Gwen slashed at the writhing tide that scurried at her feet, her frustration mounting.

"Deta! Use your fire and get rid of this abomination!" she shouted, voice tight with urgency.

I tried. I rushed forward, hand outstretched, but when I willed the fire to come, nothing but a pathetic spark flickered and died. Frustrated, I swung my arm wildly, hoping something—anything—would ignite, but before I could react, the rat-formed knight struck.

Its mace connected with my side in a brutal arc, and I barely had time to register the hit before I was airborne. Pain exploded through my body as I crashed hard onto the stone floor, the breath knocked from my lungs.

"Dang it…" I wheezed, wincing. "That thing’s stronger than it looks."

Gwen wasn’t about to let up. Her sword flashed, severing its remaining arm in one clean motion. But as the limb hit the ground, it didn't remain a lifeless hunk of metal. It dissolved—melted—into a wave of rats, scattering and reforming, surging toward her like a sentient plague.

Nearby, Rinn was thrashing, his curses growing more panicked as the rats swarmed over him, biting and clawing.

"Dang it! Get off me, you filthy little—gah!" He kicked wildly, trying to shake them off, but they clung to his sleeves, gnawing through fabric and flesh. "This is why I hate dungeons and caves! Rats, traps, and—ow!—you useless vermin!" He flailed harder, but the more he struggled, the more they latched onto him. "I swear, when I get free, I'm burning this whole place down—with you two in it!"

"As if!" Gwen shot back, slashing through another wave. "You should just die already, so shut up!"

The rat-puppet swung again, its mace crashing down. I barely rolled aside, feeling the wind of its strike as it missed my skull by inches. Scrambling upright, I gripped my staff and slammed it against its side with every ounce of force I had. The impact sent a shudder through the armor, and suddenly, the creature collapsed—crumbling apart as the rats lost cohesion.

"I hate this thing!" I snarled, kicking at the vermin gnawing at my boots.

"Yeah? You think I like them?" Gwen snapped, carving through the swarm with growing frustration.

Across the battlefield, Rinn was losing his fight, his movements growing more frantic as he was nearly buried in squirming bodies. Gwen spotted another surge of rats racing toward us and didn’t hesitate. She darted forward, slicing through them in two broad sweeps, then stormed toward Rinn. She grabbed the collar of his shirt and yanked him free, hurling him away from the worst of the swarm.

I swung the last few rats against the wall, their bodies smacking against the stone with wet, sickening thuds. Those still alive scurried away into the darkness.

Just as I caught my breath, I saw it happen—Rinn, scrambling to his feet, shot Gwen a wicked grin before kicking her legs out from under her.

She hit the ground hard—right into the pile of seething rats.

Rinn snickered and turned to run, but Gwen still had the rope. She yanked it, sending him sprawling once more. "I'm going to kill you for that," she growled, her voice dripping with murderous intent.

I rushed forward, swiping at the rats clinging to her. "I'll try not to hit you, Gwen!"

"Forget that! Just kill them!" she barked, slashing wildly.

With two final, decisive swings, she carved through the remaining swarm. The few survivors scurried into the shadows, retreating into whatever horrors had spawned them.

Breathing heavily, she glared daggers at Rinn, but instead of gutting him where he stood, she dug into her bag and tossed me a small glass vial.

"Drink this," she muttered, her voice edged with exasperation. "It won’t fix your legs, but it’ll help."

I caught it, still trying to process the sheer awfulness of what we had just fought. I gulped down the bitter liquid, wincing as it burned its way down my throat. A moment later, the sting of my scratches faded, the splinters in my legs sealing up as if they had never been there.

“That’s incredible! Thanks, Gwen!” I flexed my legs, relieved.

She smirked, wiping her sword clean on a rag. “No big deal. Now, which way?”

Two paths stretched ahead. After a quick scan, I pointed toward the farthest tunnel. Gwen took the lead, stepping over rat carcasses while I kept an eye on Rinn, making sure he didn’t try to pull anything. As we walked, barrels lined the walls—whiskey, ale, and who knew what else.

The passage opened into a small room. In the far corner, a huddle of rats twitched, their beady eyes gleaming in the dim light.

“I want to try the fire again,” I told Gwen, tightening my grip on my staff.

She gave a quick nod. “Go ahead, but be quick.”

Focusing hard, I forced a flicker of warmth into my fingertips. A small flame flared to life in my palm. I hurled it at the rats, and they scattered in panic, some catching fire and squealing as they darted away.

“I did it!” I grinned.

Gwen rolled her eyes but kept her stance firm. “Nice work, but we’ve still got a few more to deal with!”

A fresh wave of rats surged toward her. She swung twice, each arc of her blade slicing through the swarm with brutal efficiency. But one of the vermin leaped up, sinking its teeth into her hair.

“I’ve got this!” I called, already raising my staff.

“Wait—”

Too late. I swung, knocking the rat away—along with a solid hit to Gwen’s head.

Rinn burst out laughing. “Oh, that was beautiful.”

We were too exhausted to argue, but Gwen, scowling, turned and slugged him in the arm—right where he was already injured. He yelped, stumbling back.

“What was that for?!” he whined, cradling his arm.

“Because I don’t like you.” Gwen didn’t even look at him as she muttered it.

I scanned the room, rubbing my sore shoulder from the recoil of my staff swing. In the far corner, three barrels stood side by side. Curious, I pried one open and found it stuffed with potatoes. The next held rice, and the last, beans.

“Well,” I sighed, stepping back. “At least we have food now.”

Gwen dragged Rinn over without a word and plopped down. “Let’s eat a little and rest.”

I nodded, sinking onto the floor beside them.

As we approached, my eyes caught on an odd tile among the others—a little too smooth, a little too out of place. Suspicious. I turned to Rinn.

“Rinn, step on this.”

He shot me a glare. “Do I look stupid? That’s a trap.”

Without missing a beat, Gwen punched him hard in the face. He stumbled back with a curse, but she didn’t give him a chance to recover. Snatching his golden knife from its sheath, she pressed the cold metal to his throat.

“You talk too much,” she muttered.

Rinn went rigid, his lips curling in fury, but he stayed silent. Gwen, unimpressed, flicked the knife toward me. “Use this.”

The blade hit the ground with a metallic clatter, bouncing a few times before settling. I crouched, hesitated, then carefully placed it on the odd tile. The stone sank slightly—but nothing happened.

I exhaled, ready to move on. But something about it nagged at me.

Grimacing, I started stacking dead rats onto the tile, one after another. Their bodies, still warm, left streaks of blood against the stone. The scent of singed fur and rot curled in the air, but I kept at it.

Then—click.

The tile lowered, and with a low grind of stone against stone, a hidden door creaked open.

Gwen and I locked eyes, tension thick between us. I leaned forward, peering into the opening. Beyond, a dark hallway stretched into the unknown, a faint glow flickering at the far end. No sign of movement.

Without hesitation, I gestured for Gwen to follow.

We stepped inside, the air thick and stale, dust shifting with every footstep. Then—suddenly—the floor beneath me gave way.

A startled gasp tore from my throat as I plummeted. My stomach lurched—then thud! I hit something soft and wrong. A sickening squelch spread beneath me.

My vision blurred. And then I felt it move.

When my vision came to, there was a dull ache in my skull accompanied by dizziness. Blinking rapidly, I saw Gwen rushing toward the edge of the hole, pulling Rinn along with a rough yank.

"You okay?" she asked, her tone sounding tense with concern, but there was no real care behind it. I nodded, though my mind was still hazy from the fall.

My breath caught in my throat as something caught my eye—a monstrous centipede, the size of a small house, its body covered in slick, glistening segments. But it wasn’t just a centipede. Tentacles sprouted from its grotesque head, swaying like serpents, while its thousands of legs twitched, skittering across the ground with unnerving speed.

The creature was still yet alert. It must have been disturbed by the collapse when I fell through the floor. It sniffed the air, testing the scents around it, before its many eyes fixed on me, narrowing slightly. Then, without any warning, it scurried up the wall, its legs scraping against the stone, and crawled along the ceiling as if gravity didn’t apply to it at all.

We stood frozen, all eyes locked on it, not daring to move. The only sound in the room was the creature’s legs scraping, the faint rustle of the air as it shifted its enormous body.

I wondered, irrationally, why it hadn’t attacked me. I glanced down—and then it became clear. I was surrounded by the lifeless bodies of adventurers, their faces frozen in horror, their limbs twisted at unnatural angles. Mixed with the debris, I blended into the mess. The creature had mistaken me for just another fallen scrap, as motionless as the broken wood and stone littering the floor.

I heard Gwen stir above me, her eyes darting between me and the centipede. She was already thinking. She always was.

Without a word, she turned to Rinn, who stood sullenly behind her. "You're coming with me."

Rinn grumbled under his breath, but there was no fight in him. He knew better than to refuse. He followed her begrudgingly, the tension in his posture a stark contrast to her steely calm.

Gwen moved swiftly across the room, her boots making barely a sound against the cold stone. She reached the entrance of the adjacent room and glanced back, her eyes meeting mine for a split second. She grabbed a handful of loose rocks from the floor then hurled them into the pit below me.

The rocks tumbled and crashed, startling the creature. It paused, its antennae twitching as it turned its head down toward the sound. Satisfied that the distraction had worked, Gwen grabbed another rock, and with a practiced flick of her wrist, sent it sailing directly into the creature’s head.

It howled—no, shrieked—a low, guttural noise that rattled the walls. Pain and fury filled its strange, alien eyes. The centipede reared up and, with an angry hiss, slithered back down the wall, claws clattering against stone, heading straight toward the source of the provocation.

Without wasting another second, Gwen yanked Rinn along as they sprinted back towards the room they had just left, the furious creature hot on their heels

 "I want no part of this! Unhand me!" Rinn protested, pulling against Gwen’s grip. But as Rinn glanced back, he realized there was no choice but to keep running. "Never mind! Hurry, run!" Rinn exclaimed, his eyes widening in terror.

Gwen rolled her eyes and leaped into the pile of corpses, dragging Rinn down with her. "Deta! Move!" she shouted, scrambling free.

I stumbled to my feet, heart pounding, and spotted a passageway on the west side of the room. We rushed down the path, breathless, only to find ourselves in a dead-end chamber.

Before we could react, the insect-like creature crawled down the wall toward us. Trapped, we had no choice but to retreat into the small room.

Once inside, we spotted three chests and each of us ducked behind one, hoping to remain unseen. But our hiding spot was only a brief respite, as the monster began to approach, drawn by the scent of death the corpses had left on us.

Rinn hissed, "This is madness! We're going to be found!"

Gwen snapped back, "Then be quiet and let’s figure something out!"

The creature sniffed around, inching closer to our hiding spot. I urged the others, "Check your chest! Find whatever you can and get ready to fight!"

I found a bottle of gray liquid—no clue what it was, but I hoped it would be useful. The others turned up nothing but worthless trinkets, like golden circles.

Desperate, Rinn demanded, "Give me my harp!"

"Absolutely not! You're not escaping!"

"Either give me my harp, or we're dead!"

Seeing no other option, I groaned and shoved the instrument against his bound hands, hoping he could make use of it.

Just as the creature screeched its way into the room, I downed the drink. Energy surged through my veins, igniting every nerve.

Gripping my staff with renewed strength, I charged forward, shouting, "Let's go!"

Only one thought lingered in the back of my mind—what on earth had I just consumed?

As I rushed the monstrous creature, I swung my staff with all my might, shattering part of its exoskeleton. Gwen followed with swift precision, shooting something she found in her chest piercing its left eye.

The monster let out a blood-curdling scream, rearing back to strike—but before it could, Rinn stepped in front of us. With his wrists still bound, he awkwardly positioned his hands and dragged his fingers across the harp strings.

A wave of powerful sound erupted.

The creature was hurled backward, and I struggled to keep my balance as a deafening ring assaulted my ears. Yet Gwen, unfazed, loaded another shot and fired. The monster screeched in agony before collapsing, lifeless.

Rinn flashed a victorious grin, his hands now free, then turned with a chuckle. "See you later, fools."

With a flick of his wrist, he played another melody, and a thick cloud of black smoke billowed from the ground, plunging us into darkness. As Gwen cursed and rushed after him, I stumbled over the fallen creature.

Emerging from the smoke, I saw Gwen storming back and forth, kicking debris out of her way. She screamed furiously in a language I didn’t understand, her voice rising with every roll of her tongue.

“Skarveznar fururcrakarzhur yarerahrahsar! Ir sarwarerahrah taror ervezrahyar brulorererdruzhur kharahrah, rahirnarnar, ir’khal furlorahyar yarorur sarlororwar ahvrak morahkarer yarorur warahtarcrahar!”

Suddenly, she whirled around and slammed one of the bodies against the wall with a sharp crack. Even without knowing the words, I knew they were anything but pleasant.  

She slammed her sword into the ground with a bone-rattling crash, her breath coming in sharp, furious gasps. Folding her arms, she glared at the spot where Rinn had been. "That idiot—I'll tear him apart. Just watch."

Then she glanced at me, sprawled on the ground. "Are you going to get up or take a nap?"

I chuckled. "Getting up." I stood, brushing the dust from my clothes. "I just didn't want to interrupt your…venting."

She rolled her eyes. "Whatever. I just want out of this stupid cave."

I nodded in agreement, then looked up at the hole in the ceiling where the hallway continued. We made our way back toward the room and the passage beyond.

Gwen huffed, still seething. "What are we doing back here?" she snapped, her frustration barely contained.

"Well, the hall continues. Might as well see where it leads!" I shot her a quick look, trying to ignore the tension. "I think I can make it."

Gwen shook her head as I took a running start and leapt across, barely clearing the hole.

"See?" I said with a smirk. "Made it!"

I backed up, offering my hand to help her across, but she simply walked to the edge and hopped over with ease. She strode past me with a sly grin, flicking her hair. I rolled my eyes and laughed as we continued down the hall. Gwen took the lead. When we reached the end, the hall opened onto the underground beach.

A dying campfire smoldered nearby, its smoke curling in the damp air. Three bodies lay motionless, their forms marked by violent, scorched wounds. The smell of burnt flesh mixed with the salt of the sea, heavy and acrid. One body was nearly unrecognizable, its skin blackened and burned in patches, likely from the blasts of fire. The others were marked with deep, charred holes—small, precise burns, leaving raw, singed flesh around each wound. Their faces were frozen in agony, as though death had come swiftly, but painfully.

Gwen noticed a crate by the water's edge and moved to inspect it, but my attention was fixed on the bodies.

My heart stopped when I saw it—the dark-colored shoe with the small white frill, clutched in one of the lifeless hands. Rose's shoe.

She had been here, but now she was gone. My knees buckled as a wave of grief and guilt crashed over me. "Are we too late...? She's... dead..."

Tears blurred my vision as I collapsed to the ground. "I promised to protect her, and now she's gone!" My fist slammed into the earth, my voice a raw shout, "No!"

Gwen stopped beside me, her gaze flicking to the shoe and the fragments of Rose’s dress scattered nearby. She took in the scene with growing realization, her eyes narrowing. "Hey... she might have escaped," she said, her voice softer now, though doubt still lingered in her tone.

I wiped away my tears. "What do you mean...?"

Gwen smiled. "Her body's not here. There's a chance she got out." She gave me a light punch on the shoulder. "Don't lose hope. You'll find her."

I forced a smile at Gwen's optimism, but it felt fragile, like it might shatter at any second. I slowly stood up, my knees trembling as the weight of everything hit me again. My breath was shaky as I exhaled, trying to push the grief aside. "Yeah... you're right," I muttered, but the words felt hollow. I let out a bitter laugh, then returned her gentle punch, the gesture more automatic than anything else. "Let's keep going."

Gwen led the way toward the faint glow, and I followed, the light growing stronger as we neared. It reflected off the uneven cave walls, casting long shadows around us, guiding us deeper into the cavern. As we rounded a bend, I recognized the place—it was the same cave where Rose and I had been before she was taken.

“Watch out!’ I put my arm out stopping Gwen before she fell into the hole I did upon entering.

        “I saw it..” She rolled her eyes and jumped over it

Rubert stood waiting, exactly where he said he would be.

"Ah, Sir! You’ve returned!" he called out, spotting us. "And it seems you’ve gained a new female companion."

I smiled. "Yes, I’m back, but we didn’t find Rose."

Rubert gave a low bow. "I am truly sorry. But I did see a human female who resembled her run out of this cave not too long ago. She only had rags left on her, poor thing."

My eyes widened. "You saw her!?"

Rubert stepped back slightly. "W-well, yes. Should I have stopped her?"

I looked up at the sky with relief. "No, no... it’s fine."

I lowered my gaze back to him. "Everything's alright now, friend!"

I turned to Gwen to share the news, but her expression was one of disbelief, as though watching someone talk to a horse they couldn’t hear.

"You sure are strange, Bushy."

I chuckled, feeling a bit self-conscious.

We rode back to the city on Rubert, the wind slicing against our skin and whipping through our hair, carrying the scent of damp earth and distant chimneys. The rhythmic pounding of his hooves echoed through the quiet stretches of road, each jolt jarring our weary bodies as we tried to process everything that had happened. As we neared the city, the distant hum of life swelled into a chaotic symphony—street vendors shouting their wares, the clatter of cart wheels on uneven stone, the occasional bray of a restless mule.

The moment we passed through the gates, an old man hurried toward us, his tattered cloak fluttering with his hurried steps. His eyes, wide and glistening with anticipation, darted over our faces as though searching for an answer before we could even speak. The sharp scent of ink and parchment clung to him, mixing with the faint tang of sweat, and his gnarled fingers twitched at his sides as though barely restraining the urgency that propelled him forward.

"Sir! Were you able to recover my family’s heirloom?"

My heart sank for a moment, anxiety pushing down on me, remembering how that had slipped my mind in the heat of everything. "I’m sorry, sir... all I found was this," I said, handing him Rinn’s golden knife. "I wasn’t sure if—"

Before I could finish, the old man’s face lit up with excitement. "Oh my great Entian! You’ve found it! This is it! Thank you, thank you!"

I breathed a sigh of relief, glad to know it was still something of importance. "I’m just happy we could help," I said with a chuckle, feeling the weight lift off my shoulders.

Just then, a kind-faced woman, likely his wife, approached us from a nearby stall. "Dear, is everything alright?" she asked, eyeing the golden knife.

The old man beamed and nodded enthusiastically. "Everything’s perfect! These fine folks recovered our family’s treasure."

The woman smiled at us, then turned to Gwen, noticing her weary state. "You look exhausted, dear. Why don’t you come with me? Our shop is just over there, and I can help you freshen up. We’ve got some food too—something warm to ease your travels."  the old lady pointed off somewhere into town.

Gwen shrugged, letting out a sigh. “Why not?” she said, her voice low and tired. Without waiting for another word, she followed the woman, the old man trailing behind them with a quiet smile, guiding her towards the direction they had pointed.

Suddenly, a voice interrupted my thoughts “He returned alive!” . It was Beans, alongside the Demon Knight.

"Impressive," she said, her eyes gleaming with admiration.

After an awkward chuckle in exchange they asked for me to explain what happened, so I did.

Beans chimed in, “I'm surprised you made it back alive!”

His comment stung, but I smiled. "When the old man told us that the Bard we locked up earlier had escaped—Rinn, no less!—and how he stole the family's magic dagger, we were going to send out a search party!" Beans exclaimed, his excitement palpable.

Confused, I asked, "What do you mean?"

Beans explained that Rinn had a reputation for killing those who stood in his way and that no one had really seen what he looked like since he would use magic to disguise himself. "Naturally, we didn’t want someone the king had an eye on to die," he added.

One of the knights scoffed. "That’s an understatement," he muttered. "The last person to cross Rinn was found in pieces—burned from the inside out like his own blood had turned to fire." Another knight shuddered. "I've heard he doesn’t even need a blade. Just a touch, and a man’s bones twist in on themselves like wet parchment."

“So, what happened to the princess's maid? Why is she not with you?” Beans asked, his voice hinting with worry.

Swallowing hard, I forced the words out. “She was taken,” I said, my voice tight. “By Rinn.” The weight of their stares pressed against me, suspicion creeping into their expressions. I could still see the moment she was dragged away, the terror in her wide eyes, the way her hands clawed at empty air as she vanished into the dark.

“She escaped somehow,” I added,

Bluma walked up, placing a hand on my shoulder. "Comrade," she said, tapping her chest. She pointed to a nearby inn, and we headed inside.

The inn was quaint and warm, the wooden floors creaking beneath our feet as the soft lighting cast a welcoming glow. Bluma arranged a room for me with a large bed and a tray of potions. Beans mentioned that he and Bluma wanted to talk later, but for now, I should rest.

I spent a few hours cleaning up, reflecting on everything that had transpired. My thoughts kept drifting back to Rose, a pang of guilt lingering. But at least she had survived, and that gave me some comfort. Wherever she was, I hoped she was safe.

CHAPTER 5                                                                                                                     Service Never Goes Unnoticed

Gwen’s View

I followed the old man and his wife through the lively streets, their easy pace a contrast to the bustle around us. The old man hummed a tune under his breath, while his wife smiled quietly beside him. The warmth of the cobblestones beneath my tattered boots felt oddly comforting. The smells of fresh bread and spices drifted through the air, mingling with the noise of the crowd—shouts, laughter, the clink of metal from the blacksmiths. I glanced around at the marketplace, the bright stalls and colorful fabrics catching my eye, but it all felt a bit distant.

“So... what kingdom is this?” I asked, still taking in the sights with little more than passing interest.

The old man turned to me, smiling warmly. “This is the Kingdom of Sumring! It's been standing since before the Frost Era. We’ve survived countless attacks, thanks to the Crowned Royal.”

I raised an eyebrow. “Crowned Royal? What’s that?”

He gave a quick chuckle, his eyes twinkling. “Ah, it's just a term we use to refer to the royal family line. The ones who’ve ruled us for generations—protecting the kingdom through thick and thin.”

I nodded, barely listening, already bored by the long-winded explanation. “Right... sounds like they’ve done their job. But where exactly are you taking me?”

“Oh, we’re heading to our shop,” the old man chuckled. “I’m the town’s blacksmith, and my wife here is the finest caretaker in the kingdom. We’ve served Sumring for years, crafting blades and tending to its people.”

The old man chuckled softly, then gestured to his wife with a proud smile. “This here is Nana, my better half.”

Nana, his wife, giggled and added, “I’m more of a healer and seamstress these days, but I still do what I can.”

Her laughter was warm, though it barely registered over the noise of the street. I gave a small smile at the way they seemed so at ease with each other.

As we walked, I thought about my worn-out sword and smirked. “I could use a new blade.”

The old man beamed with pride. “You’ve come to the right place! I’ve made weapons for the King’s knights. Some of my finest work. I’m sure I can find something just for you.”

When we reached the shop, the old man pushed open the door, and I stepped inside, immediately hit by the smell of iron and smoke. The air was thick with the warmth from the forge, and I could feel the heat radiating off the glowing coals. Swords, axes, and shields lined the walls, their polished surfaces gleaming in the flickering light. The hum of the forge’s steady rhythm, the rhythmic clang of metal on metal from the back, added a certain pulse to the atmosphere. The wood beneath my boots creaked slightly, the scent of burning wood mixing with the sharp tang of metal. It was a place of steady work and unspoken history.

“Impressive,” I muttered, my fingers tracing the hilt of a beautifully made sword.

“Thank you!” The old man’s face lit up. “Take a look around. I’ll be in the back getting my tools ready to fix your armor.”

Nana, who had been quietly watching me, stepped closer. She frowned at the dirt and grime covering me. “My dear, you look like you’ve been through a battle. Why don’t I help you get cleaned up while my husband works?”

I hesitated for a moment, the memory of past… discomfort rolling in but the thought of a bath was too tempting to resist. “Alright.” I said pushing the unease aside.

Nana led me to a small, cozy room at the back of the shop. She filled a tub with warm water and handed me a fresh set of towels. “You’ll feel much better after this. I’ll take care of your old clothes and get something new ready.” She then left the room.

I sank into the bath, letting the warmth ease the soreness in my muscles. I let the water eat away the layers of dirt and blood with some scrubbing, feeling lighter as the grime washed away.

After a while, Nana knocked gently on the door. “May I come in, dear?”

“One moment,” I called, stepping out of the bath and wrapping myself in a towel. I cracked the door open. “Yes?”

Nana smiled, handing me a set of new clothes. “I made these for you while you bathed. Your old ones were beyond repair.”

Surprised by the gesture, I took the clothes. “Thank you... you really didn’t have to.”

“It was no trouble,” Nana said with a dismissive wave of her hand. “I wanted to make sure you were comfortable.”

I dressed in the new outfit: a brown-gray cloth undershirt that hung to my mid-thighs, a sturdy chainmail shirt, and a steel corset fastened with leather straps with a red cloth tied around my waist. The fitted leather pants felt like a second skin, included with them were brown leather boots with a small heel, and hand braces that were well-crafted and durable.

Admiring the fit, I couldn’t shake the feeling that these clothes had been made just for me. The way they fit, the little details that seemed too perfect—it didn’t sit right. Maybe it was the kind of thing people do when they’re trying a little too hard to be accommodating. I wasn’t sure, but something about it felt off.

When I emerged, Nana beamed. “Oh, it fits you perfectly! Not too tight, I hope?”

“No, it’s great,” I chuckled. “Much better than what I had before.”

“I’m glad you like it. My husband’s in the workshop, probably done with your armor by now.”

I made my way downstairs, I made my way downstairs, the floorboards creaking underfoot, but it was the silence that really got to me. The closer I got to the heavy door of the workshop, the more something felt off. My skin prickled, the air felt thicker, like something was being hidden. Maybe I was overthinking it, but something didn’t add up.

Opening the door, I saw the old man hammering at an anvil, completely absorbed in his work.

“Hey, Grandpa!” I called, but the noise of metal drowned out my voice. After a few more attempts, he finally noticed me.

Turning with a smile, he said, “Oh, hello, dear! I just finished your armor, made a few upgrades, and crafted you a new sword!”

“Really? A new sword?” I asked, surprised.

He nodded and handed me the long sword. The leather-wrapped hilt fit perfectly in my hand, the blade gleaming and well-balanced. I swung it, amazed by its weightless feel. It was perfect.

“Incredible! I love it!” I said, grinning from ear to ear.

The old man’s face lit up. “I’m glad to hear it! Just need to add some finishing touches. It’ll be flawless when I’m done.”

I nodded, handing the sword back. He suggested I wait in the living room while he wrapped things up.

Wandering through the living room, I noticed a peculiar book on a shelf. The lettering along the spine caught my eye—I think it was in Elvish. Curious, I pulled it down and opened it, only to find the pages blackened and brittle. Each one crumbled at the lightest touch. Frowning, I tried another book. The same result—burnt and ruined.

My suspicion deepened. Why keep these charred books? Before I could dwell on it, Gramps entered with a proud smile, holding up the finished sword. Its sleek black blade seemed to hum with power.

“I call it the Fighter’s Spirit!” he announced, swinging the sword with practiced ease. “As the name suggests, it responds to the courage one has! The more courageous the lighter and bigger it may grow. However someone who is a coward will pull out a dagger that is hard to swing” he let out an amused laugh.

I hid my unease behind a smile. “It’s beautiful. Thank you.”

As I prepared to leave, Gramps stopped me with one last remark. “Oh, one more thing. That blade’s part of a set. The other belongs to a strong lady, much like yourself. If you find her, tell her Omar says hello.”

I raised an eyebrow but nodded. “Alright, will do,” I said with a soft laugh.

Stepping outside, I took a deep breath, the weight of the new sword resting comfortably on my back. I made my way through the busy streets, the encounter with Gramps lingering in my mind. Brushing off the unease, I soon spotted the leaf-head, standing near the entrance of an inn.

Deta’s View

I felt a tap on my back, “Hey Bushy. What are you up to?” I turned, recognizing Gwen’s voice, but her appearance caught me off guard. She looked strikingly different from the last time I saw her. Her once battered, grimy armor was replaced with clean clothes, and her thick, curly hair appeared vibrant.

“Gwen? Is that really you?” I asked, still taken aback.

She rolled her eyes, “Yes, it’s me, you Leaf Head!”

I chuckled at her response, but it came out more nervous than I intended. I tried to shake off the awkwardness, realizing I hadn’t recognized her right away. It was a bit embarrassing, but I hoped she wouldn’t notice.

“Well, I’m glad you’re looking better! You’re almost unrecognizable without all the dirt and blood.”

Gwen’s expression shifted, arms folding across her chest. “Rude,” she said, turning away.

I panicked, thinking I’d crossed a line. “Wait! I-That’s not what-”

She smiled, rolling her eyes. “I swear, Bushy... So, what are you up to?”

I gave a nervous grin and explained I was on the hunt for the Demon Knight and her partner, Beans.

“Beans?” Gwen tried to stifle a laugh, her shoulders shaking. “That’s... an unfortunate name.”

I stood there, puzzled as she kept giggling.

“What’s wrong with his name?” I asked, still not getting it.

Gwen patted my shoulder like I was a bit slow on the uptake. “Ah, Leaf Head. You’ll figure it out,” she said, walking ahead with a smirk playing at her lips. “You coming? I want to explore this new kingdom,” she called back, her smile both teasing and inviting.

I shook my head, still unsure why she found it so funny, but followed anyway. There was something about her that made me feel like I was missing the punchline.

Beans’ View

Bluma and I were walking up the castle tower, climbing the endless stairs. My legs burned with each step, my breath coming in ragged bursts as the weight of the climb wore on. I was starting to feel every inch of my dwarven frame—short legs and lack of stamina didn’t exactly make stair-climbing easy.

As I grew weary, Bluma hoisted me onto her back without a second thought. I didn’t protest; I was too tired to do anything but sigh in relief, grateful for the help. Carrying me was effortless for her, and I felt deeply grateful.

"Sorry, Bluma... I don't mean to be a burden," I said with a hint of regret.

Bluma kept walking but turned her head to me. "Good," she replied in a bright and cheerful tone.

After ascending a bit further, we reached the door we were searching for. Bluma set me down and pushed it open. The room stretched about thirty feet across, lined with tables and shelves crammed with scrolls and ancient scripts.

 A few chests brimming with documents sat in the corners, but they weren’t our concern; we had come to speak to the King's sorcerer, Burlog so that he could advise us on some sort of tracking spell. People had been disappearing from the kingdom lately, no clues, no mess, just gone. The princess being the most recent. If this keeps up the kingdom may fall before the change of season, for it won't take long before they choose to go after the King and Queen.

"Burlog," Bluma called, her voice clear and commanding, ensuring he knew we had arrived.

We scanned the room but saw no sign of him. Suddenly, something tumbled from the ceiling. I looked up, and a smile spread across my face. "Hello, Burlog!"

Burlog chuckled. He was sprawled out on the roof, some of his belongings spilling from his black robes. "Greetings, Squire Beans and Demon Knight!" he sighed, a grin crossing his face. "I attempted one of the scrolls... seems I might’ve read it wrong."

I let out a laugh. "Looks like it! How do we get you down?"

Burlog glanced around and pointed toward a potion on his desk. "Grab that bottle and toss it at me! It’s a dispelling potion!"

I picked up the potion and handed it to Bluma with a wide grin. "Here you go, my lady!" Bluma gave me a light pat on the head before throwing the potion at Burlog.

The bottle shattered against him, and he immediately began plummeting toward the floor. Bluma dashed forward, catching him before he hit the ground, and set him down gently.

"Oh, thank you! Forgot how to land," Burlog laughed.

 Burlog turned to Bluma. "So, How can I assist? I do have an order from the Queen but I'm sure I can make time for the kingdom's best knight."

I cleared my throat and spoke up. “Have you heard of the recent disappearances?”

Burlog let out a heavy sigh. “Yes. Very tragic. Those poor knights and soldiers…”

“I know, some were good friends of ours.” I hesitated before adding, “Thankfully the princess has returned.”

Burlog’s face brightened. “Ah, now that is good news! I was beginning to worry we had lost her too.” He shook his head, relief evident in his voice. “The kingdom needs her if something were to ever happen to her parents.”

Bluma gave a firm nod.

Before the moment could settle I got eager and asked, “Do you think you could whip up a tracking scroll for us?”

Burlog rolled his eyes as he turned to me with a flat expression. “You think magic is as easy as making bread, child?”  He sighed, rubbing his temples. “That said… it's not impossible. But it’ll take time.”

He then went to one of his cluttered shelves, bottles rolling and clinging together as he dug through it and pulled out a parchment. “That said, it won't do you much good without having a suspect to pin it on. However I think I have a pretty good idea as to who it is.” Burlog continued, " from what I’ve pieced together, I believe it could be Rinn, the Dark Elf."

Bluma wasn’t surprised to hear Rinn’s name and as Burlog went off into an explanation as to why, I surveyed the room. My gaze rested on what looked to be a Dwarven scroll with the seal of the Queen on it. Curious, I picked it up and scanned its contents. Why would the Queen put her seal on a Dwarvish scroll of all things? Why is it here in the first place?

Still absorbed in his explanation, Bluma glanced over at me with her four golden eyes, she too noticed the seal and the fact that it was Dwarvish. As she approached, she saw the color drain from my face as if I had seen a ghost. Before I could say anything, Burlog strode over and snatched the paper from my hands.

"Easy there, kid! We don’t need you floating to the ceiling too!" Burlog gave a nervous laugh.

I stared at him, seriousness in my eyes. "That wasn’t a spell, sir. It looked like a hit list..." I turned to Bluma, my voice trembling slightly. "It had the names of all the missing people, including the Royal knights and the princess!"

Bluma extended her hand toward Burlog, silently demanding the paper.

Burlog hesitated, his gaze fixed on me. "No, child. Keep your mouth shut," he muttered with a mix of annoyance and disdain. "The grown-ups are talking!"

Although his words stung, I pressed on. "Also, the list had the names of the remaining royal family, the other guards, and even... me--"

"Silence, child!" he bellowed, his voice echoing through the room.

I stepped back, my fists clenched, glaring at him. "I’m not a child! I’m a Dwarf!"

Burlog’s expression darkened, and his hand began to tremble, a deep, furious red light glowing from his palm. "Dwarfs and children are the same!" he sneered, his voice dripping with contempt. "Both filthy, worthless creatures!"

Burlog's rage intensified, and he began muttering incantations, preparing to unleash a devastating spell on me. Before he could finish, Bluma, sensing the danger, surged forward, grabbing his arm and flinging him across the room with a forceful throw.

Burlog slammed into the stone wall with a heavy thud, crumpling to the floor. Groaning, he pushed himself up, eyes blazing with fury. Bluma, standing protectively in front of me, had her great sword drawn, the light gleaming off its edge. Her expression was hard, her voice fierce.

"Squishy," she said, as though reminding me she would always protect me.

Burlog dusted off his tattered robe and let out a deep, frustrated sigh. "I am sick of being pushed around!" he shouted. "I should be the one in charge! I possess magic! I have the power of the Fallen One! The King is weak! Too soft! He doesn’t have what it takes to defend this kingdom!"

I glared at him, disgust welling up inside me. "You're nothing more than a madman obsessed with power!" I spat, my voice trembling with fury. "You’re willing to harm innocent people for your own selfish gain!"

Burlog’s eyes darkened with fury. He extended his hand, and the stone beneath Bluma’s feet shifted and twisted, transforming into a giant hand that grabbed her. Bluma, caught off guard, struggled to break free, but the enchanted stone held her in its unyielding grip. My heart sank as I watched her struggle.

"Bluma!" I screamed, terror gripping me.

Without thinking, I pulled out my hand ax, anger surging through me. I glared at Burlog, who wore a twisted smile.

"How dare you touch her!" I roared, my voice cracking with emotion as I hurled the ax with all my might.

The ax buried itself deep into his shoulder before he could react, a scream of pain tearing from his throat. Blood soaked his robes as he stumbled, summoning lightning to his remaining hand.

With fury burning in his eyes, Burlog swung at me, his hand crackling with electricity. I managed to dodge the first strike, but in my haste, I tripped and fell. Burlog saw his opportunity and grabbed me by the throat, lifting me off the ground. Pain surged through my body as he electrocuted me, my scream echoing through the chamber. My limbs went numb, and my vision blurred as I felt consciousness slipping away.

Just before everything went black, I saw Bluma. She had shattered the stone hand that held her and was charging at Burlog, her face a mask of pure rage. Burlog, sensing the imminent danger, conjured a fireball and hurled it toward her. The explosion was deafening, flames engulfing the room. He laughed, believing he had won.

But as the smoke cleared, his laughter died. Bluma was still standing, just inches from him, her sword raised high. With a single, powerful swing, she severed his remaining arm and one of his legs. Burlog’s scream was blood-curdling as he tumbled down the staircase, finally crashing at the bottom, unconscious.

Bluma, panting from exertion, rushed to my side. She cradled me carefully, checking my pulse, and breathed a sigh of relief when she felt it. Without wasting any time, she lifted me in her arms and carried me out of the room, heading down the stairs we had climbed earlier.

As she carried me, I drifted in and out of consciousness, slipping into a memory—one I hadn't thought about in years. The day Bluma and I first met.

Some Years Ago

I dreamt when I was just seventeen years old, dressed in shabby clothes with holes in my shirt and pants. I was working tirelessly in my family's field, which had become extremely tough and dry. It had been a rough year for us as the soil had lost its nourishment, but I refused to give up. Every day, I kept working with the hope that things would eventually improve. Later that day, my father called for me to come inside as we had some unexpected visitors.

"Coming, father!" I shouted, as I made my way back home.

I couldn't help but wonder who these visitors could be. We hadn't planned for anyone to come over. I shrugged and continued walking, my mind buzzing with curiosity.

As I entered the kitchen through the back door, I called out to my father in a loud voice, "Yes, Father?" I kicked the dirt off my shoes and made my way to the living room, eager to know who the unexpected visitors were. And there they were - Royal knights standing in the living room.

My father cleared his throat, his long black beard wobbling as he spoke. "Beans, sit down. The knights have something important to discuss with us."

I felt a wave of anxiety wash over me, fearing that they were going to draft us into some war. Were there any wars going on? No, I don't think so. Why are they here? I sat down on the chair next to a family picture, the warmth of the memory doing little to calm my nerves. I tried hard to contain my flatulence, an odd yet very real concern in the midst of everything else. The more I focused on it, the more difficult it became. It was like my body was staging a rebellion against my attempts to remain composed.

The knights exchanged glances and nodded in unison. "We thank you for your hospitality," spoke the first knight with a firm but amicable tone. "As emissaries of the king, we have been tasked with a special request for the nearby farms."

I was also intrigued by the knights' request and listened intently as my father asked for more details. "What might that request be?" he asked, his tone polite yet assertive. The knights were about to respond when the front door suddenly swung open, revealing my mother's arrival.

"Sorry I'm late, sweetheart!" she exclaimed, her voice bubbling with a mix of excitement and exhaustion. "The main district was so busy today, but I think I got the right tools for us to try…" She smiled, unaware of the knights in the room at first.

But as soon as her eyes landed on them, her expression shifted to one of shock. She gasped, her hands instinctively rising to cover her mouth in disbelief. "Oh my goodness, I'm so sorry!" she stammered, bowing slightly. "I didn't realize… What can I do to help?" She straightened up, her nerves kicking in, but she quickly composed herself.

The knights reassured her that there was no need for apologies and proceeded to explain their mission. They informed us that the King was hiring all the nearby farmers, as he knew they were having trouble with their crops. If they were to accept the king's offer, they would be paid fifty gold and given a fertility spell scroll to assist in the planting season.

My father, mother, and I were flabbergasted by the offer—and we accepted it on the spot, barely giving the guard time to finish.

The guard gave a tight shrug. “It’s simple work, mostly. One of the King’s top knights is looking for a successor. Word got out, and now we’ve got half the realm trying to cram through the gates.”

We followed his gaze to the distant swell of voices beyond the courtyard walls.

“They need help managing the crowd. Sorting names, keeping tempers down. Just for a few days.”

Simple enough. At least it sounded that way.

With excitement bubbling in my chest and a grin stretched across my face, we boarded the cart and made our way toward the inner kingdom walls. The road beneath us gave way to polished stone, and the fields turned to brick and bustling energy. I leaned over the side, eyes wide as towers pierced the sky like spears of gold.

As we drew closer, the kingdom unfolded before us in a blur of motion and color. People darted between wagons and tents, calling out over the clatter of wheels and the bark of orders. The air was thick with the scent of fresh bread, manure, and something metallic—maybe blood, maybe steel. Flags snapped in the wind above market stalls, and scaffolding creaked under the weight of hurried workers preparing for the surge of visitors.

I had never seen anything like it. Never imagined a place so alive. Our little farm felt like a faded dream in comparison, a quiet world of soil and silence traded for stone and noise and fire.

For the first four days, everything went surprisingly smoothly. My mother tended to injured contestants with a steady hand and kind words, while my father kept things running—checking rosters, smoothing disputes, directing traffic like he’d been doing it all his life.

I, on the other hand, was given the noble task of sweeping.

Which, honestly, I didn’t mind at all. The best part of the job was that I had a perfect view of the tryouts.

The Demon Knight herself stood at the center of it all, searching for a new apprentice. Each day, contestants stepped into the ring with fire in their eyes—fighters, spellcasters, strategists—each with their own plan to unseat her. The rules were simple: move her from her spot by any means.

But no one could.

She didn’t dodge. She didn’t block. She didn’t even flinch. And still, no matter how they came at her, none of them could make her take even a single step.

It was terrifying. And mesmerizing.

As I watched the fights, I couldn't help but feel fortunate to be there. I thought to myself, I'm so lucky to have come to the kingdom and witness the greatest knight of all time spar with people! Just look at her! The Demon Knight stopped someone's blade and threw them across the ring.

I smiled and sighed, "She's so cool…" My heart raced with excitement as I watched the thrilling battles unfold before me.

I was so enraptured that I didn’t notice as one of the king's knights approached me and interrupted my view.

"Hey, I know you're enjoying the fights, but an accident occurred in the preparation barracks. Could you clean it up?" he asked.

I nodded and replied, "Of course! I'll head there right away!" I then quickly made my way towards the preparation barracks, where one of the contestants had vomited after their fight with the Demon Knight.

Though I was not happy to clean it up, I did so anyway because I wanted to stay and watch more. As I cleaned, the other contestants laughed at me for my size and for being the one tasked with cleaning up the mess. However, I didn't let it bother me. I was just happy to be there.

Just as I was about to leave, one of the contestants shouted after me, “Hey, cleaning boy! Go fetch!” He laughed as he kicked a clump of dirt and bits of trash straight into the ring.

I sighed, gripping the broom tighter. Frustration bubbled up in my chest, but I swallowed it down. I wasn’t strong enough to stand up to him—and besides, I didn’t want trouble.

The Demon Knight, cheered on by the crowd, stood in the ring, waiting for her next challenger.

Muttering under my breath, I shuffled into the ring to sweep up the mess. “Every day it’s the same—sweep, sweep, sweep while they get all the glory…”

Thud.

I bumped into someone.

Then silence.

I blinked, confused, and glanced up.

The Demon Knight had staggered a half-step forward. She turned around slowly, her shadow falling over me. I stood there, broom still in hand, heart caught in my throat.

“I—oh, sorry,” I stammered, not yet realizing. “I’ll just clean this and get out of your way—”

Then I saw my parents, standing frozen at the far end of the ring, eyes wide with fear. My stomach dropped.

“Mom? Dad? What’s—”

That’s when I realized.

Somehow, without noticing, I had stepped fully into the ring.

I was standing face to face with the Demon Knight.

And the crowd had seen it, too.

Laughter erupted from the stands.

“A kid? They’re letting kids try out now?”

“He’s gonna die!”

“Get the mop outta here before she uses it to scrape him off her boots!”

I wanted to disappear. My legs locked in place. I’d seen what she could do—what she had done—and now I’d practically charged at her with a broom.

From the edge of the ring, several knights scrambled in alarm. I saw them start to run, armor clanking, faces pale with panic. They knew I wasn’t supposed to be there. They knew what might happen next.

I backed away, heart hammering, and bowed low in apology. “I—I’m so sorry! I didn’t mean to interrupt you! I’m just the cleaner!”

The Demon Knight stepped forward.

I flinched.

She crouched down, meeting me at eye level. Her piercing gaze scanned my face, quiet and unreadable. Then, without warning, she reached out and ruffled my hair.

“Squishy,” she said softly, like it was the most natural word in the world.

The crowd fell silent again.

And just like that, the fear melted off of me. A warm, tingling calm spread through my chest and down to my toes. I didn’t understand it—but I knew at that moment, she wasn’t going to hurt me.

She wasn’t angry.

She was... curious.

My parents hugged each other and shed tears of happiness, knowing that their son was going to have a prosperous life under the protection of the legendary Demon Knight. As she walked away pulling on my collar, dragging me off away from the ring.

Overwhelmed by the turn of events, I stuttered out a question: "Y-you chose... me?"

She nodded, her face unreadable. I felt a tear roll down my cheek, but quickly wiped it away.

"Could I... could I ask for your name?" I asked in a hushed tone.

The Demon Knight glanced around before whispering back, "Bluma." She patted my head gently before turning and walking away. I hesitated for a moment, then followed her into the hallway, excited for what was to come.

Present 

The memory faded as I opened my eyes to find myself back in the Barracks. Bluma was sitting beside me, sorting through a collection of potions. When she noticed I was awake, she gave me a small nod. "Awake?"

I chuckled softly. "Yeah, I’m awake." I glanced around the room, spotting the familiar photos on the bedside table—pictures of me and my parents, and one of Bluma and me after our first mission together.

"It’s hard to believe it’s been seven years," I said with a smile, feeling a swell of gratitude. "The best seven years of my life!"

Bluma looked away for a moment before nodding in agreement. "Rest," she said as she helped me lie back down and covered me with the blankets. I chuckled and reluctantly agreed. As I lay there, I still felt the same warm feeling that I always had whenever I was near Bluma. I never wanted this feeling to go away.

CHAPTER 6                                                                                                                          Some Love to Spare

Deta’s View

Gwen and I had made our way from the inn and already found the kingdom to be surprisingly peaceful and quaint. Despite the constant hum of voices and the steady clatter of footsteps on cobblestone, there was a gentle rhythm to everything—vendors calling out in friendly tones, laughter drifting from nearby alleys, the scent of fresh bread wafting through the air. Even the guards strolled more than marched. It was a city that breathed easy.

“I see a lot of humans around… but not many of the other races,” I said, slowing my pace as I glanced around. The crowds bustled past—faces flushed with laughter, arms full of goods—but almost all of them were human. It hadn't struck me before, but now that I was paying attention, the absence stood out like a missing color in a painting.

Gwen gave a quick roll of her eyes. "That's because this is a human kingdom. Most races stick with their own kind."

I nodded in agreement, trying to make sense of the place. "So, you’re comfortable here since you’re human, right?" Based on her appearance, I figured this was a safe assumption.

Gwen's expression shifted immediately. Her eyebrow arched, her words came out sharp. "What do you mean by that?"

I blinked, surprised by her reaction. "I mean, since you're human, and we’re in a human kingdom..." I trailed off, unsure of where I had gone wrong.

Gwen cut me off, her voice sharper now. "And what makes you think that?"

My mind raced, trying to figure out what I had missed. "I... I thought you were human. Aren’t you?"

She scrubbed her hands over her face and let out a sigh. "You know what, it doesn’t matter. Don’t label me, Bushy." With that, she turned and walked down a quieter street, away from the bustling crowd.

"Label? What did I do?" I muttered to myself, completely confused. But with no clear answer in sight, I sighed and followed after her, Alright, she did not like that. I will not bring it up again. But if she isn't human, what could she be?

The small street, narrow and slightly winding, led us into a quiet, residential neighborhood, where the houses stood close together, their gardens bursting with overgrown vines and bright flowers. The sound of laughter filled the air, punctuated by the rhythmic clash of the wooden swords as three children pretended to be brave knights, their faces flushed with excitement.

"Come back here!" one of them shouted, grinning from ear to ear.

"You will never catch me, hero! I am the Frost Lord!" The Frost Lord pretended to throw something and then the hero pulled some feathers from his pocket and tossed them into the air.

"Oh no! My body is frozen! What shall I do?" he said dramatically, pretending to faint.

I chuckled at their antics, curious to see what they would do next.

Gwen rolled her eyes “Let’s go,” she whispered, with a wave of her hand.

“Why? They look like they are having fun!” I responded whilst watching them continue to play.

 A little girl's voice suddenly caught my attention. "I will save you, hero!" she called out from atop a crate, wearing a bucket on her head. She jumped down with a stuffed animal that looked like a bear-bird hybrid and declared, "Get him!"

Throwing the toy at the Frost Lord, he caught it with a grin. "Oh no! The monster has got me! Ah!"

The little girl giggled as she removed her bucket and brushed away the feathers from the hero's feet. "Thank you, miss! Now let us defeat him!"

She beamed, "Yes! And be free from the cold!"

Together, they charged toward the Frost Lord, drawing their swords. The girl tapped him lightly on the arm, while the boy smacked him, causing him to cry out.

The Frost Lord started crying as the hero had hit him a bit too hard with his wooden sword. "Jacob!! That hurt!" he wailed, rubbing his eyes.

Jacob immediately dropped his sword and hugged the other boy. "Oh! Sorry, Aaron," he apologized.

         The little girl looked worried, her eyes wide and her grip tightening on her wooden sword as if it were a shield. I slowed my pace, trying not to startle her. I knelt down, lowering myself to her level. "Hey, are you alright, kid?" I asked, my voice gentle, hoping to bring some comfort.

They didn't answer, just stared at me with a mix of caution and uncertainty.

"Who are you?" Aaron asked, still sniffling.

Gwen stood nearby, crossing her arms and leaning against the wall. “Here we go..” She said in an unenthusiastic whisper.

Smiling, I introduced myself. "My name is Deta." I knelt and pressed my hand to the dirt, coaxing a flower to bloom. The children gasped—eyes wide, mouths parted. The little girl bounced on her heels, squealing, "Wow! He can do magic!" Jacob leaned in close, grinning ear to ear. I laughed, their wonder infectious.

Curious, I turned to Aaron and asked, "What's your name, kid?"

He hesitated before replying, "My name is Aaron."

"Nice to meet you, Aaron," I said with a smile. "Hey, could I see your arm for a moment?"

Aaron looked puzzled but held out his arm for me to inspect. I noticed a painful bruise forming where Jacob had hit him with the wooden sword.

"Ouch, that looks like it stings," I said, my voice full of sympathy. "Let me try something." I placed my hand over the bruise, closed my eyes, and focused on healing the injury. After a few moments, I removed my hand and smiled at Aaron.

"There, all better," I said softly, patting his arm.

Aaron glanced at his arm in amazement—the bruise was completely gone. "Wow, thank you!" Aaron exclaimed, grinning widely. The other children cheered in excitement, and I couldn't help but feel joyful seeing their smiles.

I smiled and said, "No problem!"

The little girl then turned her attention to Gwen, eyeing her sheathed sword. "Why do you have a sword, lady?"

Gwen looked at the small girl and replied, "Yes, I do. What's your name?"

The girl's face lit up as she answered, "I'm Sarah!"

Gwen sighed a little and said, "Nice to meet you, Sarah… Would you like to see the sword?"

         Sarah eagerly nodded and exclaimed, "Yes, please!"

Gwen knelt down and said, "Go ahead, draw it out."

Sarah grabbed the handle and pulled the longsword. "Wow, so cool!" she exclaimed, though quickly realizing it was too heavy for her to swing.

 "Careful, don't hurt yourself," Gwen cautioned.

She gently took the sword back from Sarah and sheathed it. "It’s dangerous, so we need to be careful," Gwen explained.

Sarah nodded in agreement. "Okay!"

Jacob picked up his wooden sword and eagerly said, "Hey! Can we fight?"

 A jolt of surprise sparked through me."You want to fight?"

He nodded enthusiastically.

I smiled "Um... all I have is this big stick, and you have that cool sword! I don't think I can win."

 Jacob grinned.

Aaron, noticing the situation, offered his wooden sword and said, "Here! You can use mine!"

I chuckled and thanked Aaron, taking the wooden sword from him.

Gwen pulled over a wooden box and sat down, saying with a wry smile, "This should be interesting." Sarah and Aaron sat next to her, their eyes gleaming with excitement.

 Jacob smiled and charged at me, swinging his wooden sword with all his might.

"Wow!" I dodged his attack, making him and the others laugh. He came at me again, and I blocked his strike.

"Wow! You're so strong!" he exclaimed.

I smiled, watching the way Jacob’s eyes lit up with determination. He laughed and shoved at me again, trying to push harder this time, like he really thought he could win. I let him think he might. There was something fun about pretending I was struggling—like I was part of his little game, not just humoring him. I stepped back a few paces, waiting until the last second before I jumped aside. He stumbled forward with a surprised yelp, and I couldn’t help but grin wider.

"Hey!" he laughed, while Aaron and Sarah giggled. Gwen let out a small sigh, but didn’t seem irritated.

Jacob yelled again and swung at me, missing by inches. I let out a mock scream and bolted, arms flailing as I ran in exaggerated circles around the yard. He chased after me, laughing between shouts of "Get back here!" while the others shrieked and cheered like it was the best game in the world.

I called out, "Ah! Run away!"

Sarah and Aaron were laughing as they watched, and they then asked if they could join in. Jacob agreed right away, and they all turned toward me, grinning.

"Uh oh. They are after me!" I giggled

They screamed and chased after me. I ran ahead of them and then turned around, lifting my arms. "Now I’m going to catch you!" I declared. They paused, giggling, before turning and running away, shrieking with laughter.

Sarah, being younger and a bit slower, began to panic, calling out, "Jacob, help!"

Jacob stopped and grabbed her hand, and they ran together.
