Charmed by their teamwork, I gave a soft chuckle but picked up my pace just enough to close the space between us. I hunched forward, and reached to gently touch Sarah’s hair making her jump and shout, "Ah! Faster!"

She let out a shriek and cried out to Jacob, “Ah! Faster!”

They didn't pick up the pace, but I pretended to slow down, letting them think they were outpacing me.

They ran to a box and clung to it, shouting, "Base! Base!"

I stopped and laughed. "Aw man, you win!"

We all laughed until a woman's voice called out, "Aaron, Jacob, Sarah! Time to come back!"

It sounded like their mother confirmed it when Jacob yelled, “Okay, Mom!”

Sarah echoed him a moment later, and the two of them hurried off together.

 Aaron stood up and thanked Gwen, which caught her a bit off guard—she hadn’t done anything. Not really. She blinked, unsure how to respond, unsure why anyone would be thanking her.

I called after him, "Hey, wait! You forgot something!"

         He turned around, saw his wooden sword, and ran back to grab it. "Thanks!" he shouted, before dashing off again.

I waved. "No problem! Bye, Aaron!" He smiled as he ran.

         Gwen stood up and remarked, "They liked you."

I turned to her, smiling. "Well, back home, I used to play with baby deer, and we’d do similar things."

Gwen raised an eyebrow. "You’re an odd one, I’ll give you that." She started walking, and I followed behind.

"Being weird is fun," I exclaimed.

She sighed, her tone dripping with doubt. "Uh huh. Sure."

Before I could reply, our attention was pulled toward a commotion in the distance. We saw a small, elderly woman frantically waving a giant pot around while yelling, "Whoa... whoa, careful... watch out!" The pot, somehow set loose, teetered and wobbled wildly across the cobblestones, barreled toward us, but Gwen swiftly extended her arm, grabbing the top of the pot to stop it in its tracks.

"Thank you," the old woman said, peeking out from behind the pot. She was a petite figure, barely four feet tall, with a large hair bun streaked with gray, white, and hints of brown. Her oversized glasses perched on her nose, and her simple clothing added to her modest appearance.

"No problem," Gwen replied, her eyes narrowing as she glanced at the cart stacked high with pottery, probably for her store brimming with large pottery. "Why isn't your husband helping you with all this?"

The old woman sighed deeply, a wave of sorrow passing over her features before she spoke. "He died many years ago from the plague…"

Gwen’s expression softened as she cast her eyes down. "I'm so sorry…" she murmured.

I stepped closer, offering my own condolences. "That must have been incredibly difficult for you…"

The woman nodded, her voice tinged with quiet grief. "Yes… my four boys were taken from me too… so I've been on my own for many, many years."

I hesitated, thinking how lonely that must’ve been—to lose her family. "Would you mind if we helped you?" I asked, hoping to offer more than just words.

The old woman’s eyes widened in surprise. "Oh no, I couldn’t ask that of you."

I chuckled gently and said, “No, really, it’s no trouble. We’d be happy to help, right, Gwen?” I turned to Gwen with a grin.

“Sure…” she replied, sounding less than enthusiastic.

The woman’s eyes filled with tears as she whispered, “Thank you. It means so much to this old lady.” She laughed softly, wiping her eyes.

I clapped my hands together. “Alright, let’s get these pots inside!”

Gwen’s View

As I moved toward the cart, I glanced back at the woman. “Why do you need so many pots?” I asked. It was a lot. Even for someone running a shop.

She smiled faintly. "This is how I make my living. I’ve never been good at heavy labor, but I’ve always been skilled with my hands." Then, with a small laugh, she added, “If my husband were still around, you could ask him.”

I gave a short nod. "Cool. So, where do you want this?"

I grabbed one of the taller pots—thing was almost as big as me—and followed her inside. It was a tight fit through the doorway, but I managed not to slam it into anything. The room was packed with pottery—bowls, plates, weird animal statues. “Quite the collection,” I said, mostly to say something.

She brightened up. "Yes, it’s what’s kept me going all these years. Could you place that one over there in the corner?" She pointed toward a spot near some other large pots.

I headed over and set it down carefully. Then I heard a click under the base. My brow creased. That wasn’t normal.

A faint sliding noise came from behind me, followed by a dull thunk. I turned. The floor had opened up. Of course it had. There was a box inside. And a note. Because nothing in this town could ever just be simple. “Naturally,” I muttered.

Deta came in right then, arms full of smaller pots. "Where do you want these, ma'am?" they asked, chipper as ever.

“By the fireplace, dear,” the old woman said. Then she noticed me lingering by the open floor. “Did something catch your eye, love?”

I shrugged. “Not really.”

She followed my gaze anyway, spotted the compartment, and crouched down to check it out. "What’s this now?" she mumbled, pulling out the box and the note.

"I don’t remember putting this here..." she murmured, brushing dust from the box. "My husband must’ve hidden it long ago." She unfolded the note, her eyes scanning it briefly. “It’s... a reminder to smile when things get hard,” she said quietly, her voice cracking. “He used to leave little notes like this everywhere.”

She turned it over in her hands, found the keyhole, and wound it up. The top popped open with a soft click, revealing a button inside.

Her face softened like she'd just stumbled across an old memory. "My late husband was a musician, you know. He played the Tubanarium." She motioned to a photo on the wall—some guy with a shiny bell-shaped instrument. "He used to play for the neighborhood kids. Our eldest, Philly, picked it up too. Traveled around. Sent letters for a while, then stopped when work got busy."

She took off her glasses and wiped her eyes.

I looked at the photo. There was something kind of nice about it, but I didn’t linger. “What’s your name?” I asked, keeping it casual.

She laughed quietly. "Oh, I’m sorry. I must be getting old. My name is Elewen, but everyone calls me Eve."

“Nice to meet you, Eve,” I said. “Looks like Bushy over there’s done hauling your stuff in.”

Deta’s View

Eve looked over, laughing at the sight of me with two pots comically stuck on my hands. I had been arranging the smaller pieces to resemble a goat. "Very creative," Eve said, her chuckling making me jump in surprise, which only made her laugh more.

"Thank you," I replied, grinning as I freed my hands. "I brought in the rest of your things, so you won’t need to worry about them."

Eve smiled warmly, patting my hand. When she let go, I felt something small in my palm. Opening my hand, I saw an amber-colored rock. Curious, I licked it, and my taste buds were hit with a mix of sweetness and savory flavor.

"It’s called a caramel drop," Eve explained with a chuckle. "You put it in your cheek and let it melt. Like this." She popped another one into her mouth, so I did the same.

My eyes widened with delight. "This is incredible!"

Eve beamed. "I’m glad you like it," she said, handing a few to Gwen as well.

As the evening drew closer, Eve glanced outside. "You two should get going—it’s starting to get dark." I looked at the sunset casting warm orange hues over the streets.

"Oh, it is late," I admitted.

Gwen rolled her eyes but turned to Eve with a smile. "It was a pleasure meeting you. I hope everything goes well."

Eve smiled back, mouthing the words "thank you" as she disappeared around the corner, she reached back and pushed the button on the music box. Soft, enchanting music filled the room—like something meant to linger long after she was gone. and soft, enchanting music filled the room.

Gwen and I stepped outside, savoring the caramel drops. "This caramel is amazing! How have I never heard of it before?" I exclaimed.

Gwen sighed. "You haven’t been out in the world much, have you?"

I shook my head. "Not really, but I have to bring some back home for Vomete!"

Gwen nodded, popping another caramel into her mouth. "Mm... yeah, this is good," she admitted.

"Told you!" I said, smiling. She rolled her eyes again but didn’t argue.

As we continued walking, something terrifying caught my eye. Approaching us at an alarming speed was a creature making strange noises.

"Mivomafisockmas, Mivomafisockmas!!" I screamed, instinctively taking a few steps back, and Gwen, seeing my panic, gripped the hilt of her sword and scanned our surroundings.

"What's wrong!?" she asked. I pointed at the approaching monster.

Gwen looked in the direction I pointed, then back at me, bursting into laughter. "You've got to be kidding me! You're scared of that thing?" She doubled over, still chuckling. "It's just a snail, Bushy. What’s so terrifying about it?" She sauntered over to the snail, picked it up, and pretended to fling it at my face. I let out a startled scream, stumbling backward and landing flat on the ground. Her laughter turned into wheezing as she clutched her sides. "Bushy, afraid of a snail? That's gold. What were you even trying to say?" She tossed the snail away with a laugh.

I brushed myself off, still feeling the sting of embarrassment. "Well… I said Mivomafisockmas, It is a phrase in my tongue…  but literally means comfort… I say it when I’m scared."

Gwen, still recovering from her laughter, apparently not listening. "Just a snail," she repeated, giggling. "That was priceless." She walked over and  playfully slapped my back. "Don’t worry, the terrifying creature has been vanquished!" Her laughter bubbled up again.

"Do you even know what snails eat? Worms, bugs, and greens! And I’m practically made of greens!"

As her laughter died down, she gave me a teasing smile. "It was just a tiny snail. Do you honestly think it could kill you?"

"Yes!" I replied, dead serious.

Gwen chuckled and shook her head. "Alright, alright. Don’t get your vines in a knot." She added, "I’ll be your fearless protector from the evil snails, Bushy," with another laugh.

I sighed, shaking my head. "Thanks, I guess."

Still chuckling, we continued our walk as the day wound down. The streets grew quieter as children headed home, and shopkeepers locked up for the night. The night guards began their shifts as the large, full moon rose over the horizon, illuminating the kingdom in soft, silvery light. The stars twinkled overhead, and knights lit pedestals along the inner walls and paths, casting a warm, orange glow.

Looking up at the night sky, I felt a wave of homesickness wash over me. Back home, Vomete and I would take evening walks, and she’d tell me all about the stars—their origins, meanings, and the stories they held. Those moments were always magical. Gwen, too, found herself lost in the beauty of the starry sky. It had been so long since she’d taken a moment to admire it. Her quiet contemplation, however, was interrupted by a low-hanging sign that smacked her right in the face.

"Ow!" she yelped, rubbing her forehead. "Stupid sign!"

I couldn’t help but laugh. "Sorry about that, Gwen. I don’t think the sign knew it was in your way."

Gwen glared at me, her voice dripping with sarcasm. "Haha, very funny." She kept walking, still rubbing her head.

I grinned. "Come on, you have to admit it was a little funny." But as I continued to laugh, I tripped over another sign lying on the ground.

Gwen chuckled. "Yeah, I guess it is a little funny."

After dusting myself off again, we continued walking until we found ourselves standing in front of a place called The Boiling Potion, nestled between the outer gates of the kingdom and some sort of an animal shop. Lively chatter and bursts of laughter poured out of the building, and I couldn’t help but wonder why humans always seemed so loud. Didn’t they enjoy peace and quiet? They were constantly talking over one another.

Curious, I studied the sign hanging outside the door, which displayed the name of the establishment in several different languages. "The Boiling… Potion?" I asked, puzzled. "Is this some kind of… shop?"

Gwen's face lit up in excitement. "No, it’s a tavern!" she declared, clearly eager to get inside. Without waiting for me, she strode through the front doors, fully ready to immerse herself in the lively atmosphere within.

CHAPTER 7                                                                                                                Drunken Promise

Bluma’s View

I left the barracks and made my way to the upper district, where preparations for Liberty Day were well underway. The streets buzzed with energy as the citizens set up decorations, and colorful banners fluttered in the breeze. For over a thousand years—exactly one thousand one hundred eleven, to be precise—the people had celebrated this day with joy. It served as a reminder of the challenges their ancestors faced during the Frost Era, a time of great hardship, and the hope and abundance they now enjoyed in a land filled with life and light.

As I walked, I came across the Kingdom's oldest building: The Leaping Lantern. I stepped inside to find that it still retained its Frost Era charm. The walls, carved from a natural cave, gave the place a rugged feel, while the floor and ceiling were covered with wooden beams. Some floorboards had broken over time, exposing thick wool insulation beneath them, a reminder of the days when keeping warmth in and the cold out was a matter of survival.

The moment I entered, the tavern fell silent. All eyes were on me, the Demon Knight, a figure known throughout the land. I moved with quiet purpose, and the patrons watched her with a mix of curiosity and caution. I took a seat in a corner booth, my gaze sweeping the room. A simple wave of my hand was all it took for the crowd to return to their conversations, though they kept their voices low and their eyes alert.

Moments later, Deta’s companion burst through the doors, with Deta trailing behind.

Deta’s View

"Ah, this looks like a place to fight!" Gwen declared with a grin, her voice brimming with excitement.

I sighed, already anticipating the trouble. "Come on, Gwen, we already got kicked out of the last place because you started a fight. We didn’t even get to sit down!"

She rolled her eyes, clearly unbothered. "So what? That fight was glorious!"

Shaking my head in disbelief, I noticed the Demon Knight sitting quietly at the back of the room. "Gwen, let's sit over there," I said, gesturing toward the empty seats at Bluma’s table. I grabbed her hand and led the way, dragging Gwen along.

"Hey, Demon Knight, mind if we join you?" I asked politely, hoping Bluma wouldn't object to our company.

A few tavern patrons turned to see how this encounter would play out. Bluma seemed to study us for a moment, then nodded, motioning to the empty seats at her table. I smiled in gratitude and plopped into one of the chairs, with Gwen following close behind.

Gwen leaned in toward Bluma, her eyes alight with interest. "You look like a warrior! What’s your name?" she asked, grinning eagerly.

Bluma’s four eyes narrowed as she sized Gwen up, her silence speaking volumes before she finally replied, "Bluma."

Gwen’s grin widened. "Bluma, huh? Well, Bluma, how about a spar? I’d love to see which one of us is stronger!" she challenged, her voice full of enthusiasm.

Bluma simply stared at Gwen, not offering a response. An awkward silence stretched between them until someone approached our table. Before I could speak, Gwen piped up, "We’ll take three of your strongest and largest drinks!" She tossed two gold coins onto the table, and the waiter nodded before hurrying away.

I blinked, confused. "Gwen? What did you just give her?"

Gwen turned to me, incredulous. "Are you serious? How dumb are you, Randeths? That was gold! I gave her money, and in return, she’ll bring us drinks. What do you even use as currency if you've never used gold before?"

I smiled nervously. "Um… I’ve never actually paid for anything before. Vomete and I live on our own, so we just take care of ourselves." I realized she must have taken some of the golden circles from the cavern when I wasn't looking.

Gwen stared at me, her disbelief evident. "Seriously!? Wow, that sounds amazing—living out in the woods with nothing to worry about." She laughed, clearly enjoying the idea, even though I knew the reality wasn’t quite so carefree.

Before I could explain further, the person returned with three large wooden mugs filled with a pungent liquid that made my nose wrinkle. "What is this?" I asked, eyeing the drinks warily.

Bluma turned toward me, her voice low. "Alcohol," she replied simply, before turning her attention back to Gwen.

Gwen, unconcerned, began chugging her drink without hesitation. I hesitated for a moment before taking a cautious sip of my own.

"So, Bluma, right?" I asked, setting my mug down and trying to steer the conversation in a more productive direction. "I think I mentioned a few days ago that the king has tasked me with forming a group to hunt down a creature in the castle’s dungeons. I was hoping to ask if you and Beans would consider helping us out?"

Bluma didn’t immediately respond. She studied me for a moment before her gaze drifted to the window, lost in thought. Just as I was about to speak again, Gwen slammed her empty mug onto the table with a loud thud, the sound cutting through the tavern’s din. Her face was flushed from the drink, a lopsided grin creeping across her lips. She leaned heavily toward me, her arm wrapping around my shoulders before I could react, her finger poking insistently at my side.

"Gwen!?" I stammered, startled by her sudden burst of energy.

Her laughter spilled out, light and unsteady. "Oh, lighten up, Bushy!" she said between hiccups, her words slurring slightly as she gave me another poke. "You're so stiff." Her finger jabbed again, and she giggled, the hiccup that followed making her laugh harder. "C'mon, let’s have some fun!"

Before I could form a response, Gwen pushed herself to her feet. She swayed for a moment, catching her balance with a giggle before her eyes locked on the empty stage across the room. The tavern bustled with life, but Gwen’s focus was unwavering. With a reckless grin, she staggered her way to the stage, her movements unsteady but full of purpose.

I watched, frozen, as she turned to face the crowd. My heart sank as she cupped her hands around her mouth and shouted, "Hey, you lot! Does anyone here know how to play!?"

For a moment, the tavern seemed to pause, heads turning to her. A low groan escaped my throat as I lowered my head into my hands. Oh no. Not this again. Hopefully no one will respond. From the table next to us, a man stood up, his grin as wide as Gwen’s.

"Why yes, madam, we do!" he called, motioning to his group—a mix of elves and orcs who looked all too eager to join her. Slowly, they rose, gathering their instruments as the anticipation in the room grew.

Gwen’s eyes sparkled with excitement. "Alright! Get up here, and let's make some noise!" she called, clapping her hands together.

One by one, the musicians joined her on stage, tuning their instruments and testing strings as the rest of the tavern watched. A rhythmic beat filled the air, starting slow but quickly picking up speed. The lively music began to swirl through the room, drawing attention as feet tapped and heads bobbed in time.

Then, to my shock, Gwen opened her mouth and began to sing. Her voice, clear and strong, filled the space, commanding everyone’s attention. For a moment, I forgot the anxiety bubbling in my chest. I just stared at her, her energy infectious, the music wrapping around the room like magic.

Despite everything, I couldn’t help but smile. Gwen's voice was absolutely captivating as she sang with passion and intensity, drawing the attention of everyone in the tavern. Her melodic voice filled the space, and the musicians supporting her only enhanced the enchanting atmosphere. It was as if time had slowed to a crawl, and everyone in the room was entranced by the mesmerizing music echoing from the stage, joining in with her.

I smiled and let out a soft laugh, "Huh... that didn’t go as I expected. That's a good thing!" I chuckled and turned to Bluma, but she was nowhere in sight. Her cup sat empty, and her sword rested on the table before me. Puzzled, I glanced around the tavern, searching for her but without any luck. Letting out a sigh, I picked up her sword and studied it for a moment before turning back to the stage.

We spent several hours at the tavern, enjoying the music and the lively company of the other patrons. As the night wore on, Gwen drank more and more of the alcohol, leaving her barely able to stand by the time we decided to leave. The darkness outside made me decide to walk her back to the inn across town, Bluma's sword still in my hands.

When we arrived, Gwen tried to convince the innkeeper for more alcohol, but I quickly intervened. We managed to secure a room, and I encouraged Gwen to go in so we could rest for the night.

"Fine... you're not my dad!" she blurted out, and I couldn't help but smile awkwardly, hoping not to disturb the other guests.

"Okay, I'm not your dad, but it's time for bed," I replied, hoping she'd listen.

She groaned and muttered, "Alright, alright, don’t be such a stick in the mud, Vine Hair!" before stumbling into the room. She collapsed on the bed and instantly fell asleep.

I exhaled a sigh and began preparing for bed myself when I noticed Gwen was still strapped with her sword and carrying her bags. She probably doesn’t want those ruined, I thought, surveying the room. I carefully removed her bags and sword, but as soon as I touched the weapon, she punched me square in the face. I stumbled back, quickly realizing she was still sound asleep.

"Great... that’s not fun," I mumbled, rubbing my sore cheek. Eventually, I managed to take off her gear, giving her sword a closer look as I did so. "I wonder what her blade looks like?" I mused, holding Bluma's long sword next to Gwen's shorter one. "They're about the same size," I concluded before setting them aside and finally crawling into my own bed.

As I drifted off to sleep, my mind slipped into a vivid dream. I saw my home, and there in the garden, Vomete stood alone. Suddenly, she looked toward the sky, appearing much younger, and then hurried inside. At that moment, a beam of light pierced through the sky, and a radiant entity descended from it. The being spoke, but Vomete couldn't understand its words. She asked, "What do you want from me?" The entity handed her a wrapped object and stroked it tenderly before vanishing.

"Vomete... What just happened? How did it know your name?" I called out, but there was no reply. As I tried to move closer, my body became painfully sluggish. I tripped and plunged into a pit, screaming for Vomete's help as my vision faded to black. I woke abruptly, sitting upright.

"What... was that?" I asked aloud, my heart racing. Is Vomete okay? Was it real or just a nightmare? Shaking off the lingering thoughts, I got up and headed to the nearby washroom, splashing cold water on my face.

Returning to the room, I saw Gwen still sound asleep. A smile tugged at my lips as I sat by the window. A familiar surge of energy coursed through me, and my vine-like hair sprouted fresh green leaves. "Ah... that’s better," I whispered contentedly. A rustling noise grabbed my attention, and I turned to see Gwen sitting up with her hair in disarray.

"Morning, sleepyhead," I teased.

Gwen yawned, "Morning..." before shuffling to the washroom.

After some time, we both finished preparing for the day. At the counter, the innkeeper greeted us with a smile as I settled the bill. "Hope you both slept well!" he said.

I smiled back and replied, "The bed was perfect! Thanks so much!"

Gwen, nibbling on an apple, rolled her eyes and muttered, "It was fine..." The innkeeper chuckled, and we went on our way. Stepping outside, Gwen eyed the sword in my hand. "When did you get a sword, Bushy?" she asked.

I paused, confused, then quickly remembered. "Oh, right! Bluma left it with us last night, and I figured we should return it," I explained.

Gwen examined the black metal and commented, "She must be pretty skilled to carry this. If it meant that much to her, she wouldn’t have left it behind."

I glanced at Gwen and said, "Hey! It was probably just an accident. Let’s just get it back to her, alright?"

Gwen sighed but agreed, "Fine. But do you even know where she is?"

That’s when I realized my mistake. "Um... no, but we can ask someone!" I suggested scanning the area.

I spotted a knight nearby and politely asked, "Excuse me, do you know where we might find the Demon Knight?"

The knight turned, his hand resting on his sword cautiously. "Why do you ask?" he questioned.

Offering a warm smile, I began explaining, "She accidentally left one of her swords with us, so..."

The knight raised his hand, cutting me off. "You’re her friends? In that case, you’ll find her at the Barracks near the castle gate. Her shift starts soon."

Grateful, I thanked him and led Gwen toward the Barracks. Once inside, we navigated through a sea of knights preparing for the day. After a short search, we found a door with both Bluma and Beans’ names etched into it. "Looks like we found them!" I said with relief.

Beans opened the door, his expression one of mild surprise. "Hey, you two. Something up?" he asked.

I held up Bluma's sword with a grin. "She left this with us last night, and..." Before I could finish, Bean grabbed us by the wrists and quickly ushered us inside, closing the door behind us.

"Bluma gave you her sword?" he exclaimed, shocked. "What did you say to her?" His sudden concern was strange, but I explained our conversation from the previous night, and his tension eased. He smiled and said, "Oh! That means she accepted. We'd be happy to help you both out!"

At that moment, Bluma entered, and her eyes fell on the three of us. She glanced at Beans, who nodded. Without a word, Bluma took her sword, sheathed it, and gestured for us to follow her outside.

Bluma led us out of the room with Beans trailing behind. I exchanged a glance with Gwen, who just rolled her eyes. After a short walk, we found ourselves in an open field outside the kingdom walls. I scanned the surroundings, noticing the distant forest and a portal a few miles away.

"We're pretty far from the kingdom..." I observed, looking over at Bluma. "What’s going on?"

Bluma took a few more steps forward, turning to face us as she drew her sword. Gwen smirked, pulling out her massive greatsword, which seemed impossibly large for its sheath.

I stared in disbelief, "How did that even fit in there?"

Gwen shot back, "Questions later!"

Bean interjected, explaining, "Bluma wants to join you, but first, she needs to test your skills."

Gwen's eyes gleamed with excitement as she responded, "So, it’s a sparring match. Let’s dance."

I sighed, shaking my head as I readied myself. "Why does everything have to end in a fight?"

Gwen launched the first attack, swinging her sword at Bluma, who deftly blocked it with two blades that appeared from thin air. I attempted to disarm her, but Bluma swiftly evaded by leaping backward. Gwen wasted no time charging again, determination in her eyes.

"Hold still!" Gwen yelled.

Bluma parried, but her armor wasn’t enough to withstand Gwen’s relentless strikes. The greatsword cut through a small section of Bluma’s armor, causing her to grimace as it bit into her arm. Beans, watching from the sidelines, took a step back as Gwen's strike landed.

"Uh oh..." Bean whispered as Bluma’s eyes began to glow faintly.

In an instant, she flung her sword aside and unleashed a rapid flurry of blows with her dual blades, hitting Gwen multiple times in quick succession. I rushed in to intervene, swinging my staff toward Bluma, but she ducked and dodged my attack effortlessly.

"Bad move," Gwen muttered as she steadied herself.

Raising her sword, she landed another hit on Bluma’s back, slicing through her armor once more. Bluma retaliated, striking Gwen’s knee, causing her to fall to the ground. Realizing she was outmatched, Gwen sat back, breathing heavily.

Bluma turned her attention to me. I took a deep breath, feeling my anger swell at seeing Gwen hurt. Roots and vines erupted from the ground at my command, attempting to snare Bluma. However, she broke free, her strength too much for the plants to hold. The brief distraction allowed me to close the gap between us.

I exhaled a cloud of green poisonous mist, blurring Bluma’s vision and disrupting her balance. Seizing the moment, I lunged with my dagger, but Bluma quickly grabbed my arm and tossed me to the ground. Before I could react, I felt the cold edge of her sword against my neck—a clear sign of defeat. Bluma sheathed her sword and collapsed, overcome by the effects of the poison.

"Bluma!" Beans cried out, rushing to her side.

Mustering my strength, I sat up and crawled over to her. Extending my glowing hand, I began to heal her wounds.

Beans looked on in amazement. "How... how are you doing that?" he asked, tears forming in his eyes.

I smiled, my hand still hovering over Bluma’s arm as the last of her wounds began to close. "It’s a trick I learned from my Vomete when I was younger."

Bluma looked at her arm in awe before pulling Beans into a one-armed hug.

I went to help Gwen, but she pulled away, her eyes wide with a mix of panic and desperation. "Gwen, seriously! Let me help," I said, reaching out.

She scooted further away, shaking her head fiercely. “No,” she whispered, her voice tight. Her chest was rising and falling faster than normal, her hands trembling. My patience was thinning, and the last remnants of my energy were slipping away. I summoned vines, their roots snaking across the ground to hold her in place.

"Hey! That’s cheating!" Gwen gasped, her voice cracking as she thrashed against the constricting vines.

I wasn’t going to let her wiggle out of this "Stop moving!" I growled, stretching my hand to heal her arm. But no matter how much I reached, she kept shifting, her body stiff with a tension as if she was trying to flee, almost as if there was fear in her movements.

“Just hold still!” I shouted, frustration making my voice sharp. Gripping her arm, I pressed my palm against the injury, but the touch sent a visible shudder through her. Her breath caught, and I could feel her body trembling beneath my hand, like she was resisting every inch of contact.

It felt like her entire body was bracing against an old, instinctive fear, one that she couldn’t outrun. But the wound was healing, slow and steady, despite her protests.

The second I let go, Gwen’s fist collided with my chest. The force of the punch knocked me backward, and her words hit harder than anything else. “I told you not to touch me!” she yelled, her voice raw with something I couldn’t quite place. She turned her back on me, her shoulders stiff, her posture taut as if she was waiting for the next blow, real or imagined.

I stayed silent, too exhausted to defend myself. When she glanced over her shoulder, I was already crumpled on the ground, my energy completely drained. The world dimmed as Gwen’s voice, soft but filled with an unspoken weight, called my name from far away. “Don’t—” I couldn't respond. Everything faded to black.

CHAPTER 8                                                                                                                     Surface Secrets

When I awoke, I could not recall the end of our fight with Bluma, and was lying in a strange room—quiet, unfamiliar, and just roomy enough for two. A window let in the amber light of sunset, and a small bookcase stood off to the side, filled with little of interest. As I sat up, I noticed something more pressing: my belongings were gone.

There hadn’t been much in the room to begin with. "Where could they be?" I muttered, eyes sweeping the space. After a moment, I spotted them—bundled neatly and set off to the side, as if someone had taken care to keep them together. "How odd…" I knelt beside the bundle, untying it carefully. One by one, I returned each item to its place—clothes, tools, notes—everything accounted for. Once I was fully packed, a quiet sense of readiness settled over me.

I stepped out into a long stone hallway, the walls cool and uneven beneath the glow of wall-mounted torches. A distant noise—something like laughter—echoed faintly in the air. “They’re louder than I’m used to,” I muttered under my breath, trying not to flinch at the echoes.

As I walked down the hallway, it led me to a balcony that overlooked a bustling dining hall. There, I spotted Bluma, Beans, and Gwen seated at a table, enjoying their meal.

"Hey guys!" I called, raising a hand. They turned toward me—Beans beamed, Gwen looked away. I smiled and added, “I’ll be right down!”

My eyes landed on a narrow staircase to my left. I moved toward it, voice lifting, “After this, we need to let the king know we’re ready—”

But as I turned the corner at the bottom of the stairs, I stopped short. The king was standing right there, facing me.

He wore a broad smile and laughed warmly. "Glad to hear it, Deta!" he said with enthusiasm. "Your comrades have shared their stories with me and told me they're now part of your team, ready to face the monster below! It's wonderful to confirm it directly!"

The King patted my back and led me to the table. My mind wandered to what my companions might have shared in my absence. Sitting next to Bluma, I noticed Beans and Gwen were across from us. Beans looked relieved, grinning like nothing had gone wrong. Gwen didn’t meet my eyes. I wasn’t sure why—something was off—but I figured I’d ask her about it later.

The King studied me for a moment, expression unreadable. “Perhaps you're unaware, Deta, but tomorrow marks the grand festival of Liberty! It's a joyous occasion, and I'd like to extend a personal invitation for the four of you to be my special guests!"

Bluma and Beans exchanged uncertain glances

The King quickly picked up on it. "Bluma, as the Queen's trusted knight, I know your duty and that of your squire. However, this time, I'd be delighted if you joined us not as a knight, but as yourself.”

Bluma nodded, and Beans couldn't hold back his excitement. "Thank you so much, your highness! This is going to be so exciting!"

Gwen, however, remained quiet, arms crossed and gaze fixed on the floor, though her jaw was tight—like she was biting back words.

Grateful, I said, "Thank you, sire!" The King chuckled softly. "Of course! Now, enjoy your day and prepare for the festivities!"

Beans and Bluma were the first to leave, with Beans dashing off and Bluma chasing after him. Gwen stood and left the room quietly. Concerned, I quickly got up and called after her, waving my hand in hopes of getting her attention.

"Gwen, wait up!"

King’s View

As they left, my wife appeared around the corner, expressing her concern, "Darling, are you sure it's wise to invite strangers to this event? For all we know, he could still be a spy from the kingdom of Mt. Tarifa..."

I gave a small smile and held her close, reassuring her, "It’s fine, my dear. The kingdom of Mt. Tarifa won’t be a threat to us. I’ll make sure of it." I cupped my wife's face and kissed her, saying, "I love you, my Sundrop."

My love then smiled and replied, "I love you too my Moonbeam."

Just then, a knight entered to inform me that my presence was needed in the courtroom. With a sigh, I bid my dear a temporary farewell. “I shall see you tonight my love, tell Maggie I will tuck her in tonight”

My wife grinned, a spark of mischief in her eyes. “I’ll let Margret know…” she said, her voice just a shade too cheerful.

Deta’s View

"Gwen!" I called out, grabbing her shoulder to stop her. By then, we had reached the main plaza. "What's going on...? You're acting… weird."

She shrugged my hand off and resumed walking, saying, "I'll be fine, Deta. Just leave it." With a quick wave, she disappeared into the crowd. I stood there, feeling unsure of what to do next. Not wanting to be in anyone's way, I decided to take a walk.

Lost in thought, I soon found myself outside the city walls, strolling along a wooden picket fence. I let out a deep sigh, wondering, "Did I do something wrong?" I absent-mindedly let my hand trail above the fence as I walked.

"Maybe she's just having a rough day," I mused. That’s when I noticed a Dwarf in a nearby field, his black beard bushy and full. He was tilling the soil, probably preparing the seeds for planting.

I called out to him, "Hey there! Need some help?"

The Dwarf looked up with a grin and replied. “That would be a big help! Hop over the fence, and I’ll grab you a garden hoe."

I followed his instruction and eyed the fence warily—it creaked under my weight as I vaulted over, but held. I landed with a heavy thud and walked toward where he was working, trying not to leave deep footprints in the soil.

"So, what’s your name, kid?" he asked with a hearty laugh.

I chuckled and answered, "You can call me Deta."

The Dwarf raised an eyebrow, intrigued. "Deta? Are your parents ‘Detations’?"

I shook my head. "Not that I know of. What’s a Detation?"

The Dwarf chuckled and explained, "Oh, it's a popular religion. I’m not religious myself, but they're good folk. There are quite a few of them around here, but they’re some of the finest people you’ll meet—always willing to lend a hand."

I smiled, pleased. "That’s nice to hear! Oh, I didn’t catch your name!"

The Dwarf laughed again, "Right, call me, Veir!"

We kept talking as we made our way across the field toward his barn, which sat a good hundred paces off, its roof half-swallowed by ivy. Our conversation drifted from tools to weather to the last time someone got kicked by a mule—Veir had a knack for spinning simple stories into something worth laughing at. Inside the barn, he handed me a spare hoe from the corner. We’d just stepped back into the sunlight when a sharp female voice called out from behind us.

 "Now where do you think you’re going?" they said in an expectant tone.

Veir turned around quickly and exclaimed, "Ah, my dearest! This young man has kindly offered to help me in the field!"

I turned to see a female Dwarf with blonde hair tied in a messy bun. She wore a plain dress and a brown apron, both showing signs of wear. She looked at me and asked, “What’s your name, dear?”

I smiled and replied, "Oh, I’m Deta, ma’am!"

She returned my smile and said, "That’s a sweet name. Thank you for helping my husband. I’ll bring out something for both of you to drink soon. Now, off to work, you two!"

Her kindness warmed my heart, and Veir chuckled, "You heard her!"

On our way back to the field, Veir proudly mentioned, "My family’s owned this land for generations, long before the kingdom was even founded, back before the Frost era!"

Intrigued, I asked, "What’s the Frost era?"

Veir almost tripped when he heard my question. "Your parents never taught you? What were you raised in a forest or something?"

I laughed and replied, "Actually, yes, to both."

He shook his head, then looked at me with curiosity. "So, what species are you, anyway?"

I waved my hand and said, "I'm a Randeth!"

Veir looked at me, astonished. "A Randeth!? Seriously?" He threw his hoe in surprise. "Then why did you make us fetch these tools? Use your magic, boy!"

I chuckled and sat down on the ground. “That's a strange response…” I wondered aloud. “Aren't Randeths supposed to be a myth to people?"

Placing my hands in the dirt, I began to converse with the earth in my native tongue. "Flu shetiiuyuta bogofluuta tiishuti, tiflusitmas: Flu mivomamashuti bogorg cn masgansitme shuti shetemivomate finapamasflutiite."

As the words left my lips, the soil beneath us began to stir. At first, it was subtle—a faint tremor. Then, the earth shifted, its color deepening from a light brown to a rich, dark shade. I watched as the once hard-packed ground softened, becoming looser with each passing moment. Veir’s eyes lit up with excitement, and he crouched down, running his fingers through the now pliable soil.

A wide smile spread across his face, his joy unmistakable as the earth yielded to my touch.  "Impressive! But what did you say? Was that Randeth speech?" He tilted his head, one brow raised, waiting for my answer.

I chuckled and nodded, "Yes! That was my native language! But all I did was make the dirt healthier."

Veir nodded in understanding. "Oh, right! Randeths have the ability to command the earth and make it more fertile for life to grow!"

I was genuinely surprised by how much he knew about my abilities. "If you don't mind me asking, how do you know so much about Randeths? Most people think we're fictional, let alone know about our magic."

Veir laughed heartily and replied, "Oh, my boy, you're not the first Randeth I've encountered! Although it was many years ago, it didn't immediately click with me!"

My excitement grew. "May I ask if the Randeth you met was named Vomete?"

Veir took a moment to think and responded, "Erm... I'm not quite sure. As I said, it has been a few hundred years, so the details are a bit hazy." He shrugged, uncertain of any further information.

Nonetheless, I was glad to have found someone who knew Randeths were real. "Well, should we put these tools away?" I suggested picking up my hoe and getting up from the ground.

"That sounds like a good idea, lad. No need for them to get rusty! They get a nice vacation this season" Veir chuckled, and together we went to put the tools away. Once we had finished, he invited me inside to sit and relax for a while. I gladly accepted, hoping to make it back to town before nightfall.

As we entered, his wife peered around the corner. "Is everything all right, dearest? You're already inside…" she then took on a more stern tone “Did you hurt yourself?”

Veir chuckled and reassured her, "I'm fine, love. Our new friend here fixed our field in a matter of seconds!"

She was visibly surprised and skeptically remarked, "Really..." She stopped what she was doing in the room and walked toward us, casting her eyes upon the revitalized field.

“Oh my! You really did it!” She turned to me and added with a chuckle, “If I had a daughter, I’d ask you to marry her!”

I froze, my joints locking for a moment. “What!?” I said sharply, voice catching just slightly.

Veir laughed heartily at my reaction. “Indeed! That way, we could keep you around!” He and his wife shared a laugh, but I couldn’t shake my discomfort. Veir heartily patted my back and said, “We were just joking. Please, come in and have a seat. We’d love to get to know you! It’s not every day we get a Randeth visitor.”

I chuckled, appreciating their warm hospitality, and agreed to join them. I settled into a chair in the room, taking in the sights of their lovely home adorned with family pictures and various mementos. One particular photo caught my attention as I noticed two familiar faces.

Veir and his wife entered the room a few moments later, carrying a mug of alcohol for me. I accepted it graciously but couldn't help but wonder, do all creatures drink this all the time? We chatted casually for a while, until a framed photo on the mantel caught my eye.

"Who's that?" I asked, nodding toward it.

Veir’s wife perked up immediately. “Oh, that was taken years ago—hang on, I’ll go get it.” She stood, almost too quickly, clearly eager to relive whatever memory the picture held.

"This picture was drawn seven years ago when our son, Beans, brought his mentor to meet us,” she said, her voice brimming with warmth and pride. “He was absolutely thrilled to introduce her to us!”

I thought I recognized the faces in the picture, and excitement filled me. "Beans is your son? I know him! He and the Demon Knight are joining me and my friend on a quest for the King!"

Beans’ mother grew incredibly excited upon hearing that I knew her son. She proceeded to share numerous things she wanted me to relay to him, and shared many, many stories… The rhythm of our work carried us through the day—talking, pausing, laughing now and then—until the sky dimmed and shadows stretched long across the fields.

I gazed out the window and muttered, "Oh, geez..."

Veir looked at me curiously and asked, "Is something wrong, boy?"

I let out a sigh and replied, "Well, the King is hosting a party tomorrow, and I got to return to town soon."

Veir's wife chimed in, "Oh! Will Beans be accompanying you?" I nodded in affirmation, prompting her to snap her fingers and exclaim, "Alright! He dropped off his suit earlier today. Would you mind taking it to him? I can also whip up one for you!"

I smiled gratefully and said, "Oh, I must have just barely missed him. Thank you for the offer, but you don't have to-" Just then a rock shattered through the window.

Veir stood up, exclaiming, "Not again! These darn Basilisk-folk show up every night and steal our crops!" He turned to me and pleaded, "Could you turn them into some kind of animals or something?"

I felt a twinge of hesitation as that was… impossible. "I could try to help," I replied tentatively.

Veir nodded eagerly and said, "Great! Let's go!"

The two of us rushed out the door, only to be greeted by five lizard-like creatures as tall as Gwen wreaking havoc in the fields. These creatures had long tails, fins running from the back of their heads all the way down their spines, and large feet. Their arms were of medium length, and their eyes gleamed with a menacing red hue.

Veir turned to me, his voice urgent. "Can you do something?"

I gazed at the lizard people, observing the destruction they were causing, and suddenly felt a surge of confidence. Something clicked inside me, and without hesitation, I charged toward the nearest creature.

As I sprinted toward the beast, my instincts took over, and I transformed into a mighty elk, the symbol of the Randeths. The Basilisk-folk turned to face me, but before they could react, my antlers pierced through their scales, sending one of them flying through the air and impaling it on a fence post.

This dramatic turn of events caught the attention of the remaining creatures, scattering them. They retaliated by hurling rocks from their slings in my direction. Some struck me, but undeterred, I charged toward the next closest Basilisk. It dodged my attack, while the other three beings converged on me, brandishing their slings, and the one I missed drew a dagger and lunged at me.

Seizing the moment, I reared up on my hind legs, causing one of the Basilisk-folk to miss its strike and fall beneath my hooves. With nimble movements, I darted past the other creatures, but a fence at the corner of the field blocked my way. This gave them enough time to close in, and they started throwing daggers.Each blow from their blades chipped away at me, until my transformed form shattered, forcing me back into my humanoid body. The world spun—I still felt hooves where my hands should be. Instinct took over, and I lunged forward like a beast, only to catch my own foot and crash hard, face-first into the dirt.

By the time I scrambled upright, they were already mid-leap—fangs bared, eyes wild.

I threw out my hand without thinking, and the earth answered. Thick roots erupted from the ground, snaking and thrashing like wild serpents. They coiled around limbs, yanked bodies mid-air—but in my panic, I overreached. The vines caught my legs too, locking me in place just as the nearest Basilisk landed with a hiss inches from my face.

Both the Basilisk and I struggled to break free from the entanglement, but our efforts were useless. Two of the Basilisk-Folk threw daggers that grazed my arm. Clutching my arm, I tore myself free from the roots, determined to finish with the remaining creatures.

Approaching one of the Basilisk-folk, I extended my hand, releasing a cloud of gas. The creature inhaled the gas, writhing in discomfort before succumbing. With two foes left, one tried to flee, while the other hurled another dagger at my arm.

I advanced on the fleeing creature, repeating the same process. As it realized escape was futile, the last Basilisk-folk pleaded, "Please don't kill me! I beg you!"

Coming to a halt right in front of it, I replied, "If you promise your clan will never set foot here again, I will spare your life." My firm tone conveyed the seriousness of my words.

The creature agreed and vowed to stay far away. I helped it escape the entanglement, and after grabbing its fallen comrades, it bolted.

Exhausted from the battle, I collapsed onto the ground, my breath heavy. Veir approached, offering his congratulations and a place to stay for the night. Fatigued and unsteady, I accepted, realizing I wouldn't make it back to town on my own.

The next morning, as the sun timidly crept over the horizon, Veir woke me. "Hey, kid, wake up. You need to get going if you want to reach the kingdom by noon."

Still groggy, I mumbled, "Hm... But Vomete... I haven't photosynthesized yet..." Yawning, I opened my eyes and saw Veir. "Oh! Uh, sorry, Veir."

He chuckled. "No problem, but if you want to make it back to the kingdom, you need to set off now. Come downstairs and grab something to eat before you leave."

With that, he left the room,which, from the looks of the knight decor—polished suits of armor standing sentinel in the corners, faded banners stitched with old heraldry, and iron sconces shaped like crossed swords—seemed intended to impress, happened to be Beans’ old room. Letting out a sigh, I got up. Waking up before sunrise wasn't my usual routine, since I relied on sunlight for energy, but I had enough reserves to last a few days. However, after the intense fight, I felt completely drained.

Heading downstairs, I found Bean's mom waiting for me. "Hello, darling. Thank you so much for your help last night! Those stupid lizards have been causing us so much trouble."

I let out a soft chuckle, still drowsy. "No problem..." I yawned again. She handed me a satchel. "In here, you'll find some clothes that should fit both you and Beans. As well as some bread. Take good care of my son now, alright?" She smiled warmly.

I nodded and made my way outside.After a few hours of walking, I reached the city gates. Upon entering, I was greeted by a bustling town transformed for the celebration of Liberty Day. Children darted between stalls with ribbons in their hair and sticky sweets in their hands, their laughter ringing through the air. Adults clustered in groups, drinking, dancing, or clapping along to the music played by passing bands. The streets were draped in colorful banners. A smile crept across my face as I took in the heartwarming scene. Suddenly, I heard a familiar voice beside me.

"There you are, Deta! How are you?"

I turned to see Beans, dressed in a tunic and tan pants, with Bluma in more relaxed attire. I greeted them, "Hey, guys! Funny enough, Beans, I was just at your parents' place."

Beans stepped back, surprised. "What!? Why were you there?"

Bluma patted his head as I quickly explained, "I was wandering in and ended up helping in the field. Then some lizard people attacked, but everything's fine now! We fought them off!" I tried to rush through the explanation to prevent worry, but it had the opposite effect.

Beans exclaimed, "Basilisk-folk!? Are my parents okay? Why didn't they tell me?"

Chuckling, I reassured him, "I'm not sure but, your parents are perfectly fine. There were about five or so of them."

Beans breathed a sigh of relief. "Oh, good... I'm glad they're okay. But five of them? Really? One is easy to take down, but as a pack, they're a challenge."

Bluma then spoke up, noticing Gwen was not with me. "Gwen?"

I sighed and replied, "Last time I talked with her she seemed to need some time alone. I'm sure she's alright."

Bluma nodded, then noticed the satchel I was holding. Once she pointed to it I then remembered why I had it. "Oh! Yes, Beans, your mom wanted me to give you something."

Beans stopped me just as I reached into the bag.
“Oh, really? Heh, awesome! Come with me. Bluma! I’ll be right back!” He said with a giant grin.

Before I could see Bluma’s response, He practically bounced ahead, leading me down the street and up the stairs of a nearby inn. As we reached a small room at the end of the hall, he grinned.
“The suit’s already done?” he laughed. “That’s my Mama for you—she works fast!”

Pulling it out, the shirt was a long white tunic with a simple, thin black sweater and pants. Beans beamed with excitement. "Thanks for bringing this! I can't wait to surprise Bluma!"

He shoved the suit into his satchel, and we headed out of the inn. I left mine in its bag—Once we got back, Bluma and Beans practically shoved me toward the festival.

During my walk, I noticed several stands set up in the Central Plaza, so I wandered over. In one stand, a pool of little fish was the main attraction, with kids trying to catch them. Depending on the size of the fish they caught, they could win more as prizes.

Although it looked fun, I noticed there was a fee to participate, and having no money, I simply observed. That’s when I saw a child nearby, their small fists clenched at their sides, lower lip trembling. Their eyes, wide and glassy, flicked back and forth between the game and the few coins in their palm, as if willing more to appear. Frustration clung to their face like static, and they teetered on the edge of tears, shoulders rising with every shallow breath. Something about their silent struggle tugged at me.

I whispered to the fish, “Hey, over here.” They turned toward me. Pointing to the child, I sent my message, and the largest fish handed itself over, leaping straight into the child’s bag.

The child’s face lit up, and they jumped for joy. The parents were ecstatic, and the family walked away brimming with happiness. Watching this, the other kids became eager to catch their own fish. Just as I was about to leave, the man running the stand approached.

“Hey, I saw what you did there, kid,” he said with a gruff tone of voice.

Startled, I quickly apologized. “Oh, I didn’t mean any harm!”

The man chuckled, shaking his head. “Relax. I was going to help the kid anyway, but you saved me the trouble. Thanks"

I smiled, thankful I didn't upset him somehow “Oh no worries!” I said before leaving to explore more.

As the day wore on, more games and activities were set up. Toward sunset, three knights entered the plaza. Two of them blew their horns, grabbing the crowd’s attention while the third stepped forward, announcing:

“In honor of Liberty Day, King Aldric and Queen Elara are hosting a grand ballroom party at the palace! All are invited!”

Cheers erupted from the crowd, and people either began preparing their stalls or rushed home to get ready. The knights spotted me and approached. One of them asked, “Are you Deta?”

I nodded, and the knight bowed with respect as the one in the center spoke. “The king has requested we escort you to the ballroom. Will you come with us?”

Trying not to chuckle at the bow, I agreed, and the knights led me to the castle. As I entered the grand ballroom, the sight took me in. Banquet tables stretched along the walls, covered in crisp white cloths, each set with polished silverware and modest centerpieces of roses and lilies. The marble floor gleamed softly, catching the gentle light from chandeliers that hung high above, casting a warm glow. Every corner was adorned with subtle flower arrangements and soft lighting, creating an air of understated elegance throughout the room.

 “Wow, they really went all out,” I muttered in awe.

As I wandered inside, I saw Gwens face on the opposite side of the room, just entering. “Oh, Gwen!” I called out, walking over and stepping in front of her with a smile.

Once I got over, my eyes were drawn to her dress—a rich blue that caught the light in subtle, flattering ways, complementing her every movement. The fabric fit her figure perfectly before flowing into a soft, full dress that draped naturally to the floor. Around the neckline, feathers in varying shades of blue added a touch of depth and texture, gently swaying with each step she took. The feathers brought a playful element to her otherwise elegant look, highlighting her effortless grace and charm, a blend that quietly invited admiration.

“Well?” Gwen snapped, arms crossed. “Are you going to say something, or should I just walk through you?”

Chuckling, I stepped back a few paces, allowing her through. She rolled her eyes and walked on. “It looks good on you, Gwen,” I called after her.

 She paused slightly, her head tilting just enough to acknowledge the comment. After a brief silence, she muttered, “...thanks,” before continuing on.

I entered a smaller room just off from the main to change into the suit that Beans’ mother had made for me. It was similar to Beans’ outfit, consisting of a thin black jacket and trousers made from fine wool, paired with a crisp white shirt. The suit felt slightly loose at first, but once I layered it over my clothes, it fit perfectly. Smiling to myself, I admired the transformation.

As I was about to leave the room a small fire lily plant near the window caught my eye. Its slender stems reached upward, crowned with vibrant red blooms that resembled tiny flames. The plant’s magical properties radiated warmth and comfort. I approached and gently touched it, causing it to sprout and spread its soothing warmth through the room.

I slipped out of the room and made my way back to the ballroom. The King stood off the main platform, chatting with Beans and Bluma near the food tables—not far from the throne, but not exactly royal about it either.

CHAPTER 9                                                                                                                                The Beginning to an End

As the evening progressed, the four of us found ourselves scattered throughout the lively ballroom. Bluma and Beans were chatting with other knights while enjoying the music. Gwen, on the other hand, seemed to have vanished from sight, though I had glimpsed her discreetly gathering berries from the banquet table and stashing them in a small leather pouch. As for me, I stood awkwardly to the side, uncertain of how to fully engage in the festivities.

The music came to a halt, and a clear voice rang out across the hall, announcing that it was time for a break—to enjoy the spread and mingle. Almost at once, the crowd stirred with fresh energy, drifting toward the long banquet tables set beneath hanging lanterns and soft golden drapery.

The tables were lavish, almost sagging beneath the sheer weight of the feast. Glazed meats shimmered under the lights—whole roasted pheasants with crisp, crackling skin pulled tight over tender flesh, and thick ribs lacquered in a dark, sticky glaze that clung to the bone. There were carved fruits shaped into elaborate flowers—some familiar, others strange and jewel-toned, with flesh like pale blue honey or deep crimson velvet.

There were soft, steaming breads dusted with fragrant herbs, their crusts flaking at the lightest touch, and cheeses stacked like miniature towers, ranging from creamy and pale to waxy blocks the color of burnished gold. Dishes of bright pickled vegetables glistened like gems, and small, delicate pastries sat arranged in perfect rows, their sugary shells cracking open to reveal molten fruit or spiced cream.

I couldn’t smell any of it—not the slow-roasted meats or the tang of citrus in the sorbets melting into their dishes. But I could see how the others reacted—eyes widening, lips parting as they breathed in the aroma-laced air. One woman near me even closed her eyes and smiled as she lifted a slice of something red and glistening to her mouth.

I didn’t eat, but I watched.

The pheasant looked tender, its skin golden and crackling with roasted herbs. A thin sheen of glaze caught the light, glistening faintly amber. Pastries broke apart in buttery flakes, steam curling from their centers as warm apple and spice spilled out. Sorbets shimmered in delicate glass bowls, already starting to melt into swirls of color.

People murmured to each other between bites—praising this sauce, that marinade—while others traded gossip between sips of wine. The room had taken on a new kind of music: the clink of cutlery, the hush of velvet sleeves brushing past, the low murmur of voices punctuated by laughter and soft, satisfied sighs.

Beans and Bluma approached me then, their faces flushed like roses. I couldn’t help but chuckle at the sight of them.

"Are you two okay?"

Beans giggled and responded enthusiastically, "I'm great!" He hiccupped and then turned to Bluma, saying, "I'll be right back!" He swayed slightly as he walked over to the food, for a moment it reminded me of rose when we were in the tavern.

I laughed, amused by his cheerful demeanor, but more to mask the sorrow from the memory of failing her and her sisters, then I turned my attention to Bluma, who also seemed flushed.

Curiously, I asked her, "And what about you? Have you had a drink as well?"

Bluma shook her head, denying any involvement with alcohol, and said, "No."

Her response sparked my curiosity, and I wondered what had caused her rosy complexion. I made my way over to them, figuring I might as well enjoy the feast and see who else was worth talking to.

Continuing my exploration of the festivities, I noticed the absence of the Queen and the Princess as I reached the front of the room. Only the King could be found seated on his throne, and when he caught sight of me, he beckoned me over. I approached him, curious about his summons.

The King let out a sigh before speaking. "Deta, could you please check on my wife and child? Your friend also accompanied them to the balcony." Concern filled his voice as he expressed his worry. “I mean no disrespect but I do worry about my Queen”

I nodded in response, assuring him. "Of course. I will go and check on them right away."

With gratitude in his eyes, the King thanked me, and I began my search, navigating through the labyrinthine corridors of the castle in an effort to locate the specific balcony in question.

Gwens’ View

The Queen’s voice cut through the silence like a blade. “You’re not much of a fan of parties, are you?”

I didn’t bother to look at her. Just kept flicking fire berries into my mouth and breathing out soft bursts of flame. The sky was clearer than I expected—uncluttered. Peaceful. A stark contrast to the palace.

I groaned. “Not really. I’d rather be out doing something useful. Or at least something fun.” I hesitated, thumb brushing the edge of the pouch. “I spent too long being trapped by other people’s expectations. I’m not about to throw myself into another cage.”

She hummed, and I could hear the practiced smile in it. Polished, polite, but with something sharper just beneath.

Before she could say more, the door slammed open behind us, bouncing off the wall.

“Look, Mommy! I found it!”

I turned just in time to see the Princess rush in, a stuffed bear clutched in her arms like a prize. Her curls were bouncing wildly, eyes bright. If she’d brought that thing in here, there’s no way she’d been with the Queen the whole time. Probably wandered off again. And no one stopped her?

The Queen gave a soft laugh that didn't quite reach her eyes. “I’m so proud of you, my dear. Now, back to your father.”

The girl beamed and ran off, the door swinging halfway shut behind her. I watched it for a moment, waiting for someone to close it. No one did.

The Queen finally stepped closer, leaning beside me against the railing. She didn’t even glance at the stars.

“Tell me,” she said, her voice syrupy sweet “Why do you feel the need to go gallivanting across the world? Why not stay, settle down, start a family?”

I snorted, shaking my head. “Good one. I’ve had enough people getting in my way—or worse, getting hurt because of me. I’m fine on my own.”

She laughed lightly, like I’d said something charming. I didn’t like it.

Then she held out a hand, palm up. “May I?”

I hesitated, then slapped a berry into her hand. Her fingers curled around it like she was holding something fragile... or filthy.

“You could always join my Knights,” the Queen said, like she was offering me a glass of wine instead of a life sentence. “You’re strong. That hit you landed was impressive.”

I blinked at her, slowly. “What hit?”

“The Randeth, of course.”

My spine stiffened. Of course.

I almost laughed—almost. My fingers curled tight around the berry pouch.  So that’s what she thought this was. A job interview. A recruitment pitch.  Like knocking Deta down made me some kind of hero. Like hurting him was the goal.

I forced a smirk, sharp as broken glass. “Didn’t realize you were scouting during a crisis.”

She smiled back, calm as ever. Like she hadn't just insulted someone I actually gave a crap about. Like she didn’t see him as anything more than a thing.

And maybe she didn’t.

“I mean, not everyone can handle creatures like that,” the Queen said, turning the berry over like it was already rotting in her hand. “They’re unpredictable. Wild. Dangerous. Better off with someone to keep them in check.”

My jaw locked.

He saved you, I reminded myself. That’s all. You owe him. That’s it. This wasn’t about caring. I didn’t care. That was stupid.

She crushed the berry—slow, deliberate. Juice dripped down her fingers, dark red against her pale skin..

Her eyes stayed on mine, daring me to flinch instead.

“But I suppose,” she said, soft and sharp, “that’s why we need people like you, hmm? To keep them from getting out of hand.”

I didn’t look away. I wouldn’t.

That’s all it was.

I wasn’t angry because she called him dangerous. I was angry because she said it like he wasn’t a person at all.

Deta’s View

I wandered through the quiet halls, the sounds of the ballroom muffled behind thick stone walls. The whole place felt too grand, too imposing. I didn’t belong here, and it was starting to weigh on me.

As I rounded a corner, the door to a side room swung open, and Maggie practically launched herself at me.

“Deta!”

She wrapped her arms around my legs in a tight hug, grinning up at me with that same innocent brightness. I froze, unsure how to react. I didn’t have skin—couldn’t really feel it—but there was something about her warmth, her trust, that made me feel... something.

“I’m glad you’re here!” she said with a giggle. “Mama didn’t like you at first, but I told her you were nice.”

I awkwardly patted her head, my stone fingers clicking against her hair. “I... appreciate that.”

She pulled away to look up at me with wide eyes.

“Where’s the Queen? And Gwen?” I hesitated, the mention of the Queen making something in my chest tighten. But Maggie was looking at me expectantly, so I gave her a small smile.

“They’re in there, Mama’s talking to a lady.” She pointed to the door nearby. “You can go see now!”

I nodded and gave her a small wave. “Thanks, Maggie.”

I walked to the door little Maggie told me to go to and heard Gwen and the Queen talking but couldn't make out what they were saying. I then opened the door fully as they turned to see who it was. “Is everything okay?” I asked while looking at Gwen.

The Queen’s smile faltered for a split second before she forced it back. “Oh, we’re quite alright. Thank you, though. I suppose you could say we’re having a... stimulating conversation… Randeth…”

Gwen then stepped away and approached the door with purpose. She gave the Queen a polite nod. “Thank you for the… offer. For now, I have other plans that I need to keep my word to but I’ll think about it.” Gwen then walked past me.

I turned to observe the Queen, who directed a deathly glare my way. However, I maintained a smile on my face, unaffected by her animosity. As the Queen closed the door behind us, I took a deep breath and proceeded to catch up with Gwen, who seemed deep in thought. I glanced over, brow furrowing. “You alright?”

Gwen let out a sigh, one of those weary ones that tried too hard to sound like nothing. “Yeah. I’m fine,” she said, but her voice had an edge, like something was gnawing at the back of her thoughts.

Before I could press, she reached into her pouch and tossed something into my hand. A handful of small, dark-red berries.

“Here. Eat these.”

I blinked at them. “What are—”

Too late. I popped the whole handful into my mouth.

Her eyes went wide. “Wait—oh my tachi’guf! That’s terrible! You ate all of them!?”

I froze mid-chew.

“Fire berries,” she said, already laughing.

My eyes shot open as the heat exploded in my mouth—like someone had poured molten metal over my tongue. I choked on a gasp, nearly tripping over myself as the fire spread down my throat.

“Wh—what the—!” I staggered back, fanning my mouth like it would do anything to help. “Ow—Gwen! Not funny!”

She was doubled over, howling with laughter, barely managing to breathe between snorts.

I burped, and a puff of smoke curled out from my lips. “Seriously?!” I coughed, sweat starting to bead along my stone brow. My lips tingled like they’d been stung.

Gwen was already walking away, cackling like a maniac.

I lunged for the nearest drink and downed it in two gulps, the cool liquid easing the worst of the burn. I wiped my mouth, still coughing, and glared after her.

She sauntered back with her own drink, eyes twinkling. I muttered under my breath, “You’re the worst.”

“Mmhm,” she said, raising her glass. “You’re welcome.”

"How do people eat this stuff?" I sighed, saying. "Nice joke, Gwen... Now I have to find a way to get back at you somehow."

She grinned and replied. "Good luck, Bushy."

Taking another sip, I realized it had the same taste as the alcohol I had before and knew what would happen soon. "Oh boy..."

Just then, a knight made an announcement, "It's the last dance of the night!" While the knight continued speaking, I noticed Gwen had disappeared again. Looking around, I spotted her whispering to the band responsible for playing the music at the party.

"Oh goodness gracious... Here we go."

As soon as the knight finished speaking, the band nodded at Gwen and rushed back. The band launched into a faster-paced formal song, much to the crowd's delight. I chuckled, watching Bluma and Beans dancing on the floor. Even the King seemed to be enjoying himself. Standing there, a robed man approached me.

"Hello there,” he said. “Aren't you planning to join the festivities? As one of the King's guests, I assume..."

I chuckled and replied, "Well, I'm not much of a party person."

The robed man smiled and suggested, "Ah, I see. Have you tried using alcohol to ease your discomfort?"

I sighed. "Doesn’t do anything for me. I’m not exactly built like everyone else."

The man pondered this for a moment. "I have an idea," he said, flicking my head, causing both of us some pain—I felt the impact of the flick, and he winced at hitting solid wood

"What was that for?" I suddenly felt a warm sensation inside, and the man smiled.

"I've magically made you drunk. It should have more effect as the night goes on. Now, go and have..." His words began to blur and fade, drifting away as if they were floating through water. A strange warmth spread through me, and the world felt just a little softer around the edges.

The next thing I knew, I was lying on a bed. The wooden ceiling above me seemed to spin slightly as I blinked against the sunlight coming through the window. My head felt heavy, like it was wrapped in cotton, and there was a faint ache behind my eyes. Sitting up, I rubbed my face and tried to get my bearings.

Looking around, I saw Gwen asleep in another bed, her arm hanging lazily over the side. Beans was curled up in a blanket, snoring quietly, while Bluma was already awake, sitting on her bed and putting on her armor with calm precision.

I tried to remember what had happened, but everything felt muddled—just bits of laughter and blurry faces, nothing clear. The room swayed a little as I stood, and I had to steady myself, wondering how much of last night I had missed.

"Good morning, Bluma," I said, yawning. She turned to me and waved while continuing to don her armor. "That party was interesting... I can hardly remember anything."

Bluma chuckled, and as I glanced outside the window at the town, I sighed, saying, "Today is the day we explore what lies beneath it all, huh?"

Bluma finished fastening her armor and nodded. She then walked over, placed her hand on my shoulder, and said, "Courage." Afterward, she went to Beans.

I smiled and replied, "I'll try."

I glanced at Gwen and blinked. She was wearing one of those strapless dresses—bare shoulders, a lot of skin. I turned away, because I remembered humans get weird about that. Then I frowned. “Wait... but she is wearing clothes.”

 Getting up, I poked her on the face trying to get a response, "Gwen?" She didn't respond, so I paused to think and then got an idea.

"There's a fight waiting for you," I said.

Her eyes widened, and she jumped up, exclaiming, "Where's the fight? I'm in!" After realizing we were still in the inn, she gave me an unamused look, "Oh, very funny..."

Chuckling, I retorted, "Got you back!"

She glanced down at her dress, rolled her eyes, and commented, "I have to change out of this hideous thing.”

Bluma then grabbed my arm, ushering me out of the room. She gently pushed the sleepy Beans out as well and closed the door behind us.

I was quite confused. "Uh... what?"

Beans rubbed his eyes and yawned. “They’re changing. They need privacy.”

“Oh.” I tilted my head. “So that’s normal? Humans change clothes a lot?”

Beans nodded. “Yeah. Daily, usually. It’s a modest thing.”

“Huh. Randeths don’t really do that. I mean we own a pair of clothes… We wash it, fix it if it tears. Clothes aren’t for us—they’re to keep lost travelers comfortable.”

Beans blinked. “Right. Okay, maybe... don’t say that part out loud either.”

I nodded, understanding the difference in customs. "Things work differently here than in the woods," I said with a smile.

After a while, Gwen and Bluma emerged from the room, both wearing their armor and swords. Gwen, though, now had a strange device slung across her back—metal and wood, shaped oddly, with string stretched tight.

I pointed. “What’s that on her back?”

Beans looked up. “Oh, that’s a crossbow. Shoots bolts real fast—like a bow, but easier to aim.”

I blinked. “That’s a weapon?”

“Yep. The King had some made for folks like us—non-magic types. Helps even things out.”

As the two walked past us, Gwen smiled. “Don’t take too long in there, ladies.”

I chuckled at her teasing remark, and then Beans and I changed out of the party wear. I simply took mine off, straightening my normal clothes underneath, while Beans started throwing on his armor. His set was a simpler version of Bluma’s—same red and gold, but more dull. His breastplate had that dark red look, with just a bit of gold trim here and there, nothing too fancy. The pauldrons were smaller, more practical, and the rest—gauntlets and greaves—were tough but plain.

Afterward, we made our way toward the inn’s door, only to halt in surprise at the sight of knights standing just outside. Their armor gleamed in the fading sunlight, the metal catching the last warmth of the day.

"As a token of our gratitude, we have cleared a path to the castle," one of the knights announced, his voice solemn as he bowed slightly. His dark helmet obscured his face, leaving only a hint of shadow where his expression might have been.

Gwen grinned, her eyes flashing with excitement. "V.I.P. treatment. I like this." The words rolled off her tongue with a sense of playful entitlement.

Beans, standing beside her, chuckled—a deep, hearty sound that broke through the tension. Bluma merely nodded, her usual silence masking any emotion, while I managed a polite smile and voiced my thanks to the knights.

We stepped forward, the crowd that had gathered on the street parting with murmurs. Concerned gazes followed us as we moved toward the castle. The atmosphere felt heavy, as though the townspeople were watching something they didn’t fully understand. I caught the eye of a young woman with a basket of flowers, her lips pressed tight in worry. Offering her a small smile, I waved at her and a few others, hoping to alleviate the tension, even if just for a moment.

The castle loomed ahead, towering and imposing. When we entered, the air turned cooler, a sharp contrast to the warmth outside. Bluma and Beans took the lead as we approached a wide staircase spiraling upward. The stone steps echoed beneath our feet, each step seeming to pull us higher into the gloom. I hated these stairs. The way they coiled upward without end, as though we were climbing a mountain, not simply moving through a building.

Minutes turned to what felt like hours as we ascended for what seemed like an eternity, our breaths becoming heavier with each step. I tried not to let the others see how much I despised this endless climb. Bluma, of course, seemed unaffected, moving with her usual grace. Finally, after what felt like thirty minutes of unrelenting stairs, we reached the top, breathless and aching.

CHAPTER 10                                                                                                          Delving Deeper

A heavy wooden door greeted us. Bluma pushed it open, the hinges creaking in protest, revealing a room scorched and blackened by flames. The air smelled faintly of smoke. Rubble lay scattered across the floor, chunks of stone and charred beams strewn like the remnants of a battle. Still, a few items had somehow survived—the outline of a tapestry on one wall, half-burnt furniture huddled in one corner, their shapes barely recognizable.

We stepped inside, the sound of our boots crunching over the debris echoing in the silence.

"What happened here?" I asked.

Beans replied, "This is where we fought a traitor to the kingdom, and this was his vengeful act."

I nodded in pretend understanding, and Gwen smirked, saying, "Nice..."

Bluma walked over to a chest in the room and examined its contents. She handed each of us a rolled-up piece of paper and a gray drink in a glass bottle. "Emergencies," she explained.

Beans nodded and unrolled the paper to see what it contained. "These are potions of strength and scrolls of slow falling. Keep them with you in case of any unforeseen circumstances."

Gwen looked at the items curiously and asked, "Why would we need these scrolls, anyway?"

Beans glanced at her and replied, "Well, the dungeon is very old and built on top of a cave system. We're unsure about its stability, so it's better to be safe." Bluma nodded in agreement, and Gwen sighed before whispering something in another language.

We stowed the items in our satchels then proceeded to descend a different set of stairs, which felt damp and chilly. Midway down, Beans spoke up, warning us, "This is the dungeon, where the monster is said to reside. Be cautious, as there are creatures lurking everywhere."

Upon hearing Beans's warning, we became alert and walked on our toes. At the bottom of the stairs, we encountered two doors. Bluma opened one, and we followed her inside. We had now entered the underground.

Passing through the doorway, we found ourselves in a long hallway that appeared to have been excavated. Water dripped from the ceiling, causing Bluma and Gwen's hair to frizz slightly.
