Bluma took the lead, carefully observing our surroundings. As we walked down the hallway, we noticed rooms branching off from its sides. Beans looked into the farthest room, while I checked the one closest to me.

Beans slowed as he stepped into the small room. “Huh. Dead end,” he muttered, eyeing the cold remains of a long-forgotten campfire. He crouched down and poked at the ashes. “Someone used to be here... but it’s been a while.”

He stood, dusted off his hands, and turned to follow Bluma. “Nothin’ useful. Let’s keep going.”

I stepped cautiously into the room, my gaze drawn to the strange mounds on the floor. They looked like they’d been excavated—dirt and debris piled up, then refilled haphazardly, as if someone had dug them up and decided to cover them again. I took a few steps forward, my curiosity piqued by the oddity of the room.

Suddenly, I felt a strong tug at my collar. Before I could react, Gwen yanked me back, causing me to stumble awkwardly. “Hey!” I protested, more surprised than anything. “You don’t have to be so rough…”

Gwen glanced at me, her expression unreadable. She let out an exasperated sigh before releasing my collar with a muttered, “Fine, whatever.”

I didn’t understand what had her so on edge, but I didn’t press it. We were all tense, unsure of what we’d find in this place.

Bluma paused at the end of the hallway in front of a door. She studied it for a moment, her hand resting on the handle. With a sharp look, she gave a simple, “Move.”

The room beyond was empty—nothing more than bare stone walls and dust. There was another door on the far side of the room, and one more on the left wall. The stillness was unsettling.

Bluma nodded toward the far door. “Go,” she said quietly, her voice sharp but calm.

Beans scanned the surroundings and noticed dwarven runes etched into some of the stones. He headed toward the door in front of us, prompting Gwen to ask, "Beans, what are you doing?"

Beans paused and looked back, his nerves evident as he wasn’t used to taking the lead in a large group. "Well, I noticed these markings resemble dwarven architecture. I thought it might be safer for us to go this way."

I smiled and said, "Sounds good to me!"

I glanced at Gwen and Bluma, who both nodded in agreement, and we followed Beans into the room. As he entered, two large shadowy creatures lunged at him and latched onto his torso. He let out a scream and jumped as one of the creatures bit him.

Bluma swiftly rushed past Gwen and me, drawing her swords and decapitating the creatures in one fluid motion. Beans, still shaken, let out a sigh of relief.

"Thanks, Bluma... I’ve never seen them that big before..." he chuckled, and she affectionately patted his head.

Upon closer inspection, we noticed the room was filled with ransacked food, and the creatures turned out to be giant rats that were the size of Beans.

“What's with this place and giant rats and spiders?” I whispered to Gwen

Gwen shrugged and rolled her eyes. "Alright, let's keep moving," she said, leading the way. We followed her out of the room and headed towards the other door.

As Gwen pushed the door open, the creaking of the hinges echoed through the hallway. We stepped into a large room that stretched out before us. The air was thick with dust, and the faint smell of mildew lingered, making the space feel stagnant. The room was dimly lit, with only a sliver of light filtering in through cracks in the walls.

To Gwen’s left, a doorway led into another shadowed area, its edges worn and splintered. Farther into the room, we could see another door, half-hidden in the gloom. The walls were made of rough stone, but they were scarred—scratches, chips, and the faintest traces of paint, now faded and peeling. The floor beneath our feet was cold and uneven, worn smooth in some places, rough and jagged in others. The room had a man-made appearance, but the signs of time’s erosion were everywhere. The stone felt old, and the quiet made the room feel abandoned, as if it had been forgotten by those who once inhabited it.

As each of us entered, Beans noticed a peculiar sign that seemed out of place. It read, "Welcome to Iron Hallow. Prisoners are welcome!!" with a cat drawing etched in at the end.

"Well... that's reassuring," Beans chuckled.

Gwen brushed past Beans, ready to explore the other side of the room, but Bluma stopped her. Gwen glared at Bluma and whispered, "What's the big idea?"

Bluma held her finger to her lips, signaling for silence. As we moved through the room, I heard the faint murmur of voices—voices I didn’t recognize, speaking in a language that wasn’t mine. Gwen seemed to pause, her posture stiffening slightly. She turned her head, listening intently, and I could see the way her brow furrowed, as if trying to place the words.

I tilted my head, confused. The sounds didn’t make sense to me, but I knew they were important to Gwen. I waited for her to explain, but she remained silent, her focus on the distant voices. I couldn’t help but wonder if they meant something to her—or if they were just as unfamiliar to her as they were to me., and eventually Beans noticed it too. Bluma placed her hand on her sword and cautiously peeked around the corner, discovering an open doorway.

Bluma and Gwen took the lead, prepared for a potential fight. Bluma glanced back at us and whispered, "Basilisk-folk..."

Gwen smiled and began to move towards the door, but I grabbed her arm, attempting to stop her. "Gwen, no. I don't think they are the problem"

She looked at me with frustration in her eyes and retorted, "Well, they could be! Why not kill them now? Even if they aren't, it would be good practice!”

I let go of her arm and pleaded. "We need to save our strength, I don't think they are the ones that have been making the ground shake."

Gwen stared at me as I released her arm, contemplating my words. After a moment, she let go of her weapon and nodded.

I smiled, relieved that she was willing to cooperate. "Thank you... now let's try a different door," I suggested. I started walking backward, then turned around to face forward, with Gwen following suit. Bluma and Beans grumbled as they caught up, urging us to keep moving.

Beans and Bluma exchanged glances, then nodded, deciding to follow me. I pushed open the other door, revealing a larger room that curved around. At the end, I spotted a normal-sized rat.

I grinned and waved. “Hello there.”

The rat froze, its eyes wide with fear. “What!? Who are you!? Don’t eat me, please!! Don’t eat me!!”

I held my hands up, trying to appear non-threatening. “I’m not going to eat you.”

The rat blinked, then hesitantly stopped panicking. “Wait… you’re not going to eat me? And you can understand me?”

I nodded. “Yes, I won’t eat you. I don’t eat ani-”

The rat cut me off, its voice high with urgency. “You don’t eat!? Well, good! Because there isn’t any food here… nope! None at all!”

I sighed, feeling sorry for the rat. "I'm sorry to hear that. I was wondering if you could help us. There's a big monster down here that we've been sent to get rid of. Do you know where it is?"

The rat stood in silence for a moment, then spoke up, "Um... well... There is a big monster in the middle! Um, yeah, the middle."

I chuckled and asked, "Could you show us how to get there?"

The rat scratched its head, saying, "Uh, well, I use this hole, yeah. This hole. But you're too big, so I don't know."

I let out a disappointed grumble, but still maintained a smile. "Well, thank you. Here, take this." I reached into my bag and found some rations, breaking off a piece of bread and offering it to the rat. "Here is some bread."

I tossed it to the rat, which seemed confused at first. It slowly grabbed the bread, nibbled on it, then paused to stare at me before continuing to eat. I turned around and headed back to the others, a little confused as to why this rat could speak and not the ones from the cave where I met Gwen.

"Who was that?" Beans asked, confused by the light tone I was using.

I smiled “Oh it was a little rat, he was-”

Gwen interrupted, "A rat? First a horse, and now a rat?"

Beans looked at her and asked, "Does he do this often?"

Gwen shrugged and replied, "He talks to every animal we're not fighting, apparently."

Feeling slightly attacked, I explained, "No, guys, it's not like that. I'm not crazy. All Randeths can speak to animals, but only certain ones... It's a long story."

Bluma raised an eyebrow, and Beans glanced at her. Gwen simply shrugged, saying, "Whatever..." She then noticed a door to my right and pointed it out, asking, "Who wants to see what's in there?"

When I opened the door, I noticed another small rat cowering in the corner. Taking my time, just as I did with the previous one, I tried to calm him down. Eventually, he started speaking and told me that he was waiting for his friend.

The rat explained, "Yeah, we came in here, and then suddenly it got really warm with a bright flash. And when I turned around, he was gone! So I'm waiting."

I smiled and replied, "Alright, then we won't bother you. Here." I placed some bread on the ground in front of him.

"Oh, food!" he exclaimed, running over to the enticing piece.

However, as soon as he grabbed hold of it, the room suddenly spewed out fire, burning the bread to ashes. This caught me completely off guard, and I jumped back, and screamed, the smell of grilled rat filling the room.

Concerned, Beans and the others approached. Beans asked, "What happened?"

Startled, I replied, "The rat just burst into flames!"

Beans then looked into the room and noticed a pressure plate along with holes scattered all over. "Well, this place is trapped. Make sure you keep a close eye out. and not fall for it yourself."

We all nodded and continued into the room, we discovered a door at the far end. As I reached out to touch the door, Beans reminded me about traps and to stay vigilant. I nodded and opened the door, revealing an incredibly small room with another door at the opposite end. The room appeared to be about fifteen feet long.

"Well... It doesn't look trapped," I remarked, scanning the area. After a minute, I found the string. "I've found the trap," I announced as I carefully maneuvered around it.

Once each of us had crossed safely, Gwen opened the next door. Inside, we froze. Two Basilisk-folk sat calmly, their sharp eyes locking onto ours. For a heartbeat, the room was dead silent, the tension thick enough to slice. We stared at each other, the air crackling with unspoken words, each of us sizing the other up.

Bluma stood perfectly still, her expression unreadable, while Beans looked a little too unsure, shifting his weight like he wasn’t sure if this was a stare-down or an awkward meeting. I could almost hear him wondering, Are we fighting, or... are we just standing here like idiots?

Gwen noticed that they weren't attacking and observed a doorway on the other side. Keeping her sword at the ready, she cautiously walked around the side of the room. The rest of us followed suit, maintaining a distance from one another. As Gwen approached the doorway, one of the Basilisk folk rushed to block her path.

"No, you can't go that way!" he panicked, while the other one joined him and added, "Yes, you can't!"

Gwen tried to pull out her sword but I got infront of her in a panic and inquired, "why not?"

The taller Basilisk-folk responded, "Because you can't! Uh... yeah!"

The smaller Basilisk-folk looked at his companion confused and asked, "Why can't they?"

The larger one took a moment to think and responded, "Uh... because... because... Someone told us not to let them pass!"

Beans chimed in, saying, "But we need to!"

The Basilisk-folk glanced at each other and then the smaller one wagged its tail and said, "Oh! Are you here to see the Lizard King?"

I then looked to Gwen who glanced at Beans, who then looked at Bluma, who then looked at me. In a panicked tone, I said, "Yes."

The taller Basilisk-folk spoke up, saying, "Well, you can't see him!"

Unsure of what to do next, I went along with it and asked, "But why not?"

The smaller one replied, "Because we think we need to guard this way!"

Gwen interjected, "How can you be guarding something if you don't have a purpose? It's clear you don't have one."

The smaller Basilisk-folk stuttered trying to think of something and responded again, saying, "Well... we are hunting..."

Beans had an idea and said, "Oh, really? Well, there were some rats in a room not too far back."

The two Basilisk-folk perked up at the mention of rats. "Our traps worked, little brother!" the bigger one said to the smaller one.

Beans nodded and continued, "Yes! I think there were two or three of them!"

Excited, the Basilisk-folk jumped over me and rushed off to see the rats.

"Go, go, go!!" Beans exclaimed as he dashed out through the opposite door and down a hallway.

We all chased after him, eventually catching up. The hallway was long and dim, except for the echoes of our feet, we walked mostly in silence to avoid alerting the lizards.

When we entered the new room, it was spacious and curved around a corner. As the group made their way around, I noticed another rat peacefully eating and whispered, "Don't go down the hall!"

The rat looked at me and then glanced at the hallway, panicking. "What!? Why!? What's down there? Should I stay or leave!?"

Before I could calm him down, Beans accidentally tripped on a wire, causing a net to fall on him.

Then Basilisk-folk came running out of the tunnel, exclaiming, "We caught a rat! Oh... it's just you again... Why are you in our net?"

Then the smaller one noticed the rat and eagerly exclaimed, "Oh! A rat!" He jumped on it and devoured it.

As they did so, Gwen could see the discomfort on my face as the rat’s screams of pain filled the room. A tightness twisted in my chest as I watched the lizard folk tear into it. The suddenness of it—so brutal, so cold—sent a chill down my spine. I had just spoken to the rat, and now it was being devoured right before me. My hands clenched at my sides, the helplessness gnawing at me as I struggled to look away, the scene pressing down on me with every agonizing sound.

“What are you doing down here?” the larger lizard asked, his gaze fixed on me.

Beans attempted to deceive them once more, saying, "Uh... well, you gave us the wrong directions."

The two Basilisk-folk looked at each other, they were both confused from the looks of it and the smaller one replied, "No, we gave you the right directions."

I chimed in, saying, "Well, you did tell us about the trap."

The larger Basilisk-folk chuckled and replied, "Pfft. We set that up yesterday! Everyone should know about it by now, dumb-dumb!"

We looked at each other and shrugged. "Well, sorry about that. We'll help you put it back together," I apologized.

The two Basilisk-folk glanced at each other and shrugged, saying, "Sure, why not?"

We then proceeded to free Beans from their net and assisted them in resetting it. Afterward, they spotted another rat and chased after it, giving us the chance to leave.

As we continued walking, Gwen grinned and teased Beans, saying, "So, Beans, what was that about avoiding traps?"

Beans turned red with embarrassment but laughed along with her, saying, "I.. meant to do that!"

I smiled and said, "Well, try not to forget again, alright, Beans?"

He nodded and replied, "Yeah, we don't know if they'll keep falling for our trick."

Gwen scoffed and said, "Keep it up? That's a little boring."

Bluma shook her head, and Beans looked at her. "We need to conserve our—"

Gwen interrupted him, saying, "Conserve our energy, yeah yeah, I know. Geez." She rolled her eyes and crossed her arms.

I sighed and said, "Do you guys have to argue? Let's try to keep moving."

I offered a light-hearted smile as Gwen turned away, making a disapproving sound.

Beans nodded and said, "Alright, focus time."

He looked at Bluma, who patted his head and called him "Squishy." Beans chuckled at the nickname.

Observing their interaction, I asked Bluma, "Why do you call him that?"

Bluma looked at me for a second, then avoided eye contact.

Beans chuckled and said, "Aww, Bluma." He seemed to understand what was going on, but I was lost.

Beans explained that it was her pet name for him, and when I asked what he called her, he said, "Oh! I call her a Spicy Nugget!"

Bluma's face turned red, and she playfully punched him while he laughed.

I smiled and said, "Oh, that's cute… but aren't nuggets small?"

I wondered about the meanings behind their nicknames, but before I could inquire further, Gwen sped  off. "Hurry up, you guys. I want to kill whatever it is we were sent to kill."

I chuckled and remarked, "Always ready for a fight, huh?"

As we walked, we passed a door and continued towards the one straight ahead. However, as we passed by, we heard the sounds of flames erupting from within and caught a whiff of cooked rats. Given my discomfort from my previous encounters with rats, I chose not to open that door.

As Gwen opened the next door, she encountered two more Basilisk-folk standing guard. As soon as they saw her, they drew their daggers and growled. One had bright green scales while the other had orange scales.

The orange lizard scowled, crossing its arms. "Who are you? And how did you get here?"

Gwen didn’t even stop. She just headed for the nearest door, which led to a stairway, and called back over her shoulder, “The others told us to come this way.” She kept walking, clearly uninterested in further explanations.

The green lizard perked up, a wide grin spreading across its face. "Oh, you mean Sam and Tom?" he asked, leaning toward us with curiosity.

“Yeah, those guys are awesome!” I said, nodding enthusiastically.

As they started chatting, we tried to sneak away, hoping to blend into the background. But I was the last one in the room, and just as I was about to follow the others up the stairs, the lizards hit us with another barrage of questions.

“Wait—why would they be here?” Orange asked, furrowing his brow at Green.

“Uh... oh! Are you guys the exterminators? Did the Great Lizard send you?” Green grinned like he had just figured everything out.

Beans shot a nervous look at me, then stammered, “Uh, y-yeah! The Great Lizard!”

I quickly chimed in, my voice way too enthusiastic, "Oh yeah... yeah, he hired us exterminators, yup!"

Green nodded excitedly. “Oh yeah, isn’t the Great Lizard just the best?”

Orange hesitated, clearly uncomfortable. “Uh, maybe I don’t really—”

Before he could finish, Green jabbed him in the ribs, and Orange quickly corrected himself, “Oh, uh, yeah! He’s the best!” His nervous laugh almost made me laugh too.

I gave them both a forced smile, and realized Beans was already out of sight. I waved at the lizards, trying to sound confident. “Yeah, he is. Well, we’ll see you later!”

With that, I hustled up the stairs to catch up.

Green smiled after us. “They seem nice.”

Orange sighed, his tone dark. “Yeah... probably gonna die. Those monsters are scary.”

Green nodded, the smile fading from his face. “Yeah... but, uh, they’ll be fine. Probably.”

As I ascended the stairs, I looked at everyone, and they all seemed to be holding back laughter. "Is everything okay?" I asked, confused.

Beans snickered and said, "Oh, yes, it's fine, Mr. Exterminator."

We all burst into quiet laughter, the tension in the air easing just a little, and then followed Gwen into the next room.

As I stepped in behind her, I noticed strands of thick, silvery silk hanging from the ceiling and clinging to the walls like a webbed curtain. Gwen groaned ahead of me.

“Great… spiders,” she muttered, her voice laced with irritation.

The sight of the webs sent a chill down my back. It brought back the memory of that first cavern we’d stumbled into—walls crawling with giant spiders, the way their legs scraped against stone, the panic in our chests.

Gwen moved cautiously now, her sword drawn and ready. I mirrored her, glancing up at the strands above, wondering if any of them were watching us from the shadows.

The room stretched out, curving around a corner. As we approached the corner and peeked around, we discovered more webs and a door. Remaining vigilant for traps, we moved closer.

Upon entering the next room, we noticed spherical orbs of webbing clustered in the corner, with a door located on the opposite end.

Confused, I asked, "What are these?"

Bluma looked to Beans and muttered: "Splich?"  

Gwen shivered and remarked, "A splich? I'd rather deal with spiders."

"What's a splich?" I inquired, my curiosity piqued. "I've never heard of it before."

Beans pondered for a moment and replied, "Most people don't survive after encountering one. The stories vary but they are bad news, stay on guard."

Gwen pointed toward the webbed clusters lining the walls. “Burn the web-orb things, Bushy,” she said. “I’d rather not deal with them or the splich on our way back.”

I held out my hand and set the nearest one ablaze. The fire caught quickly, crackling through the silk. As the flames spread, I caught Beans staring at his hands, eyebrows furrowed. He looked back up without saying anything, and we moved on through the next doorway.

The room we entered was wide, with a second doorway on the same wall we came through and a staircase directly across from it. Unfortunately, this chamber had even more of those webbed orbs—bigger ones.

“Burn them too,” Gwen muttered.

I stepped forward, flames at the ready—but before I could strike, one of the orbs burst open. A large, glowing spider-like creature lunged at me with startling speed, launching a sticky strand of web straight at my face.

I stumbled back with a yelp and threw the fire instinctively. The flames slammed into it, and the creature screeched as it caught fire, writhing in pain.

"It's a splich!" Gwen shouted, drawing her sword along with Bluma.

They launched an attack, with Gwen landing the first blow and severing some of the creature's legs. It shrieked and lunged at me with its fangs bared, but Bluma swiftly struck it down, causing it to squirt out glowing yellow blood.

Before Beans could make an attempt, another splich emerged from the other side of the room, shooting a web at him and trying to reel him closer. Beans stumbled, grasping onto the floor's broken tiles, he pulled back, breaking free from the web's grasp.

The splich tried to jump out at Beans however he managed to pull out his ax and smack it away. The splich landed on its back then hurriedly scrambled to its feet.

As the creature scuttled away, I tried to call out—but the web was still plastered across my face. I clawed at it, stumbling back, but the sticky threads clung tight, sealing over my mouth and nose. Panic bubbled up in my chest. I dropped to my knees, fingers fumbling at the strands, but they stretched like glue. My heart pounded as I yanked harder, growling in frustration.

I could barely hear the others over the muffled sound in my ears, just the thrum of my own pulse and the sharp rasp of my breath.

Gwen chuckled and grabbed a cross-bolt to cut me out. I quickly stood up and looked around, asking, "What happened!?"

Gwen smiled and replied, "Oh, nothing too serious." She then walked over to the dead splich and stuck her sword into it. "Which way now, boss?"

I stood up, surveying the area, seeing that the room had two doors. I opened the closest door and saw a short staircase, walking up, I discovered a dead end to my left, but to my right, there was a long hallway that stretched beyond my line of sight. "..hmm Hey Beans! What does the other door look like?" I asked, reluctant to venture down the dark corridor.

Beans opened his door and yelled back, "Looks like the room takes a turn around a corner, but besides more silk, not much."

I descended the stairs and said, "Well, let's go that way first." Gwen, still gripping her sword and began moving toward the door, with Bluma and me following suit.

Upon entering, we discovered four more doorways, but none with doors. "For the love... Why can't the big bad evil guy just show up already!? I want to fight them!" Gwen exclaimed in frustration.

I chuckled and reassured her, "We'll find them soon, Gwen. I want to get this over with as much as you do.." Gwen groaned in response

Beans then took a look at all the doorways “Deta and Gwen, you both take a door, and I'll take this one in front of me. Bluma, you could stand in between so that if something goes wrong, you can reach any of us the fastest."

Bluma nodded, and each of us headed towards a doorway. I barely had time to take a step before something struck my back—thick, sticky webbing latching onto me like a trap. I yelled out, reaching for the doorframe, but the force yanked me off my feet and dragged me backward across the floor.

From the corner of my eye, I saw Gwen get snatched in the same instant, her sword clattering to the ground as she struggled. Beans shouted something—cut off as a strand wrapped around his arm and wrenched him off balance.

I twisted, trying to burn the web with a spark, but the strands were too fast, too strong. We were all pulled toward the dark room ahead, helpless against the pull. I caught a glimpse of Bluma lunging forward, arms outstretched for Beans—but she vanished behind the silk just as he was yanked through the doorway.

As I was dragged in, I saw I was being pulled by a large splich. It attempted to bite me, but through a sloppy dodge that landed me on the floor, the splich hit the wall and fell to the ground. In a panic, scrambling to get off the floor, I extended my hands, trying to cast fire. To my surprise, just as the spider got up and tried to rush me, a sphere made of flames formed between me and the splich, causing it to jump backward in confusion.

"What... what the heck!?" I muttered, eyes wide in disbelief.

As I jolted my hand back out of shock, the fireball followed, keeping the same distance from me. Moving my hand to the side, I watched as it trailed obediently, still hovering. Suddenly, the splich jumped at me again. Instinctively, I swung my arm around, and the ball of fire engulfed the creature in an instant.

For a moment, I thought it was over, but the splich, burning and enraged, managed to sink its fangs into my arm. Pain shot through me as it clamped down harder, its strength not yet spent.

I screamed as the splich bit into my arm, trying to tear it off. The fireball I’d summoned was still burning the creature, but not fast enough. My lack of control was dragging the fight on. With my other arm trapped, I couldn’t reach for anything else, and I was terrified of burning myself with the flames.

I looked towards the doorway in hopes someone might be able to help me, but saw a strange figure with a bow and arrow pointing at me. I tried to move the ball of fire to the man but the splich ripped off a chunk of my arm then quickly bit down again causing me to yell out in pain and the fireball to slam on the ground, putting it out.

The splich latched onto my arm, its pincers digging into the stone and bark of my body, trying to chew through like I was meat. I shouted, twisting, trying to slam it against the wall—but it clung tighter, shrieking with each impact.

A sudden thud hit the floor nearby—something fast, heavy. Then a loud twang echoed through the chamber, followed by a sharp crack and a yelp from the creature. Something hard smacked into its side—maybe a blade, maybe a blunt edge—and it reeled back, shrieking as it finally let go.

I hit the floor, gasping, just as two more sharp strikes pierced the Splich. One stabbed straight through its bulbous head, the other into its abdomen. The monster gave one last spasm, then slumped, unmoving.

I looked up in a daze, breathing hard. Gwen stood over me, sword drawn and panting. Bluma was beside her, silent but still and tense, her own blade pulled free from the creature’s twitching form.

Beans skidded into the room behind them and rushed to my side, grabbing my arm. "You good, Deta?"

I winced, sitting up slowly. "Not really. But I think I will be."

Gwen’s gaze flicked toward the doorway, her expression tightening. "We have company..."

As we turned to look, we found ourselves face-to-face with four other individuals staring right back at us.

CHAPTER 11                                                                                                                         From a Camp to an Army

As I gazed at the four men, I noticed the diverse range of races and sizes among them. I was taken aback by the presence of humans down here, so I asked them, "What brings the four of you down here?"

A scruffy, short Dwarf cleared his throat, donning a rusty old chest plate and sporting a jet-black beard with a streak of white in it. "Well, we were just sitting by our camp... and noticed a damsel in distress," he replied with a chuckle, while Gwen seemed ready to unleash her fury.

 "Why, you little..." she began, reaching for her sword to pick it out of the splich. Quickly, I stepped in front of her, and Bluma attempted to calm her down.

"Thank you," I expressed with a smile, hoping to prevent Gwen from attacking them.

The old Dwarf chuckled in response, "Not a problem. We are all prisoners down here..." His eyes fell upon Beans, who wore the king's crest on their armor, a symbol typical of knights and squires. Then, his attention shifted to Bluma, who stared back at him.

His gaze turned cold with malice. "You..." he uttered.

Bluma narrowed her eyes, unamused. "Baltimore," she said curtly.

At the sound of her voice, his expression twitched. He blinked, once, like he couldn’t believe she had the nerve to speak to him that way. His jaw tensed.

"Bluma," he muttered, low and sharp, then took a step forward. "Of course it’s you down here. Always so damn quiet, like you’re better than the rest of us. Still playing bodyguard for strangers, I see."

She didn’t respond, just watched him with the same unreadable stillness she always had.

His nostrils flared. “What the hell are you even doing down here?” he snapped, voice rising. “You uptight little knight!”

The other prisoners exchanged confused glances, clearly unsure of what to make of the outburst.

Beans, on the other hand, stepped forward, face tightening with growing fury. “Hey!” he snapped, fists clenched at his sides. “You don’t get to talk to her like that.”

I blinked, surprised by the sharpness in his voice. Even Gwen raised an eyebrow, while Bluma said nothing, her blank face somehow seeming even more unreadable than usual.

Baltimore scoffed, “What, the squire’s gonna lecture me now?”

“Try me,” Beans growled, taking another step forward. There was no trace of his usual nervousness now—just raw protectiveness burning behind his eyes.

“Easy,” I said, instinctively holding a hand up between them, though I wasn’t sure who I was trying to calm down.

Baltimore raised his hands mockingly and leaned back against the wall. “Fine, fine. I’m not here to make friends anyway.”

That didn’t stop Beans from glaring holes through him.

Gwen muttered under her breath, “Well… this just got interesting.”

"What's a knight doing down here?" an Elf asked, eyeing Bluma with an unreadable expression. His voice held a mix of curiosity and skepticism.

The human beside him shrugged, seemingly uninterested. "I don't know... maybe she got exiled? Look, she still has her armor and the king's crest. Doesn't look like someone who's fallen out of favor."

Their conversation barely registered with Bluma as she kept her gaze fixed ahead, but the Dwarf’s voice suddenly broke through the murmurs. He was yelling at Bluma, calling her names and questioning her worth. The insults grated against the air, and it didn’t take long for Beans to tense up beside me.

His usual hesitation evaporated as his anger flared. "Hey, back off!" Beans barked, stepping toward the Dwarf, his face flushed with indignation.

The Dwarf’s eyes flicked to Beans, a twisted smile creeping onto his face as he grabbed a rusty blade from his belt. "You got a problem with me, boy?" he sneered, advancing toward him.

Bluma’s hand shot to her black longsword before any words could be exchanged. The blade was drawn with deadly precision, its dark sheen glinting in the dim light. But just as tension reached its peak, the Elf acted swiftly, seizing the Dwarf by his hair and pulling him back with a surprising amount of force.

"Enough!" the Elf snapped, his voice firm and commanding. "We welcome you four, regardless of the circumstances. There's no escape from this place, so there's no point in fighting."

Baltimore, still fuming, grunted, crossing his arms tightly over his chest. "Whatever, you stupid elf," he muttered under his breath. "Let’s just get back to camp." Without another word, he turned and stormed off, his boots echoing through the stone corridor.

The human and other figures followed the Dwarf, while the Elf turned back to us. "I apologize for his behavior. Come on! Let us lead you back to our camp! We are all prisoners to Iron Hallow."

Bluma looked at Beans, who nodded in agreement. Reluctantly, she agreed as well and let out a sigh. However, Gwen crossed her arms and expressed her skepticism.

"You two can go, but I'd rather cut them up," she remarked.

I sighed, trying to reason with her. "Gwen, come on. This gives us a chance to rest in a safer area of this dungeon for a while."

She rolled her eyes. "What if it's a trap to lure us in with a false sense of security and strip us of our gear, then take us prisoner?"

Shaking my head, I assured her, "If that's the case, we won't be fooled. The moment you sense something suspicious, let us know, and we'll leave, alright?"

Gwen gestured towards the Elf and the others. "Are you telling me that THAT isn't suspicious!?"

The Elf chuckled awkwardly, and I groaned. "Gwen, please. They are better than dealing with those splich creatures."

She groaned in reluctant agreement. As we followed the Elf and the others towards their campsite, I noticed several hallways branching off, each crowded with people. The corridors seemed to lead to small rooms where prisoners lived. As we continued, we were led into a large, round chamber with halls stretching in every direction. The Elf stepped forward, approaching a man clad in what looked like scrap armor, and began speaking with him in low tones. Meanwhile, figures in the hallways peeked out, their eyes on us, whispering among themselves.

"Tch... where are they taking us?" Gwen murmured, her mistrust evident. She held her sword tightly, ready for any sudden movements.

Beans looked around and commented, "I'm not entirely sure, but the farther we go, the more this resembles a dwarven city."

Just then, one of the men hurried down one of the halls. The Elf turned back to us, sporting a smile. "Right this way," he gestured, indicating the path the man had taken.

We exchanged glances, each of us now prepared for whatever might happen, and proceeded down that hallway. It was wide and well-lit, with torches placed every ten feet, providing clear visibility. Gwen and Bluma kept their swords at the ready, anticipating any potential threats, while Beans and I remained vigilant for any traps along the way.

We proceeded through the uneventful hallway and entered a large room guarded by stationed guards. At the center of the back wall, there stood a throne constructed from metal scraps, bones and wood. Seated upon the throne was a towering Orcish person, adorned in remnants of armor and a makeshift crown. As we approached, he greeted us with a crooked smile.

"Welcome. We are glad you have managed to make it safely here. My name is Albuquerque the Half-Orc, but you can call me Ale. I am the chieftain of this dungeon."

Returning his smile, I replied, "It's a pleasure to meet you, Ale."

The chieftain chuckled at my response. "Now, if I may ask, what brings you down here? What did you do to be sent here? Who did you kill?" This caused the whole room of people to  burst out laughing.

I hesitated, aware that revealing the truth about the king sending us could potentially make enemies out of them. "Well, actually, we came down here by choice."

Silence flooded the room, heavy and unsettling, as if the very air had stilled around us. I could hear Gwen sigh from behind me.

Ale leaned forward, sitting on the edge of his throne, and spoke with a hint of suspicion in his voice, "By choice, you say... Why?"

Panic surged within me, as I tried to come up with a plausible explanation. Beans, equally nervous, struggled to contain his flatulence but let out a faint squeak. Which made everyone burst out in awkward laughter.

Coughing slightly, I continued, "Well, we had heard tales of a mighty and powerful lizard residing here. We have come to challenge and slay the beast."

The chief leaned back in his chair, scratching his chin thoughtfully. "Slay the beast, hmm?"

I nodded eagerly, adding, "Yes! And perhaps we could seek your assistance in this endeavor?" I chuckled nervously, but Ale responded with a menacing glare. He summoned one of the guards and whispered something to them.

The guard nodded, and the chief turned back to us. "I’m surprised you were able to know of this great beast.. Maybe that means some of the men made it out and turned tail on us…," he growled and declared, rising from his throne and approaching us. "We shall embark on this venture together. However!”

His voice echoed loudly through the room and everyone still holding their weapons out gripped them tighter.

Ale stood in front of me and put his hand on my shoulder. “Not before giving you time to rest and showing you around." A warm smile replaced his previous menacing expression.

I believe we were all surprised by that but I expressed my gratitude. Ale led us down a hallway to the left, guiding us on a tour of the area. "These are forgeries," he explained. "This place used to be a dwarven kingdom, but one day, The current royal house was built over the ruins. The forge itself is broken, so we can't do much with it, but we make do."

Peering inside, we observed individuals of various races and genders, attempting to repair the forge and hammer away at the metal, only to face repeated failures.

As Ale chuckled, Beans remarked, "Wow, there are lots of people in there. I thought prisoners would fight to the death down here…"

Ale nodded in acknowledgment. "Indeed, some of them were born here. This is all they've ever known. We hope that one day we can escape and give our children a better life..."

Bluma didn’t say much. I could tell she wasn’t focused on his words—just staring ahead with that quiet calm she always had. I knew she believed the children were innocent, but that their parents… had earned what came to them. She probably helped send some of them down there, after all.

We continued the tour, with Ale showing us a few more rooms. Finally, we reached their farmhouse. Upon entering, I was disheartened by the lack of plant life and the dirty water. Determined, I walked into the center of the room and sat down. Ale raised an eyebrow as a green light emanated from me. Some of the people in the room raised makeshift spears, ready to attack, but an Elf intervened.

"Calm down, brothers. He's using magic. I'm not sure what kind, but it doesn’t seem dangerous." Gradually, the people lowered their spears.

Gwen’s View

Ale turned to me and the others, informing us that the tour was complete and we would reconvene the next morning at the sound of the horn. With a slight bow, he departed.

I sighed in frustration. "Great. Now what do we do?"

Beans seemed to think for a moment before suggesting, "Well... I kind of want to see the forge again. Maybe I could help with the repairs?"

Bluma, arms crossed, reluctantly nodded. She didn't trust some of the people, but she had to keep up appearances. With a sigh, she joined Beans in heading back to the forge to lend a hand.

I rolled my eyes, glanced at Deta, and sighed before setting off to find something to do.

Deta’s View

A few hours later, some people returned to the farm, dropping their weapons as they entered. They were met with an astonishing sight—the once barren land had transformed. Lush greenery now covered the area, with healthy crops and even fruit trees sprouting. I remained seated on the ground, surrounded by blooming flowers.

One of the men tapped my shoulder and asked, "Excuse me... did... Did you do this?"

I stood up and smiled. "Yes, I did."

The men expressed their joy and gratitude for the transformed land. They were thankful that their families would finally have fresh food. They asked if they could do anything to show their appreciation, but I simply requested they take care of their families. With nods of agreement, they eagerly began harvesting. Feeling drained from using magic, I left the farm and wandered through the camp.

I watched as Bluma roamed the camp, observing how the prisoners had managed to create a semblance of life in the dungeon. As she walked, she noticed a few hooded men watching her intently. Beans, on the other hand, was exploring the forge, asking questions and immersing himself in the workshop. Bluma leaned against a wall, watching him with a soft chuckle.

Suddenly, a large man wearing a tattered hood approached Bluma and requested her presence. Intrigued, she followed him to the training room, where several men and women were sparring. As she entered, the combat stopped, and all eyes turned to her. Without warning, a man charged at her from behind with a rusty dagger. Bluma swiftly evaded the attack, disarmed him, and tossed him aside. The others readied themselves for a fight, but Bluma drew her sword, ready to teach them a lesson without causing serious harm.
        Eventually, I found Gwen in the training area, pushing the prisoners to improve their combat skills. She was relentless, urging them to persevere and warning them of potential dangers. I chuckled softly at her determination and continued exploring. I stumbled upon a room where many people were sleeping, cared for by a compassionate woman. She smiled gently and offered me a place to rest. Grateful, I thanked her and settled down.

The following day, we prepared for the upcoming battle. Ale, Gwen, Bluma, Beans, and I gathered to discuss the plan. Ale informed us that the reptile we sought resided in the dungeon’s central area, surrounded by rooms infested with spliches. We acknowledged the need for caution and speed to avoid detection. Ale rallied his men, emphasizing the significance of defeating the serpent as a means to secure their freedom. The men cheered, fueled by hope for a future outside the dungeon. With our combined force of about forty, we set out confidently, listening to their voices as they shared dreams of life beyond the dungeon.

Gwen and Baltimore seemed to fight for leading the way, I turned to Ale, who was focused and ready. "Ale, if you make it out, what are your plans for the future?"

My question caught Bluma's attention. She seemed to lean in a little, as if she were eager to hear the answer.

Ale took a deep breath before answering. "Well... I think I'll seek a peaceful life. In the past, I was just a tool of war. Nothing could stop me," he said, clenching his fist. "But that thrill faded. Taking lives no longer gave me fulfillment." He looked at me and smiled. "Once I’m out, I plan to rediscover myself."

I smiled back. "That sounds like a good plan."

Ale chuckled and playfully raised his fist. "You're alright, Plant Man." I bumped my fist against his.

"Thanks. You're pretty alright too." We both laughed, but it stopped as we reached the next room.

As we entered, we found the halls choked with sticky webs. Green spheres had sprouted since our last time here, clustered tightly across the corridor like some sick imitation of a wall. But no Splichs stirred in sight, and we decided to lead the army forward.

That was a mistake.

Just as we maneuvered to turn around, the webs behind us twitched—snapping underweight. Basilisk-folk poured in, not slithering like I expected, but running—some on two legs, some on four, armed with hooked spears and jagged shields. We barely had time to form a defense.

It was chaos.

Gwen shouted orders. Bluma took the front line, her sword flashing in the dim torchlight. Beans ducked low, swinging his axe with precision, while Ale’s staff pulsed with purple light, casting illusions to disorient our attackers. I fought beside Gwen, slashing and shielding, trying to keep the Basilisks from breaking our formation.

But there were too many.

For every one we knocked down, two more surged from the side tunnels. A red-scaled one lunged at me with fangs bared—I blocked the bite just in time, but the force knocked me off my feet. I scrambled up, only to see Ale nearly impaled by a long pike. Gwen tackled the attacker before it struck true.

“This is bad!” I gasped, backing toward a wall.

Ale turned, scanning the scene—our army was being cut down or cornered, our fighters scattered. He looked like he wanted to argue with fate itself.

“Retreat!” he yelled, voice cracking under the weight of it.

We broke up. There was no formation left—only a desperate scramble to survive. We sprinted through webbed halls and past the green globes, some bursting underfoot and leaking sickly fluid. It took what felt like hours to find a pocket of safety—a collapsed section where the Basilisks couldn't easily follow.

We collapsed there. I could barely breathe.

Ale stood near the edge, looking pale. “Half the army... they didn’t make it,” he whispered.

Gwen sat with a grunt, tearing cloth to wrap a deep gash on her arm. Beans and I moved from one injured soldier to another, using what healing we could spare. The air buzzed with pain, fear, and doubt.

Then Baltimore snapped.

"You knew we’d die!" he screamed, staggering to his feet. "You never intended to kill the Lizard King! You led us here to die!"

But then he froze, eyes locked past me.

I turned—and my stomach dropped.

A hundred Basilisk-folk, maybe more, lined the hall behind us. No longer rushing. No longer fighting. They moved like they already knew they'd won.

A towering blue Basilisk with feathery wings stepped forward. His voice was gravel smoothed by smoke. “Tie them up. The Lizard King will decide their fate.”

We fought, of course—we tried—but it was over before it began. We were outnumbered, surrounded, broken.

They bound our wrists and marched us in a line. Gwen and I ended up just behind Baltimore. Beans, Bluma, and Ale were further back, watching silently. The air hung thick with mildew and rot, and the only sounds were footsteps and the drag of rope on stone.

Baltimore wouldn't stop muttering—angry, venomous words—and Gwen snapped. She kicked him hard behind the knee, sending him stumbling.

"What the hell!?" he barked.

She spat at his feet. “Screw you, Baltimore. If you’d stayed behind, we wouldn’t be in this mess.”

He whirled around, shouting again—but a tall orange Basilisk slammed the butt of his spear into Baltimore’s head. He dropped without another word. The Basilisk slung him over a shoulder and moved to the front.

And then we walked—silent, humiliated, bound. Every step took us deeper, the stone walls damp and narrowing, as if the dungeon itself wanted to swallow us whole.

I felt a rush of nerves go through my body causing me to shake slightly and pull my arms up. After a few seconds I realized, the ropes weren't on me, looking at my wrist I could see bits of the rope hairs stuck on some of the wood and rocks on my wrist… how long was I free?

In a panic I looked around, and seeing a Basilisk walking towards us I grew vines and had them wrap around my wrists hoping to trick them.

Just as I did so a guttural voice rumbled from behind me. "Keep moving!"  a green Basilisk with slitted yellow eyes, shoved me forward with the butt of its spear. I stumbled but managed to keep my balance.

Once he walked away toward the front of the group, I looked to Gwen and saw her quicken her breathing and sweat began to form.

Gwen’s View

My thoughts spiraled out of control, like waves crashing over me, threatening to drag me under. "Stay calm. Breathe. You’re fine. It’s just rope." I tried to convince myself, but the words felt hollow, as if I were grasping at smoke. The panic swelled in my chest, my heart hammering so violently it was as if my rib cage could no longer contain it. GET THIS OFF OF ME! The scream echoed in my mind, rattling louder than anything around me.

The ropes felt too tight, suffocating, like they were pressing into my skin, into my bones. My breath came in shallow gasps, each one more desperate than the last, like I couldn't get enough air. It was happening again—I’m trapped!

Flashes of past horrors flooded my mind. The feeling of being bound, helpless, vulnerable—left to rot, or worse. My throat tightened as if I were reliving every moment of those torturous days. I'm not okay! I'm never getting out of this... I'm going to be trapped here forever! I could barely think beyond the panic, my vision blurring as tears filled my eyes.

I can’t do this again…

The dark thoughts wrapped around me tighter than the ropes, squeezing the hope out of me. It was as if the air around me thickened, making it harder to breathe, harder to think. My body tensed—every muscle locked, my mind screaming at me to either run or give in, to stop the torment that gnawed at my sanity.

But then, something shifted—a small, barely noticeable movement. At first, I couldn't make sense of it. My hand felt something, a brush of motion, soft but distinct. Blinking through the haze of panic, I forced myself to look down.

Deta was behind me, his arms no longer tied behind his back, somehow, he'd managed to free himself. He was so focused on the rope, his fingers working at the knots of rope that bound me, silently undoing my restraints.

I was still trapped in my own head, my mind fought him. It’s not enough. He can't save me, We won’t make it out of this. It’s just another trick, another way to break me...

Then I felt my hand had somehow found its way to him, my fingers wrapping around his pinky. It was small, almost insignificant, but it was real. He didn’t flinch, didn’t hesitate. That tiny touch became my anchor, I wanted to let go and get out myself… but my grip tightened as if holding on was the only thing keeping me from drowning.

Deta’s View

I looked at her, and to my relief, she had stopped sweating profusely, and her breathing was gradually slowing down. I smiled, realizing that she understood I was genuinely trying to help her, and also glad she didn't intend to tear my pinky off, as her grip began to loosen even though she was still twisting it painfully.

"Alright, everyone, line up in the center!" a commanding voice boomed as we approached a large cave entrance.

As we entered the cave, the lighting seemed dim to me, but some of the human prisoners grumbled about not being able to see properly.

"Tch... humans," Gwen muttered, rolling her eyes.

"Can you see in here?" I expressed surprise.

She looked unimpressed. "Yes, I'm half elf. We can see in dark places."

I chuckled and said, "Oh, that makes sense!... Wait, you're half elf?"

She sighed. "Yeah, yeah. Now hurry and untie me. The Lizards forgot to take away people's armor and weapons."

"Oh, right, good idea... but can I use my pinky?" I asked. As soon as the words left my mouth, she quickly released her grip, and I let out a sigh of relief, grateful that her grasp was no longer causing pain.

Bluma, surveying the surroundings, noticed that every wall appeared normal except for one that seemed slightly convex. To the west, a portion of the wall appeared distinct. Several Basilisk-folk congregated in the center and began hissing and screeching, causing the wall to shift. Everyone froze as the wall moved, revealing itself to be a huge dragon with fiery red scales.

With a large yawn the dragon unleashed a blast of flames, engulfing nine prisoners and claiming their lives. "Who dares awaken me from my slumber?"

The large orange Basilisk-folk, who appeared minuscule in comparison, spoke up. "Oh, great Lizard King! We have brought you a sacrifice! We hope it pleases you!"

All the Basilisk-folk prostrated themselves before the dragon, redirecting its attention to our group.

The dragon grinned menacingly. "Very good... it has been a long time since I feasted on flesh this fresh."

The room grew hotter and brighter as the dragon's scales radiated a vibrant orange glow. One of its wings appeared to have been torn off, while the other spread out like a rolling sunset.

The dragon then approached our group, consisting of nine survivors and nine charred bodies. It reached down and devoured the burnt victims with a chuckle. "Medium rare... quite delightful," it remarked, relishing the grisly feast.

Meanwhile, Gwen glanced back towards the entrance. "Something is coming," she warned.

I turned my attention to the path we had traversed and heard faint hissing noises that grew louder. The dragon paused its feast, acknowledging the escalating hissing sound that echoed throughout the room. Suddenly, a colossal snake emerged from the entrance, towering in size similar to the dragon.

The dragon sneered upon seeing the colossal snake enter. “You're still alive…"

The snake spoke with disdain. "Unlike you shall be here soon!!" With a resolute charge, the giant snake trampled over most of the Basilisk-folk, engaging in a cataclysmic battle with the dragon.

The ground shook as the dragon and snake tumbled, those of us who were still standing were forcefully struck by the serpent's tail and flung against a wall. Gwen and I tumbled to the ground.

I quickly got up and went to Gwen who was face first on the ground. “Hurry up and untie me, Bushy!” She yelled.

I pulled at the rope and finished untying her. “You're free! What is that thing?" I asked, bewildered.

She stood up as fast as she could and retrieved her crossbow and fired a bolt at the dragon. "It's a giant snake and dragon what's it look like!!" she then rushed towards Bluma to free her.

I ran to Beans and pulled the ropes off him, he stood up and pulled out his ax, "It's the Guardian Serpent!" Beans watched their fight and upon turning alerted us, "Behind you!"

Three Basilisk-folk attempted to ambush us. "You're not getting away!" they yelled in unison. Before I could even reach for my weapon, Ale swung his glowing staff, sending the trio flying through the air.

"Are you two alright?" he asked, concern etched on his face. Beans and I nodded in response. "Good! Now let's aid the Serpent!" he declared, charging into the fray to battle the Basilisk-folk.

Beans looked at me as we rose to our feet, preparing our weapons. Gwen then untied Bluma from the ropes along with a few other prisoners, and we charge towards the battling serpent, dragon, and Basilisk-folk.

The Serpent's powerful strike and coiling caused the dragon to fall, shaking the entire cavern. As they fell over, the ground beneath us began to crack, and we realized the danger. Bluma and Gwen quickly rush towards us, attempting to pull us away from the potential collapse. As the two ran towards us the floor gave out from underneath us and them, sending us plummeting into the dark abyss below.

The four of us, along with some prisoners and Basilisk-folk, plummet into the abyss. Screams echo all around us, and panic ensues.

In the midst of the chaos, Beans shouts, "Use your scrolls!" and he pulls out his own. The three of us took out our scrolls, and upon speaking the writing on them, a light gray aura formed around us, slowing our descent. I glance at Bluma and Beans with a sense of relief.

“Bushy!!” Gwen screamed. I snapped my head around just in time to see her plummeting, her scroll malfunctioning, spiraling out of control. Dread crept in my chest as she disappeared into the darkness below. Panic surged through me.

“Gwen!!” I  shouted, my voice breaking with terror.

I spun toward Bluma, my eyes wild with desperation. “Bluma—throw me!”

Without hesitation, Bluma kicked off the wall and shot toward me. With every ounce of her strength, she launched me into the abyss after Gwen. Wind whipped past my ears as I plummeted through the void. I caught a glimpse of her, just a shadow now, falling faster than I could reach.

I cursed, frustration boiling inside me as I continued to slow down.

In one frantic motion, I summoned my thorn whip, feeling it thrash violently in my grip. My mind raced. I had to act fast. I tied an empty potion bottle to its end, giving it weight. With a wild swing, I hurled it toward Gwen, desperation in every movement.

The whip snapped tight. I felt it catch her leg. Relief flooded me as her descent slowed, but my heart still thundered, knowing we were both far from safe.

"Are you okay?" I ask Gwen, my voice filled with concern. I started receding the whip causing me to pull in closer to her.

She looked at me, her face a mixture of fear and relief. "What do you think?! I almost died!" Her face bore a frightened and annoyed expression.

After a moment, we spot the ground approaching, and we brace ourselves for the impact. Upon landing, Gwen quickly untangles my vine whip from her leg.

I am about to speak when she interrupts, her voice filled with reluctant gratitude. "Thank you... This is the second time you've saved my life."

CHAPTER 12                                                                                                                                 In the Dark

I smiled and replied, "No problem. Besides, I owe you one for helping me with that splich yesterday."

She shook her head. "No, Bluma did most of the work, so I'm still in debt." Then she turned to me and said, "Don't think you're getting rid of me until I repay that and have you owe me!"

I smiled and chuckled, saying, "Sounds like a deal."

Suddenly, we heard a faint yell from above. "Hey! Are you guys okay?" We looked up and saw Bluma with Beans waving at us.

"We're good!" I shouted back, "But hurry and come down here so we can go back up!"

Beans chuckled. They both then landed next to us. Beans looked around and asked, "Where are we?"

We all froze when Gwen spoke up, her voice so soft it barely reached us over the distant echo of dripping water.
"We're in the Underworld."

The words settled like a curse in the air.

I looked around slowly, my breath catching. Towering caverns stretched endlessly in every direction, cloaked in shadow and silence. Jagged stalagmites jutted up from the stone floor like fangs, while thick stalactites dripped from the ceiling above, some so long they nearly kissed the ground. The air felt thick and damp, clinging to my skin, and every step echoed too loud—like the cave itself was listening.

"The Underworld?!" Beans’ voice cracked as he stumbled back a step, the sound bouncing off the rock walls in jagged fragments. His wide eyes flicked to Bluma, who gave a slow, grim nod. Even without words, her meaning was unmistakable. Whatever this place was, it was bad.

That nod alone sent a cold spike down my spine.

I turned to Beans, trying to grasp what they already seemed to know.
"The... Underworld?" I repeated, uncertain. The name meant nothing to me—just a word—but the look in their eyes told me enough. Gwen’s pale face. Beans’ trembling hands. Bluma’s clenched jaw. They were terrified.

Beans whipped around, eyes darting like something might leap from the dark at any moment. He leaned in, voice just above a whisper.
"Shh! Don’t say it like that!" he hissed. "The Underworld is a place no one wants to be. Everything down here—everything—is twisted. Evil."

A low wind stirred through the cavern, but it carried no scent and made no sound. It felt wrong.

As if on cue, a deafening roar echoed through the cavern, sending a shiver down my back. Bluma wasted no time, yanking us behind a nearby stalagmite.

"Quiet," she hissed, her eyes darting around.

The thumping of heavy footsteps grew louder, shaking the ground beneath us. Against my better judgment, I leaned out to see what was causing the noise. I froze, as I spotted a massive stone creature, its body blending seamlessly with the stalagmites.

The creature crawled up the wall and clung to the ceiling, finally going still. I exhaled in shaky relief— I shrill squeak then echoed by us. I turned to Beans as the last time I heard that, it came from him.

He turned bright red. "Sorry," he whispered, his voice trembling with fear.

"Move," Bluma whispered urgently.

Beans and I nodded, inching forward behind her. But as I glanced back, I noticed Gwen, still crouched behind the stalagmite, her face pale. Her whole body was trembling, her breath coming out in rapid, shallow gasps. She didn’t look like she could move at all.

"Gwen?" I called softly, stepping toward her. No response. Her eyes were wide, fixed on some distant point in the cavern, unblinking.

I reached out slowly, my hand barely brushing her arm. She jerked back violently, eyes wide with terror. "Don't touch me!" she cried out, her voice echoing through the vast cavern. The sound made everyone freeze. Bluma and Beans turned to her, wide-eyed, as Gwen clamped her hand over her mouth, tears welling in her eyes.

The creatures began crawling down from the cave's roof, resembling the colossal one we had seen before. "Run!" Bluma yelled as the monster started descending the wall. Gwen, Beans, and I sprinted alongside her, the monsters chasing after us, their stone legs pounding loudly against the cave floor. Bluma made a sharp left turn, and when Gwen and I followed, we froze, nearly falling off a cliff. Looking ahead, I saw Bluma running along the edge toward a rock bridge stretching across a giant crevasse.

"Come on, Gwen!" I urged, and she nodded as we ran as fast as we could.

Just as we reached the bridge, the stone monsters burst around the corner. Some tumbled into the crevasse, while others pursued us onto the bridge. As I watched some of them fall, I noticed a bright red light at the very bottom, where they seemed to disappear.

Gwen and I reached the midpoint of the bridge when some of the stones gave way, and I almost fell. Gwen looked back and rushed to my aid. "Deta!"

She helped me up, and an idea struck me. "Gwen, go! I have an idea!" I turned toward the approaching creatures.

"You idiot! You're going to die!" Gwen protested, but I extended my hand, summoning a large ball of fire.

"Just go!" I shouted.

Reluctantly, Gwen ran off as I hurled the fireball at the bridge, hoping to destroy it. A few cracks formed beneath the impact, but before I could strike again, the fireball fizzled out and suddenly exploded, knocking me back and scorching my skin.

Frustrated, I tried to summon the fire again, but something felt wrong. Instead of heat, I felt a strange, heavy pressure beneath my feet. The air around me shifted, and the rocks at my feet began to tremble, rising slowly into the air. I gasped as they started spinning, whirling faster and faster, pulled into a chaotic orbit around me.

"Come on… work!" I muttered, trying to regain control. But it was like the magic had a mind of its own, tapping into something deeper than just fire.

The rocks spun violently, obeying this wild energy, and I could feel the power spiraling out of control. With a desperate shove, I sent the rocks flying into the air, crashing them back down onto the bridge.

The impact was far more powerful than I'd intended. The stones slammed into the surface, shattering the bridge as deep cracks rapidly spread outward, racing toward me.

Yes, it worked! I thought, but my relief quickly turned to panic. Shoot, it worked too well! The entire structure was falling apart beneath me. I turned and ran, the sound of collapsing stone thundering behind me, as the monsters chasing us plummeted into the pit below.

I kept running, boots slamming against ancient stone as the bridge cracked and crumbled behind me. The deafening sound of grinding rock echoed through the chasm, each slab breaking loose and plunging into the void below. Dust exploded around my feet, and I could feel the very earth disintegrating beneath me.

“Crap! Come on!” I shouted, forcing myself to move faster, even as the ground trembled with every collapsing section. My breath came in ragged bursts, lungs burning, panic pounding in my chest. The far ledge was in sight—but the bridge was vanishing behind me, catching up too fast.

“Hurry!” Bluma's voice rang out above the chaos. She stood at the edge, one arm outstretched, her four eyes wide with alarm. Her fingers reached for mine, desperate and sure.

I launched myself forward with every last ounce of strength I had. The final chunk of stone crumbled beneath my foot mid-jump, sending a jolt through my body. My fingers stretched out, straining for hers.

For a heartbeat, I thought I had it—thought I was safe.

But I missed.

My hand swung through open air, and my stomach lurched. Gravity took me.

“No—no—no—!” The sickening drop tore a scream from my throat as I fell.

“Deta!” Beans and Gwen shouted in unison, their voices jagged with panic. I caught a glimpse of their terrified faces peering over the edge, the wind whipping their hair as dust swirled around them.

“Deta!” Beans cried again—but then his expression changed. His eyes widened in sudden hope.

I threw out my hand mid-fall, summoning vines in a panic. They burst from the stone walls with a crack and a hiss, wrapping tight around me just before I hit bottom. The impact yanked the air from my lungs, but I was safe—dangling in a cocoon of green, suspended just above the jagged rocks below.

"I'm alright!" I called up, voice shaky but alive. "Though I could really use some help getting up…” I added with a nervous chuckle, eyeing the vines with uncertainty. They creaked ominously under my weight, leaves fluttering in the updraft.

Above, I saw movement as Gwen and Beans scrambled into action.

And I tried very hard not to look down again.

Gwen smiled down at me. "That was so dumb, Bushy,"  she then pulled out a rope and lowered it down. After several minutes of tugging and effort, they finally managed to pull me back up.

"Thanks, guys," I said, catching my breath, grateful to be back on solid ground.

Beans clapped me on the back with a jump, his relief evident. "We're glad you're okay, Deta," he said with a smile.

I smiled back. "Me too, let's figure out how to get out of here."

Gwen’s View

Bluma and Deta took the lead, their footsteps echoing softly against the damp stone, while I hung back, keeping to the rear. Beans walked somewhere in between, casting glances over his shoulder. He must've noticed the way I held my arms tightly to myself, or the way my eyes kept darting to every shadowed corner.

He slowed his pace until he was beside me. “Hey… what’s wrong?”

I didn’t look at him for long—just a brief flicker of eye contact before I turned away, pulse quickening with that awful, creeping tightness in my chest. The kind that made it hard to breathe, like the air itself didn’t want me here.

Beans sighed. “Gwen, if something’s on your mind, speak it. If not, then quit acting rude.”

I exhaled hard, not quite ready to talk but knowing he wouldn’t drop it. My voice came out quieter than I meant. “I just… have bad memories here.”

His expression changed—eyes searching my face, some of the frustration fading. “Wait, you’ve been in the Underworld before?”

I nodded slowly. The stone corridors around us seemed to close in tighter with every step. “Yeah. Multiple times. Since I was really young…”

I hugged myself, the cave walls starting to blur at the edges. My feet kept moving, but everything in me wanted to turn and run the other way.

Beans fell silent, his gaze softening, but he didn’t press for more. I was thankful for that. I didn’t want to unravel. Not now. Not here. I kept walking in silence, staring ahead, the only sound the distant echo of dripping water and a far-off growl that made my stomach twist.

“...Well,” Beans murmured, “you’re not anymore.” He offered a small, lopsided smile before drifting back to walk beside Bluma.

I watched him go, the echo of his words settling deep in my chest, though the unease still clawed at me. The air down here carried something heavy, something ancient and cruel. Each gust from the tunnels brought with it memories I didn’t want. Memories I didn’t speak of.

A low roar rumbled in the distance. I tensed. Every sound bounced too long, like the place was alive and listening. “I just want to stay safe and as far from here as possible,” I muttered under my breath.

Distracted, I walked straight into Bluma’s back. She glanced at me, her expression unreadable, then turned forward again. The group had stopped. I shifted to the side to see why.

Up ahead, pale blue lights floated like slow-moving fireflies in the dark.

“What are those?” Deta asked quietly, his voice edged with wariness.

“They’re fufus,” I answered, stepping a little closer before realizing I’d instinctively moved ahead of the group.

“Fufus?” he repeated.

Beans cocked his head. “What are those?”

I glanced back at them, managing a faint smile. “Fufus are the only nice things down here.”

As I spoke, the lights responded—softening in color and drifting toward us, like they understood. One of them settled on my outstretched hand: a small, furred creature, weightless and warm. Its two eyes blinked up at me as its coat shimmered between soft hues of blue and green.

The gentle presence of the fufu eased something inside me. Not enough to erase the memories—but enough to let me breathe.

Deta laughed quietly, stretching out his hand. “Aw, they’re adorable.”

Another fufu landed there, curling into his palm as he stroked its downy fur.

“They’re drawn to mental energy,” I explained, still watching the one on my hand. “That’s their food source.”

Beans, wide-eyed, immediately took a step back and covered his head. “I don’t need a fufu eating my brain!”

I laughed—an actual laugh—and shook my head. “Not like that, Dwarf. They duplicate your thoughts and memories, then eat the copies.”

The fufu on my hand blinked slowly, then pressed its tiny head against my thumb, as if offering comfort. I stroked its back, my voice softer now. “They’re harmless.”

For the first time since we arrived, the air didn’t feel quite so heavy.

Deta’s View

Suddenly, the fufus turned purple and floated away. Bluma, Beans, and I smiled as the fufus departed. Beans softly admitted, "I guess they are kind of cute," which elicited chuckles from Bluma and me.

When I turned to look at Gwen, however, I noticed that she was trembling, her sword at the ready, although the blade seemed much smaller than usual.

"Gwen?" Bluma called out, also puzzled by her behavior, but she didn't respond. I approached her to speak, but the words shriveled on my tongue.

In the darkness ahead, a massive, luminous green eye hovered in the void—unnaturally still, unblinking, and far too focused. It watched us with a predator’s patience, dissecting our movements like a butcher deciding where to make the first cut.

Then came the voice—low and rotted, as if it clawed its way through gravel and rust. "Why... hello... there."

The ground quivered beneath my feet. A root snapped free from the stone and coiled up my wrist, growing bark as it hardened into my staff. The wood throbbed with a sickly green pulse as I fed it magic. My grip tightened around the shaft, bark groaning under the strain. I leveled it forward. “Who are you?”

"My name... does not matter... You four... seem lost, yes?" the creature croaked, each syllable caught between a wheeze and a chuckle. It turned its attention to Beans and Bluma, its eye narrowing like a tightening noose. "I can... help... guide you in the right direction..." It coughed—wet, phlegmy, as though it was trying to clear tar from its lungs.

Gwen shook her head. She didn’t speak, but her jaw locked and her stance grew tense.

Then the creature stepped into view.

Its body was man-sized, but everything about it was wrong. Its skin resembled stretched wax—pale, semi-translucent, and strung over twitching sinew. One enormous eye, veined and slightly glowing, dominated its head, while a grin of needle-thin teeth split its lower face. Spikes jutted from its back at uneven angles, echoing the jagged stalagmites above. Each time it moved, it made a wet clicking noise, like joints too long dry now grinding together.

Its gaze fixed on Gwen. "You seem... familiar..."

Bluma unsheathed her sword in a single motion. Beans’s voice cut through the tension. "What is it you want from us?"

I stepped in front of Gwen. The air grew colder.

The creature hissed as I moved. "Hm... I seek magic... Give me your glowing staff, boy..."

Its fingers curled as it reached forward—long, knotted digits tipped with blackened claws that gleamed wet in the cavern’s dim glow. I yanked the staff back.

"And why should I?" I asked. The air between us was thick with damp, moldy breath.

It didn’t blink—maybe it couldn’t. "Give me the staff imbued with magic, and I will tell you where you can find a way out... Does that sound fair, boy?"

It stretched its arms wide, talons catching the little light there was, and opened its fists—revealing claws sharper than any blade. My pulse thudded behind my ears. “If I give you my staff, will you tell us how to leave?”

The creature nodded too quickly, its body jittering with anticipation. "Yes, yes... I told you. Now give me your staff!!!"

It lunged, but Gwen moved faster. Her sword kissed the creature’s throat with a metallic whisper. It froze, that single eye twitching in its socket.

"Directions first, then the staff," Gwen snapped, though I saw the tremble in her sword arm.

The creature gurgled something foul and pulled back slightly, claws flexing in frustration. "Fine." It pointed a crooked, clawed finger northward. "Go through the Shroom Jungle to the Crystal Plains... You'll find someone who knows a way out..."

Beans stepped forward, skeptical. “I thought you were going to tell us how to get out of here.”

The creature turned its head sharply, vertebrae cracking audibly as it hissed, “I am!... to the best of my… abilities!!” It coughed again—harder this time, spattering something dark onto the stone.

Gwen and I locked eyes. She shook her head. I frowned and murmured, “It’s better than nothing.” Then I turned to face the creature. I forced a smile. “Thank you. And a deal is a deal.”

I handed it the staff.

The light inside died the moment it touched its warped hands—but it didn’t notice. With a shrill, delighted screech, the creature darted backward into the shadows, limbs bending at wrong angles as it vanished.

And just like that, we were moving too—fast, silent, and not daring to look back.

"Well, that was creepy," Beans remarked, a sentiment I shared.

"Yeah, I'm just glad we have some directions now," I responded.

We then heard a contorted scream. Gwen's face turned pale, and she held her sword shakily. Bluma unsheathed her sword, and Beans gripped his ax tightly. I  tried to reach for my staff, only to remember that it was no longer in my possession.

"Shoot." I muttered.

Bluma immediately whispered loudly, "Hide!" and we dispersed, taking cover behind nearby stalagmites.

Soon enough, we heard the creature approaching, raging about being tricked “You can't hide from me magic user! I will tear you apart and feast on your friends' bones!”

We recognized it as the same creature from earlier. As it ran past us, consumed by revenge, we remained hidden until it was at a safe distance, and then cautiously emerged.

"What did you do?!" Beans whispered angered and bewildered.

"I just gave him my staff!" I replied, equally perplexed and shocked.

Beans and I started arguing while trying to stay quiet, but before it escalated further, Bluma smacked both of our heads. "Enough," she scolded us in a hushed tone.

We then decided to alter our path, deviating from our original plan, hoping to lose the pursuing creature. Bluma and Beans took the lead, though Beans was still visibly upset.

"Angry..?" Bluma commented, surprised by his lingering frustration.

Beans' words drifted toward me as I walked beside Gwen. "Well, now we have a monster chasing us because of him! We don’t know how strong it is, and—" He trailed off as Bluma suddenly halted, crouching down and placing a hand on his shoulder. The silent exchange passed between them, and Beans gave a reluctant nod.

I couldn’t quite make out the words, but the heavy silence that followed was enough. My stomach twisted. I wanted to turn and speak, to say something, but I couldn’t bring myself to.

When Bluma straightened and resumed walking, Beans let out a long sigh, then began to approach me. His footsteps were hesitant, and I couldn’t help but feel the weight of his impending apology.

"Hey, Deta," he greeted.

I turned to face him, smiling. "Oh, hey, Beans. Something wrong?"

He returned the smile and said, "Well... I wanted to apologize. I didn’t mean to get so angry at you back there."

I smiled, giving it some thought, and replied, "No worries. We're in a dangerous place, so it's only natural to feel agitated."

Beans chuckled and teased, "Are you calling me scared?"

I responded playfully, "Maybe."

We both chuckled before he went back to join Bluma.

"I think that went well," I chuckled to myself, then looked at Gwen, who had a smile on her face.

"You two are so weird," she commented, picking up her pace. I was left bewildered, unable to comprehend her statement. As we continued walking, rocks suddenly began pelting down from above.

"Watch out!" I shouted, barely dodging a falling stalactite in time. "That was close..." I breathed a sigh of relief and turned to check on the others, only to see tentacles sprouting from the creature’s sides and a giant red eye appearing. It scanned its surroundings and, upon spotting us, lifted itself off the ground, reaching out with its tentacles to grab me.

Bluma rushed over with her sword, parrying the creature's tentacles and managing to slice one off. However, the severed tentacle quickly regenerated, and the creature let out a fierce roar. It was massive, reminiscent of the creatures we had encountered when we first entered this underground realm.

"Run!" Bluma commanded, continuing to fight off the tentacles. Gwen immediately took off, but Beans stayed behind.

"Deta! Make sure she doesn’t do something stupid! I’ll stay and help Bluma!" he shouted. I nodded and sprinted after Gwen.

Gwen’s View

“Gwen! Wait up!” Deta’s voice echoed behind me, but I couldn’t stop, my heart pounding in my chest. I ran, my thoughts a blur, until Deta finally caught up, grabbing my arm. I jerked back instinctively, desperate to break free.

“Let me go!” I shouted, twisting in his grip until I saw his face. My muscles tensed, my breath coming in sharp bursts.

“Gwen…?” he said, voice softer now. I turned away, ready to flee, but he moved in front of me, blocking my escape. “What’s going on? You’ve been off ever since we got down here.”

I kept my eyes fixed on the ground, a knot tightening in my stomach. “Why do you care? I’m not going to be your prisoner,” I muttered, the words cutting through the tense air. His face twisted in shock.

“Do you really think I’d make you a prisoner?” Deta’s voice softened, confusion laced in his tone.

I glanced at him, still suspicious, still guarded. “Why else are you being nice? You’re just setting me up for a trap,” I said, taking a step back, determined to get away.
