“Gwen...” Deta followed, his voice steady but laced with concern. “I would never make you a prisoner. None of us would! We need to go back and help Bluma. She’s our friend—”

“Your friend!” I spun on him, my anger flaring. “She doesn’t care about me, and you know it!” The words lashed out, raw and full of hurt. I watched the sting register on his face before I turned away, my footsteps heavy as I tried to distance myself from him and the doubt clouding my mind.

Before I could make sense of anything, a shadow lunged from behind, its cold, scaly hands like iron bands around my throat. I gasped, feeling its claws dig into my skin, the rancid stench of decay flooding my senses. Its breath was thick with rot, a sour, fetid odor that made my stomach churn as it growled in my ear.

The creature’s voice was a low, guttural rasp, the kind that scraped at my soul. “Now I have dinner! And nothing you do can save her!” it hissed, its single glowing eye gleaming with a hungry, sickening light.

I kicked, thrashing against its grip, but its claws tightened, choking the air from my lungs. My vision blurred as I fought, my chest aching for a breath.

Just as darkness began to take over, a burst of fire streaked across my vision, crashing into the creature’s side. It howled in pain, releasing me as flames danced over its scaly skin.

“Don’t you dare hurt my friend!” Deta’s voice rang out, fierce and unyielding.

The creature snarled, its twisted form rippling as it turned toward Deta. Its long, spindly limbs coiled like a serpent ready to strike. Jagged, yellow teeth gleamed in the dim light, and its skin, slick and almost liquid in appearance, shifted as it moved.

As it lunged, its claws were mere inches from Deta’s throat. My fingers gripped my sword on their own, the warmth of its magic pulsing through me. The blade shimmered, lighter than air, as if it was part of me, an extension of my will. Fear ebbed away, replaced by cold focus.

In one fluid motion, I swung the sword. The metal cut through the air, and the creature’s head rolled from its shoulders with a sickening thud. Its body crumpled to the ground at my feet.

Deta stood frozen, his mouth slightly open in shock. My pulse hammered in my ears, but for the first time in what felt like forever, I allowed myself to smile—genuine and triumphant.

“Fine,” I said, glancing over my shoulder toward where Bluma was, still in danger, trying not to look at the blood. “Let’s go help that demon,” I added, gripping my sword with newfound confidence. The weight of my earlier fear seemed to vanish as I felt my connection to the sword, to the fight, solidify within me.

Deta’s grin spread wide, lighting his face. “There’s Gwen!” he said with a laugh, shaking his head.

Beans’ View

Bluma struggled to close the distance to the beast, every attempt blocked by a tentacle whipping her away. The monster was relentless, its slimy limbs striking with precision and force. I gritted my teeth, fury boiling in my chest as I saw her stumble back again. This thing wasn’t going to stop unless we made it stop.

I gripped my ax tightly and hurled it with all my strength. The blade spun through the air and buried itself deep into the creature’s eye. A shriek of pain tore from its throat, a high-pitched wail that made the ground tremble under my boots.

The monster thrashed wildly, blinded, its tentacles flailing in every direction. I dodged one as it came crashing down beside me, but Bluma wasn’t as lucky. The beast’s massive arm coiled around her, squeezing her tightly. Her body contorted in pain, and I could see her strength fading fast as the creature began to drain her life force.

I didn’t think. I just moved.

Charging forward, I leaped onto the creature’s side, yanking my ax from its ruined eye with a sickening squelch. Blood and ooze splattered everywhere. With a roar, I brought the ax down again, splitting the tentacle holding Bluma. She fell to the ground, limp but alive.

The creature bellowed in agony, but there was no time to celebrate. Its remaining three tentacles lashed out at me with deadly speed. I barely raised my ax in time to block, but the force nearly knocked me off my feet.

Before I could react, Gwen darted in, her colossal sword swinging in a blur. With a mighty sweep, she severed all three tentacles in one clean strike. The sound of the severed limbs hitting the ground was like thunder.

"Deta!" I called over my shoulder, eyes locked on Bluma, who lay pale and unmoving.

Deta, always quick on his feet, sprinted to her side. I saw the glow of his magic as he knelt beside her, healing her wounds. His face was a mask of focus, lips moving in quiet incantation. Slowly, color returned to Bluma’s cheeks, and she opened her eyes. With Deta’s help, she got to her feet, her strength renewed.

She nodded gratefully to him before rushing back into the fight. The beast’s tentacles had already begun to regenerate, sprouting from the stumps where Gwen had cut them. I growled in frustration. This thing just wouldn’t die.

Bluma and Gwen moved in sync, hacking away at the tentacles as fast as they could grow back. I could see their frustration building. No matter how many limbs they severed, the creature just kept regenerating.

"Everyone, move!" Deta's voice rang out, sharp and commanding.

I glanced back to see him standing tall, hands outstretched as three glowing fireballs spun in the air above him. With a flick of his wrists, he sent them hurtling toward the creature. They struck with a blinding flash of light, and the beast let out an agonized scream that echoed across the battlefield.

Seizing the moment, I sprinted forward. This was our chance.

With all the strength I could muster, I drove my ax deep into the monster’s remaining eye, the blade sinking into its skull with a satisfying crunch. The creature let out one final, ear-piercing shriek before collapsing in a heap, lifeless.

I stepped back, panting, blood and sweat mixing on my skin. My heart was still pounding in my chest, but the battlefield was finally silent. The creature lay still, its massive body crumpled on the ground.

CHAPTER 13                                                                                                                                   A Light in the Depths

Gwen wore a smile until her gaze landed on the blood clinging to her sword. The color drained from her face. She staggered back a step, then turned away and vomited.

I moved toward her instinctively, taking the sword from her shaking hands. My chest tightened. I hated seeing her like that.

Beans looked bewildered. “Is she okay?”

I nodded, though my voice was quieter than usual. “She’ll be fine.” I glanced at Gwen, who was wiping her mouth on her arm, still pale. “She despises blood.”

Beans furrowed his brow and looked at Bluma. “A fighter who hates blood? Isn’t that... unusual?”

Bluma gave a short, hesitant nod. “Strange.”

Gwen took a deep breath, straightened up, and forced a grin. “Alright, let’s head to the jungle!” She patted Bluma on the back as she passed, like nothing had happened.

Beans hesitated, clearly unsure how to react. Bluma followed slowly, casting one last glance at Gwen. I walked behind her, watching her carefully. The others couldn’t see it, but I could tell—her hands were still trembling.

None of us spoke for a while. The silence stretched between us as we made our way forward, each step carrying the weight of what had just happened.

Eventually, the rocky cavern floor gave way to softer ground. Faintly glowing mushrooms began to scatter across the path, their gentle light painting the earth in shades of blue and green. They clustered like a tiny, glowing garden.

Beans let out a soft chuckle, the tension in his voice easing. “This is the jungle? A little disappointing”

I smiled and tilted my head upward. “Look up.”

He did—and stopped in his tracks. Towering mushrooms loomed overhead, their caps glowing like lanterns in the dark. Vines draped between them, and glowing spores drifted lazily through the air, lighting the space like tiny stars.

"Oh... this is the jungle," Beans muttered.

"It's breathtaking," I said, marveling at the sight.

Bluma, captivated, nodded.

After a few minutes, we pressed forward, venturing deeper into the jungle. The soft glow of mushrooms lit our path, and the air grew still—almost too still.

Then Beans slowed, his boots making a soft splash. He looked down and stiffened.

"Uh, Gwen," he said carefully. "Don’t look down."

We all followed his gaze. Blood. A shallow pool of it shimmered beneath the glowing spores, so thin and still that it had gone unnoticed—until now. Gwen stumbled back, hand over her mouth, eyes wide.

Bluma knelt, touched the edge. "Fresh."

Beans looked toward the slope beside the path. His voice was low, but urgent. “There’s someone down there.”

My stomach turned. I stepped forward, heart pounding. “We have to check,” I said, already moving in the direction he pointed.

At the bottom of the hill, we spotted a figure lying in the underbrush, half-covered in dirt and blood. My heart stopped for a moment. It wasn’t Rinn—but the resemblance was too close. The same messy straight white hair, the way his clothes clung to his slender frame. Gwen, standing behind me, breathed deeply, almost a growl. She must’ve noticed it too.

The man's legs were broken—twisted, arms weak and almost unable to pull himself across the ground. Blood poured from his wounds. His voice was faint, but full of desperation. "I can’t die here. I can’t..."

I stepped forward to help him, but Bluma raised a hand in front of me, stopping me. Confused, I followed her gaze to a bush behind the injured man.

We crouched low. From the bushes emerged a massive, dog-like creature with eight eyes and a tentacled tail, spikes gleaming at the tip. Five more followed. The man—so like Rinn—sensed their approach and turned, panic flooding his eyes. His lips moved, but no sound came out at first. Then, in a hoarse whisper, he cried out.

"No! No, please! Go away!"

His pleas went unanswered as the creatures pounced, ripping him apart. Gwen turned away, unable to watch, while I covered my ears to block out his screams. In moments, his lifeless body lay still. A few of the creatures grabbed him with their tails and dragged him into the underbrush.

We remained silent, the heavy air pressing around us, until the ground beneath our feet shifted. Then we rose—only to lock eyes with one of the creatures, its gaze piercing through the shadows.

The stench of damp earth mixed with something rotten, and the creature's massive form loomed just beyond the reach of the dim glow, its skin a mottled blend of dark green and gray. The heavy, pulsating thud of its breath echoed in the stillness, and its yellow eyes gleamed like fireflies in the dark.

Startled, we jumped back, the sharp scrape of metal against stone as we unsheathed our weapons. The creature’s low growl vibrated through the ground, and its jagged, gnarled teeth glinted in the eerie light, daring us to make a move. We stood frozen, weapons at the ready, senses screaming as the tension thickened in the air.

"Careful," Bluma whispered.

"Obviously," Gwen muttered.

As the dog-like creature edged closer, its heavy paws making the softest crunch on the moss-covered ground, a thunderous roar suddenly shattered the stillness from our left. The air seemed to vibrate with the force of it.

The creature froze mid-step, its nostrils flaring as its yellow eyes darted toward the source of the sound. Before any of us could react, a massive, hairless, purple tiger with four gleaming eyes erupted from the underbrush. Its massive claws dug into the earth with a sound like tearing fabric, and its fur-less skin glistened in the dim light, sending waves of tension through the air.

The dog-like creature didn’t hesitate. It bolted, its frantic footfalls pounding the earth as it vanished into the thick jungle.

The purple tiger gave a final, guttural growl, watching for a moment before it too disappeared into the shadows, leaving the jungle as quiet as it had been moments before. The air, still thick with adrenaline, pressed in on us, and our weapons remained poised, though nothing else came.

"Are you all alright?" a voice called out.

We turned, startled, as a man in a cloak—its dark fabric almost blending with the surrounding shadows—stepped from the underbrush. His cloak was speckled with mushrooms, their pale caps catching the faint glow of the jungle light. "Those Halusanines almost had you," he said with a grin, his voice smooth but laced with something mocking. "Glad I was patrolling nearby."

He smirked, catching sight of our drawn weapons. "Relax, kittens. I’m not here to harm you. Name’s Flevoka."

I raised an eyebrow, the tension still humming in the air. "Flevoka?" I asked, folding my arms, my gaze steady. "That’s a Randeth name for a girl…"

His grin faltered for just a heartbeat, but it was enough. "Randeth?" he repeated, his voice forced, the hint of discomfort slipping through. He quickly tried to laugh it off. "Nah, call me Adam."

I didn't buy it. There was something in his eyes—something behind the forced smile. The hesitation was obvious, and judging by the way Bluma’s four eyes narrowed in suspicion, she saw it too. Whatever game he was playing, it was unraveling faster than he could keep up with.

Gwen, always impatient, sheathed her sword with a sharp, practiced motion. "Enough with the chit-chat. Let’s keep moving."

Adam chuckled, but the sound was tight. "Impatient, huh? Well, if you’re looking for civilization, follow me—or stay and see if those Halusanines come back for round two."

Gwen shot me a glance, one that suggested her patience was already worn thin. I shrugged. "Better than dealing with those dog creatures."

The air around us felt thick with uncertainty, but with no other options, we followed him into the jungle, wary but with no choice but to trust him—at least for now.

We followed Adam through the dense jungle, the air growing warmer with each step as we neared a small camp. The crackle of a fire reached our ears, and the faint scent of roasting meat mixed with the earthy aroma of damp moss.

As we entered the clearing, the sight of several dead Halusanines greeted us. Their bodies were bound and sprawled out carelessly, the dull, twisted forms of their limbs giving off a faint, unpleasant odor of decay. One of them hung skewered over a blue fire, its flesh sizzling and spitting as the flames danced around it, casting eerie shadows on the surrounding trees. The heat from the fire made the air shimmer slightly, and the strange blue hue gave everything a surreal, unnatural quality.

The silence of the camp was thick, broken only by the crackle of the fire and the occasional rustle of leaves in the wind. It felt wrong—too still, too empty, but Adam seemed at ease, walking up to a nearby log and sitting down as if this were an everyday occurrence.

"Welcome to the Trapper’s Camp," Adam said, other half-elves emerging from their tents. The camp, perched near a cliff, offered a view of the jungle below. He then asked Gwen to help move the Halusanine that was just brought in and with some convincing she went to help.

Bluma took in the sight of various mushrooms the trappers had harvested. Beans studied them too. "I don't like this... we need to leave the underworld as soon as possible," Beans expressed his concerns as we observed some trappers dismembering Halusanine.

"I agree... let's find Gwen and see if we can find any information to guide us in the right direction," I responded quietly, not wanting to attract attention. Beans and Bluma nodded in agreement and left, while I set off to locate Gwen. As I walked, I spotted her near the pile of Halusanine, placing something into her bag.

"Gwen," I whispered with urgency, causing her to jump.

"What?" she snapped, irritated by the sudden shock.

"We're planning to leave," I informed her.

Hearing this, she grinned and exclaimed, "Finally! Let's get moving!" I sighed, though a smile crept across my face. "Bluma and Beans are searching for any clues to guide us," I added. Gwen groaned in response. "Alright, let's start searching."

Beans’ View

Bluma and I wandered through the camp, the humid air thick with the musk of rotting foliage and ash. Each tent we searched smelled like mildew and old sweat, filled with the clutter of supplies stacked carelessly—half-melted wax candles, chipped blades, bags of grain chewed open by vermin. The ground squelched faintly beneath our boots, soft with damp moss and spilled food.

Most of what we found was basic—cracked bowls, rusted weapons, threadbare blankets. I sifted through another crate of useless odds and ends, the wood rough beneath my fingers, splinters biting at my skin. Stepping out of the tent, I let out a sharp sigh, the air catching in my dry throat. "Nothing useful in there," I muttered, my frustration rising like heat off the fire pits.

Bluma, eyes always scanning, paused. She raised her hand, her four-eyed gaze fixed on something further out. “Beans,” she said, her voice low and steady, motioning toward a large tent that sat isolated on the camp’s edge, close to the tree line and far from the cliffs.

I followed her gesture. The tent was larger than the others, its canvas taut and darkened from age and use. “Worth a look,” I agreed. “Let’s go.”

We padded through the underbrush, trying not to disturb the brittle twigs and dead leaves underfoot. But before we could get close, I saw them—massive, hairless tiger-like beasts sprawled across the sun-warmed earth. Their purple skin shimmered faintly, almost oily in the light, and their four eyes blinked slowly even in sleep. Each exhale made their bellies rise and fall like bellows, and the rumble of their snoring rolled through the air like distant thunder.

I stopped short and threw out a hand to halt Bluma. My heart slammed against my ribs, and my stomach seized with panic. I leaned in, barely breathing. "We need to go around. We can't risk waking those giant cats."

Bluma simply nodded, her expression unreadable as always. Together, we began to circle wide, our movements slow and deliberate. The jungle felt heavier here, dense with moisture and tension. That’s when I spotted it—a slit torn into the back of the tent, just large enough for someone my size to squeeze through.

I turned to her, managing a nervous smile. "Alright, I’ll be right back," I whispered, though my voice quivered slightly. With one last look at the sleeping beasts, I slid inside.

The fabric rasped against my skin as I squeezed through. The air inside was thick and musty, and the dimness made everything feel close and oppressive. My stomach twisted with nervous energy, a familiar and unwanted pressure beginning to build deep in my gut.

The tent was cluttered with clothing—mounds of it. Damp shirts clung together, stained trousers lay folded with disturbing neatness, and something sour hung in the air like mold and sweat mixed with unwashed bodies. I dug through the piles, trying to ignore the wave of nausea rising in me.

Great. Waist-deep in laundry, I thought bitterly, suppressing a gag.

Then—footsteps. Heavy. Confident. My pulse spiked, and the pressure in my gut surged. Panic clawed at me as I looked around, eyes landing on a large crate. Without thinking, I dove inside, the edges bruising my shins. I yanked a heap of scratchy clothes over myself, forcing my breath to slow.

Three men entered, their boots thudding against the packed dirt floor. Their voices carried a harsh rhythm in a language I didn’t know. Trappers. One of them snorted a laugh, and I caught a few words as they slipped into Common.

“The captain’s going to be in for a surprise when he sees what we’ve brought back. Ain’t nobody expecting this kind of haul.”

“True. But I don’t think we’re done yet. There’s still that group hiding out in the woods. Think they’ll be worth the trouble?”

“Who cares?” another scoffed. “As long as we bring them in, the boss’ll be happy. Heard one of ’em’s got a bounty. Could be worth a fortune.”

My stomach clenched. Us. They were talking about us. I pressed my back into the side of the crate, every muscle rigid. The pressure inside was unbearable now. My mouth went dry as I tried not to move, not to breathe too loudly.

“Yeah, let’s round them up. Easy money,” the first one said, his voice too close for comfort.

They lingered, laughing and tossing out crude jokes, their boots scraping on the floorboards. Every second dragged like wet cloth over stone. I couldn’t hold it in much longer.

Come on. Leave already, I begged in silence.

At last, the voices began to fade. I stayed still, counting each second. Then—pfft. The tiny, betraying noise escaped me.

Not now, I groaned inwardly.

"Another reason why I hate elves," I muttered under my breath, climbing out of the crate. The pile of clothing reeked—sour body odor, blood, and something like fermented fish. I gagged and waved a hand in front of my face.

That’s when I saw the room at the back of the tent. Something about it pulled me forward. The air shifted as I stepped through the threshold—cooler, quieter. A wide table stood in the center, surrounded by mismatched chairs. Spread across it was a massive map of the Underworld, drawn in precise ink strokes and marked with strange symbols.

“Wow…” I breathed.

I moved closer, the parchment smooth beneath my fingers. At the far end, a tightly rolled scroll caught my eye. I reached for it—then froze. Voices again.

Dread settled in my chest like a stone as I dove under the table. Two sets of footsteps entered the room, then halted nearby.

“After we lead them to the slave traders, we’ll get quite the reward, right?” one said, snickering.

“Indeed. But first, we need to make sure they trust us. Right, Adam?”

Adam. My throat tightened.

He was working with them. I knew it.

I balled my fists under the table. I wanted to leap out and scream, but I forced myself still. One of the trappers turned back, and Adam's voice called from just outside: “Bring me the rolled-up map.”

The man plucked it off the table. I silently cursed, watching my only lead disappear through the canvas flap.

I waited, listening. Adam’s voice echoed as he chatted with someone just outside the tent. The scroll had been set on a crate, barely five feet away.

This was my chance.

I crept from beneath the table, moving slowly, deliberately, knees trembling with each shift of weight. My breath came in shallow bursts. That internal pressure pulsed like a second heartbeat.

Not now, Beans. Almost there.

I reached out, fingers brushing the parchment. Then Adam’s silhouette shifted, his head turning slightly. I yanked the scroll back and dove into another crate, my legs cramping up as I curled in tight.

Sweat dripped from my brow, soaking into my collar. I clutched the scroll to my chest like it could shield me.

I need to leave… I need to leave…

Eventually, the voices faded again. I didn’t wait this time. Bursting from the crate, I shoved through the tent’s slit and stumbled into the fresh air, drawing in a gasping breath. My body sagged as the tension bled out of me.

Bluma stood there, calm as always. She tilted her head, one brow lifting at my ragged state.

“Good?” she asked.

“Yeah, just... stress,” I muttered, wiping my forehead. “But I got the scroll.”

She gave a single nod. “Good.”

We spread the parchment between us on a flat rock. It was a map, sketched in fine lines, showing a crystalline structure labeled Temple to the northeast. A city sprawled to the northwest.

“Well, we’ve got our map,” I said, a tremor still in my voice. But a grin tugged at the edge of my lips. "Let's go find Gwen and Deta."

Bluma nodded again. “Right.”

Deta’s View

Roughly twenty minutes passed before we all met up again. Beans was the first to speak, eyeing us with curiosity. “Did you two find anything?” Gwen shook her head “Nothing but junk” She groaned. ‘What did you two lovebirds find?”

Beans and Bluma turned red when Gwen called them "lovebirds."Beans cleared his throat. "We found a map," he said. "It shows a path to some kind of Temple."

Gwen immediately wanted to see it, and Beans handed it over. After studying it she almost threw it back to him “We are not going to that temple…”

This left us puzzled, as going through the temple seemed like the quicker option. Before I could ask, Gwen cut me off, insisting we avoid the temple. She rolled up the map and stashed it in her pouch. "Just trust me on that… Let’s head to the city" she said, turning to leave.

At that moment, Adam appeared in front of Gwen, disappointment evident on his face. "Leaving already? Too bad. We were going to help you get home," he sneered.

Gwen reacted first, her hand flying to her sword. Tension snapped through the air like a drawn wire.

Adam’s grin widened—not with surprise, but satisfaction. He’d been waiting for this.

Before any of us could speak, he lunged, twisting through the air like a serpent, his curved dagger gleaming in the dim light. Every strike was deliberate, rehearsed—he wasn’t fighting to win. He was fighting to enjoy it.

Gwen barely dodged the first blow, the blade hissing past her armor with a sharp scrape. Bluma met the second with her sword, the clash rattling up her arms. Beans caught the third with his ax, the impact bursting into a flash of sparks.

Before Adam could press his advantage, I seized the moment and swung the staff with all my strength. Magic pulsed through it, glowing with a green and blue aura as it struck Adam’s side. The power hurled him into the air, but instead of being stunned, he twisted mid-flight, landing on his feet with the grace of a predator. He grimaced, clutching his ribs, but the fight in his eyes burned brighter than ever.

He moved again, this time with greater speed. His movements carried more caution, weaving between us like a shadow. He lunged at Bluma, forcing her back against a jagged boulder, while Gwen swung her massive sword, aiming to cut him down. Adam ducked under the blade, escaping, and swept his leg at Gwen’s knees, causing her to lose her balance.

With a roar, Beans charged, his ax raised high. Adam, swift as ever, flicked a hidden knife from his wrist. It whizzed through the air, cutting Beans' cheek, leaving a thin line of blood.

"You’re too slow," Adam spat, a smirk creeping across his face.

Refusing to back down, I rushed in. I swinging the glowing stick once more, targeting Adam’s chest, but he anticipated my move. Sidestepping, he grabbed my arm and threw me to the ground. The stick slipped from my grasp, rolling just out of reach.

Gwen, Bluma, and Beans quickly closed in, forming a tight circle around him. Adam’s eyes darted between us, calculating his next move with precision. There was no room for hesitation.

Bluma feigned left, then lunged at his right side, while Gwen’s sword descended in a powerful arc. Adam twisted out of the way, using his dagger to deflect Bluma’s strike, but Gwen’s sword cut into his shoulder. He winced, blood staining his leather armor, yet his determination never wavered.

Just as Adam prepared for another attack, I scrambled to retrieve the stick. With a sudden swing, I caught him off guard. The force sent him flying once more, this time skidding closer to the edge of the cliff. He slammed into the ground, his body sliding across the rough surface.

Panting, Adam shoved himself upright, blood smeared at the corner of his mouth. His eyes burned—not with fear, but with something darker. Delight.

He spat to the side and sneered, “That it? Come on. I expected more from the ones screwing up my plans.”

His dagger twitched in his hand, eager for another round.

The ground trembled beneath him as he staggered toward the cliff’s edge, the rocks shifting under his weight. Gwen advanced, her sword raised, but before she could strike, Adam lunged at me with one last desperate effort. I swung the stick again, this time connecting squarely with his chest. The magic surged through him, launching him backward.

He hit the ground hard, his momentum carrying him to the edge. With one final misstep, the earth crumbled beneath his feet, sending him plummeting into the abyss.

I watched as Adam plummeted to the ground in silence and couldn't help but feel a twinge of guilt. Gwen noticed my expression and reassured me, "Don't feel bad. He attacked first. Now let's get out of here… his friends probably heard the fight” We followed Gwen and sneaked out of the Trapper camp.

As we ventured through the jungle, I played with the magical stick I had acquired, realizing its power to send objects flying when pushed with it. I felt a sense of satisfaction in possessing such a weapon.

As we examined the map, Gwen, Beans, and Bluma engrossed themselves in a discussion. Meanwhile, I noticed a peculiar mushroom nearby. It had numerous bubbles on its surface and swayed gently. Intrigued, I approached it and reached out to touch it.  To my surprise, the bubbles burst, releasing a foul-smelling gas that engulfed the area.

I turned just in time to see the cloud of gas drifting lazily toward the others. Though harmless, it stank like something long-dead and reheated. I let it waft closer, curious to see who’d crack first.

Gwen was the unlucky one. Her face twisted with disgust as she slapped a hand over her nose. “Beans! Did you just fart?” she blurted, her voice muffled behind her fingers.

Beans recoiled like he'd been accused of a crime. “No! This isn’t me—this is awful!” he gagged, doubling over as he tried to wave the smell away.

Bluma, ever unbothered, gave a single shake of her head and calmly pushed the air aside like it was a mild inconvenience.

I couldn’t stop myself from laughing. “Is everything okay?” I asked, keeping my tone as innocent as possible.

Gwen shot me a withering glare, eyes watering. “Yeah, we’re just—” Her words faltered as the smell intensified. The silence that followed was heavy and awkward.

Beans, now looking a bit green, stumbled back a step. “I, uh… I’ll be right back.” He bolted behind a massive mushroom without another word.

Gwen hesitated, nose wrinkled, then followed him without saying anything. Her shoulders were tense, jaw set tight.

A few moments passed, then came the unmistakable noises from behind the mushrooms.

I snorted, unable to hold it in.

Bluma looked at me with her bottom two eyes and walked over to me “Explain..” she said in a firm tone but her voice laced with curiosity I then showed her the mushroom.

A few minutes later, Beans and Gwen emerged from behind the mushrooms. Both looked mildly disheveled—Gwen with her lips pressed tight, and Beans avoiding eye contact like the ground had become suddenly fascinating.

“Everything okay?” I asked, failing miserably to keep the grin out of my voice.

Beans gave a stiff nod. “Peachy.”

Gwen just muttered, “Shut up,” without meeting my eyes.

I shrugged, still smiling. “Hey, just checking.”

Gwen growled then cleared her throat, attempting to regain focus. "If we head north for a few miles and then east, we should be able to bypass the temple and reach the city."

I grinned ready to proceed. "Sounds like a plan!"

We continued our journey. After walking for hours, the soft glow of the mushrooms cast eerie shadows that seemed to follow our every step. The forest had grown silent, save for the occasional rustle of leaves, though we could never quite tell if it was the wind or something more. The bioluminescent fungi painted the enormous mushrooms in faint greens and blues, a surreal light that danced along their rough surfaces. Every so often, a low hum resonated from the ground beneath us, as if the earth itself were alive and watching.

We were walking close together when I turned to Gwen, who seemed on edge. "Do you feel like we’re being followed?" I whispered, my voice barely louder than a breath in the stillness around us.

She nodded, her grip tightening on the hilt of her sword. "Yes, but I can’t tell if it’s real or if it's just this place."

The shifting colors of light pulsed around us, making the forest feel alive—breathing in rhythm with our steps. Some mushrooms cast only faint glimmers that vanished into the dark, while others glowed with an eerie brilliance, bathing the air in strange, otherworldly hues.

The air hung heavy with dampness, thick with the scent of wet earth and slow decay. Distant roars echoed now and then, breaking the silence like claws through fabric. I kept pausing to listen, heart racing. The quiet wasn’t just quiet—it pressed down on us, watchful, like the forest itself was holding its breath.

After a long stretch of silence, we stumbled into a clearing bordered by jagged rocks and towering mushrooms draped in thick moss. Beans rolled up the map with a flick of his wrist. “Let’s rest here,” he said, glancing around. “We’re almost out of this mushroom forest.”

We all agreed and set up camp. I used my magic to draw roots from the ground beneath us, which Beans chopped down to make a fire. Gwen pitched her tent and disappeared inside the moment it was finished. Once the rest of the camp was prepared, Beans slipped into his tent while I settled down against the base of a towering fungus. Bluma remained on watch, her eyes scanning the forest around us.

Gwen’s View

I woke up restless, sleep refusing to come back. “I hate this place,” I muttered, more to the air than anyone. Peeking out of the tent flap, I spotted Bluma sitting by the campfire, her silhouette flickering in the low light. Two other tents stood quiet nearby.

I stepped out, the cool air biting at my arms, and wandered over to her.

“Hey,” I said, my voice still gravelly. I settled beside her on the mossy ground. “Everyone still out?”

Bluma gave a small nod, not looking up. She was focused on cleaning one of her swords—a sleek blade of black metal, its golden hilt etched with strange markings that shimmered in the firelight.

“Nice sword… What do those symbols mean?” I asked, getting more comfortable.

She paused, glanced at me, then around the camp, cautious. With one finger, she wrote in the dirt: Demon’s Wrath. Then she slid the sword back into its sheath.

“‘Demon’s Wrath,’ huh? Sounds about right.” I gave a dry chuckle, and to my surprise, she echoed it.

I nodded toward the blade at her side. “That one yours?”

She pointed at the hilt of my sword instead.

“Huh? Oh, this thing? The old man who gave it to me called it Fighter’s Spirit or something like that. Probably enchanted,” I said, unsheathing it. The blade came free with a quiet hiss—massive, wide as my torso, and only a little shorter than me. The scabbard had been built for a longsword, but the blade didn’t quite match the mold.

I offered it to her, curious. Bluma took it with both hands, eyebrows raising when she felt how light it was. She stood, gave it a test swing—clean and practiced—but halfway through, the weight shifted, and the blade shortened. She stumbled, clearly caught off guard.

“Impressive,” she murmured, shaking her head. Her eyes sparkled a little as she adjusted her stance. She gave it another couple swings, more controlled this time, then passed it back to me.

“Yeah,” I said with a smirk, sliding it home. “Way better than the junk I used to swing around. Some old guy named Omar made it for me.”

Bluma’s expression shifted. All four of her eyes locked on me at once. “Omar?”

I raised a brow. “You know him?”

She nodded, gaze drifting to her own sword. “Same.”

“Wait—he made yours too?” I blinked.

“Yes.”

We both fell quiet for a beat. Then, without really trying, we just kept talking. The fire crackled between us, and the night stretched on—soft and strange and a little warmer than before.

Deta’s View

After a long rest, I stretched and yawned, trying to shake off the remnants of sleep. As I glanced down, my eyes widened in surprise. My body had grown roots, deep into the mushroom I’d been lying on. “Well, that’s new,” I muttered, a mix of amusement and unease in my voice.

I’d always relied on the sun's energy to keep me going, so waking up with this... this connection to something else, something unexpected, was definitely a surprise.

Turning back toward the tents, I saw Bluma sitting by the dying embers of the fire, but Gwen was nowhere to be seen. "Hey, Bluma... did you sleep well last night?" I asked, suppressing another yawn. Bluma looked up, gave a quick nod, then covered the fire with dirt. I followed her gaze toward Gwen's tent. "Is she still sleeping?" I asked.

Bluma shook her head. "Cleaning," she said. Just as she spoke, Gwen stepped out of her tent, rolling up her bedding, already preparing for the day.

I smiled and greeted her, "Hey, Gwen, everything alright?" She looked up briefly, gave a nod, then went back to packing her things.

Before long, the rest of the camp stirred, and we all finished tidying up. Beans, ever resourceful, had found some edible mushrooms, He and the others bit into them complaining about the squeaking sound they made as they ate them.

We hadn’t traveled far when a sudden chill crawled down my spine, and I felt an uneasy shift in the air. The feeling was confirmed when Gwen and Bluma instinctively reached for their swords, while Beans scanned the area, and I tightened my grip on my staff. "Anyone else feel that?"

I began, just as Gwen cut in with, "Yeah." Beans' eyes darted around.

"Whatever it is... We should stay close" I suggested, and everyone nodded in silent agreement.

A faint growl pierced the stillness, followed by the sharp snap of a twig. We froze. Quickly, we moved into a tight circle, ready to face whatever was approaching. Gwen and Bluma held their swords with precision, Beans raised his ax, and I steadied my staff, eyes searching the dense mushroom forest around us. Then I saw it. "There!" I shouted, pointing at a large Halusanine, foam dripping from its snarling jaws. Its mouth hung open, revealing sharp, menacing teeth as it charged straight for me.

 I shifted into a defensive stance, my body coiling with readiness. But before I could react, the creature’s powerful jaws clamped down on my staff. With a sudden, violent tug, it sent me sprawling through the air, my body hitting the ground with a harsh thud, as if I weighed no more than a leaf.

In the midst of the chaos, Gwen lunged forward, her sword raised high, ready to strike the beast. Her blade cut through the air, but the Halusanine dodged with unnatural speed. Before we could even react, two more of the creatures emerged from the shadows, flanking Gwen, Bluma, and Beans. The trio of Halusanines circled them, completely ignoring me.

Taking advantage of the distraction, I scrambled to my feet and charged one of the beasts, swinging my staff with all my might. But to my shock, my weapon passed right through it, as if it were an illusion. Before I could comprehend what had happened, another Halusanine rammed into me from behind, knocking me off balance.

"Did you even hit it!?" Gwen shouted, frustration creeping into her voice as she swung her sword again, only to have it slice through the air with no effect.

"I did! It just went right through!" I replied, scrambling to grab my staff from the ground.

Suddenly, three more Halusanines materialized around us, each pairing up with the ones already circling. In an instant, we were completely surrounded.

"How are they multiplying so fast!?" Gwen growled, her eyes darting between the creatures.

"They're Halusanines! They mess with your mind, make you see more of them than there actually are! Didn’t I tell you?" Adam's smug voice echoed from atop a nearby rock, where he stood casually watching us struggle. He chuckled darkly. "You actually thought you could steal my map? How pathetic!" His laughter cut through the tension, fueling Gwen's anger, and I could feel my own frustration boiling over as well.

One of the Halusanines charged at Beans, who barely dodged its snapping jaws. "Whoa! If these things are just illusions, then they can only hurt us if we believe they’re real!" Beans called out, realizing the nature of the creatures.

Adam grinned, his chuckle even darker now. "Clever, aren't you?" he taunted. "But that won’t help with this one. He’s all hyped up on snyfus" His words dripped with malice.

"Snyfus? What is he talking about?" Beans asked, confusion in his voice.

"I don’t know!" Gwen shouted back, frustration evident as she swung the blunt side of her sword like a bat, miraculously striking three of the Halusanines at once. By sheer luck, she hit the real one, causing the others to fade away as it collapsed to the ground.

"Snyfus is a virus that infects any life form with enough mental capacity! If it bites you, you’ll go insane!" I warned, urgently summoning roots from the ground to entangle the struggling Halusanine. It growled and barked, desperately fighting to escape.

Adam, watching from his perch, smiled. "Well done, well done. Very few people know about that," he remarked with a chuckle. But before we could shift focus to him, the Halusanine broke free from the roots.

"Impressive, for a dead man," Adam said, his voice dripping with smugness.

The creature stood and locked eyes with me, its body tense as it prepared to charge. Gwen stepped forward, ready to intercept it with her sword, and I conjured a flame in my hand. But just as we thought we had it figured out, the beast veered at the last moment, pouncing on Gwen instead, knocking her to the ground. Its jaws were poised to strike at her face.

Gwen tried to punch it off, but suddenly, a flash of light struck the Halusanine from the side, sending it flying back. We all froze for a moment. Gwen, catching her breath, noticed a burn mark on the creature’s side—roughly the size of a large fist.

As the Halusanine struggled back to its feet, growling with rage, Gwen stood and prepared for another round. "Your stick can catch fire, bushy?" she asked, surprised to see me holding my staff in one hand, the other ablaze with a flame.

Adam fell silent, no more smug remarks as the Halusanine lunged at us again. Bluma rushed in, her dark black sword now glowing with a faint white light, and with a single, precise swing, she sliced through the beast's hip. The creature let out a howl of pain. Seizing the moment, Gwen brought her sword down with all her strength, severing its head and finally ending its suffering.

As the creature’s lifeless body slumped to the ground, Gwen glanced toward the rock where Adam had been, only to find him gone. "Tch, that brat!" she growled, instinctively ready to give chase. But Beans stepped in front of her, stopping her with a raised hand. "He isn’t worth it," he said, his tone calm but firm.

Gwen hesitated, her frustration boiling over and cursed, throwing her sword to the ground.

As we moved along the path, we found ourselves walking beside a colossal stalagmite that loomed like a mountain. Beans took in the view of the jungle, both above and below us, and remarked, "If it weren't for the constant danger of things trying to kill us, I’d think this place would be fun to come back and visit."

I smiled in agreement. "Yeah, but I don’t think I want to come back and deal with the Halusanine again."

Beans nodded in understanding. "That’s very true."

Without warning, Beans and I bumped into Bluma and Gwen. "Oh, sorry!"

I apologized to Gwen, but she just rolled her eyes. "Look, bushy," she said, stepping aside. I followed her gaze and noticed a massive cave entrance carved into the wall of the stalagmite.

In front of it, a pile of rubble suggested something had burrowed inside. Fragments of wood and clothing were scattered among the debris. "What happened here?" I asked, feeling uneasy.

Gwen appeared uncertain. "I’m not sure, but whatever it was, it didn’t leave much behind."

Just then, Beans called out from the edge of the path. "I think I found something else."

We walked over to where Beans stood and looked down to see a strange wooden wagon lying on its side. It had four distinct sections, each with eight wheels on either side. The front was smashed, and a large hole had been dug into the ground where it once stood.

"What on earth...?" I was baffled by the bizarre design of the enormous wagon. When I turned to look for Gwen, though, she had already continued down the trail. "Gwen, where are you going?" I called, concerned.

She turned back, her voice dripping with disdain. "It’s a slave train. Just keep moving."

Bluma stepped forward and stopped Gwen in her tracks. I glanced at Beans, confused. "A slave train…?" Beans looked at the train, then at Bluma and Gwen.

“Its how they transport people from the surface" she said, her voice dripping with anxiety.

CHAPTER 14                                                                                                                              Old Faces, Old Problems

I peered down at the train and insisted, "What if someone survived? We should at least check." Without waiting for a response, I moved to the edge and prepared to slide down the slope.

Before Beans could finish protesting, I was already descending. "Deta! Stop being so reckless!" he shouted. Gwen and Bluma approached as I slid down. Gwen sighed, and jumped down to catch up. Bluma exchanged glances with Beans and followed.

Beans sighed in frustration. "For the love of...," he muttered, reluctantly joining the rest of us.

When I reached the bottom, I tried to wander closer, however Gwen fell on top of me, sending me face-first into the dirt. She dusted herself off, standing before me. Before we could say anything, a cry of pain echoed nearby, freezing us in place. Bluma and Beans arrived, having heard the scream as they descended.

Beans looked at me and said, "Well, go on. You’re the one who wanted to help whoever’s down here." His voice carried a hint of unease, and I didn’t blame him.

Gathering my nerves, I approached the first section of the wrecked train. Most of it was in ruins, but a door remained somewhat intact, connecting it to the next car. As I reached to open it, the door collapsed, causing me to stumble awkwardly into the next section. To my surprise, the floor was covered in yellow mushrooms and broken crates.

"Are you coming?" I called out. Gwen glanced at Bluma and Beans before they followed. Gwen, tense, trailed behind more slowly.

Once inside, we surveyed the area. Beans, fascinated by the glowing mushrooms, crouched to gather a few and tucked them into his satchel.

Bluma stayed close to Gwen, who seemed increasingly uncomfortable, while I attempted to lift a fallen crate. As I did, I noticed a label written in Dwarvish with large, bold red letters.  Not understanding the text, I flipped the crate and pried it open. After seeing its contents, I slammed it shut.

"What in the ring of hell?” I exclaimed.

Curious, Beans asked, "What is it?" He noticed the label and grimaced. "Didn't you read it? It says..."

I cut him off, not wanting to dwell on the discovery. "Yep, dead stuff. Uh-huh. No more boxes!" I forced a chuckle, and Beans nodded in agreement.

Bluma, still hovering near Gwen, glanced around. "Mushrooms," she muttered, trying to make conversation.

Gwen nodded, clearly unsettled. "Let’s finish up and get out of here... I don’t like this place." She hugged herself for comfort. Bluma, sensing her discomfort, looked at us.

"Right! Good idea," I replied with a smile.

We ventured further down the train car, encountering more mushrooms and crates with Dwarvish markings. Beans and I exchanged nervous glances, both uneasy about the boxes, though I tried not to think too much about it.

We reached the next door, its handle missing. I pushed it, and it swung loosely like a pendulum. I helped Beans through, and we each managed to squeeze past. On the other side, we found piles of food and leather sacks.

Beans’s stomach growled, making Bluma giggle. "Sorry, haven’t eaten in a while," he said sheepishly.

"Why don’t you take a break and eat?" I suggested.

Without hesitation, Beans rushed toward the food. "Sold!" he exclaimed. Gwen reluctantly grabbed something to eat as well.

I leaned against what used to be the roof, only for it to give way. I tumbled outside. "Whoa!" I yelped, landing on my back. The sound startled everyone, and they rushed over to find me sprawled on the ground. "Sorry about that," I said, standing up and rubbing my head.

Gwen sighed, and Beans laughed. "You scared us for a second there, Deta," he said, grinning.

I chuckled, "Yeah, my bad."

Beans went outside, collecting broken wood.

"What are you doing?" I asked.

"Starting a fire to cook the meat!" he replied.

I shrugged. "Need help?"

Beans grinned. "Sure! You grab some meat while I get the fire going."

I nodded and gathered the food. While doing so, I saw Bluma and Gwen sitting in a corner, Gwen nibbling on an apple. "You two okay?" I asked.

They nodded. "Yeah, we’re fine."

Smiling, I returned to Beans with the meat. After a brief rest and a meal, we continued exploring the train. As we walked, the hallway narrowed from a four-person space to a tight two-person passage, forcing us to balance carefully with scattered food beneath our feet.

Then, we spotted a massive hammer lodged in the next doorway. "That’s a big hammer," I muttered as we approached it, stating the obvious. 

“Really? I thought it was an apple,” Gwen replied, her voice dripping with sarcasm. “You know, just your typical fruit, oversized and made of steel.”

Beans, peering around my leg, recognized it. "Oh! A crystal breaker!" he exclaimed, dashing around me and toward it.

Bluma rushed after him, grabbing the collar of his armor and yanking him back just in time. A long blue tongue shot from the hammer, narrowly missing Beans. Bluma, quick on her feet, unsheathed her sword and pinned the tongue to the ground, causing the hammer to let out a piercing scream. Eyes and teeth emerged from its form.

"Shifter!" Bluma shouted, warning us.

The creature lunged at Bluma, but she dodged, slamming into the wall to evade it.

Meanwhile, Beans, wide-eyed, punched the creature as it landed near him, and the impact sent the creature flying back.

Gwen and I wanted to help, but the narrow hallway made it impossible without risking getting hurt.

Bluma wasted no time. She charged the creature, swinging her sword, but it dodged with eight long, dark legs, avoiding a fatal blow. It scurried up the wall and leaped toward Gwen and me.

"Watch out!" Beans yelled.

We jumped back as the shifter hit the ground, splattering blood everywhere. Its form deteriorated, and Gwen seized the moment, driving her sword into the hammer’s head. The creature screeched before falling silent, its true form reverting to an amorphous blob. Gwen pulled her sword from its remains, disgusted.

Covering her mouth, Gwen exclaimed, "I’m gonna be sick..." Her eyes wide, she bolted, Bluma then squeezed around us and followed close behind. A soft splat sound told us she didn’t make it far.

I noticed her sword on the ground, so I picked it up and wiped the purple blood off with a rag. "Yuck... What even was that?"

Just as I finished, Gwen and Bluma returned. Gwen strode over, scooped up her sword, and gave me a curt nod of thanks—grudging, but genuine. Bluma lingered a step behind her, silent as always, though her eyes flicked over me with a quiet sort of approval.

I smiled. "No problem. Are we ready to keep moving?" I stored the cloth in my bag as the two nodded. Bluma led the way into the next car, but as she opened the door, she froze.

"Bluma? What’s wrong?" I asked, but she didn’t respond.

Beans peeked through her legs and muttered, "You’re kidding…"

My curiosity grew. "What is it?"

Gwen tapped my shoulder and pointed to the roof. I glanced up and saw an upside-down sign that read, “Slave Room.” My eyes widened as I took in the scene. Inside, bodies of slaves from various races and species were scattered in cages. It was a grim sight.

We stood in silence until the sound of a box falling startled us, and we drew our weapons. A gray hand, chained to the wall, caught my attention. I stepped closer and heard a faint groan.

"They’re alive!" I shouted. We rushed to clear the debris, revealing a familiar face.

"...you..."

Gwen tightened her grip on her sword, and a wave of bitterness washed over me. Beans looked at us and then at the unconscious figure. "Is that—?"

I nodded. "Rinn."

Rinn’s View

After a while, I stirred, my body aching as I realized I was chained to a giant mushroom. My eyes darted around the area—tents scattered in a circle and a campfire flickering nearby. Someone sat close to the flames, their silhouette hunched over. It hit me then: I was trapped. I yanked at the chains, but they didn’t budge. The clinking sound drew the attention of the figure by the fire—a Dwarf. He stood up and walked toward me.

“You’re awake,” he said, stopping just out of reach.

I shot him a glare, my voice rough. “I’m fine.”

The Dwarf crossed his arms, clearly unimpressed. “That’s no way to talk to someone who might just save your life.”

I couldn’t help but scoff. “You? Save me? You expect me to believe that?”

He sighed, turning his back to me. “Hey, he’s up,” he called out to the camp. As he moved away, three figures emerged from the tents. Two of them I recognized instantly, and I couldn’t stop the sinking feeling in my gut.

“Oh, for the love of…”

Gwen approached me, a smug grin on her face. “How does it feel to have the tables turned?” She reached for the collar around my neck, but I kept my mouth shut, refusing to give her the satisfaction.

She chuckled, but then the young creature beside her placed a hand on her shoulder. “Gwen, don’t antagonize him.”

Gwen shrugged, backing off like it didn’t matter. “Fine. This is enough payback.” She wandered back to her tent, leaving me alone with the creature.

I sneered at them, my frustration boiling over. “What do you want, young creature?”

They smiled softly, reaching into their bag and pulling out some bread. They broke it in half and offered me a piece.

I hesitated, then took it reluctantly. “Are you going to try and make me your slave?” I asked, my voice laced with suspicion as I took a bite.

Their eyes widened, looking startled. “No. I don’t want a slave.” They glanced at the bracelet around my neck, their expression turning serious. “What’s with the bracelet?”

I sighed, my hand brushing against it. “It’s a slave brace. The people who caught me put this on, planning to sell me. It stays on for seven years, which is why Gwen doesn’t have hers anymore.”

They chuckled awkwardly, clearly uneasy. “Is there any other way to get it off?”

I shot them a sharp look. “You think I’m going to believe you’ll free me? A Dark Elf, who would kill you without a second thought?”

They sighed, their tone softening. “Stand with us for now, and we’ll see about getting it off.”

I did not answer,  there is no way that this creature is this incompetent.

Deta’s View

Rinn stayed silent as I returned to the camp. "What’s the matter?" Gwen asked, chewing on a piece of meat.

"Nothing. Let’s just get out of here." I gazed at the ceiling of the underworld. "I’d like to see the sun again."

Gwen sighed heavily, her shoulders slumping. She watched the bone sizzle in the fire, remembering her old, painful memories of this place. "A lot of people would."

Beans and Bluma emerged from their tent, their arrival snapping her back to the present, but the shadows of the past still lingered in her eyes.

"Alright, everyone! We’ve got the map figured out, ready to go?" Beans asked.

Rinn’s ears twitched, but he couldn’t move much, still bound by chains. We packed up the camp and continued through the mushroom jungle. Gwen held Rinn’s chains while I looked up, spotting a flock of small creatures in the sky. I smiled briefly before focusing on the path ahead.

As we walked, I noticed potholes along the sides, filled with water and floating bones. "Beans?" I called out.

"Yeah?" He responded half way, distracted by the map.

"Did we take a wrong turn?" I asked, eyes fixed on bones that laid across the ground.

Beans checked the map and frowned, now noticing the bones too. "Malachite holes…?" he muttered.

Before anyone could react, three frog-like creatures crawled out of the holes. Their bodies were covered in fresh wounds and their mouths dripped with blood.

Bluma and Gwen drew their swords, and Beans readied his hand ax. I conjured fire in one hand and cracked my whip in the other.

The creatures screeched and charged. Bluma’s sword gleamed as she drove it through the first Malachite, killing it. Gwen blocked another’s attack, using her sword to fling it back. Beans dodged the swipes of the third, too quick for the creature to land a hit.

The third Malachite lunged at Rinn, who was still bound. I whipped its arm, pulling it back and hit it with a fireball. It screeched in pain.

"Thanks, young creature…" Rinn muttered.

I turned back to him. "Call me Deta." Then I noticed two more creatures emerging. "More of them?!"

Rinn groaned. "Malachites live in tribes. There’s bound to be more."

Bluma swiftly decapitated one of the creatures. Gwen punched another, driving her sword through its chest. "I hate frogs!" she yelled.

I retracted my whip and retrieved my staff, delivering a powerful blow to one of the Malachites, causing it to fly into its companions. Mistaking the attack for an internal assault, they started fighting among themselves.

Rinn looked at us and urged, "Let's get going!"

I nodded, turning to the others, and we all swiftly made our escape. As we began running, the screeching of the Malachites gradually faded, providing us a momentary sense of relief. We slowed our pace.

"I hate frogs," Gwen groaned.

Beans, still catching his breath, huffed in agreement. "Couldn't... agree... more, ugh," he managed to say.

Glancing back after catching my breath, I questioned, "Why did they attack us?"

Bluma sheathed her sword, sighing with relief. "Territorial," she explained, looking at me before walking over to join Gwen and Beans.

Rinn nodded and added, "Yes, Malachites are very territorial. But not that inclined to knowledge." He chuckled. "If we keep moving, they'll likely forget about us in a few days."

Gwen sheathed her sword but kept her hand firmly on the hilt. "A few days is longer than we have. We need to find a way to escape."

I nodded in agreement. "Yes, let's keep moving and try to find a way out."

"Sounds like a plan to me," Beans replied, finally catching his breath and straightening up. He pulled out the map, attempting to determine our next course of action.

Beans’ View

Rinn approached me from behind and peered at the map from above. I noticed his shadow, Not trusting him I cleared my throat and readjusting the map. "What do you want, Dark Elf?"

Rinn, with his hands bound by cuffs, pointed to a specific area on the map. "If we head north for a few hours, we can avoid theTrade Center."

I looked at him curiously. "First, what is this Trade Center?"

Rinn let out a sigh. "In the Underworld, Trade Centers are places where various items are exchanged—goods, monsters, and slaves, to name a few."

I proceeded with my questions. "Second, why should I trust a Dark Elf?"

Rinn rolled his eyes, visibly annoyed. "You Dwarves are always so pretentious... It is in my best interest, as well as hers," he gestured towards Gwen, who was engaged in conversation with Deta, "Avoid the Trade Center or they won't leave… they are valuable after all, the person who gives them away, with their strength and magic, would be set for life.."

I could feel a grin form on his face as his words tried to slither their way trying to convince me. Bluma then put her hand onto my shoulder as she knelt down at my level and looked to me with two of her golden soft eyes. The other two looked at Rinn, sharp and narrow.

Deta’s View

"Why don't we just leave him? It's not like we need him," Gwen declared loudly, her crossbow in hand as she walked away. "We could make it out on our own."

 I let out a sigh. "Well, maybe, but..." I glanced at Rinn and then back at Gwen. "He deserves a second chance."

Gwen placed her palm on her face in disbelief. "Unbelievable... You're going to give a murderer a second chance!" With that, she walked off.

I tried to call out to Gwen to get her to come back but she had already walked off. As I stood there in defeat, a pulling sensation began to build in my chest, with an almost melodious ring to it "It's the Soul Stone…” I whispered, looking back at the group I thought to myself. "I need to get to it."

Beans rolled his eyes and addressed me. "Alright, there's a city that way. If we're lucky, they might have a way out. If not then we can at least get something to eat." His attention then turned to where Gwen was, but had disappeared. "Where did she go?"

Gwen’s View

I made my way through the thick brush of the mushroom jungle, crossbow at the ready, still seething. "I swear... Deta is too soft," I muttered, my grip tightening on the weapon. The thought of him letting Rinn live after everything—that monster—made my blood boil. Seven years of torture, and Deta had the nerve to show him kindness. How could he even think Rinn deserved mercy? After all the pain he'd caused us—caused me.

The quiet around me was shattered by the sound of children giggling nearby. I paused, forcing my anger down as I turned toward the laughter, cautiously approaching their location.

In the distance, I spotted a little Dark Elf boy and girl playing, with glowing pink Fufus floating around them. A smile tugged at my lips as I watched their joy, but my attention quickly shifted to a nearby pit, glowing ominously red. From the pit, a hand emerged, followed by a small child-sized creature made of burning earth.

Instinctively, I reached for my sword, but before I could fully draw it, three more of the creatures crawled out, their attention quickly fixating on the children. They rushed towards them, the Fufus turning red and fleeing the scene.

The boy noticed the danger and shouted, "Run, Lann!" as he grabbed his sister's hand and began to run. But the little girl stumbled, falling to the ground.

She turned back, screaming in terror as the creatures closed in. I burst out of the bushes, dropping my crossbow and pulling out my sword, charging toward them. With a swift strike, I knocked one of the creatures backward with the blunt side of my sword.

 "Get out of here!" I yelled to the children, who scrambled to their feet and ran.

A Dark Elf woman, hearing my shout, rushed over, her eyes wide with fear as she called out, "Shunn! Lann!"

The children ran to her, and I turned my focus back to the fight. I swung my sword, slicing through one of the creature’s torsos. It let out a screech as it split into two pieces, each glowing intensely. Sensing an explosion, I planted my sword into the ground and ducked behind it just as the creature burst in a fiery blast of magma.

The remaining three creatures, enraged by the death of their comrade, charged at me. I quickly grabbed my crossbow from off the ground, firing a bolt into the head of one of them, which exploded, splattering magma all around. Some of it hit my right arm. I cursed, shaking off the burning liquid. My arm throbbed in pain, burning deep and angry.

As the last creature lunged for my hair, I dodged, leaping out of the way and delivering a hard kick that sent it tumbling into a nearby lake. It sank beneath the surface, its fiery glow fading into the depths until it was gone.

Breathing heavily, I walked over to retrieve my sword, feeling the sting in my arm as I sheathed it. My eyes fell on the Dark Elf woman and her children, the fear still clear on their faces.

Softly, I said, "You should keep a closer watch on your kids." I turned to leave, but the little girl’s voice stopped me.

"Here!" she called, holding out a stuffed Fufu toy with both hands, a bright smile on her face.

I blinked in surprise, hesitating. "Are you sure? I wouldn’t want to take it from you," I said, glancing at the toy.

She nodded eagerly. "Mhm! Here!"

With a soft smile, I took the stuffed Fufu and gently patted its head. "Thank you," I told her.

"His name is Shelly! Take good care of him!" she announced before running back to her mother. They waved as they walked away, and I found myself waving back.

Looking down at the toy in my hands, I chuckled softly. "Well, Shelly, looks like you’re coming with me." I tucked the little toy into my bag and made my way back to the group through the brush.

Deta’s View

I watched as Beans played with his hand ax when we heard the rustling sound coming from off the path. He readied his weapon but lowered it as Gwen emerged from the bushes. "Oh, you're back," he greeted her with a smile, putting away his ax.

Gwen nodded. "Yeah, I'm back."

I noticed her red cloth that was around her waist now wrapped around her arm. “Did you get hurt?” I asked her.

While glancing at Rinn, eyes narrowed with hate, she answered that she was fine and then turned to Beans. "Have you figured out a way yet?"

Beans nodded in affirmation. "Yep–”

I interrupted as fast as I could “Yes! It's that way!” I pointed in the general direction I felt the call before starting to head off. I need to help that Randeth.

Gwen rolled her eyes playfully. "Well, let's get going then."

I smiled and stood up from where I had been sitting on the ground. Bluma walked over to Gwen and patted her on the back, and Beans led the way as we continued through the jungle.

CHAPTER 15                                                                                                                        Don't Be Fooled

As we continued, Gwen and I exchanged glances, both noticing the ground beneath us transitioning from soft dirt to smooth stone. The dim jungle light faded behind us, and the air felt different—less damp, more still. I glanced around, curiosity bubbling up.

"Hey, Beans? Where exactly are we heading?" I asked, my voice breaking the quiet.

Before he could answer, Rinn cut in with his usual smug tone. "We are approaching our only connection to the Overworld. Welcome to the Crystal Plains."

The transformation was striking. Gone were the towering fungi and their eerie glow. Instead, immense crystals floated serenely above the ground, refracting light in shimmering patterns. The terrain stretched out, flat and vast, and far in the distance, a city gleamed like a mirage beneath the crystal sky.

The crystals emitted a gentle, comforting glow, imbued with an air of mystery. "Wow... These crystals are really pretty," I murmured, reaching out to touch one as we continued walking. Some of them towered so high I couldn’t see the top.

Beans crouched to the ground and picked up a shard, his eyes wide with wonder. “I’ve never seen anything quite like this before,” he said, turning it over in his hands.

I gathered a few of my own, the facets catching flashes of distant light. “These are so cool! I can’t wait to show Vomete!” I stuffed them into my backpack, grinning.

Behind me, Rinn gave a low chuckle. “You're quite taken with them, young one,” he said, his tone almost too smooth.

Gwen was tracing her fingers along one of the floating crystals, her brow furrowed. “I don’t like how quiet it is here,” she muttered.

Rinn’s smile deepened, but there was no warmth in it. “You catch on quickly,” he said. “Despite its calm exterior and your lack of memories, this place is infested with horrors. Lurking. Watching. So yes... tread carefully.”

He let the warning hang in the air like smoke, clearly enjoying the tension he’d stirred.

Beans turned to him with a groan. “Now you tell us?”

Rinn only smirked in response, the corners of his mouth curling with amusement. With an exaggerated roll of his eyes, Beans gave up on arguing, and we resumed our trek across the crystalline expanse.

As we passed a colossal shard jutting from the ground like a jagged monument, something caught my eye—a structure in the distance, tucked just off the path to our left.

“Hey, Rinn…” I called out, narrowing my eyes. “Is there supposed to be a house here?”

My words brought everyone to a halt. One by one, heads turned to follow my gaze, landing on the lone house nestled among the crystals. The silence returned, heavier than before.

Constructed from wood and various other materials from the Overworld, it seemed very out of place in this underground. Beans scratched his head in bewilderment. "A shack… down here?"

Gwen turned to Rinn with a sneer. “Any thoughts on this, creep?”

Rinn didn’t rise to the insult, only rolled his eyes as if her hatred amused him. He studied the structure in the distance with a thoughtful hum. “How peculiar…” he said, voice slow and deliberate. “I’ve never seen an Overworld structure this deep. Someone’s either lost—or hiding.”

He glanced at her then, the corner of his mouth twitching upward. “Curious, isn’t it?”

As we stared at the house, a sharp, high-pitched ringing sliced through the air. It wasn’t loud, but it drilled straight into my skull, like pressure behind the eyes. My vision warped for a heartbeat—colors bleeding into each other, the edges of the world smearing like wet paint. A sudden weight pressed down on my limbs, heavy and unnatural, as if gravity had thickened around me. I blinked, staggered slightly, but the feeling clung like cobwebs.

Then, cutting through the stillness, came a deep masculine voice from behind us—sudden, calm, and entirely out of place.

"So, you've stumbled upon my humble home…”

We turned, startled by the unexpected voice, and saw a towering figure with purple skin and a crystal beard standing before us. He had two green circles in a metal frame that rested on his nose and caught the light from the crystals.

Beans gripped his ax tightly and demanded, "Who are you?"

The man glanced down at Beans and calmly replied, "Call me Nek’tar. I am a humble researcher, so your weapons are unnecessary."

It was hard to trust his words, considering our encounters thus far in this dangerous underground realm. I should’ve been more cautious too, but... something about his voice made the tension in my shoulders ease. My thoughts felt distant for a moment—like they were echoing through fog.

Sensing our skepticism, Nek'tar addressed our hesitation, saying, "Please, join me in my home. You must be weary from your travels."

With that, Nek'tar proceeded forward. I looked back at the group, unsure of what to do. "Should we... see if he—?" I began.

Before I could finish, Gwen exploded, "Absolutely not! We won’t be lured into another trap!"

Rinn nodded in agreement, adding, "I’ve heard stories of a figure dwelling in this area—a creature that seeks knowledge by devouring brains."

I gave a nervous smile. “But those are just stories, right?”

My voice sounded distant to my own ears, like it was coming from somewhere else. I blamed it on fatigue, shaking my head lightly.

Rinn’s eyes narrowed as he shrugged. “In the underworld, the line between truth and tale is as thin as smoke.”

Feeling a mix of nervousness and uncertainty, I sighed, “Okay, then…”

But before anyone could speak further, Beans called out, “Hey, dark elf... What are those flying things up there?”

Rinn rolled his eyes and turned to look—then froze. His expression shifted in an instant. The usual arrogance drained from his face as his eyes locked onto three towering creatures circling above. They had wings like torn shadows, beaks sharp enough to pierce steel, and twelve writhing tentacles that slithered and coiled like grotesque serpents. Their bodies were a nightmare stitched together from impossible parts—glistening, slick, and alien.

A screech tore through the air, a sound so shrill and unnatural that it felt like it ripped into my very soul. It echoed, bouncing off the walls, deep and unsettling, as if the noise itself was a weapon, designed to tear away any semblance of sanity. The tentacles flailed, twitching with an insidious hunger, while their beaks snapped, eager to sink into flesh.

Every movement they made felt wrong, like they didn’t belong in this world at all. Their presence alone was enough to make the air feel heavier, darker... suffocating.

“Nu’puls…” Rinn breathed, his voice a whisper of panic. Then louder—“We need to run! Now!”

The creatures dove, talons flashing, their massive forms cutting through the air like knives.

Gwen groaned and cursed “Everyone, to the researcher’s house!"

With urgency, we sprinted toward Nek’tar's home, desperate to escape the pursuing creatures or at least buy enough time to come up with a plan. Bluma swiftly carried Beans, who was starting to lag behind.

Rinn stumbled, hindered by his chains, was pulled back as one of the towering beings screeched, its wings rustling ominously as it extended its tentacles, closing in on Rinn. Just as it was about to reach him, he fell to his knees, bracing for the worst. He shut his eyes, only to feel a sudden force tackle him aside. Rolling on the ground, he realized Bluma had pushed him, saving him from the creature's grasp.

Bluma glared at him with the bottom set of eyes, pulling Rinn to his feet. We continued our frantic dash toward Nek'tar’s house. Bluma quickly opened the door, and we rushed inside just as one of the towering creatures slammed against it, trying to force its way in. Gwen spotted a crystal couch and made a move toward it, Rinn rushed to help her lift it.

“I don’t need YOUR help!” she yelled at him, her voice rising above the chaos as she strained to lift the heavy couch. Her muscles burned, each inch of movement demanding more than she felt capable of giving.

He groaned in frustration, sweat glistening on his brow. “Hate me later!

The creature’s tentacles smashed through a window, grabbing Beans' leg and trying to pull him out. “Let me go!” Beans shouted, struggling fiercely. He managed to grab his small ax and struck the tentacle, causing the monster to screech and release him. Disoriented, Beans dropped his ax but steadied himself.

The creature relentlessly slammed against the door again, each impact reverberating through the air like a drumbeat of dread. Bluma pressed her back against the splintering wood, muscles straining as she struggled to keep it shut. Her heart raced in time with the creature's violent assaults, each crash sending jolts of fear through her.

Beans and I surged forward to help Bluma, our combined weight pressing against the door. The creature slammed against it again, its force nearly overwhelming. My hands gripped the splintering wood, and I leaned my shoulder into it, fighting against the creature's relentless assaults.

"We need to keep it out!" I shouted, my voice barely breaking through the chaos.

With a final, thunderous thud, the monster broke through part of the door, its sharp beak piercing inside, splinters flying as the wood splintered under the pressure. Bluma felt the cold rush of panic swell within her. She shifted her position, wedging her shoulder against the frame, but the added weight of the creature’s mass made it harder to maintain her grip. The relentless creature pushed, its beak inching closer, a dark void framed by jagged edges.

Desperation clawed at her throat as she fought to keep the door closed, sweat beading on her brow. With every ounce of strength, she pressed against the door, her breathing growing shallow. She could feel the creature's hot breath on her face, a terrifying reminder of how close it was to breaking through.

“Gwen, help us!” I called as she hoisted the heavy couch. Standing up, I gripped my magic staff tight, swinging it at the creature’s beak and sending it flying. Gwen and Rinn seized the opportunity to wedge the couch against the door with a resounding thud. Sweating from the effort, they gasped for breath. I tried to help her but couldn’t even lift the couch.

“How heavy is this thing?! It feels like it weighs a million tons!” I exclaimed in frustration.

Gwen chuckled, replying, “Heavy enough to keep those monsters out.” They tried to straighten their backs just as another creature tried to break through. But with the couch in place, it couldn’t succeed and thrashed its tentacles in frustration. Gwen growled and grabbed a pillow, throwing it at the creature’s tentacles.”Just leave us alone already!” Just as she reached for her sword, mistaking the pillow for possible food, the creature gripped it tight and, along with the others, flew away.

We all let out a collective sigh of relief, but it was short-lived—another screech echoed from outside. Two smaller ones flew in through the windows. One landed on Beans’ head, while the other darted around, trying to attach itself to one of us. Gwen unsheathed her sword, attempting to strike the small beast, but with the small area of movement, it dodged every move. Meanwhile, the one on Beans clung tightly, digging into his flesh. In agony, Beans cried, “Get this thing off me!” He struggled fiercely to pry it loose.

"I’ll help!" I shouted. I grabbed Beans' ax from the floor, using its blunt side to swing at the creature. Its exposed body burst on impact. In my eagerness, I swung again but accidentally hit Beans on the head. "Ow! Dang it, Deta!" he barked, rubbing his head.

"Sorry!" I quickly apologized as the creature fell dead to the floor.

It was then that a voice from behind us spoke. "Well... seems you decided to come after all."

Still on edge from the fight, our group spun around. Nek'tar sat in a grand-backed chair that hadn’t been there before, a delicate teacup held between his fingers. The steam rising from it smelled faintly of lavender and something darker, almost metallic.

He set the cup down with a soft clink. Gwen, tense, instinctively gripped her sword’s hilt.

Nek’tar sighed, the sound strangely hollow. “Be at ease, half-elf. I do not intend to harm you as my brother would.”

Beans blinked, brow furrowed. “You're an elf!?”

Gwen’s gaze remained locked on Nek’tar, her tone clipped. “Half, genius.”

Nek’tar stood, movements smooth but almost too fluid, as though the air resisted him. He gestured lazily toward a nearby room. “Please, make yourselves comfortable in the meeting room. I shall join you shortly.”

When I glanced left, I saw the room he spoke of—though I was sure it hadn’t been there before. Cushioned chairs in a perfect semi-circle, the walls shifting in tone like candlelight on water.

“Alright, let’s go, guys,” I said, voice sounding distant to my own ears, motioning them inside.

Beans, of course, couldn’t help but prod. “Why didn’t you tell us you were an elf?”

Gwen rolled her eyes. “I’m sorry I forgot to share my entire life story with you. It’s none of your business!”

Beans scoffed. “Of course, an elf would think like that—”

Gwen stood so fast her chair skidded. “Half! I am not an elf!”

Bluma’s sword gleamed in the flickering light as she stepped between them, her voice quiet but firm. “Half.”

Trying to steady the rising tension, I spoke gently, though my throat felt dry. “Gwen, we understand... but why do you have such strong feelings against elves?”

Rinn interjected, always curious, “Pardon my intrusion, but—”

“Don’t you dare finish that sentence,” Gwen growled.

Bluma slowly sheathed her sword, the motion oddly delayed, like time was stretching at the edges.

“My… captor. Was a purist elf… I’ve been in slavery and tortured for it, for as long as I can remember, which isn’t much anymore.”

Rinn looked away. The light on his skin shimmered strangely. His voice, for once, was barely audible. “Given the extent of her physical and emotional trauma… the memories would fade along with the scars. That’s the nature of the restoration potion.”
