Gwen’s breath trembled. “My first owner kept me for twenty-one years. Having a slave that long is considered an ill omen.”

Rinn’s shadow seemed to flicker even in the still air. “He couldn’t wait to dump his cursed burden, so he sold you to me for a measly copper.”

Gwen snapped, lunging—but before she made contact, Nek’tar lifted a finger. With a pulse like thunder muffled underwater, she collapsed into her seat, frozen.

“Hey!” Gwen cried, unable to rise.

Nek’tar’s calm smile returned. “Please, no violence. I just had the carpets cleaned from your entrance.”

He sat beside me, the warmth of his presence oddly cold. “Now, let’s get down to business. Who owns the dark elf?”

I swallowed. My mouth tasted like ash. “Uh… none of us… We’re trying to free him.”

Nek’tar’s eyes shimmered white. “Fascinating… Even after what he’s done? He did kidnapped your friend Rose.”

Her name echoed, a soft whisper that seemed to linger in the air. I blinked, feeling the weight of it. "How... Do you know that?"

His voice slithered through the air, curling around me like smoke, then suddenly, it was inside my head. “Will you claim him as your slave, or do you still intend to save him?”

My heart pounded. Images flooded in—Rose smiling, then screaming, tortured by magic, burned alive. I clutched my head. “Stop it!” I cried.

But his voice merged with her scream. What will you do, Randeth? Will you let the fire consume you?

I opened my eyes—and flames consumed me. The heat was unbearable. I screamed, thrashing, the scent of scorched flesh filling my nose. My skin blistered, vision warped in waves of heat. Nek’tar’s face loomed. I struck him, and he flew back—

Then the fire vanished.

I sat in the chair again. The air was cool. No one else remained.

I gasped, checking my limbs—no burns. No smoke. “What the hell…”

Everyone was gone.

“Gwen?” I called. “Beans? Bluma?”

Silence.

I staggered through the hall. Shadows curled along the walls. In a circular mirror, I caught my reflection—my eyes glowed pink.

“I’m… under a spell,” I muttered. My fists clenched. “When did that happen? Where is—”

A door creaked open.

I rushed through it. “Nek’tar!”

Roots tangled around the entrance. I shoved through, breath quickening.

At the base of a staircase, a room bathed in pink light waited. Four pillars burned with ghostly flame. When I turned to leave—the stairs were gone.

A voice spoke. I turned.

Rose stood in a black gown, eyes shining with fury. “No thanks to you.”

“Rose! You’re okay!” I stepped forward—

“Stay back.” Her hands burned with pink fire.

“Rose, I tried to save you—”

“But you didn’t.” She raised a sword of flame.

“Rose, please!”

She charged. Her blade slashed, searing off my arm. I cried out, stumbling.

In desperation, I kicked her back, summoning roots. They twisted around her like snakes.

“I hate you!” she screamed.

“…I’m sorry, Rose…” My voice broke. “I tried to save you…”

Her screams followed me even as I shut the door.

I slumped against it, exhausted. Books scattered around. “I wanted to help you…”

My arm… had healed. Fully.

 What…? I shouldn't be able to heal that fast…

I rose, now unsure of anything. “Maybe I can still help…”

Opening the door again—an endless black ocean. I slammed it shut.

Next, a field of flowers under a too-blue sky. To the north, a kingdom. South, a forest.

I stepped forward—

The ground swallowed me whole.

“No!” I screamed, flailing.

Darkness.

Then light.

I blinked. A cave.

“Rubert?”

He beamed. “Yes, good sir!”

I ran to him, embraced him—then froze.

“I wouldn’t be so sure about that,” he said, and changed.

His form melted away, robes and floppy hat replacing his features. A man smiled where Rubert had been.

“What are you doing?” I asked.

“Wake up, Deta.”

The world shattered like glass.

And I awoke.

Beans’ hand reaching down, voice raw with panic—

“Deta! Wake up!”

Confusion and panic gripped me as I realized I was trapped in a small crevasse in the ground. "What's going on?!" I asked, my voice trembling.

I watched as Bluma was thrown over Beans, and he urgently shouted, "No time! Hurry, grab my hand!" Struggling to free my arm, I finally managed to squeeze it out from my side and reached out, desperately grasping for Beans' hand. "Guys! He's awake! Help!"

I watched in horror as the colossal, purple, worm-like monster with countless teeth in its gaping maw roared, its massive form descending upon us. The air vibrated with the sound of its rage, and in an instant, its terrifying presence engulfed us, casting a shadow over everything.

CHAPTER 16                                                                                                                               The Belly of the Beast

I woke up on the ground, finding it strangely soft, slimy, and pink. Quickly regaining my footing, I scanned my surroundings, calling out, "Guys!? Where are you?"

Worry crept in as I spotted the scattered rocks and rubble, fearing my friends had been crushed. I rushed toward the pile, just as Gwen's head poked out from beneath the debris, struggling to free herself.

"Stupid worm," she muttered, her frustration clear. When she saw me, she quipped, "About time you woke up! Now help me out of here, Bushy!"

I hurried over, eagerly shifting rocks to help her escape. As she stepped onto the squishy ground, she sighed. "Thanks," she said, glancing around.

"Where—?" I started but before I could finish, more rocks tumbled down, revealing Bluma and Beans, with Rinn perched on Bluma's shoulders.

Relief washed over me, and I smiled. "You guys are okay!"

Bluma nodded confidently. "Yeah, it takes more than that to bring us down." Beans smiled proudly.

Chuckling, I added, "I'm glad we all can see in the dark well but... what happened?"

Gwen exhaled sharply, her eyes flashing with anger as she said, "That geode creature put us under a spell. When I woke up, we were chained up on a cart, like we were nothing more than property. He was planning to sell us as slaves." Her fists clenched tightly, her voice thick with fury. "I got in one good hit on him, but then that giant worm showed up and ruined everything."

Beans nodded. "Yeah, Bluma and I broke free after the worm destroyed the cart. It ripped whatever his name was in half and turned on us."

Gwen glanced at Rinn and sneered. "Wow, the princess is still out cold.”

Beans looked at Rinn and saw chains on him, "weird..."

Gwen frowned.

"What is it?" Beans pointed to the glowing green chains.

Gwen’s laugh started low, almost as if she couldn’t believe what she was seeing. It grew louder, richer, like a weight lifting off her chest, each note sharpening. It wasn’t just joy—it was the sound of justice finally catching up, a bitter edge woven into every gasp for air. Her eyes gleamed with satisfaction as the laughter spilled out, unstoppable, a release of everything she’d held inside for so long.

“Look at that! The chains have changed color! Just what he deserves for all the pain he caused!” Gwen grinned, her arms crossed smugly as she took in Rinn’s new, shackled state. Her eyes danced with cruel delight, unable to mask the vindication she felt.

Confused, I asked, "What do you mean?"

Still chuckling, Gwen replied, "That means someone has claimed him as a slave. I wonder who it is!" She couldn't stop giggling. “Can't be that crystal dude because he is definitely dead, so that means one of us did it when we were being swallowed!” She laughed more, hunching over to hold herself.

Meanwhile, Beans noticed his hand ax had become lodged in the ground. As he pulled it out, the whole area trembled, and a deafening roar filled the air. Startled, I instinctively covered my ears, as did the others.

When the noise subsided, we noticed the walls and ceiling contracting and expanding, accompanied by a low, rhythmic breathing. Gwen’s laughter now gone, frowned. "Looks like we're inside the purple worm..."

My eyes widened. "What!? We're inside it!?"

Beans echoed, "We're... inside a worm?" It took a moment for the realization to sink in.

Glancing up, I noticed the worm’s spine arching above us, a jagged, sinuous ridge pressing against the fleshy ceiling like the backbone of some ancient beast. It stretched on endlessly, its segmented bones shifting with each subtle tremor, reminding me just how alive—and massive—the creature we were trapped inside truly was.

“How do we get out?” Beans asked, his voice trembling with anxiety as his eyes darted around, scanning for any signs of escape.

Gwen surveyed the area, her gaze sharp and focused, before climbing atop the rocks for a better vantage point. She pointed toward a dark, elongated opening that tapered at one end, its smooth, muscular walls glistening slightly to us.

 "Over here! Let's try breaking through." she then jumped down the other side.

Beans and I followed her up the rocks, while Bluma stayed with Rinn's unconscious body. Gwen swung her sword at the closed esophagus, but nothing happened. "Tch," she scoffed, striking it again to no avail.

"Here, let me try!" Beans jumped down, swinging his ax at the obstruction, but it didn't budge.

I was standing at the top of the rock pile—watching, when suddenly, a cold sensation crept up my back. Panicking, I slid down the rocks, landing near Beans and Gwen. Looking up, I saw two jellyfish-like creatures drifting toward us.

"Gwen! Beans!" I called urgently. They stopped and followed my gaze.

Seeing the white jellyfish, the group readied their weapons, but to our surprise, it floated effortlessly through the closed esophagus, as if it were not there. "What... was that thing?" I asked

"I don't know. Stay on guard," Beans responded, his ax held tight.

Gwen said, glancing at me, still on the ground. "You gonna get up or just stay there?" she teased.

Laughing, I stood. "It gave me a jump scare."

Gwen rolled her eyes while Beans chuckled, but our relief was short-lived. A white tentacle lashed out, wrapping around Beans' arm. He screamed in pain as the creature tried to pull him into the fleshy walls. Gwen reacted quickly, slicing the tentacle with her sword.

Beans threw the severed tentacle aside, acid hissing as the tentacle splattered on the ground, his skin was a mess of blistered, raw flesh, the acid having burned deep in the few seconds it touched him.

"Beans! Are you okay?" I asked, panic rising in my voice as I rushed toward him, unable to tear my eyes away from the damage.

Bluma was already at his side, her eyes wide with alarm as she examined the burns, moving quickly to check for any deeper injuries.

"Yeah, yeah, I'm fine..." Beans winced, trying to shake it off despite the obvious pain. "It just burns." His voice strained, but there was a toughness to it, the kind that suggested he'd faced worse and lived to tell the tale.

I sighed and placed my hand over his arm. A green glow spread from my touch, healing the injury.

"Thanks," Beans said, though he winced slightly at the sensation.

"No problem." I smiled, finishing up the healing.

Gwen asked, "Why didn’t it burn you? It touched you when you got scared, right?"

I nodded, puzzled. "Yeah, it did touch me. I wonder why it didn’t hurt." Removing my hand from Beans' arm, I added, "There you go, all done."

He tested his arm and chuckled. "Thanks, Deta."

Gwen spotted the jellyfish creature reemerging from the walls. "Let's keep moving before it grabs one of us again," she urged.

We scrambled back up the rocks, noticing the creature moving blindly. When Gwen landed on the other side, she noticed green liquid coating the ground. We stepped through it carefully.

"So, what's the plan now?" Gwen asked, looking at me.

Surprised, I hesitated. "You’re asking me?" She nodded. "Uh... well, we could—Behind you!" I shouted. We turned to see five more jellyfish floating toward us. We all took out our weapons and tried to slowly backup.

"What are these things?" Gwen muttered, drawing her sword. Beans hurled a rock, missing completely. "Nice shot," Gwen deadpanned. Groaning, Beans retrieved his ax.

“Watch.." Bluma pointed to where the rock had landed. The jellyfish floated toward it, inspecting it with their tentacles before drifting away. Beans stared, trying to figure it out. Then, a Nu’pul suddenly darted out of the rocks and charged at me. I reacted, striking it with my staff and sending it flying into one of the jellyfish.

The jellyfish wrapped its tentacles around the creature, dissolving it into a mush that was absorbed into the floor leaving a terrible smell in its place. "Ew..." Beans wrinkled his nose.

 "It looks like they don’t see, they just feel around for anything that’s not a rock," I said.

Gwen rolled her eyes. "So, anything that isn’t a rock is a threat to them. Great, while we die Deta can live here forever."

"Gwen, look," I said, pointing as the jellyfish retracted into their gelatinous bodies. "I think they were searching for us, and they mistook that thing for one of us. Now that it's gone..."

Gwen let out a sigh and asked, "So, what does that mean?"

I replied with a sigh of my own, "It means this." Raising my hand, I channeled energy into Gwen, causing her to emit a green glow and her skin to transform into a woody texture.

"Hey! What are you doing, Bushy?!" she exclaimed.

"Well, if they didn't harm me, and my body is composed of wood, stone, moss, and other elements, I thought that by encasing you guys in wood, we might remain safe as long as we don't provoke them," I explained.

Gwen crossed her arms and reluctantly agreed, "Fine, but if I'm stuck like this, you'll pay for it!"

I smiled and turned my attention to Beans, Bluma and passed out Rinn. After a few minutes, Bluma, Gwen, and Beans all had wood-like skin, while Rinn had taken on a stony appearance.

"Now that we have some protection... the only option I can think of is to make our way towards the exit," I suggested.

"Ew! That's gross!" Beans protested, his expression contorted in disgust.

Gwen added, "It's repulsive. No way!" Even Bluma seemed disgusted.

I sighed "Unfortunately, going back the way we came.. does not seem possible, so there's only one way out."

Bluma shook her head, clearly reluctant, but joined me, standing by my side.

"Really, Bluma? You're okay with this plan?" Beans asked, surprised and defeated.

Bluma nodded “Yes” She said solemnly to which Beans let out another sigh and joined us, and after a lot of convincing, Gwen finally agreed.

After Bluma picked up Rinn, we began our descent down the giant worm's body, making our way towards its stomach. As we arrived, we witnessed large boulders and small stones being digested.

"This thing actually eats rocks… yay…," I muttered, concern evident in my voice.

Gwen sighed, "Well, this is just great. If we fall in, our disguises will be gone and then we get those stupid jellyfish things."

Beans nodded in agreement, and Rinn began to stir. Gwen rolled her eyes as Rinn regained his senses.

"What...?" he murmured, noticing he was slung over Bluma's shoulder like a limp fish. "Excuse me, would you put me down? I don’t need to be carried around like some trophy by a Demon woman!" pushed himself off of Bluma, causing her to stumble to the side.

Beans bristled at Rinn’s remark. "How dare you! Bluma saved your life! You should be thanking her, not insulting her!"

Rinn shrugged dismissively. "Please. I’m not a peasant who worships anyone. And she hardly qualifies for adoration. Demons like her are all the same – complete idiots."

Frustration surged in Beans, his pulse quickening. Bluma straightened her posture, her eyes narrowing at Rinn's words, silently conveying her strength despite the insult. "Hardly qualifies? Bluma is the strongest knight in the land! Her training since childhood has made her an unmatched warrior!"

Rinn scoffed. "Unmatched? She wouldn’t last a day in the field without help; she couldn’t even beat a child in a real challenge. Her lineage alone disqualifies her from true valor."

Beans' fists clenched, anger igniting his words. "You think your heritage defines worth? Bluma could take you down any day! Strength doesn’t just come from blood—it comes from grit and determination!"

Rinn groaned, uninterested in the exchange. "Her IQ can be easily manipulated. What can a creature like her truly understand about strategy or honor?"

Beans threw an exasperated hand toward Bluma, who remained silent but resolute. "She’s the smartest woman I know! You’re just scared of her power because it challenges your narrow view of what a knight should be."

That earned him a laugh from Rinn. "If she were so smart, she’d have found a way out of this mess by now. But instead, here she is, carrying a pathetic excuse for a knight."

Beans tilted his head, a smirk creeping onto his face. "Have you found a way up yet?"

Gwen chuckled at Beans’ retort. “Oh this is gonna be fun”

I looked to her confused as to how an argument could be fun to watch especially since they seemed like they wanted to kill each other.

Silence fell, and Beans' grin widened. "Bluma isn’t just beautiful; she’s also brilliant. Her scarlet hair and deep eyes reflect her incredible spirit. Years of discipline have sculpted her into a warrior whose very presence commands respect!"

Rinn crossed his arms, unimpressed. "Beauty is subjective. Physical strength? That's hardly proof of intelligence. I’d take wit over brute force any day. And as for her skills? I've seen nothing that impresses me."

Beans’ blood boiled. "You’re just jealous! Bluma's dedication and ingenuity are unmatched. She’s saved lives not just by swinging a sword but by outsmarting foes. She can anticipate moves before they happen!"

Rinn smirked. "Saving lives just means she can swing a sword. It’s not exactly genius work. Besides, does she really think she’s special? Just another Demon playing at being a knight."

Bluma's turned away as she covered her face with on hand getting tired of the argument and looking slightly embarrassed.

Rinn’s sarcasm dripped from every word. "Oh, how noble. But we live in a world where strength and power reign supreme. A knight’s valor may earn a nod, but it crumbles under true intellect. Her kind has never been known for wisdom."

Beans shook his head, fists clenched. "You underestimate the importance of being well-rounded. Bluma proves you don’t have to choose between strength and intelligence. Body and mind can work together, and that’s what makes her extraordinary."

I looked at Gwen again. “Should I do something?”

Gwen chuckled and firmly replied. “Nope.”

Rinn’s smirk returned. "You can keep your idealism. Bluma may swing a sword well enough, but she lacks the depth that true intellect demands. Life is more than following orders and pretending to be a warrior."

Beans’ determination surged, fueled by pride for Bluma. "Her courage inspires everyone around her. It’s not just about physical battles; it’s about the battles she fights every day against those who would undermine her."

Rinn rolled his eyes, but his expression faltered at the intensity of Beans’ passion. "If you’re so taken with her, why don’t you both get married? Oh, wait. As a Royal Knight, one or both of you would be banished, or even better killed! So why not just give up while you’re ahead?"

Before Rinn could finish his sentence, Bluma struck him in the neck, causing him to fall unconscious. “Lout..” She said in a hiss like whisper.

Gwen chuckled and looked to the acid lake we had to cross “We could throw him in there-”

I interrupted her quickly shouting that we would not do that.  After a moment of silence, she spoke up, “Let’s hurry up and get over this ocean of death, hm?” A smile danced on her lips.

I chuckled nervously, knowing that was quite literally true for me. “Yeah... let’s get going.”

Gwen took a few steps back and then ran forward, jumping onto the first floating boulder. As she landed, it sank into the water slightly before floating back up. “Whoa,” she exclaimed, trying to maintain her balance.

“Careful!” I called out, making her roll her eyes.

“I know that!” she sighed before leaping to the next boulder. Bluma and Beans followed suit.

I stood on the edge, contemplating how badly things could go, and I started shaking.

“Hey, Bushy!” I looked up to see Gwen on a platform in the middle. “Get over yourself and get moving over here!”

I took some deep breaths, but my heart raced like a wild animal trapped in my chest. “Mivomafisockmas…” I whispered, trying to steady my breath, yet the taste of fear filled my mouth, leaving it dry and heavy. I stepped back, my gaze fixed on the edge, but the terrifying thought gripped me: If I fell in, I wouldn’t come back out.

“Deta! Hurry up! It’s starting to rise!” Beans yelled, his voice piercing through the haze of panic. My eyes widened as I turned to see the ominous rise creeping toward me, dark and unyielding. It loomed like a predator, ready to swallow me whole. My instincts screamed at me to run, but terror rooted me in place.

“I can’t do it,” I whispered, my voice barely audible over the pounding in my ears. The ground beneath me felt like it was shifting, each tremor echoing the urgency of the moment.

Suddenly, a splash of acid hit my leg, and I screamed, clutching it in agony. The searing pain surged through me, but it only fueled my desperation. “I need to get over there,” I gasped, glancing at the platform where Gwen and the others were safely positioned, their faces a mixture of concern and urgency.

I began cautiously leaping from one boulder to another, making every effort to avoid the corrosive stomach acid that threatened to engulf me.

“Come on, Deta!” Beans urged, urgency lacing his voice.

“Move your butt, Leaf-head!!” Gwen chimed in, her tone a mix of encouragement and impatience.

I nodded in determination and pressed on, successfully reaching the last boulder, which teetered on the edge of disintegration. Barely being able to balance as the ground trembled beneath me.

“Deta! Jump!” I heard Gwen shout, noticing that the platform they occupied had risen further while the acid level began to recede. Without hesitation, I leaped as high as I could, but I watched in horror as the rock beneath me crumbled away, vanishing into the depths of the acid below.

Gwen reached down, her eyes wide with fear, trying to catch me, but my jump fell agonizingly short. I could see the determination etched on her face, the desperation in her outstretched hand. Time seemed to stretch as I flailed in midair, feeling the weight of the moment crush me. My heart thundered in my chest, drowning out the chaos around me.

Before I could grasp her fingers, something surged up from the acid—a creature with glimmering golden eyes that seemed to shine like tiny suns amidst the murky depths. Its brown scales glistened, slick and unyielding, as it latched onto me with a grip that felt like iron. Panic flooded my veins as it yanked me downward, the burning liquid swallowing me whole.

“Deta!!!” Gwen cried out, their voices hauntingly distant as I splashed into the seething abyss.

Holding my breath through the burning pain, I caught sight of an eel-like creature with small golden eyes and brown scales. It clutched me firmly in its mouth, dragging me deeper into the seething depths.

Desperately, I began striking at its eyes, hoping to loosen its grip, but my efforts not only seemed to infuriate it further but more quickly break my body down. It clamped down harder on my torso, causing excruciating pain. Out of pain, I unintentionally inhaled, scorching my insides. Struggling against the creature, the corrosive acid slowly drained my strength, gradually eroding my consciousness.

My mind started to detach from the situation as my thoughts went to Vomete, the Soul Stone, Gwen, and the others. “I’m sorry... I can’t stay awake... much longer...” I murmured in my thoughts. I could feel the Stone so close… but it couldn't do anything.

Just as I began to close my eyes, I noticed two blurry dots approaching from above. One latched onto the eel hitting it with something, causing it to release its hold on me. The other figure was swimming near me, but before I could discern their identity, my eyes shut.

When I eventually opened my eyes, a sensation of weightlessness enveloped me. Despite the excruciating pain, I felt an overwhelming sense of peace and happiness. Is... this what death is like? Has my stone shattered? Am I dead...? Suddenly, a brilliant light materialized to my left. As I gazed toward it, I discerned a woman clad in white robes, radiating a brightness surpassing that of the sun.

“Deta... you mustn’t allow them to triumph,” she said, her voice resonating with familiarity.

Intrigued, I inquired, “Triumph? Who will triumph? What do you mean?”

The woman’s smile was gentle yet enigmatic. “The council has conspired against you, as such I bestow upon you a second chance... do not squander it. My assistance is limited, for they must remain unaware.” Extending her hand, she intertwined her fingers with mine, and a surge of revitalizing energy coursed through my being.

“What, who are you referring to?” I asked, confused by her words. However, she refused to answer me. Suddenly, a radiant light emerged from behind me, propelling me toward another source of illumination. “Wait, am I dying?” I questioned, my voice filled with trepidation.

The woman chuckled softly. “Quite the opposite.”

In an instant, my entire field of vision transformed into a blinding white, accompanied by a deafening ringing in my ears. As the ringing subsided, my sight gradually returned, revealing Beans yelling something in my direction while Bluma stood behind him, her hair drenched and acid dripping off her, causing fragments of her bark-like skin melting away like snow.

"Deta! Can you hear me?" Beans exclaimed, relief flooding his voice.

I managed a faint smile. "Yeah... your voice is loud and clear... mostly loud, though."

His face lit up with joy as he fell backward onto the ground. "He's alive!" he exclaimed, laughter filling the air.

Suddenly, a surge of intense pain coursed through me like a crashing wave, prompting me to gaze down at my arms, which bore the ravages of the acid. However, a faint white glow enveloped my body, causing my wounds to regenerate.

With gratitude, I silently thanked the mysterious woman. "Thanks, lady... you're a true lifesaver."

Summoning my strength, I managed to sit up and immediately noticed Gwen's absence. Confusion washed over me as I asked, "Where is Gwen?"

Bluma knelt beside me, pointing, where I spotted Gwen sitting next to the colossal and now dead eel, her head buried in her arms. Her drenched black hair covered her face, revealing slightly pointed ears, while her bark-like skin had been completely stripped away. I noticed her sword impaled in the eel's head and many stab wounds, a bit away from where she sat at the end.

Beans let out a sigh. "She kept repeating some strange words when you wouldn't wake up," he explained.

I looked at him intently. "What was it?" I asked, curious to unravel the mystery. Beans took a moment, trying to recall the word.

"I think it was something like... Mivo... miva..."

Bluma then chimed in, "Mivomafisockmas." My eyes widened in astonishment.

"She said that?" I was genuinely surprised, not expecting Gwen to remember it. Beans then inquired about its meaning. Letting out a sigh, I responded, "It means... comfort."

I walked over to retrieve Gwen's sword, finding it slightly stuck in the eel's head. After some effort, I managed to pull it free and carried it back to her, settling down beside her.

Silence stretched between us for a few seconds before I spoke softly. "Are you... doing okay, Gwen?"

She lifted her head, surprise etching her features. "You're... alive?" I smiled and nodded, only to be sent flying by an unexpectedly powerful punch that made me drop the sword. "What was that for?!" I exclaimed, bewildered by her reaction.

"You could have died!!" Gwen yelled, her voice laced with worry, tears filling her eyes.

Defensively, I got up from the floor. "Hey, I didn't want to die!" I protested, confusion and frustration swirling within me which quickly died down upon seeing her tears.

Gwen's voice softened, but the tears still welled in her eyes. "Well, you should have thought of that before you got us involved!" she retorted, the weight of her words resonating with the shared anguish of Beans and Bluma, who now stood nearby, shedding tears of relief.

I turned my gaze back to Gwen, realizing the depth of their care for me. Smiling warmly at Gwen, I reassured her, "Well, I'm not dying again... I promise."

She raised an eyebrow, with a small chuckle and a mix of disbelief and growing amusement on her face. "You're a weird one, Bushy." With that, she picked up her sword, stowed it away, and stood up.

"Hey, the tree lives!" Gwen said to Beans and Bluma. They exchanged glances, relief washing over their faces before bursting into laughter. I joined in, the air filled with shared joy and gratitude.

But our respite was abruptly cut short as the ground beneath us began to shift, moving us toward the roof. "What's going on!?" Beans exclaimed, confusion and worry creeping into his voice.

I scanned our surroundings, desperately trying to make sense of the situation. My eyes landed on a hole slowly opening near the roof. Realization struck me. "Guys... we're inside the stomach. Where does food go after being digested?!"

We exchanged concerned glances, and Gwen voiced our collective thought, "Well... this was supposed to be our way out, right?"

I smiled uncomfortably, the gravity of our predicament sinking in. "Yeah... but um..." I glanced at the lifeless eel before us. "Everyone, help me move the eel!"

"What do you think you're doing, Bushy?" Gwen asked, confusion etched on her face as she and the others rushed over. "If we angle its head, it can slide down easier."

The eel's head proved quite heavy, but with Gwen's assistance, we managed to maneuver it. Beans joined us, skepticism and concern flickering in his eyes. "How does helping the thing poop better help us?"

I met his gaze and replied, "Better than yall being drained of your juices”

At that point everyone agreed to get into the eel, throwing Rinns passed out body first. Once inside the floor began to rise towards the top of the stomach.

 “This may feel tight,” I warned.

The hole near the roof widened, and as the eel's body then pressed against the ceiling of the worm's stomach, it began sliding toward the opening. It dropped on the other side, hitting the ground with a thud and quickly drying up, causing its skin to become brittle and breakable. One by one, we emerged from inside the eel, greeted by a chorus of disgusted exclamations.

Gwen crawled out of the eel's mouth, holding her arms in disgust.

"Gross!" Beans yelled, having tasted some eel gut. Bluma carefully dragged Rinn out and set him down on the ground, her expression weary, and I followed suit.

"Bushy, after this, I am never going back inside another creature!" Gwen declared, her tone a mixture of exasperation and determination.

I chuckled, attempting to lighten the mood. "I swear, we're done with this after today." However, as I surveyed our new surroundings, my heart sank. We found ourselves in another vast and cavernous chamber within the colossal purple worm.

"You've got to be kidding me... we're still not out?" Beans groaned, frustration evident in his voice. He walked over to the lifeless eel, ripped out a rib bone, and flung it away in irritation.

The bone soared through the air, landing behind a large mound of brown matter and producing a faint chime upon impact. Beans and I exchanged intrigued glances and ventured closer to investigate.

Gwen, with a mix of reluctance and curiosity, questioned our actions. "What are you two idiots doing?"

I paused and turned back to her. "We heard something behind that pile and wanted to see what it was."

Gwen appeared as though she wanted to argue, but she rubbed her eyes and sighed. "Alright, whatever. Be careful, alright?"

I smiled and nodded in agreement. Then Beans let out a cry, I hurried over to see what had happened, fearing something bad had occurred.

"Beans, what is it? Is something wrong?" I turned the corner to find him clutching three gems. "I found elemental stones! I have to show Bluma!" Without wasting a moment, he darted off to show her and Gwen. I chuckled and glanced back, only to spot a skeleton holding an open box.

Just as I was about to walk away I felt a wave of energy shoot out of the box, the energy caused me to pause for a moment. “There is no way..” I muttered.

Slowly making my way to the wooden box. I then, with caution, removed the box from the skeletons hands and just as I was about to open it, I could feel an intense heat from my side, looking towards it I caught sight of a pillar of fire hurtling toward me.

"What the heck?!" I swiftly leaped out of harm's way, narrowly avoiding the flames and the large brown mound.

Glancing back at where the pillar came from, I was surprised to see Gwen wearing a broad smile, a gem now adorning her sword's blade. "This is awesome!" she exclaimed, laughing. "You're not so bad after all, Dwarf!"

Gwen then turned and noticed me on the ground. "Why are you lying on the floor, Bushy?" I got back up and walked over to her.

I retorted as I tried to stand up "Because I nearly got set on fire! What was that?"

Gwen grinned. "The stones Beans brought gave my sword enchantments." Her sword now glowed white and as she swung it around fire followed it through the air.

I smiled nervously, considering the newfound powers she possessed.

Beans couldn't help but chuckle at the show "And there's a blue and white gem! They represent water and air magic, respectively. These gems are some of the rarest in the world!" Beans stowed the remaining two gems in his pouch. "I'm going to hold onto them!"

Gwen looked to Beans excitedly “Oh! You gotta let me try those out!”

Panicked that Gwen might summon a tornado inside, I cut her off before she could reach the stones. “Well how about we wait till we are all back home huh?”

Meanwhile, next to the eel, Rinn slowly sat up and surveyed his surroundings. "Where... Where in the nine realms are we?"

Gwen responded quick and blunt. "We're in the worm's butt."

His face twisted in disgust. "The indignity..." Standing up, he noticed that his cuffs had turned green. "Who has done this? I refuse to become someone's slave! It's an abomination!"

Upon hearing this Gwen couldn't contain her laughter. "I find it quite fitting for you!"

I sighed apologetically. "Sorry, Rinn. We don't know who did this."

He rolled his eyes in disbelief. "Unbelievable... A slave who doesn't even get to know their master… you're all useless.”

I walked over to Rinn with an awkward smile “Well I might not be so bad, right?”

Rinn growled “Just shut-”

He flung his hand to slap me and I flinched, dropping the box, but after not feeling the impact I glanced at him only to notice a glowing chain around his arm tightened keeping him from making contact with me.

Rinn’s face then dropped “No… you can't be serious.”

CHAPTER 17                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    Away from Council Eyes

Gwen burst into laughter—loud and wild—as she strolled over to Rinn’s crumpled form. Without a hint of warning, she scooped him up and tossed him in my direction like a rag doll.

“Looks like Bushy here is your master!” she cackled, nearly doubling over. “Oh, this is hilarious!”

Rinn scrambled upright, his movements stiff and full of disbelief. “Impossible!” he barked. “This creature has no idea how to claim a slave! And I highly doubt he would ever have the courage to do so!”

I took a step back, my heart starting to pound. “Wait, hold on! I don’t want to own anyone! This has to be a misunderstanding!”

Gwen sighed, grinning. “Listen, Bushy, whether you like it or not, you now own him. And besides, it’s just seven years of his life.” She let out another chuckle like it was no big deal.

Rinn pushed himself fully to his feet, strands of his silvery hair falling over his face. His eyes dropped to the faint glow of the chains around his wrists… and I saw it—the shimmer beginning to vanish, fading into nothing like smoke in the air.

My stomach sank. So it was real.

He looked at me then. Not startled. Not afraid. Just quiet. Watching. The tension in his jaw eased, and slowly, he reached up to smooth his hair back into place. Then… he smiled.

It wasn’t a friendly smile. There was something smug in it—like he’d figured something out that the rest of us hadn’t.

I turned to Gwen, lowering my voice. “This really sucks... There has to be a way to break this.”

She rolled her eyes like I’d asked the dumbest question in the world. “Like I said, no. Just give him to Bluma once we’re out, and she can handle him if you don’t want to deal with him.”

That’s when I noticed him moving again—walking slowly toward us with the kind of calm that made my skin crawl.

“Well, congratulations,” Rinn said, voice light but sharp. “It seems I am unable to cause you any harm, young creature…” He gave a low chuckle. “But don’t think for a second that this grants you dominion over me.”

I tensed as he advanced on me. Just before he could get too close, Gwen stepped between us, her hand raised as a warning. “Listen here, you better not play any of your cruel mind games on him, or else…”

Before she could finish her threat, Rinn moved with frightening speed. His hand struck the side of her neck, hitting a nerve, and Gwen’s body went slack, her eyes rolling back as she collapsed to the ground, unconscious.

“Piece of trash,” Rinn muttered with a dark chuckle.

Bluma and Beans reacted instantly, weapons ready, expressions full of fury. “Why, you—!” Beans growled, gripping his axe tightly, but I raised my hand, signaling him to stop.

“Leave him be, Beans…”

Beans looked at me like I’d lost my mind. “Are you crazy? He attacked one of us!” He gripped his axe tighter, his knuckles white, but I didn’t waver. I moved toward Rinn instead.

Rinn chuckled at my approach, but before he could say another word, I grabbed him by the throat, lifting him off the ground effortlessly. His eyes widened in surprise.

“Do you not remember what I told you, Rinn…” I growled.

As he gasped for air, I spoke low, my voice laced with a threat. “If you say or do one more thing to Gwen, I will make you pay.”

Rinn struggled in my grip, but I could see the panic in his eyes as shackles appeared on his wrists, draining his strength.

“Deta!” Bluma shouted in shock.

Beans echoed, confusion and disbelief in his voice. “Deta! What are you doing!”

The voices of my friends felt muffled, distant—like they were calling to me from underwater. A cold, dark voice slithered into my ear, its tone insistent. “He broke her once... he'll do worse next time…”

I tossed Rinn to the ground, his chest heaving as he gasped for air. He struggled to stand, his strength returning slowly.

“Get up, Rinn...” I glared at him, my voice dripping with malice. “You said I was no Randeth... Why don’t we prove what I am?”

Rinn stood, coughing, a twisted grin spreading across his face. “A spare...? Very well.” He adjusted his posture, his voice chilling as he continued. “If you win, I will do as you say... No questions asked. But if I win, we trade… you become my slave.”

Beans’ eyes widened in disbelief. “Deta, don’t! He isn’t worth it!”

Bluma, realizing her words were failing to reach me, drew her sword and advanced toward us.

The voice inside my head came again, its tone darker now. “They will get in the way. Make them stay still. It's for their own good... for their safety.”

Without thinking, my hand shot up, and vines began to wrap around Gwen, Bluma, and Beans, pinning them in place.

“Deta, stop! What’s gotten into you?” Beans cried out as he struggled against the vines, but they held firm, his efforts futile.

"You’re not hurting them. You’re protecting them—from him."

Rinn’s smile twisted, darker than before. “Do we have a deal?” His voice was low, almost a hiss.

I responded, my voice cold. “Deal.” The word tasted wrong on my tongue, like a curse whispered from the deepest corners of the world.

A low, eerie chuckle echoed—one from Rinn, the other from somewhere much darker—as we took sixteen paces away from each other, the tension thick in the air.

Rinn’s gaze flicked to a human skeleton lying forgotten in the dirt. He reached for it, curling his fingers around the ribcage and arm bone, lifting the makeshift weapon with a grin that sent a chill down my spine. “This will do nicely,” he muttered.

We turned to face each other. My body was coiled, every fiber prepared for the clash to come.

“Now. Before he strikes again. Run him through... the voice ordered, cold and unrelenting. It was no longer my will. My body moved on its own, my heart pounding with a brutal purpose: to end him.

Rinn chuckled darkly, his fingers flicking over the ribcage like a twisted musician. The eerie sound of bone striking bone filled the air, sharp and haunting. A strange, hollow tune—broken and frantic—echoed around us. It was as if the very bones protested against the music.

“Straightforward, young creature,” Rinn taunted, his hands moving with precision. A sharp, piercing high note rang out, and a shockwave of energy slammed into me, knocking me back, rattling my body.

A second wave struck like a cannon blast, lifting me off the ground and hurling me through the air. The world spun, sound warping, but I twisted mid-flight and crashed down—hard—on all fours. My hooves struck the earth with a thunderous crack. Fury surged through me, molten and pure, washing away everything else.

Then I felt it—deep in my core, something ancient answering the call. My limbs rippled and split. Minerals surged to the surface of my skin with a sound like breaking geodes, shards of stone snapping into place as my shape twisted and reformed. Moss erupted across my back like wildfire, wrapping me in its verdant grasp. Iron ore gleamed along my antlers, branching wide like living blades.

His music fell silent.

A hush dropped over the battlefield, heavy and reverent, as if the land itself was holding its breath.

Beans and Bluma stared, wide-eyed, unable to hide their disbelief.

“You’re actually a... a Randeth…” Rinn’s voice faltered, his composure slipping for a moment as the reality of my transformation hit him.

I charged forward, my hooves pounding against the earth, sending tremors through the ground. Rinn’s eyes went wide in panic. He threw his hands over the bones, desperate to play faster. The hollow sound became a frantic blur, each note growing more erratic.

When he struck the high note again, the shockwave had no effect on me. I barreled forward, unstoppable.

Rinn leaped to the side, narrowly avoiding my antlers. But he wasn’t finished. He struck three low notes, sending glowing blue projectiles hurtling toward me. They hit with a thunderous crash, sending me stumbling back, rocks and moss flying from my elk form.

Fury surged within me, and I readied myself to charge again. But then, two swords materialized in front of me—Gwen and Bluma, standing between us with their weapons raised.

“Get them out of the way. Kill them. Now!” The voice screamed in my mind.

I stomped my hooves, signaling for them to move, but Gwen and Bluma stood firm, their eyes unyielding.

Bluma spoke first, her voice calm but commanding. “Stop.”

Gwen didn’t budge. Her sword was held steady, her eyes fierce. “Bushy, quit it already! Killing him is my job!”

The voice in my mind howled, louder than ever. “Kill the girl!”

A searing jolt tore through my ear, sharp and sudden, like a hook being yanked from inside my skull. It wasn’t pain I knew; it was worse. Foreign. Crawling. Wrong. The haze cracked. I staggered, reeling, and shook my head in panic. The sensation only grew—twisting deeper, thrashing like something alive.

Then, with a sickening Thwip, a small, white worm-like creature fell from my ear, landing at Bluma’s feet with a soft plop.

Before I could react, Bluma crushed it beneath her foot with a swift, decisive motion. The parasite’s existence was extinguished in an instant.

The battlefield fell silent. The voice inside my head, once so commanding, was now eerily quiet.

I slowly transformed back into my normal form, staring at Gwen, Bluma, and a terrified Rinn. Beans, still caught in the vines, watched in concern.

"Bushy...?" Gwen took a step towards me, but I sharply turned around and took a step back.

"I... I didn't mean to..." I whispered, then turned and ran away. Gwen chased after me, trying to catch up, but we soon found ourselves in a closed area with no clear escape route. Grabbing the box with the soul stone as I did so.

Suddenly, the walls began closing in, and a hole with a bright light appeared on the other side of the room where I was headed. Gwen sprinted towards me, while Bluma rescued Rinn and freed Beans from the vines. "Bushy! Stop!" Gwen called out, running faster to catch up.

I kept running, consumed by fear and panic, now knowing what I was capable of. I was going to kill him! I'm being consumed by the fire! Vomete, help me! I thought to myself, my mind filled with despair.

As I approached the opening in the abdominal wall, a bright light radiated from the other side. It seemed like a way to escape and keep them safe from my destructive potential. I ran towards it, driven by the desperate need to protect them from myself. Gwen, determined to prevent me from fleeing, called out, "Leaf head! Mivomafisockmas!"

I hesitated, slowing my pace. Miv- Why would... She can't possibly be telling me I'm okay. There is no way, she must be lying! I battled with conflicting thoughts holding tightly to the box.

Gwen groaned, desperately trying to catch up. "Don't you dare try to get away, you Bush!" I saw that the hole had widened enough for me to jump through. With all the strength I could muster, I increased my speed, putting distance between us, and leaped through the opening. As I emerged on the other side, a blinding white light enveloped my vision, and everything turned white.

Once the light faded and I could see, I saw beneath me trees and grass, but that was beneath me as I realized I was now falling off the side of the giant purple worm.

With little time to react, I curled into a fetal position, bracing myself for a hard impact. However, instead of crashing into the ground, I landed on something soft and squishy. Confused, I looked around and saw that I had fallen onto a gray liquid resembling a wet rock. As I tried to stand up, the liquid started to move, causing me to slip and tumble face-first onto it.

Realizing I had landed on a creature, I quickly apologized, hoping it would understand. However, it didn't respond and slowly made its way out from under me, disappearing into the bushes. I apologized once more, and then looked up at the exposed spot on the forest's canopy. "Well... at least I'm out now," I murmured to myself.

I walked out of the woods and saw the giant purple worm's body sinking back into the ground. Looking up at the tip of its end, I spotted the hole I had jumped through and noticed Gwen and the others emerging as well. It seemed Gwen had seen me at the same time, as her first words upon landing were spoken with anger in a language I couldn't understand.

Gwen's eyes locked onto me, and in the next heartbeat, she was sprinting toward me with laser-focused determination. Panic surged through me as I tried to flee, but my limbs were too slow. With a surge of force, she leaped, grabbing hold of me, and we both crashed to the ground in a tangled heap. The soul stone slipped from my fingers and rolled away.

"Don’t you dare run!" she snapped, her voice fierce as she straddled my torso and pinned my arms to the ground. "Why in the blazes did you start running off, huh?"

Struggling beneath her weight, I gasped for breath, trying to find words. "I didn’t—!"

But before I could explain, she cut me off, her frustration boiling over. "You didn’t what!? Did you think I was going to kill you!?"

The force of her words hit me like a slap. I froze, stunned by the accusation.

"No! Not at all, I just—" I stammered, but her anger cut me off again.

"Just what!?" she demanded, her voice sharp, rising in both frustration and concern.

I clenched my jaw, trying to steady myself. The words were clawing at my throat. Before I could stop myself, I shouted, "I didn’t want to kill you!" It was the first time I had ever raised my voice, and the shock of it seemed to catch her off guard, leaving me a fleeting moment to gather my thoughts.

"I was angry!" I continued, the words tumbling out like a dam breaking. "I couldn’t think straight, and I just wanted to hurt him! And then when you stepped in front of me, I heard these voices, telling me to hurt you, to kill you! Do you think I wanted that?!"

My chest heaved, each breath ragged, waiting for her to respond, but she was silent, her eyes searching mine, conflicted.

"I don’t hurt things," I whispered, voice trembling. "I’m a coward—I’m afraid... I just wanted to be left alone in the woods, to live peacefully. I only want to keep the people I care about safe. But if I hurt one of you... I could never forgive myself."

The silence hung between us, thick and heavy, before she slowly released my arms and pushed herself off me. She stepped back, her expression unreadable.

Bluma, Beans, and Rinn approached, their footsteps soft on the ground, but I barely noticed them. Gwen didn’t look back at me as she moved, refusing to let me view her face.

"Deta! Why did you run off!? Are you alright?" Beans asked, concerned, while Bluma and Rinn slowed down.

Once they stopped Rinn stood back with his arms crossed, leaning against a tree, while Bluma and Beans helped me up and checked if I was alright. Gwen, on the other hand, began to walk into some bushes. Beans turned and saw her walking off, "Gwen? Where are you going?"

Gwen stopped and without turning responded, "I'm going to clear my head."

Rinn smiled, "Good luck..." Gwen growled at his snarky remark but simply turned away and disappeared into the brush.

Gwen’s View

After trudging through the forest for what felt like forever, I finally stumbled upon a lazy little stream. The kind of place you'd find in a painting or something. Birds flitted down from the trees, splashing around like it was bath time, while fish darted under the water, living their carefree lives. A big rock jutted halfway into the stream, and it looked like as good a spot as any to sit and stew.

I climbed onto it, letting out a deep sigh that felt like it should’ve shaken the trees around me. My gaze wandered to the sky, all bright and clear, but my mind wasn’t anywhere close to peaceful. Deta’s stupid retort kept bouncing around in my head like an annoying fly. Deta… I grabbed a handful of pebbles and chucked them into the water, watching the ripples erase the reflection of my scowl.

“Why would he even... Why does he care?” My voice sounded small, even to me. The reflection staring back wasn’t much better—just a filthy, bloodstained, mud-caked mess. Dried stomach juice? Yeah, that too. I’d stopped counting how many days we were trapped. Three? Four? Too long.

The clouds above didn’t care, floating all carefree and fluffy. I flopped back on the rock, trying to let the sky take my thoughts, but peace never lasted long these days. A crack—the sharp snap of wood—echoed through the trees.

I bolted upright, every nerve on high alert. More snapping followed, closer this time, and I slid off the boulder, sword at the ready. My boots splashed quietly through the stream as I crept toward the noise.

Something floated in the water—burnt wood, still smoldering. My stomach clenched.

Then I saw it. A house. No... several houses, or what was left of them, scattered like toys dropped by some careless giant.

I stepped out of the stream, scanning the wreckage. My foot landed on a branch, and the crack it made seemed louder than thunder. I froze, heart hammering, as rustling came from one of the houses.

“Who’s out there?” A sharp, gruff voice cut through the silence.

Before I could think of an answer, a goblin stomped out, a rusted sword in hand. He squinted at the woods like he owned them. My hand went to my sword hilt, ready to strike, when another voice—a small, piping one—made him pause.

“What’s wrong, Daddy?”

A little goblin girl peeked out from the doorway. The sight made my chest tighten, though I wasn’t sure why.

“Nothing, sweet pea. Go back inside with your mother.”

She obeyed, casting a quick glance over her shoulder before disappearing. The goblin man muttered something about adventurers and loot as he shuffled toward the stream. He didn’t even notice me until he turned around—and found my blade inches from his throat.

I crouched to his level, finger pressed to my lips. “Shh. I won’t kill you. Your little girl needs a father.”

His whole body shook, sweat glistening on his green skin. “W-What do you want?” His voice cracked like dry wood, heavy with fear.

I pressed the blade just enough to remind him who had the upper hand. “You’re clever. Take a wild guess.”

Deta’s View

An awkward silence hung over everyone after what had just happened inside the worm, and hearing what went through my head.

Beans was the first to break the silence. “So... what are you going to do once we all get back to the kingdom?”

Bluma didn’t answer, just sat there still as stone, eyes locked on Rinn but listening closely.

I let out a breath and rubbed the back of my neck. “Well… I’m not really sure. I got what I came out for, so… probably head home?”

Rinn tilted his head, that usual edge in his voice creeping back in. “Unsure? What does that mean?”

I looked over at Rinn and replied, "Well, I don't know. I have a lot to think about right now." Rinn sighed, looking displeased with the answer, but said nothing further.

I then saw the Soul Stone lying on the ground under a bush near Rinn’s feet, I panicked realizing I dropped it and bent down and quickly grabbed it before Rinn could see what it was.

I then turned to Beans and asked, "What about you and Bluma? Are you both going back and getting married or something?" Beans choked on air, and Bluma went more red as she turned away and put her hand to her forehead. Rinn burst into laughter as the two fell silent.

"W-well, you see, Deta. We couldn't even if we wanted to. If," Beans explained.

I tilted my head and asked, "What do you mean?"

Beans sighed and continued, "You see, as a squire, I can't pursue Bluma in public. She is my boss, and if we were to see each other in that sense, we would both lose everything."

I was taken aback and commented, "Lose everything? That seems extreme, don't you think?"

Beans sighed and replied, "If I were a knight, that would be fine, but if we are caught together, then Bluma would lose her Knight ranking and be banished back to her home, and I would be banished from the land. We would never see each other again. Plus, she is the Queen's knight... and she isn't the friendliest of people."

I chuckled and said, "Yeah, I could tell... but I understand." I didn't fully understand, but I didn't want to push too far.

Rinn sighed and whispered to himself, "Adventures four... coming to a close." He then got onto the ground to sit, and something rustled in the nearby bushes. We all looked, expecting Gwen, only to see a small goblin emerge.

Beans and Bluma drew out their weapons and readied for a fight. The goblin put up his hands and whimpered out “Wait! Please, do you know a girl named Gwen?”

Hearing her name, I spoke up. "Yeah, we know her. Is something wrong?"

The goblin smiled and replied, "She told me to tell you to: “move your butts and follow me.” He then turned around and walked back into the shrubbery.

I was about to follow when Beans stopped me.  "Deta, it's a goblin. They are always up to something." I looked at Beans, then at the brush, and then back.

"Then we'll be careful. But we can't afford to lose someone now, after we've made it this far."

Beans sighed and glanced at Bluma, who nodded in agreement. Then four of us followed the small goblin to the stream. I asked, "So, how do you know Gwen?"

The goblin sarcastically responded, "Oh, we went to wizarding school together! What do you think? She put a sword to my neck!"

I sighed and said, "That sounds like her... sorry."

The goblin waved dismissively and groaned, "Ah, whatever. She offered to fix my house if I let you all stay for the night."

This surprised all of us. Gwen, helping someone like that? Was she sick? Was she suffering from some kind of brain dysfunction? We exchanged confused and concerned looks. I asked, "Are you sure it's our Gwen?" Before the goblin could respond, a voice called out from across the stream. We then saw Gwen, balancing a pile of wood on one shoulder and a little goblin girl on the other.

Gwen then noticed us and went to say something but then her smile faltered, and she resumed walking. "Hurry up, you four. It's almost dark." As we looked up we saw a growing night sky scattered with emerging stars. By the time we entered the goblin family's small home, we managed to find just enough floor space to settle down. After putting his daughter to sleep, the goblin father carefully stepped over the sleeping forms of Bluma, Beans, and Rinn before heading out the door.

I found myself sitting outside, leaning against the wall, lost in thought. The door creaked open, and the goblin father stepped out, noticing me. "It's late, Rocko. You should get some shut-eye," he said, his tone kind but firm.

I smiled at him. "Well, why aren't you in bed?"

He chuckled. "I'm on guard duty tonight. I'll get some sleep later, but you won't be staying here another night, so you'd better take advantage of the rest."

We both laughed softly. "Alright, alright, I'll head in soon," I said. He rolled his eyes playfully. "Sure you will," he teased before walking off into the shadows.

I stayed where I was, staring at the ground, my thoughts tangled. Suddenly, Gwen's voice broke the silence from above. I glanced up and saw her perched on the roof, peering down at me.

"Oh, hey, Gwen," I greeted with a faint smile as she hopped down, her armor clinking softly. She wasted no time. "Answer the question, Deta. Do you think you're a wimp?"

Her bluntness caught me off guard. I hesitated, then looked away. "Yeah, I'm scared. I know you think that's pathetic."

She plopped down in front of me, her tone laced with sarcasm. "Oh yeah, sure, because only a scaredy-cat runs into a cave to save his friend."

I blinked, surprised. "Hold on—"

She raised a hand to silence me. "I'm not finished. Only a scaredy-cat risks his life for three people he barely knows. Only a scaredy-cat saves a slave from her prison. Do you hear yourself?" Her voice rose slightly, careful not to wake the others but insistent all the same.

"You've done at least twenty things in the past few days that most people would run from. You've tried to keep us safe this whole trip... You were even ready to kill Rinn for hitting me!" Her words hit me hard, and I found myself staring at the ground as the truth sank in.

"You're right," I murmured.

She scoffed. "Of course I’m right! Bushy, you’re brave because you’re scared. Fear motivates you to do better, and you’ve kept doing that. Don’t you dare stop now. You hear me?"

I smiled faintly, meeting her eyes. "Thanks, Gwen." The leaves that made up my hair had closed for the night, revealing the network of vines underneath. She looked away, her face slightly flushed. "Tch, don’t look at me like that," she muttered.

"Like what?" I asked, confused.

"Doesn’t matter. Just get your butt to bed. I need some sleep." She yawned and stood, heading back inside.

"Geez, Gwen. So pushy," I chuckled as I stood up and glanced at the sky. The stars twinkled above as I whispered, "I don’t know why you saved me, but I hope I did something right." With a sigh, I followed her inside.

Queen’s View

The princess had fallen asleep in her father’s lap, her small frame rising and falling with each peaceful breath. My husband’s face softened as he looked down at her, and he spoke in a hushed tone, his love for her evident in every word. “Oh, my dear sweet flower... it seems you’ve exhausted yourself this evening.” He rose carefully, cradling her in his arms as though she were the most fragile thing in the world. Turning to me, his expression was warm and adoring, the kind of gaze he always gave me but one I no longer returned.

“My dear,” he said, his voice filled with affection, “I’m going to put our little girl to bed. I’ll join you in our chambers in a moment.”

I forced a soft smile, the one he expected from me. “Of course, my king. I’ll see you there.” My tone was sweet, bordering on syrupy. It was effortless to feign love for him; after all, he never noticed the sharp edges beneath my words. He leaned in, and I allowed the briefest kiss, keeping my expression tender.

As he carried our daughter out of the room, I let the smile fall away the moment his back was turned. My eyes drifted toward the staircase ahead of me. My steps were unhurried, and though the stone beneath my feet gleamed as it shifted to polished metal, mimicking the night sky, I felt no awe. It was all just a means to an end—a spectacle meant to impress, but not me. I had long since stopped being impressed by such things.

The gilded door at the top of the stairs came into view, its crystal handle catching the faint glow of the sconces lining the walls. I opened it with practiced calm, stepping into the chamber where seven figures waited. Their cloaks of light glimmered, their ethereal forms looming high above. They always tried to present themselves as beings of wisdom and power, but to me, they were nothing more than tools to be used.

They spoke amongst themselves as I entered, their voices overlapping in discussion. The eldest of them was the first to speak clearly, his tone laced with authority. “Brothers, the time draws near when the Lord shall return among us. And when he does, we shall surely fall.”

I lingered at the edge of the room, feigning patience as the others responded. Their talk of celestial orders and impending doom was predictable, the same song and dance they always performed. When the third spoke of surrendering to divine will, I grew tired of their chatter. Clearing my throat, I interrupted their sanctimonious musings.

“Am I interrupting something, gentlemen?” I asked, tilting my head with mock innocence.

The eldest raised a glowing hand in acknowledgment. “No worries, child. We, being in good spirits, have summoned you here to entrust you with a task.”

I let out a quiet sigh, rolling my eyes where they couldn’t see. “Well then, what is it you want this time?”

One of the younger six spoke, his voice trembling slightly as though he feared to offend. “The Lord has been spotted once again in your kingdom called Earth. We request that you eliminate him.”

That piqued my interest. I placed a hand on my hip, feigning curiosity. “Eliminate him? Interesting. Why must I kill this so-called Lord?”

The question provoked an immediate reaction. Their cloaks glowed red, and the eldest snapped, “He is no ordinary man! He will disrupt our celestial order and bring destruction upon all!”

I suppressed a smirk. The sight of their outrage always amused me. Another voice,The youngest of the seven, his voice soft yet resolute, spoke up from the edge of their circle. “Elder Brethren, it’s folly to speak ill of one who carries a pure heart. I beg ye, remember the oath we swore—to restore what was lost, once he earns forgiveness. He stands just and righteous.”

The eldest’s gaze cut through him like a blade, eyes cold as frozen stone. His lips curled in something close to disdain, and his voice, when it came, was dripping with condescension. “Oh, little brother...” His tone dripped with mockery, as though he were addressing a toddler. “We’ll not have our counsel disrupted by the prattling of a mere boy.” His voice grew louder, deeper, and the very walls seemed to shudder with his words. “You would dare lecture us on righteousness? I’d sooner listen to the wind’s gossip.”

With a snap of his fingers, the air around him seemed to tighten, and his next words boomed with the force of a storm. “Enough!” The sheer power of his voice sent me crashing backward, my body slamming into the door. My skull met the hard wood with a sickening thud, and I tasted the bitter sting of my own frustration, yet I could hardly find space for pain in the fury rising within me.

“Excuse me,” I said sharply, sitting upright. “Mind your temper. We are not all deities here.”

The eldest turned back to me, his tone tempered but still dripping with authority. “Ah yes, my apologies, child. We will not detain you longer than necessary.” A red orb materialized in his hands, descending slowly toward me.

“This is a beast of fire and brimstone. We entrust you with the power to bring your cause to reality and destroy our enemies,” he intoned.

I reached for the orb, only to hiss in pain as it burned my skin. Before I could speak, it shifted into a bracelet, its beads glinting with a sinister light and a rhombus-shaped crystal at its center. The sight of it intrigued me, though I kept my expression neutral.

“It shall be at your beck and call. Now, go,” the eldest commanded.

The room dissolved into white light, and when my vision returned, I was back in my chambers, seated on the bed. The bracelet glinted on my wrist, a tangible reminder of the power now within my grasp. A quiet laugh escaped me, cold and sharp. “Finally,” I murmured to myself. “Now, my goals are within close reach.”

The door opened, and my husband entered, his face lighting up as he saw me. “Sorry for the wait, my love,” he said, crossing the room with an easy smile.

I masked my disdain with a warm expression, watching as he changed into his nightclothes. “No worries, love. No worries at all,” I replied sweetly, lying back against the pillows.

As he joined me, the faint tremors that had plagued the castle for days returned. He sighed, his brow furrowing. “The shaking hasn’t ceased for four days now. I hope Deta and his comrades are surviving.”

Feigning concern, I placed a hand over his. “I’m sure they are safe. You mustn’t worry yourself over such things,” I said, my tone soft and reassuring.

“What if it were me down there? Or our daughter?” he pressed.

I paused for effect, then smiled gently. “They are safe. I’m certain of it.” I touched his cheek, letting my fingers linger. “Now... shall we enjoy the rest of our night without fretting over the kingdom?” My voice was light, playful, the perfect mask.

He chuckled, pulling me close, and I let him. He never saw the frost behind the warmth of my smile. He never would.

CHAPTER 18                                                                                                                                An old story                                                                                                         

The next day, we gathered our belongings and expressed our gratitude to the Goblin family for their hospitality.

"Thank you so much! Is there anything we can do for you before we leave?" I asked the Goblin father.

He let out a laugh that sounded like a woodpecker hammering away at a tree. "Don’t worry about it. And please, call me Nox. Now get out of our town before I change my mind!" he exclaimed with a grin.

Gwen rolled her eyes but kept a sly smile. "Yeah, yeah, whatever."

She turned to me, and I nodded in agreement. The sooner we leave, the sooner I can get back to Vomete.

Just as Gwen and I started walking, Beans chimed in, "So, Nox, do you know where the Sumring Palace is?"

Both Gwen and I halted abruptly, realizing we had no idea where we were. Rinn chuckled, clearly amused by our sudden stop, but his expression shifted when he looked and saw Nox's little girl who was grabbing his hair and playing with it. After a brief, awkward silence, he sighed and averted his gaze.

Nox cackled. "Sumring, huh? Planning on invading it?"

His comment startled both Beans and Bluma. Neither responded, so Nox continued, "It’s on the other side of the mountains."

"Mountains? What mountains?" I asked, confused. I didn’t recall seeing any the night before.

With a small chuckle, Gwen placed her hand on my head and turned it to face a massive mountain range beyond the forest. The peaks were dark gray, their jagged edges cutting into the pale morning sky. They loomed silently, blending so perfectly with the haze that it felt as though the sky itself had folded down to swallow them.

"Oh… those," I muttered.

Nox laughed at my delayed perception. "Yeah, those ones—Spearhead Heights."

Rinn’s demeanor shifted, and he stood up straight, surprised by Nox’s words. "You mean you’re sending us to the Shadowspine Tunnels?"

Beans groaned. "You’re kidding, right? Those are a death trap!"

I turned to Gwen. "What’s wrong with the caves?"

She groaned and sighed. "They’re like a maze. Dead ends, ruins, endless halls—there’s even a drop to the Underworld..."

The mention of the Underworld sent a shiver through me. I definitely didn’t want to go back there, but I needed to get home.

"Is there any other way, Nox?" I asked hopefully.

Nox shook his head. "Not unless you want to walk around, but good luck with that. If that range is the only thing keeping Mount Tarifa from invading, how much luck do you think you’ll have?"

Rinn nodded. "We’ll be fine. I’ve traveled through once before—"

Gwen cut him off with a sharp growl. "Like we’d trust you to lead? You’re just looking for a way out of your chains."

Rinn narrowed his eyes and raised his arm, the glowing green chain appearing briefly. "Unlike you were," he retorted. "I’m not delusional about my escape."

Gwen reached for her sword, but Nox interrupted with a yell. "Hey! Quiet down in front of my house! I helped you—now get out!"

Snarling one last time, Gwen let go of her sword and stomped off. "Let’s go, Leaf-head." She grabbed my collar and yanked me forward.

"I’m coming! You don’t have to pull so hard!" I protested, trying not to trip over my feet.

Rinn groaned as the green chain tugged him forward, forcing him to follow. It faded again as Beans and Bluma led the way into the woods toward Spearhead Heights. I turned to see Rinn trailing behind, his hands stuffed in his pockets. Then I looked at Gwen, walking beside me. She avoided both my gaze and Rinn’s, her hair bouncing with each step, catching patches of sunlight.

“So, Gwen… about last night—” I began, but she cut me off sharply.

“Don’t mention it. Really, don’t,” she said, giving me a sidelong glance. Her deep blue eyes seemed to gleam in the fleeting sunlight. “And stop looking at me like that. You’re weirding me out.”

I blinked, confused. “Looking at you like what?” I tilted my head slightly, which only seemed to annoy her more.

“I said, stop it, pebble-face.” She shoved her hand against my face and pushed me back. I landed on my butt, a surprised grunt escaping me. When I got up, I caught a glimpse of her trying—and failing—to hide a smirk as she walked ahead.

Rinn stopped beside me, his long white hair catching the light as he looked down. “So smooth, young one. A truly masterful performance,” he said, his sarcasm almost tangible.

I brushed myself off and smiled. “What performance? I was just trying to thank her.” I glanced ahead at Gwen, now walking beside Beans and Bluma.

Rinn chuckled, a deep, amused sound. “Uh-huh. Let’s go. I don’t want us left behind out here.” He gave me a soft pat on the back and walked ahead. The gentleness caught me off guard, but I couldn’t help smiling. Maybe he could change.

As we continued, the trees around us thinned, their branches brittle and leaves sparse. Their sickly forms groaned, the sound haunting and low, as though the mountains themselves were draining them of life. I wrapped my arms around myself, moving closer to Gwen. My shoulder accidentally bumped hers.

“Sorry,” I murmured, though my thoughts lingered on the unnatural state of the forest.

She turned sharply, ready to snap at me, but paused when she noticed my unease. Instead, she looked toward the others. “Let’s just get through this place. I’ve got a bad feeling.”

Beans nodded. “Good idea. I’ve had enough caves for one lifetime.” He chuckled briefly, though his expression quickly turned serious.

I scanned everyone’s faces. The same worry etched onto mine was mirrored in theirs. At the entrance to the cave, we all hesitated, none of us willing to take the first step.

Rinn broke the silence, sighing. “Come on, everyone. We’ll be fine.”

Beans rolled his eyes. “No way. You’re in the back.” He marched ahead, Bluma following close behind with a nod.

Rinn shrugged but didn’t get far before Gwen shoved him against the cave wall.

“Sorry about that,” I said, offering him a hand. He took it, brushing himself off.

“Let’s get going, shall we?” he said dryly, his usual tone returning.

Inside, the air grew heavy, laden with the smell of damp earth. The walls hummed faintly, and an uneasy energy seemed to pulse through the tunnel. Shadows stretched unnaturally, and I couldn’t shake the feeling of unseen eyes watching us.

Gwen’s movements, typically steady, were careful now. Her hand rested on her sword, her eyes darting to every shadow. Her unease mirrored mine, though neither of us spoke it aloud.

Behind us, Rinn’s footsteps were quieter than usual. His glowing green chain had dimmed, and something about him seemed… off. When I glanced back, he met my gaze with a brief nod, though it did little to reassure me.

“Don’t look too hard,” Gwen murmured, her voice barely audible. “Even he’s probably uncomfortable here.”

“Yeah, well… I’m not exactly a fan of tight spaces,” I admitted, trying to lighten the mood. My words, though, felt hollow against the oppressive silence.

Ahead, Beans led the way, his posture unchanged as he moved through the darkness with ease. There was no light here—only the faint sense of shifting shapes that my eyes could barely make out in the murk. But Beans didn’t seem bothered, like he’d walked through tunnels like these a thousand times before. His usual confidence was tempered with something else now, a sharpness in his movements that suggested he wasn’t entirely sure what lay ahead.

Bluma, ever the quiet one, kept close behind him. Her eyes scanned the walls, the ground, the shadows, her expression unreadable. She’d said little since we entered the tunnel, but I could feel the weight of her concern in the way she moved.

We walked in silence, the echoes of our footsteps growing louder, stretching out into the vastness of the cavern. The deeper we went, the darker it got. The walls began to narrow, forcing us to move single-file, and the air grew colder, heavier. I couldn’t tell if it was the mountain’s chill or something more unnatural creeping in, but the hairs on the back of my neck seemed to stand up.

Then we heard a soft scraping sound, like something dragging across stone. At first, I thought it was just my imagination, but then the others stopped, and I saw the tension in their faces.

 “Did anyone else hear that?” Rinn’s voice was a low murmur, barely audible over the hum of the cave.

I swallowed hard, trying to focus, but the sound came again. Closer this time.

“Yeah,” Gwen said, her voice flat, but her hand was already on the hilt of her sword. “And I don’t like it.”

The sound stopped, but the silence that followed felt even worse. It was thick, suffocating, pressing in on us from all sides.

“We need to keep moving,” Beans said, his voice sharp, though his eyes darted nervously around the tunnel. He didn’t wait for an answer, pushing forward with a grim determination.

As I followed, my steps echoing in the dark, I couldn’t shake the feeling that the walls were closing in on us, that the tunnel was alive and breathing. The humming had grown louder, almost deafening, and now it seemed to resonate in my chest.

Gwen kept close to my side, her hand brushing mine as we moved, her usual sharpness replaced by a quiet vigilance. I could feel her tension, her readiness for whatever might be ahead, but I could see it in her eyes too—the same fear I had.

And then, ahead, the tunnel opened up, and the walls widened into a cavern so vast it swallowed what little light we had. The ground was uneven, slick with moisture, and the air was thick with the scent of decay. I could hear the distant sound of dripping water, the only other noise in the oppressive silence.

Beans stopped in front of me, his face pale as he stared into the darkness. “This... this doesn’t look right,” he muttered, his usual bravado gone.

“Don’t panic,” I said, trying to sound braver than I felt. “We’ll get through this.”

“Deta…” Bluma said softly, and as I turned to see her approach me with caution, my eyes darted around, panicked that something was going to attack me, but I froze.

“What…? Is it a snail?” I then saw Bluma pointing to my bag. Beans and the others then looked, and I saw their eyes widen.

“Deta... what's in your bag?” Beans asked, and as I looked at it, I saw the amber glow coming from inside.

“It’s... the Soul Stone...” I muttered as I took it out of my bag. It was glowing brightly, illuminating the cavern we were in. As its light shone, we saw murals carved into the walls. I saw pictures depicting what looked like a kingdom underground, with a huge monster looming over it, and what looked like ice growing from its hands and onto the kingdom.
        “How peculiar...” Rinn spoke in a soft voice, looking around. “These seem to be depictions of the Frost Era.”

I then turned to Rinn. “I keep hearing about that. What was the Frost Era?” Everyone but Gwen turned to me almost at once.

“Seriously, Deta? You've never heard of it?” Beans said in disbelief. “It’s like, a key moment in history!”

I gave a soft titter and shrugged. “Sorry?”

Gwen groaned loudly. “Who cares? I don’t know it, either.”

Beans turned to her. “Seriously?”

I looked back at the picture of the monster. As I looked towards the bottom, I saw writing on the wall. “No way!” I smiled wide, recognizing the writing.

Rinn walked up to me and looked at the writing. “That’s some ancient language... I don’t think I’ve ever seen it before.”

My smile continued as I turned to him. “It’s written in Randeth! A Randeth was here before. I wonder if it was this girl?” I then turned to the Soul Stone and lifted it a bit higher.

“I’m sorry, you can read this and... Girl? You can tell?” Rinn bent over slightly to take a closer look, his arms behind his back.

I nodded. “Yes, girl, and yes, I can read this!” I gave the writing another look. “Looks like Vomete’s writing almost…” As I looked down to where the writing led, I saw another tunnel. “Seems I get a story and a way out. Over here, guys!” I called out to everyone, pointing towards the tunnel. Gwen and Beans were the first to head towards it, with Rinn following behind.
