I put the Soul Stone back into my bag and looked up to see Bluma still looking at the murals.

Bluma looked at me, then pointed at the words, to which I nodded. “Yes, I can read that. Would you like me to?” She nodded, and I smiled as I turned to the wall and began to read aloud.

Story of the Frost Era

In an age when frost choked the breath of the living and the sun was but a pale shadow, despair claimed the land. No gold could warm the hearth, no silver could fill an empty belly. A single drop of honey cost the wealth of kings, and yet, even kings were left to beg in the streets. The wilderness became a graveyard of the forsaken, their cries silenced by the endless snow.

It began with the Ogre, a being whose heart was colder than the winds that carried his wrath. He sought to craft a world without flaw, where only the strong survived. To achieve this twisted perfection, he cast the lands into an unending winter, a realm of cruelty where mortals were but fleeting imperfections in his frozen playground.

Beneath the ice, a kingdom of stone and shadow rose. The Ice Dwarves, masters of the deep, offered refuge to those who could pay their price. But their king’s heart mirrored the Ogre’s malice. He bartered warmth and safety for loyalty, demanding more than flesh and blood could bear. Those who failed him were cast into the depths, their screams swallowed by the dark. When they returned, if they returned, they were changed—skin darkened, eyes hollow, hearts resigned to their prison of stone. Thus, the underworld became their kingdom, a realm of reluctant complacency.

Even the dragons were not spared. A mighty beast, once a symbol of freedom and fire, was bound in chains to warm the Dwarves’ halls. Its roars became the bitter song of servitude, its flames dwindled to embers, feeding the greed of its captors.”

And yet, hope flickered like a lone candle in the storm. From the frost-bound land, a generation arose—the Coldborn. Their blood resisted the chill, their resolve unyielding. Trained by the cruel Dwarf king to be his hunters, they turned their weapons against him. Relics of forgotten power guided their hands as they ventured into the frozen wastes, seeking to end the Ogre’s reign.

Their first battle was a bitter failure. Against a being of godlike strength, they were but insects before a mountain. Wounded in body and spirit, they fled. Yet, when all seemed lost, a light pierced the heavens. From it descended a being of radiant power, whose words brought strength, wisdom, courage, and hope. Empowered by the divine, the Coldborn rose again, united in purpose.

The battle shook the earth and splintered the sky. Ice and fire clashed, and the Ogre’s laughter echoed until it was silenced. Did they slay the beast? Did they bind it to an abyss, its power sealed in the Tears of Winter? The truth is shrouded in time. But with the Ogre’s fall, the frost receded, and life returned to the land.

Yet not all wounds healed. The Ice Dwarves, architects of so much suffering, became the hunted. The wrath of those they betrayed followed them to the ends of the earth. Thus, the Frost Era ended, not with peace, but with blood and fire. Its scars remain, carved in stone and memory, for those who walk these halls to heed and remember-

Deta’s View

The writing ended, and the walls of the cave looked as though they had deteriorated. I walked next to Bluma in silence for a moment before she placed her hand on my shoulder.

"Okay..." she said softly.

I smiled and nodded. "Yeah... I'm fine." I glanced back one last time, watching the writing fade from view. That really does look like Vomete’s handwriting... I hope this doesn’t take much longer.

The ground began to shake beneath us.

“Earthquake!” Beans yelled as rocks started falling from the ceiling. “Everyone stick to the sides!”

We quickly pressed ourselves against the cave walls as cracks formed, and with a deafening rumble, the tunnel caved in ahead of and behind us.

“We’re trapped!” Rinn called out.

“Oh, you don’t say!” Gwen added sarcastically.

When the shaking stopped, Beans rushed to one side of the tunnel, pushing futilely against the pile of rocks. "Come on... Move!" He let out a frustrated huff. "They're stuck tight."

"Of course," Gwen growled. "Just great!" She leaned against the opposite wall. "Guess we'll just die in—"

The wall gave way beneath her, and she screamed as she tumbled down a hidden chute.

"Gwen!" I yelled, running to the edge of the hole, her screams fading as she slid farther away.

A few seconds later, her voice echoed back up to us. “Get your butts down here! There’s another way!”

I sighed in relief and stood. Beans grinned. “Glad you’re okay!” he shouted down. “We’re coming!”

No sooner had he spoken than he pushed Rinn, sending him headfirst down the chute. Rinn’s startled yells were followed by a loud thud. Beans laughed so hard he doubled over, then jumped in after him. Bluma followed with a faint smile. I chuckled and took the plunge as well. Sliding down, I picked up speed as the twisting tube whipped me around. Faster and faster I went until I shot out of the end, slamming face-first into the stone wall.

Gwen burst out laughing. "Alright, Bushy, nap time's over. Let's get moving."

Groaning, I stood and rubbed my head. Looking around, I realized this wasn’t just another part of the cave. Stone bricks lined the walls and floor.

“This doesn’t look like a normal cave,” I said, frowning.

Beans nodded, his eyes scanning the walls. "It almost looks like an old tunnel from the Kingdom. There used to be a whole network of them connecting to it, but most were filled in and sealed off over the years. Wonder why this one was left open."

His words hung in the air, making the silence of the ancient tunnel feel heavier.

CHAPTER 19                                                                                                                Resolving Concerns: New and Old

        We proceeded cautiously through the dark hall, our senses heightened and on edge. As I surveyed the surroundings, it became apparent that the walls, floor, and ceiling were made of solid stone, gradually transitioning into naturally shaped rocks.

"I wonder where we are..." I whispered, my voice barely louder than the rustle of our clothes brushing against the walls.

"We're all wondering that. Just stay prepared," Beans replied. But before I could finish my sentence, a violent shaking and rumbling interrupted us, throwing us off balance. We stumbled and fell into one another.

"Is everyone okay?" Beans called out, scrambling to his feet.

"I'm fine!" I reassured him, and Rinn echoed the same.

"Could it be an earthquake?" Gwen asked, brushing the dust from her clothes.

Beans nodded. "Seems like it..."

The ground trembled again, and this time we managed to brace ourselves against the wall to avoid falling. The intensity increased, making it harder to keep steady.

As I leaned against the wall for support, I noticed a crack forming. Before I could react, that section of the wall shattered, and I fell through.

"Deta!" Beans shouted in concern as I disappeared. A sudden burst of orange light illuminated the corridor.

Everyone rushed over to see what had happened, only to find that I had fallen just a few feet below. Chuckling, I greeted them, "Hi, guys."

Beans let out a laugh of relief, while Bluma sighed audibly. Gwen quickly jumped down and hauled me up, but not without smacking me hard on the head, which sent me back to the ground.

"Don't ever do that again!" she scolded.

I rubbed my head, looking up at her. "What was that for?"

She didn’t answer and simply walked away.

Bluma hopped down to help me to my feet. As Beans and Rinn joined us, Beans asked, "Are you alright, Deta?"

"I'm fine," I replied, though I was still baffled by Gwen's forceful reaction.

Rinn chuckled as he followed Gwen. "Well, apart from that, let's keep moving forward."

We pressed on down the corridor. The damp air caused water to drip from the ceiling, and the rising temperature made Bluma and Gwen’s hair puff up into frizz. Bluma took the lead, her sharp eyes scanning every detail of our surroundings.

The hallway branched into smaller rooms on either side. When we reached the farthest room, Beans peeked inside and suddenly shouted, "Hey, guys!" He emerged with a wide grin.

"I know where we are!" he exclaimed.

Gwen placed her hands on her hips and raised an eyebrow. "Oh, really? Where are we?"

Beans maintained his smile, but before he could answer, another earthquake shook the ground, accompanied by a deafening roar.

Gwen, Bluma, and I exchanged startled glances.

"Seriously?" I muttered.

Rinn raised an eyebrow. "What's gotten into all of you?"

"No time to explain! Just keep up!" Gwen shouted, her voice urgent.

We sprinted down the hallway, passing the branching rooms as fast as we could. As we descended deeper, the temperature grew more intense with every step. Eventually, we reached a vast cave entrance. Just as we were about to step inside, a blast of fire erupted from within.

"Don't tell me that's the dragon!?" RInn exclaimed his expression laced with concern.

"You bet your violin it is!" Gwen shot back with a smirk.

Bluma and Gwen drew their swords, their faces set with determination. Beans tightened his grip on his ax, and I held my staff, feeling its weight steady me.

Rinn, ever skeptical, grumbled, "This is such a bad idea!" Yet even he pulled out his violin, ready to play.

As we stepped into the cavern, chaos greeted us: a colossal Guardian serpent locked in a ferocious struggle with a massive red dragon. The ground was strewn with corpses and the skeletal remains of enormous snakes, their bones gleaming white against the dark stone. It was impossible to count how many had perished. The cavern bore the scars of battle, with sunlight piercing through gaping cracks in the walls.

Without hesitation, we rushed forward to join the fray. The Serpent spotted us and boomed a warning, its voice shaking the air. "Get away, mortals! You do not belong in this fight!"

Gwen’s grin widened, her sword glowing with fiery energy. "Not a chance, scales!" She struck the ground with her blade, and a pillar of fire erupted, racing toward the dragon. The flames struck its chest but barely added to the wounds inflicted by the Serpent.

With a roar, the dragon lashed out at the Serpent, sending it hurtling into one of the cavern’s yawning pits, its massive body vanishing into the depths of the Underworld.

The dragon’s deep laughter echoed through the space. "Foolish serpent... Now, for my next meal—then my escape!" It turned its massive head toward us, baring sharp teeth in a predatory grin. The wounds from its fight were severe: one leg was missing, and its single wing hung in tatters.

The dragon opened its mouth, and a bright yellow glow built within its throat. Flames surged toward us in a fiery torrent, but before they could reach, Rinn began to play his violin. The haunting melody redirected the flames, causing them to curl harmlessly around us.

"What was that?" Gwen exclaimed, her shock matching our own.

Rinn ended his song with a satisfied smile. "Told you. I’m better with my instrument."

The dragon growled, glaring at Rinn. "So, you brought a bard to this fight? How amusing." Its deep laughter rumbled as it lunged toward us.

Gwen and Bluma rushed to meet its charge, their swords blazing with energy. The dragon swiped at them with a claw, and though they blocked the attack, its strength sent them flying across the cavern.

The dragon spun with terrifying speed, its massive tail swinging through the air. Beans stepped forward and raised his arms to shield himself. Black dust seeped from his hands, disintegrating some of the dragon’s scales on impact. Even so, the blow sent him crashing into a jagged rock wall.

The dragon’s laughter rang out again. "This is the best you can do? Pitiful." It turned back to Gwen and Bluma, coiling its tail with deadly precision. "Time for dinner..."

Focused on them, it ignored Rinn and me, who had positioned ourselves beneath its towering frame.

"That staff better work now," I muttered, gripping it tightly.

Rinn nodded sharply and struck a high note on his violin. The sound rippled outward, slamming into the dragon’s leg and forcing it to stumble. We sprinted out from under it just as another jet of fire roared past, narrowly missing the others. The dragon crashed onto its side, its ruined wing crumpled beneath it.

The beast roared in pain, thrashing as it tried to rise. Its bloodshot eyes swept the cavern until they locked onto us.

"You... will pay for that," it snarled.

Drawing in a deep breath, the dragon released three enormous fireballs. One hurtled toward us, another toward Gwen and Bluma, and the third toward Beans.

We saw no way of surviving and instinctively raised our arms, shielding our faces as we braced for the worst. The fiery onslaught hurtled toward us, and the heat of impending doom pressed heavy on my thoughts. Images of Vomete, Bluma, Beans, and even Gwen flickered through my mind.

Rinn’s View

The fire struck with a deafening roar, shaking the earth beneath us and sending shockwaves through the cavern. Just before the explosion hit I saw Deta put himself in front of me and before I could process it the explosion hurled us backward, scattering us like leaves in a storm. The dragon staggered, nearly toppling into one of the cavern’s massive chasms. Yet, with a menacing laugh, it regained its footing.

When the smoke and debris finally cleared, the dragon peered at us with a smug expression, certain it had claimed victory. But its triumph quickly turned to confusion. Despite its devastating attack, we lay sprawled on the ground, covered in soot and ash, but after pushing the young creature's body off of me, I began to stand, my body scorched by burns so severe I could hardly move.

The dragon growled, its eyes gleaming with predatory hunger as it prepared to end us once and for all. But just as it lunged, a sharp strike pierced its remaining leg. The beast howled in pain, twisting to see the Guardian Serpent. Its emerald scales, flecked with black and crimson, glistened as it sank its fangs deep into the dragon’s flesh. The dragon roared and struck back, but the serpent coiled tighter, dragging its foe toward the edge of the chasm. With a final, violent pull, both titans tumbled into the abyss, their roars fading as they vanished into the Underworld.

As I heard their howls echo into the Underworld below. I wanted to fall onto my knees however distant voices broke the silence. Through cracks in the cavern walls, a people gathered, their murmurs rising in concern.

Someone must have recognized Bluma and Beans among the fallen and quickly called for the Knights.

“Seems there is no rest for me…” I tried to limp away before the knights arrived. However, my imprisonment held my arms tightly forcing me to a complete stop. I turned to the young creature to see his own burns, one of his arms was even crumbling apart. “Young one, let me leave. I do not wish to be caught by the guards when they arrive.”

Desperation clawed at me as I twisted around to look at him—the source of my imprisonment. His body was limp, his burns glowing faintly in the green light. One of his arms had begun to crumble, fragments of stone and wood falling away to reveal raw, pulsing moss beneath. The sight made bile rise in my throat, but I forced it down.

“Dang it,” I growled, gripping the chains with both hands. “Wake up! I need you to let me go!”

The faint hum of the chains seemed to mock me. I yanked harder, my vision blurring with the effort and then—just as I feared—the unmistakable clamor of Knights being summoned.

“No, no, no!” I hissed, my movements becoming frantic. The chains glowed brighter as I fought them, their magic digging into my skin like fiery tendrils. I turned back to the creature, my breath heaving.

“Young one,” I rasped, desperation dripping from my words. “I do not wish to be caught by the guards when they arrive. Let me leave!” My voice cracked, and I reached out to shake his shoulder, though I knew it was futile. His hollow, unconscious form gave no response.

My eyes darted back to the glowing bonds. I could feel them in my mind, alive and pulsing, bound not to me, but to him. They wouldn’t let me leave—not until he allowed it.

“Please,” I whispered, the word tasting foreign on my tongue. “Wake up. Let me hide!”

Then, the chains flickered. For a moment, I thought I’d imagined it, but the steady glow wavered again, like the last moments of a candle’s flame. My breath caught as the green light faltered, the hum of magic growing softer.

The chains shimmered, their edges breaking apart like wisps of smoke. Slowly, gently, the bonds faded into the air, leaving a faint, earthy scent behind. My arms fell limply to my sides, and I stared at the empty space where the chains had been.

It was as though they’d never existed.

I froze, disbelieving, before the distant clang of armor shattered my trance. Scrambling to my feet, I ran, ignoring the sharp protests of my battered body.

 Healers arrived shortly after, tending to their injuries and carefully carrying them out of the cavern. Word of the battle spread quickly, reaching the King and even the farmers.

In the weeks that followed, they began to wake, one by one. Bluma and Beans were the first, recovering with surprising speed and resuming their duties. The King expressed his gratitude, relieved his daughter could grow up without the looming shadow of monsters. Beans’ parents wept with joy upon hearing of their son’s bravery.

 Gwen regained consciousness a few days later, though she remained too weak to return to the field. I watched them all from the shadows, stealing food and water, but staying near the young creature.

Deta’s View

When I finally opened my eyes, I found myself in a spacious room. The walls, made of finely cut stone, were adorned with green and gold silk curtains. I was on a bed, it was warm, and I was  wrapped in a blanket smoother than anything I had ever touched.

The door creaked open, and two men entered. One wore a golden laced cloak, his sharp eyes widening in surprise as he saw me awake. The other, clad in black, wore a peculiar beaked mask that obscured his face.

"You’re awake! How is this possible?" the man in the cloak exclaimed, stepping closer.

I smiled weakly, my voice barely above a whisper. "Hello... Who are you?"

The man straightened and replied, "I am Council Member Baker" After whispering a few words to his masked companion, he turned back and left. "There’s much to explain. Do you feel well enough to talk?"

I nodded, though unease began to stir within me.

Baker hesitated, then began, "After the battle, you were believed to be dead. You were unconscious for over a month, and your… appearance led many to assume you were gone for good."

His words were strange, but I listened as he continued.

"It was the Demon Knight who insisted we retrieve you. Many thought you were just rubble—stone debris from the cavern."

I let out a faint laugh, though the idea unsettled me. "I suppose I should be grateful for her persistence," I said, attempting to lighten the mood.

Baker didn’t smile. "During your coma, your condition began to change. Your outer layer—what seemed to be stone—started to crack and fall away. It wasn’t until recently that we realized…"

His voice trailed off, but I didn’t need him to finish. I raised my arms, the blanket slipping from my shoulders. My breath caught in my throat. My left arm remained as it had always been, but my right hand… It was–Flesh.

I stared in disbelief, flexing the fingers of my right hand. The movement felt alien, as if it didn’t belong to me. I pinched the skin lightly, and pain shot through it—a confirmation of its reality.

"What… What’s happening to me?" I whispered, my voice trembling.

Baker placed a hand on my shoulder, his expression grave. "That’s what we need to find out." He then handed me a pair of gloves, which I slowly put on.

His voice was calm, but there was a tremor in his grip—like he was bracing for something even he couldn’t predict.

He instructed me to stand and perform basic functions. His eyes widened in surprise as I moved, his gaze lingering a moment too long, as if he couldn’t quite comprehend how I was managing after such an extended period of unconsciousness. But I couldn’t focus on his astonishment, not when my mind was preoccupied with a single pressing question: What happened to my hand?

We walked toward the door, he muttering assessments, while I kept my focus solely on the mystery of my hand—why it felt wrong, cold, as if it didn’t belong to me.

Suddenly, a loud clatter of armor sounded in the hallway, and a group of knights ran past, swords drawn, their faces grim and determined.

“What's going on?” I asked, stepping toward the door. My muscles burned from disuse, but I still felt the urge to move, to do something.

Before Baker could answer, the ground trembled beneath us, followed by a thunderous explosion. My heart leapt into my throat, and he reacted instantly, pulling me back into the room, slamming the door shut, and locking it with swift, practiced movements.

He leaned against the door, his breathing shallow. "We must hide," he whispered urgently, his face pale. "We are under attack."

The words hung in the air, heavy and suffocating. I didn’t move. My instincts flared. Hide?

I glanced toward the door, a torrent of emotion flooding through me—confusion and frustration.

“We should help,” I insisted, ignoring the cold dread that clung to his every movement.

He tried to speak, his voice trembling, but I was already moving, my body locked in the rhythm of urgency. I unlocked the door and swung it open, feeling the cool air rush past me, a stark contrast to the heat of my pulse.

Ignoring Baker’s protests, I sprinted down the hall, my footsteps muffled by the chaos echoing from farther ahead.

I rushed through the castle, darting from room to room and hallway to hallway, uncertain of the right direction. The surroundings blurred together in my frantic search, making it difficult to navigate. Suddenly, another explosion resounded from above, prompting me to change course. I recalled seeing stairs earlier but remembered I had closed the door leading to them. Reaching the end of the hall, I opened a door, hoping it would lead to the stairs. Instead, I found myself in yet another dead end.

Frustrated but undeterred, I hesitated at the next door, drawn to the faint purple glow emanating from within. To my surprise, I found my staff lying in the middle of a weapon storage closet, alongside the rest of my belongings. Hastily, I collected them and resumed my search for the stairs. After several more minutes of searching, I finally located them and ascended, urgency driving every step.

At the top of the stairs, I emerged into a new hallway and immediately spotted a large, broken-down door. I bolted toward it, just in time to see Gwen being thrown out. Relief flooded me as I called out, "Gwen!"

She winced, clearly in pain, but her eyes widened in astonishment. "Bushy! You're alive?" she rasped. She attempted to stand but collapsed back down, her injury too severe.

Alarmed, I rushed to her side. "Gwen, don’t get up! Let me heal you. What in the world is happening?"

Her leg bore a deep wound, cutting down to the bone, and blood poured from it in a steady stream. It was a life-threatening injury. "The Queen went on a rampage," she gasped, wincing as her muscles twitched involuntarily. "Beans is chained to a wall, and Bluma... Bluma is under some kind of mind control."

Fear gripped me at her words. "What?!" I exclaimed, the weight of the situation crashing down on me. In my panic, I accidentally pressed too hard on her leg, eliciting a sharp yell.

"Ow, Bushy!" she cried, her voice filled with pain.

I pulled back immediately, apologizing profusely. Gwen let out a shaky sigh.

"Yes... Bluma was ordered to kill me, but she didn’t," she continued. "She wounded my leg and threw me out here when we heard you. She’s still inside."

I pondered her words as I worked to heal her leg, my mind racing. What were we supposed to do? Bluma was immensely strong and dangerous in this state. "She’s still in there?" I asked, needing confirmation. Gwen nodded grimly, and I knew I had to make a decision.

"Alright... then we have to try to bring her back," I said, standing and offering my hand to help Gwen to her feet. She swatted it away defiantly, her determination shining through her pain.

"Run away? Hell no! I’m fighting with you!" she declared, fire in her eyes.

I shook my head, panic rising in my chest. "No! If you fight, you’ll die! Now get out of here!" I pointed down the hall toward the stairs, my tone leaving no room for argument.

She stared at me for a moment in what looked like disbelief before growling and turning to leave.

I called out to her. "Thank you. And... I’m sorry."

She glanced back, her expression softening for a brief moment. "Don’t die, or I’ll bring you back just to kill you again," she warned before sprinting down the hall toward the stairs.

"Well... that's one way to encourage someone, I guess," I muttered, smiling to myself.

Turning my attention back to the room I had entered, I took in the horrific scene. The walls were streaked with blood, and the severed bodies of knights lay scattered across the floor like discarded toys. Bluma was nowhere in sight, and dread clawed at me as I considered the magnitude of her destructive power. My thoughts spiraled toward the inevitable confrontation ahead, knowing the danger she now posed.

Lost in my apprehension, a voice behind me made me jump. "Still playing the hero, young creature?" Spinning around, I readied myself for a fight, only to feel a rush of relief when I saw Rinn.

"Rinn!" I exclaimed, a smile breaking across my face.

He chuckled softly, stepping closer. "Hello there, young one. It's been a while... I like your new hand," he remarked, his tone as casual as ever.

Unable to resist teasing, I quipped, "I'd think you'd be itching to play the hero yourself, but I guess being my slave leaves you no choice." My grin widened at the irony.

Another tremor shook the castle, and the roof above us cracked ominously. Before it could collapse entirely, we both scrambled to safety. As the dust cleared, my heart sank at the sight before me. Bluma stood amidst the chaos, her eyes glowing an unnatural red, while the Queen loomed behind her, holding Beans in chains like a captured animal. His mouth was restrained by a steel muzzle, and his desperate attempts to communicate were muffled beyond understanding.

The Queen yanked his chains upward, choking him as she hissed, "Silence." Her gaze fell upon us, and a sinister smile curled her lips. "So, the monster and their pet unite. Oh, how romantic," she taunted, her laugh ringing hollow and cold.

Something dark consumed her body, spreading from her left arm in jagged purple rocks that glowed faintly with magenta flames seeping through the cracks. The corruption climbed to her left eye and part of her face. In her corrupted hand, she clutched a dagger forged in the shape of a feather, its dark purple hue almost hypnotic.

"The Demon Knight," the Queen addressed Bluma, her voice dripping with mockery.

Bluma raised her glowing white sword, and Rinn, never one to miss a beat, drew his violin. As I reached for my staff, Bluma lunged at me, her blade aimed to strike my neck. Panic flooded me; I knew I wouldn't react in time. Just as the sword descended, Rinn played a sharp, piercing E-flat, the sound reverberating like thunder. The force sent both Bluma and me flying. I managed to stay on my feet, but she tumbled before slowly rising, her movements stiff and mechanical.

"Thanks, Rinn!" I called over to him.

He groaned, clearly annoyed. "Shut up and pay attention!"

Bluma charged again, her strikes wild and unfocused. She swung at me, and I narrowly dodged, only for her to turn on Rinn. He sidestepped her attack with practiced ease, his expression sharp with concentration. Something about her erratic movements struck me—she wasn’t fighting like herself. Was she trying to miss us on purpose?

Back inside the castle, Rinn played a haunting B-flat that caused the roof to collapse on the Queen. Seizing the moment, he pulled me into a hiding spot and clamped his hand over my mouth.

Bluma burst from the rubble, her gaze scanning the room. The Queen snarled, "Don't just stand there! Go kill them!"

Bluma darted toward us, but instead of attacking, she sped past and disappeared down the hall.

Rinn whispered, "I cast a spell to keep her busy. Now we have the Queen all to ourselves."

I nodded, and he released me.

The Queen turned to Beans, her voice a chilling promise. "You will be my next slave. Once I make you mine, the Demon won’t resist anymore." She reached for his face, but a rock thrown by Rinn struck her arm, sending her reeling. Her furious gaze locked onto him, and I stayed hidden, waiting for the right moment to act.

"Why, you insignificant pleb!" she turned to him, readying her dagger, but

Rinn just smiled. "Pleb? How degrading, losing your mental lexicon so soon, falderal materfamilias? How disconsolate."

He laughed, which enraged the Queen and caused the magenta flames to roar. She formed a metal pole and stuck it into the ground, holding Beans' chains down, and charged at Rinn.

Rinn chuckled, skillfully dodging her attacks and making his way towards the door. "I hadn't realized the Queen was so sluggish," he remarked, further fueling her anger.

"Why you, fatuous trumpery!!" she yelled, chasing him out of the room.

Seeing this as an opportunity, I rushed over to Beans and tried to pull out the metal rod. Rinn's spell broke over me, and Beans could finally see me. He attempted to communicate something, but I couldn't understand.

"Hold on! I almost got it!" I struggled to move the beam, but it was firmly stuck in the ground. Beans’ muffled protests came again as he pointed to my bag.

"What? Is there something in my bag?" I opened it and searched inside but found nothing of much use. "I don't know what you're asking for."

Frustrated, he groaned and knocked my bag out of my hands, causing its contents, including crystals from the Underworld, to spill out. Beans grabbed one of the crystals and used it to free himself from the chains and muzzle.

Taking a deep breath, he looked at me and said, "This is what I was asking for! Now we need to save Bluma!" He got up, shaking off the metal restraints.

"But how are we going to do that? She's gone crazy!" I asked, confused. Beans groaned and ran out of the door, beckoning me to follow.

As we ran down the hall and stairs, Beans explained that a few days ago, the Queen and King had a heated argument. The Queen locked herself in her room, and when she emerged today, she was in her corrupted form and had taken control of Bluma. He mentioned that Bluma had been wearing a mask that she couldn't remove, so if we could break it, she might be freed.

"The crystals are incredibly strong and full of magic! We might be able to figure something out with them!" Beans exclaimed as we continued to run.

Suddenly, Bluma appeared from around the corner, her eyes still glowing red. Both Beans and I came to a halt, standing motionless in the hallway, unsure of each other's next moves.

Bluma ran towards us, swinging her sword violently in an attempt to strike either Beans or me. I managed to dodge most of her attacks, but then her sword hit my staff and became lodged in the middle. I held the staff above me, trying to avoid getting hit.

"Bluma, snap out of it!" I shouted.

Meanwhile, Beans approached from behind, but Bluma noticed him and kicked him, sending him to the ground. As Beans tried to recover, he turned around and saw Bluma preparing to strike him with her raised sword. He froze, unsure of what to do, his fear taking hold. However, before Bluma could hit him, I rushed forward and struck her with my staff, sending her flying back around fifty feet.

I helped Beans up, asking anxiously, "Are you okay?"

Beans shook his head, snapping out of his stupor, and nodded. "Yes, yes, I'm fine."

I nodded in relief and turned my attention back to Bluma, who was starting to rise again. "We have a chance. She doesn't want to hurt us!"

Beans remained silent but prepared himself for battle. Bluma charged towards us once more, swinging her sword. I tried to strike her with my staff, but she agilely evaded my attacks. Beans stayed close behind me, using my movements as an opportunity to dodge her strikes.

She attempted to hit me in the face with her sword, but I managed to duck underneath it. Swinging my staff at her feet, she leaped over it, repositioning her grip on the sword's handle. As she descended, her sword was aimed to pierce through my back. In that critical moment, Beans jumped onto my back and struck the side of her blade, causing it to divert and miss me, embedding itself deeply into the ground. Instead of trying to retrieve it, Bluma punched me in the face, causing me to stumble backward. However, I regained my footing and lightly struck her arm, sending her into a spin and causing her to fall to the ground. Once I regained stability, I lifted my arm, summoning roots to emerge from the ground and ensnare her.

"Beans, now!" I called out, signaling him to act.

Beans rushed towards her, gripping the crystal tightly as he raised it above his head. As his hand made contact with her mask, a cascade of black dust began to fall, enveloping them both. In that moment, an eerie silence filled the air, and Bluma found herself frozen in place while Beans carefully disentangled himself from her.

Simultaneously, the roots that had ensnared Bluma began to retract, retreating back into the earth. Gradually, she regained her footing, her eyes still emanating a haunting red glow. Beans examined the crystal in his palm, only to discover that its once brilliant surface had transformed into a lifeless black hue, crumbling into a fine dust. He shifted his gaze back to Bluma, and an intense stare-off ensued between the two of them, as if a profound understanding had passed between them.

Suddenly, cracks emerged on Bluma's mask, starting small but multiplying rapidly. They spiderwebbed across its surface, extending from the lower jaw up to her hairline. The glowing red in her eyes dissipated, leaving behind an abyssal darkness. Finally, the mask shattered completely, clattering onto the ground below, revealing Bluma's unmasked countenance.

CHAPTER 20                                                                                                                    Tyrant Size Rampage

Rinn’s View

I managed to slip away from the Queen for a few precious seconds, drawing a deep breath as I darted into the main hall. It was the same grand room where a lavish party had been held just a month before. Now, it stood empty, its opulence veiled in shadow. I pressed myself behind a pillar, straining to quiet my breath, but her voice pierced the stillness.

"Where are you?" Her cold tone echoed, accompanied by the sharp, deliberate rhythm of her heels against the floor. "I know you're in here... I can sense it."

A low, mocking chuckle followed, and with it, the oppressive heat of her magenta flames. The air thickened, and sweat pricked at my brow as my mind scrambled for a plan. Her footsteps grew louder, and the crushing weight of doom clawed at my chest—a feeling as dark and relentless as the void.

And yet, that very darkness thrilled me.

This was my life. Always evading the law, dancing on the razor's edge between sanity and madness. Grooming death with my gaze before slipping out of its grasp—this was what I did best. No, this was what I lived for. It earned me the title The Master Rogue, Prince of Shadows: Rinn. To me, her pursuit was nothing more than another game. A challenge.

The Queen’s steps slowed, then stopped. She was close now. I could feel her presence even before her voice dropped into a taunting whisper.

"I found you..."

Her dagger sliced through the air, the blade scraping against the stone where I had been. A flicker of triumph crossed her face as she stepped around the pillar—only to find empty space. Her smirk faltered. As her hand brushed the damaged pillar, realization dawned too late.

From the shadows, a massive stone golem surged forward, snatching her in an unyielding grip. She struggled, the cursed flame in her eyes burning hotter, until a burst of searing fire forced the creature to release her.

She landed gracefully, but fury twisted her features. Raising her accursed arm, she smashed the golem with a brutal punch, its form crumbling into a heap of shattered stone.

And then she saw me.

I stepped into a beam of pale light spilling from the high windows, the glow illuminating the smirk tugging at my lips. Her flames burned brighter, the creeping curse consuming more of her face as she prepared to strike.

But I was ready.

With deliberate poise, I raised my violin, its strings glinting with an ethereal light. A haunting melody filled the air as music stirred from nowhere and everywhere all at once. I inclined my head in a mock bow.

"Queens and tyrants!" I declared, my voice carrying through the hall. "It is with the greatest pride that we gather here tonight. So, relax. Put away your flames. For the Prince of Shadows is proud to present…"

I drew the bow across the strings, the music swelling to a crescendo.

"Our demise."

A grin spread across my face as I drew the bow across the strings, filling the hall with an upbeat and welcoming tune. The Queen charged at me in a blur of fury, but the Stone Golem reformed, grabbing her leg mid-stride and hurling her back toward the pillar. With an acrobatic twist, she landed against the pillar and launched herself across the room.

Her legs had transformed into a swirling vortex of black stone and crimson energy, keeping her suspended in the air. Her hair ignited into deep purple flames, blazing brighter with every second. Hurtling toward me, she snarled, “Enough of that insufferable noise!”

A fiery orb formed in her hand, seething with destructive energy, but she veered mid-flight as a massive boulder sailed toward her—a gift from the golem. It followed her motion with unrelenting precision, hurling rock after rock to the rhythm of my song. The Queen countered with a flurry of fireballs, each collision sending shards of stone scattering across the hall. She grinned, drawing an enormous fireball from thin air and hurtling it at the golem, obliterating it into a heap of shattered stone once more.

“Nice try, Rinn,” she taunted, her lips curling into a smirk, “but your little distractions have failed.”

She rushed toward me, a streak of fire and fury. Instead of fleeing, I played faster, the violin’s strings glowing with an ethereal light. The notes swirled into a crackling bolt of lightning that lashed out at her, striking her mid-charge and pushing her back a few feet.

I chuckled, tilting my head. “Oh, we’re just getting started, Your Majesty. This? This is only the warm-up.”

Her growl echoed like thunder as she flung her dagger toward my violin, aiming to sever its strings. I sidestepped and retaliated, striking a sharp chord that sent another bolt of lightning searing toward her. The Queen raised her hand, summoning a roaring stream of fire to meet the lightning. The forces collided with a violent crackle, neither relenting.

Electricity arced wildly from my violin, striking the floor and nearby pillars with resounding booms that rattled the hall. Sweat trickled down my back as the thrill of the battle fueled me. I played louder, pouring every ounce of energy into the music, and the lightning surged with newfound ferocity. Smaller bolts branched out, dancing across the air, their chaotic light illuminating the Queen’s feral expression.

But she was undeterred.

Raising her other hand, her flames erupted into a swirling inferno. The fire consumed my lightning with startling speed, forcing me to leap aside as the chromatic purple blaze hurtled toward me. I narrowly evaded it, landing in a roll as her laughter rang out behind me.

“Don’t think you can run from me!” she mocked, her voice dripping with menace.

Drawing a quick breath, I set my violin to my chin and struck a series of rapid chords. The stone around the fireplace sprang to life, snaking toward her and coiling tightly around her frame. With a deafening crack, the tendrils of stone dragged her into the roaring fire. Her blood-curdling screams echoed through the hall as the flames scorched her skin.

I took my chance. Smirking, I bowed deeply. “See you next fall,” I quipped, before slamming the heavy doors shut. Snatching a sword from a nearby knight statue, I wedged it tightly between the handles.

Spinning on my heels, I bolted down the corridor, heading for a staircase spiraling upward. “That should buy me some time,” I muttered to myself, a dark chuckle escaping my lips. “Can’t let her loose, or I’ll regret it.”

Behind me, the Queen’s screams shifted, her voice distorting into a guttural roar that reverberated through the castle. A crash shattered the stillness, and I glanced back to see the doors explode outward in a shower of splinters.

There she stood, her form unrecognizable. Her hair blazed in wild, golden-red flames, and her body dripped with molten violet lava. Her eyes were voids of seething fury.

“Insolent, pathetic wretch,” she snarled, her voice a monstrous screech that shook the very earth. “I will kill you today, if it’s the last thing I do!”

Her roar split the air, shaking the walls as she tore through the hallway in pursuit, destruction trailing her every step.

About a Month Before

The Queen paced her chambers, muttering under her breath. “Wasting time and energy on some... creature! What good will it do when it finally dies? None! Resources squandered, resources that should go to my people…”

She stopped by the window, gazing out at the kingdom below. Her subjects bustled about their lives, unaware of her frustrations. Bluma and Beans patrolled along the streets, their presence reassuring to the common folk but grating to her in that moment. She scoffed and turned away, a sneer curling her lips. My people deserve better than wasted effort and hollow sentiments…

Crossing to her bedside, she opened the drawer of her nightstand and drew out an ornate bracelet gifted by the Council of Seven. Its gem shimmered faintly with a menacing glow. She slipped it onto her wrist. The moment she did, a voice rang out, cold and commanding, echoing in her mind.

“Why not show him what you mean?”

The Queen remained composed, though her knuckles tightened. “And what do you mean by that?”

The voice chuckled darkly, its tone brimming with malice. “Prove your point. Show him your power. Demonstrate that your word is law—unyielding, absolute. Show him... the power of Hellfire.”

The gem flared to life, bathing the room in a crimson light. Flames erupted around her in a violent blaze, and when they subsided, the Queen found herself transported.

The ground beneath her feet was scorched and cracked, glowing with searing red veins of molten lava. The heat was suffocating, the air heavy with ash. She took a slow breath and turned toward the source of a guttural growl.

A colossal being loomed before her, towering over twenty-eight feet tall. Its massive frame was forged of dark red brimstone, with glowing cracks that spilled flames and liquid magma onto the ground. A single enormous eye, vivid red with a black slit for a pupil, stared down at her. Despite its humanoid form, it lacked a head, the eye embedded directly into its massive torso. It crouched to scrutinize her, radiating unbearable heat.

The Queen met its gaze, unflinching. “What is it you want of me?” she demanded, her voice resolute.

The creature’s growl deepened, reverberating like thunder.

“I seek the power to end the defiance of my husband and to rid my kingdom of that repulsive Randeth, Deta.” Her voice carried every ounce of her authority and bitterness.

The creature stilled, then erupted into a booming laughter that shook the infernal plain. “Deta, you say? Intriguing. Very well, mortal. I shall grant you power beyond imagination. But there is a price: become my advocate. Take Deta’s soul stone, and when you deliver it to me, your power shall grow boundless.”

Its massive hand reached for her. The Queen stood firm as blistering heat from the creature’s finger scorched the air. Her hair whipped about her face as the searing digit neared. When it touched her forehead, white-hot pain ripped through her. She doubled over, clutching her head, as a mark burned into her skin—three rhombuses: one sideways with two nested within, all bisected by a single line.

The pain was excruciating, yet exhilarating. Dark purple brimstone erupted from her skin, covering her face and hands. Flames licked from the cracks, and her anguished cries turned to wild, ecstatic laughter. The rush of strength and newfound power overwhelmed her senses. She straightened, marveling at her transformed body.

“So this… this is what true power feels like,” she murmured, her lips curving into a sinister smile. “It’s magnificent.”

The creature chuckled and rose to its full height, its eye gleaming. “This power will awaken fully when Deta is near—or if he does not exist to challenge you by then.” Its voice dripped with menace as it continued, “As my advocate, you are granted another gift: the ability to corrupt those you choose. Draw my mark upon their flesh, and in time, they shall bend to your every will. Now go.”

The Queen blinked, and in an instant, she was back in her chambers. The bracelet's gem pulsed faintly on her wrist, a lingering reminder of the pact she had just forged.

Present

As our fight continued I had taken notice of her movements becoming erratic and random, contrasting her previous strategic approach. While sudden changes in battle tactics might catch others off guard, I managed to evade her fiery attacks and lead her through the castle's halls. By making last-second turns, I caused her to miss me and allowed myself to gain more ground.

I turned to her and chuckled, teasing, "What's wrong? Am I going too fast?"

She yelled at me in frustration, calling me "Viel mutt," and increased her speed.

Anticipating an upcoming hall, I turned the corner earlier than expected, allowing the Queen to easily see which way I went. However, when she turned the corner, I had vanished. She searched the area briefly before yelling profanities and charging off to find me. I sighed in relief.

In the weeks leading up to this encounter, I had explored the kingdom and discovered many escape routes and hiding places. This particular hall was filled with hiding spots and had numerous offshoots. It was lined with suits of armor, behind one of which I found a small hole in the wall. It was just big enough for me to squeeze into, leading to a small tunnel that would take me to the dining hall. As I emerged from the tunnel and stood in the dining hall, I quickly assessed the surroundings, searching for anything useful.

"Time is running short... Let's see what I can find," I muttered, determined.

It didn't take long for the Queen to arrive in the dining hall. Seeing me standing there in front of the fireplace, she exclaimed, "Die, swine!" She hurled a fireball at me, but I swiftly dodged it. The fireball exploded upon hitting the wall behind me, propelling me towards her unexpectedly. She grinned, grabbing me by the neck. "Looks like your little game of hide and seek is over," she taunted, her burning grip growing hotter.

Chuckling, I responded, "You keep saying that... but you keep being wrong!" I pulled out my dagger and stabbed it into her eye, causing her to release me and allowing me to escape her grasp.

As soon as I hit the ground, I swiftly moved behind her. The Queen, dismissing the pain, quickly turned around, but I seized the opportunity and kicked her hard, causing her to stumble and fall back into the now-lit fireplace. The flames burned her, intensifying her agony

As I rushed into the dungeon with the cursed Queen hot on my heels, I looked around for any means of escape or something that could help me. The dungeon was dimly lit, with damp stone walls and a musty smell that filled the air. The sound of the Queen's enraged screams echoed through the corridors, adding to the sense of urgency.

Spotting a row of prison cells along one side, I quickly decided to seek refuge inside one of them. I hurriedly unlocked a nearby cell door and stepped inside, shutting it behind me just as the cursed Queen reached the entrance of the dungeon. Peering through the iron bars, I watched as she scanned the area, her fiery eyes filled with anger and a thirst for vengeance.

I froze at the roar, glancing back. “…Well, that’s less than ideal.”

I sprinted up the narrow staircase, my heart pounding with every step. If she caught me here, there’d be no escape. Thankfully, a door loomed near the top—a chance to outmaneuver her and finally trap this tyrant for good. The stairs seemed endless, but I reached the door at last. A laugh escaped me, but the sound of splintering wood cut it short.

Looking back, I saw her standing in the wreckage of the shattered doorway, her blazing eyes locking onto mine. My breath hitched as I stumbled through the door, slamming it shut behind me. Her enraged scream rattled the air, and I didn’t dare look back as the sound of her claws scrabbling up the stairs grew louder.

I found myself in a charred room, scorch marks covering every surface. It looked like an abandoned lab—maybe the sorcerer’s? Rumor had it he’d vanished long ago. Desperately scanning the area, I spotted a large, rusted shield behind an overturned bookshelf. It was decorative at best but sturdy enough for one hard hit. Everything else was just burned books and paper.

“Rats.”

Another door stood on the far side of the room, leading to a dark, narrow staircase. It reeked of mildew and seemed like a poor escape route. Before I could decide, the door I’d just come through exploded inward, the Queen crashing through like a raging beast. Without thinking, I grabbed the shield, jammed it beneath me, and leapt onto the stairs, riding the shield like a sled.

The improvised escape was faster than I anticipated—too fast. Every bump sent me airborne, and panic rose as I sped uncontrollably toward the bottom. The sharp edge of the stairs disappeared into a solid wall ahead. With no other option, I rolled off the shield as it hit the floor. I tumbled painfully across the stone, the shield slamming into the wall with a deafening crack before snapping in two.

Groaning, I sat up and checked for injuries. Thankfully, I seemed fine—until I noticed my violin in splinters beside me. “…Perfect.”

I looked around. Two doors stood before me. One bore a faded, crooked sign that read “Dungeon,” while light glowed faintly under the other. No time to think. I chose the lit door, stumbling inside to find a man with blonde hair and a filthy black apron. Strange machines and contraptions cluttered the room.

“Hey! You need to get out of here!” I shouted, slamming the door behind me.

The man turned, startled. “Why?”

“Because the Queen’s a monster now, and she’s coming this way!”

His eyes widened in excitement, not fear. “You brought a monster here? Perfect!”

I stared, dumbfounded. “What is wrong with you?”

He ignored me, rummaging through the clutter before pulling out a bizarre crossbow fitted with an equally strange bolt. “This is just the test subject I need!”

I had no time for his nonsense. Before he could explain, the Queen shattered the door behind me. Without hesitation, I grabbed the crossbow and fired.

The bolt hit its mark. The Queen screamed, her form warping and stretching as the curse twisted away from her body. She collapsed to the ground, separated from the magic. The curse itself took shape, writhing and unstable.

I turned on the man. “What was that?!”

He only grinned. “It works!”

The Queen had shrunk, encased in a small glowing orb, now motionless. Before the curse could rise, I grabbed the orb, stuffing it into my satchel. “We’re not done here,” I growled, shoving him toward the exit. “Now run!”

The curse screeched, its twisted form lunging as I kicked it back one last time. With no other choice, I threw myself through the dungeon door and bolted into the suffocating darkness.

Its inhuman wails echoed through the narrow halls, the sound chasing me, relentless and deafening. I ran blindly, the air growing colder with every step.

CHAPTER 21                                                                                                                     Gwen's Fight                           

Gwen’s View

The outside world was wrecked. Flames chewed through houses, and those freaky golems—same eerie junk as the Queen—were tearing through the streets. One of them was chasing three kids. The oldest, maybe ten, threw his arms out in front of the others like he could actually block a fireball. His face was a mess of dirt and tears.

“Go away! Don’t hurt us!” he shouted, voice cracking badly.

The golem didn’t even blink. It raised its arm, ready to torch them.

Too late.

Flames shot up from the ground and swallowed it whole. I sprinted in, sword flaring red.

“What the hell! You three okay?!”

The oldest looked up—and froze. Then he ran straight into me, hugging like his life depended on it. That’s when I recognized him. Aaron. We’d crossed paths before, back when things weren’t this on fire.

Their mom came tearing around the corner, scooped them up, and bolted, shouting a breathless thank-you over her shoulder.

And just as they disappeared, the ground shook. Out came another golem—twelve feet tall and twice as pissed.

I smirked, sword humming in my grip.

“Alright then. Just you and me, ugly.”

I spun on my heel and slammed my blade into its face, hard enough to crack stone. The thing screamed—if you could call that sound a scream—and I didn’t give it a second to recover. Drove my sword straight into its shoulder, deep enough to feel the heat pulsing through the thing. Using the hilt like a foothold, I vaulted over its head, twisting in the air.

Mid-leap, I tore the blade free and brought it crashing down into its back, forcing the monster to its knees with a satisfying crunch.

“Now that’s more like it,” I muttered.

Finally. I didn’t waste the opportunity. One swift strike severed its leg, eliciting an ear-splitting roar.

Do these things ever shut up? I thought, brushing damp strands of hair out of my face. My gaze shifted to a small group of townspeople huddled nearby—those who had foolishly strayed from the main group meant to protect them.

"Didn't I tell you to stay together?" I snapped. But before they could answer, the groaning creak of collapsing wood drew my attention. I turned to see one of the guard towers falling, consumed by flames.

"Mother of hell," I growled under my breath, rushing toward the stragglers. "Move, now!"

As we ran, a child's cry cut through the chaos. I looked back to see a young boy sprawled on the ground, calling for his mother. The woman tried to run to him, but I stepped in her way.

"I’ve got him! You keep going!" I shouted and sprinted toward the child as the flaming tower crumbled, threatening to crush us both.

You’ve got to be kidding me, I muttered through gritted teeth, raising my glowing sword. The gem near its tip blazed with white light. With a powerful swing, a blade of fire erupted from the sword and sliced through the collapsing tower, halving it just before it could reach us.

I scooped the boy into my arms and climbed over the smoldering debris to rejoin the others. His mother rushed toward us, tears streaming as she clutched her child tightly.

"Alright, enough with the waterworks! We need to regroup!" I barked, gripping my sword. The mother nodded, now holding the boy firmly as we continued toward the knights' barracks, where the rest of the townsfolk had taken refuge.

We dashed through the burning streets, our goal painfully far. Suddenly, distant footsteps echoed closer. I motioned for the group to follow me and ducked into a narrow alley. Peering around the corner, I saw more brimstone creatures smashing their way into homes, their lumbering forms searching for survivors. Finding none, they pressed on—straight toward our hiding spot.

I held a finger to my lips, signaling silence. For a moment, everything seemed still. Then, a child sneezed.   shhhh

My breath hitched. One of the monsters stopped and turned toward the alley, sniffing the air.

The creature’s bulk filled the entrance as it loomed over us. I pressed myself against the wall, clutching my sword tighter. The mother behind me wrapped her children in trembling arms. I can't take this thing down alone, I thought, but I’ll be damned if I let it get to them.

The monster hesitated, scanning the shadows. Then, as abruptly as it had appeared, it moved on, its thunderous footsteps fading into the distance.

A wave of relief swept over me. I motioned for the group to follow, and we slipped out of the alley, hurrying toward the barracks.

As we ran, my mind drifted to the day before when everything seemed normal. Children laughing in the streets, guards on their routine patrols, and mothers chatting while keeping watch. It felt like a dream now, overshadowed by memories of an encounter a month prior—the dragon. Unlike anything I'd fought before.

        I’d survived, but barely. Deta hadn’t been so lucky. The sight of his withered, leafless form still haunted me. You’d better wake up, Bushy. I still owe you.

Yesterday

I slipped my hand into my pocket, feeling the smooth edges of the soul stone that was vital to him. Not a chance I’m letting those healers get their hands on this for ‘experiments.’

The stone disappeared back into my pocket just as a familiar voice called out:

"Hey, Gwen!"

I turned, near unwillingly, to see Beans and Bluma approaching. Beans waved enthusiastically, a toxic grin plastered on his face.

"What do you want, short stack?" I smirked, noticing his visible annoyance.

"Very funny. Ha ha," he groaned, which made me chuckle. Bluma patted his head, helping ease his tension.

"So, what's up?" I asked, folding my arms.

Beans asked if I'd be willing to accompany them.

"What for? I'm a little busy," I replied.

Beans inquired, "With what?"

"Nonyor," I retorted.

Confusion flashed between Beans and Bluma as they glanced at each other.

"Nonyor?" Beans asked, incredulously.

"None. Your. Business," I chuckled. "I'm kidding. I'm bored out of my mind here. Let's go."

Beans groaned and chuckled, and I could tell Bluma found it amusing as well.

"Alright! Let's go!" Beans said, attempting to shrug off my amazing pun.

We walked across town toward a door on the side of the main castle.

"What's this place?" I asked, curious.

Beans smiled as he opened the door. "This is the knights' barracks!"

As the door swung open, I saw a few well-built men either donning or removing their armor. They chatted in various accents, but fell silent when they made eye contact with Bluma. I chuckled.

"So, you wanted to show me a smelly room of half-naked men?" I teased.

Beans shook his head. "It's on the other side. Follow us!"

Beans took the lead, and I followed. My sword was sheathed, so I couldn't understand why they were all staring at me instead of Bluma or Beans.

Just as Beans opened another door, a very tall, white-haired man with wisps of hair clinging stubbornly to his shiny scalp stepped into my path. Beans and Bluma froze, and I followed suit. The man’s thin, cracked lips stretched into a wide, unnerving grin that didn’t reach his watery eyes, which darted blatantly down to my chest.

“Well, aren’t you a sight for sore eyes,” he drawled, lingering far too long with his gaze.

I didn’t give him time to finish whatever vile thought was brewing. A quick roundhouse kick to the head sent him crumpling to the ground, clearing my path in one satisfying motion.

"You’re in my way."

The other men started reaching for their swords, but Bluma raised her hand, signaling them to stand down. I smiled to myself, thinking, Now I have more people to fight later. I enjoyed the thrill of combat, but that would have to wait. I followed Beans through the doorway and into a tunnel.

"Where are we going?" I asked.

Beans smiled. "The arena!"

Surprised and filled with excitement, I exclaimed, "The arena! Oh, this will be fun."

Beans smiled, and as we arrived at the door, it revealed a large, empty, flat area with incredibly large stands. I walked into the center, smiling as I looked around.

"Nice, it gives you all the room to mess around," I remarked.

Bluma chuckled. "Spar?"

I immediately turned around and replied, "Oh, heck yes."

She drew her sword, and so did I. Beans chuckled and moved to the side. Last time, when Deta and I fought Bluma, his lack of skill had made it easy for her to keep an eye on me while I had to look after him. But this time, Bushy isn't here, so I don’t have to babysit.

As I unsheathed my sword, it grew to its large size, and I smiled, assuming my stance. Bluma also drew her black sword, and we charged at each other.

Bluma approached me in an unusual line, so when we were within striking range, I jumped to the side, just out of her reach. To my surprise, she did the same. Seizing the opportunity, I jumped forward and swung my sword in a wide yet swift arc. However, she easily dodged it by leaping into the air, then attempted to swipe at my shoulder. Anticipating her move, I tried to dodge, but she managed to leave a scratch on my cheek.

In response, my sword glowed bright red as I swiped it again, sending fire blasting toward her. She darted back and forth, evading the flames, then used her sword to parry one of the fire blasts. She swiftly lunged forward, and our swords clashed, continuing the exchange of blows. At one point, I managed to dodge one of her swings, leaving a cut on her arm.

Our fight persisted late into the night until, as she ran toward me, she suddenly tripped and twitched in pain. Confusion washed over me, as I hadn't struck her in a way that would cause her to fall.

Beans rushed over to Bluma. "Bluma! Bluma, what's wrong?" He helped her up. She quickly straightened herself and held her head. I noticed her eyes flickering red.

She patted Beans' head then briskly walked away, sheathing her sword. I watched her depart, unable to shake off my bewilderment.

Turning to Beans, who seemed worried, I inquired, "What happened with Bluma?" I was still puzzled by her glowing red eyes and what made her collapse.

Beans replied, "It’s fine, but the arena serves another purpose." He began talking about the arena's true function, but I could easily tell he wanted to mention something about what had just occurred. He knew something—but what was it?

I decided not to pry into Beans' life. It wasn’t my place to do so; that’s Bushy’s job.

Beans explained that the arena served as a refuge during emergencies. If something happened in the kingdom, everyone could gather there to lay low or escape through the catacombs if necessary.

"A maze?" I raised an eyebrow. "That’s a pain, but I see what you mean."

Beans nodded in agreement. "Yes, but it’s getting late. We should probably turn in. I’ll see you when I see you!"

He smiled and ran off. I remained in the arena, gazing up at the starry night sky. I let out a sigh, remembering my first night in this kingdom.

"Bushy... you better not be dead," I muttered, then turned away and headed back to the inn.

Upon reaching the room where our crazy journey began, I took in the sight. The room contained four beds and a few windows on the wall. I sighed and approached the bed closest to the window where Deta would typically lie, sitting down and gazing out. From the window, I could see a pillar of the castle and the plains beyond the castle walls, stretching toward the east.

A snail was slowly making its way along the open window ledge, attempting to enter. Irritated, I grabbed the tiny creature and tossed it out the window. "Get out!" I muttered under my breath. I watched it fly into the sky and disappear from view. As I turned around, something caught my eye—a window in the castle pillar within view had emitted a brief, bright red glow before vanishing.

Something isn’t right here, I thought.

I closed the window and sighed, trying to push aside the growing sense of danger. I must just be tired. Some sleep might help. Walking over to the door, I locked it by placing a dresser in front of it, then lay down on the bed next to the closed window, attempting to drift off to sleep. But sleep eluded me. The air carried a sense of impending danger I couldn't shake off.

In the early hours of the morning, I left my room and wandered through the town.

As I walked, the familiar surroundings led me to the decision to visit the old man. The town was remarkably peaceful, though an unsettling feeling lingered within me. The amber-colored sky gradually rose, the moon receding over the horizon, and the kingdom began to be illuminated by the first light of day. With the sun rising and casting light on my path, I arrived at the site of the old man's house—only to find it burned to the ground.

"What the heck!" I ran toward the charred remains, sifting through the rubble. The books I had opened were now reduced to ashes. As I surveyed the scene, I realized the old metal door was gone, along with most of their belongings, either destroyed by the fire or stolen. Anger welled up within me. Who would do such a thing? The old man and his wife hadn't done anything wrong!

Attempting to comprehend what had transpired, I spotted a knight walking through the streets, heading in my direction. Determined, I approached him and demanded an explanation.

"You! What happened here?!" I yelled.

The knight looked at me in confusion and asked what I meant.

"You very well know what I mean! What happened to this house? Who burned it down?!"

The knight raised an eyebrow.

"Ma'am, calm down. This isn't recent, you know... This house burned down a thousand years ago. It's a town monument from the Frost Era."

What the hell!? What is he saying!? I was just here a month ago! I thought, growing increasingly perplexed and angry at his apparent deceit. Sensing my disbelief, the knight spoke again, trying to prove his point.

"Look, read the stone inscription on it." He pointed toward a large stone with a metal plate attached to it.

I marched over to examine it, and what I read left me astonished:

This is the home of the craftsmen family,

Beloved by those in the kingdom

Susie otherwise known as Nana would

Care for any who found themselves in need.

While her husband Harold was a Master Smith.

The only one to have been able to forge blades from the horn of a skrelp.

We honor this land to remember their kindness and also the harshness of the Frost Era in which they survived.

I stood there in disbelief as the knight spoke, insisting that the house had burned down a thousand years ago during the Frost Era. My teeth gritted in frustration.

"What the hell... What kind of bullcrap is that? How is this possible?"

The knight attempted to offer an explanation, mentioning that some people had reported seeing the house intact with two older individuals inside. He admitted that he wasn't well-versed in magic and didn't have all the answers. With that, he took his leave to continue his patrol, leaving me to my thoughts.

"Magic... Huh?" I muttered, contemplating the mysterious events unfolding around me.

In an attempt to make sense of it all, I drew my sword and inspected it closely. It appeared as new and undamaged as it should be.

"Hm... Magic makes no sense," I mused, sheathing the sword back in its scabbard.

Resolute, I continued my walk through the kingdom, the feeling of impending danger never leaving my side. I noticed a few dogs on the streets, their expressions mirroring my own concern.

"Even the dogs feel it," I remarked, resting my hand on the handle of my sword. I refused to be caught off guard.

As I continued my stroll, I found myself in the main district, where people went about their daily routines, seemingly oblivious to the underlying unease I felt. Amidst the bustling crowd, I spotted Beans walking without Bluma by his side. I called out to him, "Hey, Beans!"

He turned toward me, a smile lighting up his face. "Oh, hey Gwen! I was just about to look for you."

I crossed my arms and raised an eyebrow, prompting him to explain. Beans chuckled and told me that he had been going through the records of the prisoners and stumbled upon information about the men who stole Dragon Sap a month ago. Perplexed, I asked him about Dragon Sap, having never heard of it before.

Beans explained that it was a powerful sap found deep within the forest, possessing potent healing properties and celestial magic. He managed to acquire some from the barracks and gave it to the healer caring for Deta, our comrade who was still recovering.

"He should wake up a lot faster now!" Beans declared with a smile.

I couldn't help but smile in response, though I flicked his head hard for not doing it sooner. Beans winced, holding his forehead where I had flicked him.

"What the heck, Gwen!" he exclaimed.

Rolling my eyes, I retorted, "Well, in any case, when that pile of rocks wakes up, tell him to watch his back. I don't like waiting."

Beans chuckled and assured me he would relay the message. Before our conversation could continue, a knight approached us. His armor stood out from the others, adorned with golden trims and carvings, and he wore a red cap.

"Squire Beans and Gwen, the King has requested an audience with you," he informed us.

Beans turned to the knight, seeking more information before proceeding. The knight shook his head, stating that the king had yet to explain his reasoning but wanted to meet with both of us. After exchanging glances and subtle threats, I growled, "This better not be a waste of time."

The three of us made our way to the castle, where we found the king sitting on his throne in the grand hall. He greeted us with a boisterous laugh.

"Hello, my friends! It's great to see you well."

Beans kneeled and bowed, addressing him as "My king" and expressing his honor to be in his presence. I followed suit with a small bow. The king smiled, urging us to stand.

"It is not necessary to bow," he chuckled. "Beans, Gwen, please step forward."

Beans promptly rose and approached the king, while I took my time, not one to rush. Once we stood in front of him, the king rose from his throne.

"Gwen, as one of the heroes who saved us from the dragon beneath the kingdom, I, King Solace, grant you the title of Surco of Sumring. It is a title bestowed upon those with great honor and skill."

I couldn't help but smile at the recognition.

"Surco, huh? I'll take that," I replied, and we shared a chuckle.

Then, the king turned his attention to Beans. "And Squire Beans, you have served this kingdom faithfully for many years, and I believe you have not been given the credit you deserve."

I glanced at Beans, noting his soft smile and respectful posture with hands behind his back. The king continued, drawing a decorative sword from his side.

"I hereby bestow upon you the rank of Surco and name you Royal Knight to the King!"

Tears welled up in Beans' eyes as he expressed his gratitude. "Thank you, m'Lord. This... means so much to me." The king smiled, patting Beans on the shoulder and whispering something into his ear that made him blush. Beans whispered a response, eliciting a chuckle from the king.

"You're lucky my wife is a little... blind to these things."

Before our joyous moment could linger, the ground beneath us shook, followed by screams echoing through the castle. Instantly, my instincts kicked in, and I assumed a combat-ready stance. Beans drew his axe, and we both prepared for a fight.

The king turned to the knight who had accompanied us and instructed him to take his daughter to the safe house. With urgency in his voice, he addressed us, "We must hurry! That came from my wife's quarters!"

Beans interjected, suggesting the king go with his daughter for her safety. Unfazed, the king shed his cape and silk clothes, revealing heavy-plated armor adorned with gold and rubies. "I can care for myself, but my wife is in danger," he asserted.

Before Beans could argue further, I took charge, sprinting toward the stairs. "Then you better keep up!" I called, determination fueling my every step.

The king, resolute, ran after me, while Beans sighed but followed suit. Together, we raced to the floor where the commotion had originated and barged into a room. There, we witnessed a harrowing scene—the Queen held a knight's lifeless body in the air, half of her own body consumed by flames.

"Luna! What is going on?" the king called to his wife, his voice laden with concern.

Slowly, the Queen turned toward him, her eyes filled with an otherworldly fire. She let out a blood-curdling scream as a pillar of purple fire incinerated the knight she had been holding.

I clenched my fists, ready to engage in battle, but the king stepped in front of us, his voice commanding, "Do not harm her!"

He then approached his wife, removing his chestplate and extending his arms in an attempt to embrace her. "My love... Please come here," he pleaded.

With a malevolent smile, the Queen tossed aside the sword she had used to kill the knight. "He was always too soft for his own good," she taunted, reveling in her newfound power.

We fought the Queen throughout the castle. She easily defeated Beans and sent me flying across the room. As I got back up, she placed chains and a muzzle on Beans, happily sighing. She formed several small balls of purple fire, tossing them out the window. I assumed that’s when the beasts began to emerge from the ground, terrorizing the people.

She turned back to me. "Come now, dear, don't make a poor decision here. My offer still stands. You can rule with me, and together we can fund that part of us that's missing..."

I gritted my teeth. "Yeah right... Your missing piece is this bull. I don't want mine if that's how I’ll be."

The Queen sighed. "Oh this...? It's close, but not quite what I'm searching for."

I took a firm stance and readied my blade. "I think I'll pass."

The Queen frowned. "What a poor choice." She then grinned, and Bluma emerged from around a corner, her eyes glowing red.

The two of them charged at me. I managed to block the attack, but the force sent me flying through the floor. As I was still falling, Bluma somehow caught up, swung her sword, and cut my leg, sending me flying out a door.

My ears rang from the sheer power she had, but once I regained my hearing, I heard a familiar voice.

"Gwen!"

I looked over, wincing in pain. "Bushy!? You're alive? Ah!"

I tried not to react to the pain, attempting to stand, but the deep wound caused me to fall back down.

"Gwen, don’t get up! Let me heal you! Also, what's going on?"

Present

Deta walked over to me, and I quickly explained. He healed my leg, and we parted ways. I don’t know how, but he convinced me to leave and help people outside. Once I did, I found myself exactly where I am now.

As I returned to the present, we had finally managed to get the group of stragglers into the arena where the town had gathered. Just as I walked past the entrance, a knight called out, "Alright! That's everyone!"

CHAPTER 22                                                                                                                    Grand Escapism

Deta’s View

Beans stared at Bluma in disbelief. "Bluma… is that really you?" As the mask fell away, her true identity was revealed.

She reached out, softly touching Beans as she answered, "Yes… Squishy."

Her face, still had her four golden eyes but also soft, black freckles, giving her an unexpectedly vulnerable appearance. Her gentle nature contradicted the cold, emotionless persona her mask had created. Bluma lowered her gaze, seeming embarrassed, but Beans rushed over and embraced her tightly, surprising her.

"You're free from that dreadful mask..." Beans murmured, his eyes filled with emotion.

Bluma looked at him, her own eyes wide with disbelief. "You’re… happy?" she asked, her voice trembling.

Beans laughed, shaking his head. "Yes!  Before you didn't have a choice. But now, you do. And now I get to see your beautiful face."

Tears filled Bluma’s eyes as she hugged him tightly. "I...love… you"

The two held each other for a moment, their embrace firm and unyielding. But just then, the ground shook, and the deafening sound of buildings collapsing outside reached us. We snapped our attention to the chaos.

"Deta, we need to get to the arena! The townspeople should be there!" Beans called.

I nodded, agreement quick, and we sprinted from the castle, only to find the town reduced to ashes.

Magma monsters ravaged everything in their path. "Hurry! Follow me!" Beans dashed toward the arena, but Bluma scooped him up and ran faster, leaving me to follow closely along the castle wall to avoid detection by the beasts. Their raw power was captivating—but terrifying.

"I sent Gwen out there. She’s fine, right?" I turned back to Beans and Bluma. “I was just about to say—”

Beans cut in before I could finish, already reading my thoughts.. "Don’t worry, Deta. Gwen knows where the arena is, and she’s probably already there. But for now, we need to reach it before the knights evacuate everyone—or we won’t catch up!"

I was surprised by his understanding but nodded. Nothing about this situation surprised me anymore. "Then what are we waiting for? Let’s move!" I called, and Bluma picked up her pace, catching me slightly off guard.

As we rounded a corner, we spotted a group entering a door set into the castle’s wall. A familiar dark-skinned woman entered last, her sword at her side.

"Gwen!" I called.

As I approached the door to follow her inside, Beans and Bluma swiftly joined me, closing the door behind them. Bluma took a piece of paper from a stone box and placed it on the door, transforming it into solid stone, then gave a nod to Beans.

Beans adjusted his grip on his axe and muttered, "Alright... let’s go."

Together, we ran deeper into the catacombs.

After a while, we arrived at a fork in the road—left or right. Beans was deep in thought, trying to make the decision. I asked him, "Which way do we go?"

Bluma stepped up, patted his head, and smiled. "Let’s go left," she suggested.

We moved down that path only to find ourselves at another fork. Gwen sighed, "It hasn’t even been five minutes, and we’re already lost." Beans took a moment, then considered our options—forward, left, or right—before a strange sound broke through the air.

I nodded. "Yes, I hear it." The eerie sound grew louder, and from the left, a pack of wolves emerged, their flesh hanging loosely from their bones.

Beans turned to us, urgency in his voice. "Everyone, down the right passage!" he commanded. The people around us quickly began to flee down the passage. He turned to Bluma and me. "You two stay with them. Bluma knows the way, and Deta, you can hold your own!"

I was startled. "What? You and Gwen are staying? Let me help!" I protested.

Beans met my eyes with an unshakable determination. "You’ll be more helpful protecting the people. Go now. We can handle this."
