I stood there for a moment, then finally agreed. Bluma and I ran towards the group, and she glanced back, asking,"Deta, can you stay in the back? Make sure-"

"-Nothing sneaks up on us from behind?" I finished for her, understanding her meaning. "Sure. No problem" 

She gave a small smile and nodded. I stayed at the back, staff in hand, my senses alert for any threats lurking in the shadows.

Our footsteps echoed through the narrow tunnel as we pushed forward. The flickering torchlight cast shifting shadows along the damp walls, and for a while, no one spoke.

Eventually, the pace of the group began to ease. The panic in our breathing faded into heavy, tired exhales. When we reached a small open chamber, the group slowed to a cautious walk. A few glanced back, eyes wide but calming. It felt safer here—just enough to let the tension fray at the edges.

Boots slapped stone as someone jogged to catch up. Beans, cheeks flushed and breath uneven, rejoined us, falling into step beside Bluma. He wiped a hand across his forehead and gave her a small grin, his eyes scanning everyone with a wary kind of relief.

Bluma’s gaze softened as she looked at him, then flicked back to the passage ahead.

One man noticed my staff and, with a skeptical look, asked, "Why are you carrying a stick? What good will that do?"

The woman next to him immediately slapped his shoulder, scolding him. "Jim, quit it."

Jim and I shared a brief chuckle. "It’s fine, ma’am. But you can trust Jim. This little twig has saved me more than once," I reassured them.

Jim raised an eyebrow. "That twig? That's a bold statement."

As we continued walking, the group suddenly turned left, and I stopped.
"Well, here—see this rock?" I pointed at a rock about the size of a butternut squash.

Jim glanced at it. "Yeah? What about it?"

With a smile, I tapped the rock with my staff. It glowed green and flew into the air. "See?" I said, demonstrating.

Jim chuckled. "So it's enchanted. Not bad."

Beans’ head snapped toward him. "Not bad? That’s what you’ve got to say?" He gestured sharply at the hovering rock. "That staff's saved more lives than you’ve had hot meals. Maybe show a little respect before you call it ‘not bad.’"

Jim raised an eyebrow, clearly caught off guard. "I was complimenting it."

Beans huffed. "Sure didn’t sound like it."

 Bluma reached out and gently tugged at his sleeve. He quieted but kept his glare on Jim until the rock slowly lowered back to the ground.

Just as we were about to continue, a man came running toward us. "Deta, the lady up front asked for you to come up quickly," he informed me.

I nodded, thoughts racing. What lady? Wait… do they not recognize Bluma? The realization startled me, but then I considered that it might be better if they didn’t, especially considering what had happened earlier with her possession.

I reached the front and saw Bluma a few yards ahead, bent down and inspecting something on the ground. I thanked the messenger and approached her. "What’s going on?" I asked.

Bluma looked up at me as she stood. "Monster remains," she replied.

I glanced down at what she was studying—a scattering of bones and feces. "Ew," I muttered, remembering the box I had glimpsed back in the Underworld, which sent a cold shiver down my spine.

Bluma pointed ahead. "There’s a dead end. Take the group there, then come back, and we’ll scout ahead."

I nodded in understanding. "Got it. By the way, it’s nice to hear you talk a bit more," I remarked with a smile.

Bluma smiled back, brushing a strand of hair behind her ear. I followed her instructions, leading the group to the dead end. The space was large enough for everyone to settle in comfortably. "Alright, stay here for a moment! We’ll scout the next area!" I announced.

The men nodded. "Okay, we’ll wait here," they replied.

I gave them a reassuring smile before jogging back toward Bluma. "Alright," I said, letting out a breath. "Let’s see what’s ahead."

As we continued down the corridor, a strange sound filled the air—a piercing scream, followed by a deafening roar. My grip tightened on my weapon as we cautiously advanced. When we reached a corner, we peeked around it, and I froze.

A horse, rearing up on its hind legs, bellowed in fury. Beside it stood a chest with red eyes and sharp teeth—its monstrous form shifted before us.

"Bluma, it’s a shifter!" I exclaimed, and she nodded in agreement. "And… a horse?" I raised an eyebrow, confused. Ready to defend ourselves, I gripped my staff tighter, but Bluma grabbed my arm just before I could charge forward.

"Stop, look," she whispered urgently.

I followed her gaze and noticed the shifter wasn’t facing the horse. Instead, it seemed fixated on something further down the hall, obscured from view. Then, a massive, purple, spear-like object suddenly shot out from the shadowed passage, snatched the shifter, and dragged it away with agonizing screams.

As the shifter was pulled into the unknown, the horse dropped down on all fours and charged toward us. We quickly pressed ourselves against the wall, watching as it rounded the corner. Spotting us, the horse skidded to a halt, startled, and reared up on its hind legs, attempting to strike.

"Whoa! Whoa! Calm down! It’s okay!" I shouted, and surprisingly, my voice had a calming effect. The horse paused for a moment. That’s when I realized who it was.

"Rubert?" I asked, astonished.

"I say! It’s so lovely to meet you again!" Rubert's familiar, boisterous voice filled the hallway. I couldn’t help but chuckle.

"Rubert!" I rushed forward, throwing my arms around him in a hug. "It’s so good to see you!"

He chuckled, but then looked at Bluma. "Another female? You can’t seem to keep a mate around, can you?" Rubert’s comment took me by surprise, and I quickly laughed it off.

"What? No! She’s someone else’s mate. We were just scouting the area," I clarified, turning to reassure Bluma.

Her expression was one I recognized from Gwen when we left the cave—though this time, Bluma's face turned a deep red. "M… mate?" she asked, clearly caught off guard.

"Ah! Sorry, let me explain!" I quickly intervened. "I have a gift of speaking to animals with a certain level of intelligence. Rubert here has been curious about you—well, about humans in general— we met several months ago when I first came to the kingdom."

Bluma blinked, processing the information. "I see," she said. "Ask him about... the monster."

Smiling, I turned to Rubert and asked, "So... Do you know anything about the one who attacked the shifter?"

"Ah, the vicious beast I scared off!" Rubert’s chest puffed out in pride. "It was a shifter, unlike anything I’ve ever seen!"

I chuckled and clarified, "No, not the shifter. The one that impaled it."

Rubert huffed, an amused glint in his eye. "Ah, yes. The wall itself. That’s a giant shifter!"

Silent contemplation engulfed me as I processed the revelation—a giant shifter. I turned to Bluma, asking, “Is there any way around it?”

Bluma's response came swiftly and flatly, “No.”

It wasn’t the answer we had hoped for. “How are we going to pass it? We have to go that way to get out, right?” I pressed, seeking a solution.

Bluma nodded. "We should go back and... plan."

With a sigh, we retraced our steps to rejoin the others. Upon our return, the group was eagerly awaiting news. Not wanting to give them the full truth, we simply told them a formidable monster blocked our path, and we would need to wait for Beans and Gwen before taking any action. Though disappointed, they didn't lose hope.

About an hour passed before Gwen and Beans appeared around the corner, relief washing over me.

“We found you guys, finally,” Gwen exclaimed, her smile easing my worry, though it quickly faded as the weight of the giant shifter settled back into my thoughts.

Beans approached Bluma, while Gwen came to me. “What’s bugging you, bushy? Another snail?” Beans teased, pulling a chuckle from me.

“Well...” I began, explaining the situation.

 After some thought, we devised a plan. The group was informed, and the two eldest members were helped onto Rubert’s back. I shifted into my Celeste Elk form, carrying the young children as we made our way toward the inevitable encounter with the shifter.

“Do you remember the plan?” Beans asked as I jogged ahead, and I nodded.

“Alright. As soon as you can, take a left, then a right. Wait for us there. We don’t know what else lurks in these catacombs,” he added, his tone serious.

Gwen gripped one of my antlers to steady herself as I sprinted toward the corner where the shifter lay in wait. The moment we reached it, the enormous shifter’s mouth opened wide, revealing rows of jagged teeth and a purple tongue that lashed at us. Gwen swiftly dismounted from my back, her sword glowing vibrant red. With a precise slash, she cut the tongue, causing the creature to shriek, its wails shaking the surroundings.

Rubert and the others sprinted to our side, and we snapped into formation, weapons ready. The battle erupted. Gwen’s sword blazed, Bluma’s shone with a white light, and Beans charged in swinging an ax. Gwen and Bluma met the shifter’s strikes head-on, parrying with sharp precision.

For a while, we held our ground. But the shifter adapted—fast. It broke through our line and ensnared several of us. Gwen shouted something in a language I didn’t recognize, her voice raw with urgency.

When we finally broke past the creature, half our group lay behind. Those of us who survived stood in silence, grief pulling at the edges of everything.

Beans exhaled a heavy sigh. “This didn’t go as we wanted,” he muttered.

Gwen scanned the group, frustration etched into her face. She stepped forward, raising her voice above the sorrowful murmurs. “Hey! What are you all whining about? This isn’t the time to wallow in self-pity! Yes, you've lost family and friends, but if you don’t pull yourselves together, you’ll join them! Life doesn’t stop when you face loss! You didn’t come here to die! Stand up—keep moving! The sun will shine again! If you want to live, keep fighting!”

As Gwen spoke, the pain in her eyes was evident. These weren’t just words—they were a part of her, words she had carried her whole life. The group slowly rose to their feet, and some of the young adults ventured off further down the corridors on their own. The elderly, children, and parents stayed behind.

"Alright, let’s continue and find a way out, so you can reclaim your lives," Gwen declared.

With that, Beans led the way, and the faint sound of distant cries reached our ears. Gwen and I hurried ahead to investigate, discovering several young adults trapped inside a jelly-like cube.

One of them noticed their presence and cried out, pleading, "Please save us! We can't escape!"

Gwen approached the young man and asked, "Did your friends abandon you?"

 As he struggled, the young man’s clothes began to dissolve. In anguish, he cried out, "Please, it's getting more painful! I don't want to die!" Tears streamed down his face.

Gwen grabbed him by the hair and yanked him out of the cube. "Satisfied?" she asked, watching him collapse to the ground.

"Thank you! Thank you!" he shouted, trying to hug her, but Gwen swiftly punched him in the gut.

“Now go free, your friends.” She returned to me, muttering under her breath.

I chuckled. “Still not a fan of hugs?”

Gwen rolled her eyes. "I don’t trust him."

“Do you trust me?” I asked, his grin widening.

Gwen sighed but smiled, walking away.

“Hey, I didn’t get my answer!” I called after her, before turning to help the others who were still trapped.

As Beans' group returned, the young adults decided to join us, trailing behind through the winding maze of catacombs. The twists and turns were confusing, and I quickly lost track of our path. Every so often, we came across more individuals—some ensnared in jelly cubes, others fast asleep at dead ends. We invited those we found to join us, though a few stubbornly insisted they could manage on their own.

We pressed onward. The further we went, the more we saw people collapse from exhaustion. We halted, allowing Beans and Bluma to investigate while Gwen and I stayed behind, guarding the group.

"I can't believe they're having all the fun without us. Why can't I go with them?" Gwen muttered.

I chuckled. "I think you’re the only one who finds danger exciting."

She smirked. "What? I take pride in the scars I earn from battle!"

I smiled. "Try not to go overboard. I don’t want you getting hurt."

Gwen playfully punched my shoulder. "Oh, look who’s talking! You were dead for a month! Do you have any idea how worried we all were?"

I leaned in, voice low and amused. "Oh, so you were worried about me?"

“Tch, of course I was! We still have a debt to settle!”

I chuckled. "Is that the only reason?"

Gwen groaned. "You're such a blockhead, you know that?"

I patted my chest. "Indeed, and it's a badge I wear proudly."

We shared a laugh before Beans and Bluma returned. "Alright, we’re mostly clear, but let’s stay alert," Beans warned, eyeing the group.

"Yeah, yeah. Don’t get your ax in a twist, squirt," Gwen joked, prompting Beans to retort.

As hours dragged on, we took turns leading the way. I began to question whether we were lost for good, but kept my concerns to myself. Along the way, we fought off various monsters, doing our best to protect the survivors. Gwen stretched after plunging her sword into a zombie-like wolf. "These things are easy to beat... I just wish they didn’t come in such large packs," she commented.

I picked up my staff, scanning the area. "True. The more trouble we encounter, the harder it is to keep everyone safe."

Gwen nodded. "Exactly."

She handed me her sword to clean off the decaying blood.

We kept moving, and soon we stumbled upon a doorway. A wave of hope washed over everyone. We flung it open, revealing a clearing in the woods. The survivors scattered, some collapsing onto the grass in relief. These weren’t seasoned adventurers; for some, this was the farthest they'd ever been from town.

"I missed grass," I murmured, sinking to the ground. The sunlight hit my leaves, turning them a vibrant green as I let out a contented sigh.

Gwen chuckled. “Bushy, I swear.”

Beans and Bluma sat beside us. “Well, we can rest here for a while," Beans suggested. "After that, we should head to a nearby town or village tomorrow.”

Bluma nodded. "Sounds good, Squishy," she teased, patting his head.

I lay on my back, a soft smile on my face. "I’m just grateful to feel the sun again..."

As the evening wore on, we set up camp and gathered large leaves to keep the children warm. The parents curled up with their kids, and the others snuggled together for warmth, grateful to be safe, at least for the moment.

CHAPTER 23                                                                                                             Shattered Kingdom

The following morning, Beans gathered a few men and assigned each of them a task. Some were tasked with finding wood for a fire, others with scouting the area for trails, and the rest went hunting with the few daggers we had. Beans sighed as the groups split up, then returned to Bluma, Gwen, and me.

"Alright, we need to figure out where we are. I sent some men to scout the area for trails," he said.

Bluma smiled and patted his head. "Thank you, Squishy."

Beans blushed, and Gwen and I couldn’t help but smile and chuckle.

"Well Bushy" Gwen said, turning to me

"We're not too deep in the woods. It should take us about a day to reach civilization if we go the right way."

Beans paused before asking, "And you know the way?"

I smiled. "Well, I did grow up in the forest."

Beans turned to me, a mix of surprise and irritation on his face. "Why didn’t you say so sooner?!" he exclaimed. “I had just sent men into the woods blind when you could have prevented that!”

Scratching the back of my head, I gave an awkward smile. "I thought I had told you... Oops." My hand paused mid-scratch as a realization struck me. I glanced down at my hand, the glove cut. The wooden and stone flesh had fallen away, revealing pale skin similar to the others'. As my thoughts swirled, another worry crept in—I had left Rinn behind. He should’ve been dragged along with me; he could never stray far since I had claimed him.

Gwen noticed the concern etched on my face. With a groan, she unsheathed her sword. "Bushy, let’s find one of those groups and speed this up. I don’t want to stay here longer than we have to." She marched off without waiting for a response.

Beans gave me a reassuring smile. "Probably a good idea. The faster we gather supplies, the sooner we can find a safe place for these people to live."

His eyes shifted toward the survivors—mostly children with a handful of elders helping the mothers as best they could. Almost everyone had lost someone, whether in the catacombs or the earlier attack on the Kingdom.

I nodded and jogged after Gwen. "Hey, Gwen! Wait up!"

She didn’t stop but glanced back as I caught up. Her determined expression stayed fixed, unwavering.

"Let’s see," I said, pointing to a trail on the right. "Looks like they went this way."

She paused, turning fully toward me, waiting silently as if leaving the choice to me. Feeling the pressure, I forced a small smile and started down the path. The quiet between us stretched until, finally, she spoke.

"So… how’s your hand doing?"

The question caught me off guard. "Oh… uh, it’s fine, I guess? Just odd."

Her gaze lingered, urging me to say more.

"I think I might be able to use my magic to disguise it," I added, "like I did to you inside the giant worm."

I tried to chuckle, but the memory surfaced—the moment I’d died. The image of the glowing woman flashed in my mind, and I remembered the looks on everyone’s faces, especially Gwen’s, as they thought I was gone.

Her expression darkened as if the same memory had crossed her mind. Her eyebrows drew together, but she forced a smile. "Maybe! But hey, look—there are the people we’re looking for!"

She strode toward the group of hunters, who stood chatting with daggers in hand.

"Where are all the critters?" a burly man asked.

"There’s nothing out here," replied a wiry one.

"Yeah, like those muscles of yours," teased another, prompting a burst of laughter.

"Hey! Morons!" Gwen barked, bringing their conversation to a halt. "How do you expect to find prey when you’re louder than a twister?!"

I stifled a laugh and leaned closer. "Um, Gwen? Yelling probably doesn’t help either," I whispered.

She hesitated but quickly straightened, brushing off the misstep. "Tch… Whatever. Do you think any forest creature hears a racket and thinks, 'Oooh, I should check that out?' No! They run because they don’t want to die."

Her pointed tone earned a glare from one of the men.

"Now listen here, girly—" he began, but Gwen’s cold, piercing stare froze him mid-sentence.

I stepped in to diffuse the tension. "Let me explain how wolves hunt. They observe first—watch for tracks, follow scents, and, when close enough, they move in absolute silence to strike." I looked at the hunters. "Got it?"

Reluctantly, they nodded.

"Good. Split into pairs and act like wolves. You'll have better luck."

The men exchanged skeptical glances but eventually broke off into smaller groups.

Gwen turned to me, her stern expression softening just a little. Playful sarcasm coming off her voice. "Didn’t know we had a forest expert with us."

I chuckled. "Well, I did grow up in one."

She sighed. "Let’s find some food ourselves. Come on."

We ventured deeper into the woods, following faint signs of wildlife. The melodic chatter of songbirds filled the trees, but it took a while before we stumbled upon fresh tracks.

"This looks promising, doesn't it, Bushy?" Gwen knelt beside a set of large prints, her fingers tracing the edges. The tracks were massive—each hind paw about seven inches long, the forepaws slightly smaller. Each foot had five toes tipped with curved claws

"Looks like a bear," I grinned. Surveying the area, I added, "There’s no sign of smaller tracks, so it’s either a large male or a female without cubs."

Gwen patted my back with a smile. "Nice job, hunter. Let’s get some meat."

I opened my mouth to respond but stopped when shouts erupted nearby. A low, unmistakable roar followed.

"Looks like they found the bear for us!" Gwen smirked as we dashed toward the commotion.

We burst into a clearing to find half the men huddled against a cliff wall. Towering over them, a grizzly bear stood on its hind legs, ready to charge. Just as it lunged, I leaped forward, swinging my staff hard against the back of its skull. The bear collapsed with a thud, and Gwen followed up with a swift crossbow bolt to its head.

She pulled out the bolt with a sigh and shot a pointed look at the trembling hunters. "Careful—you wouldn’t want to be bear-chow."

I retrieved her bolt, inspecting the bear. "Definitely a male," I muttered, noting the broad head and muscular frame. "Let’s get him back to camp and skin him."

The men scrambled to retrieve their dropped daggers, then joined us to haul the bear’s massive body back. Once we returned, the camp was bustling—others had brought back a wild boar and were busy skinning it.

"Boar meat, huh? Not bad!" Gwen said, dropping the bear. "You guys might actually know what you're doing."

The next few minutes passed in a flurry of activity. The hunters divided meat, leather, and furs into manageable bundles, wrapping everything in shirts and rope before securing it to Rubert’s back.

I noticed Beans deep in conversation with the men and walked over. He turned, his voice laced with concern. "Scouts found a trail heading west—well-worn, but a bit far."

"Why's that a problem?" I asked, puzzled.

"Such trails often attract thieves and bandits," he explained, shrugging.

"Ah." That made sense. We discussed a plan: Beans and Bluma would lead, while Gwen and I guarded the rear. The children stayed protected in the middle of the group, surrounded by adults.

As we started moving, Gwen fell into step beside me. "Bushy," she said suddenly, her voice low, "when I woke up, I took this off you. Thought you’d want it back."

She reached into her pouch and handed me a small object. Confused, I extended my hand. When she dropped it into my palm, I realized—it was the soul stone. I stared at it in silence before looking at her. She deliberately avoided meeting my gaze.

"I thought I’d lost this," I said quietly, clutching the stone. "Thank you for keeping it safe."

Gwen’s lips twitched into a faint smile, but she kept her eyes ahead. And responded in almost a whisper. "Don’t mention it."

I shifted the soul stone in my hand, feeling its weight. “You know, I think you deserve an explanation about this.”

Gwens eyes looked from me and rested on the soul stone in my hand.

"It’s the main reason I got everyone tangled in this mess."

She then made a swift remark "First of all, this isn’t your fault. You didn’t make the Queen go mad, did you?"

I shook my head.

"And second," she continued, her tone firm but kind, "you didn’t drag me into this, Deta. I’m here because I chose to be." She offered me a faint smile, but her voice was steady.

Her words caught me off guard, easing a burden I hadn’t realized I was carrying. I smiled back. "Thanks, Gwen."

Taking a deep breath, I began. "This is a soul stone. It’s vital to Randeths—it keeps us alive." Gwen nodded slightly, her curiosity clear.

"When a Randeth dies, their soul stone buries itself underground to protect itself. It remains hidden until another Randeth is born, channeling its magic into the new life. Its power is why other species, especially humans, seek them out—to absorb their magic. Even the weakest human could overpower me if they used one against me."

Gwen’s gaze lingered on the golden stone. "So, it’s that powerful?"

I nodded. "Yes, and dangerous. If too much of its magic is drained while it’s above ground, it won’t have enough left to create a new Randeth. I’m hoping Vomete and I can ensure its continuation when I get back—before it’s too late."

"Too late? What do you mean?" Gwen tilted her head, concern etched into her features.

I hesitated. "Without enough magic, there are supposed to be other ways to preserve its purpose, but... I don’t fully understand them yet."

When I glanced at Gwen, her gaze had shifted away. She wasn’t meeting my eyes, which was unlike her.

I opened my mouth to ask if something was wrong when she abruptly shushed me. "Quiet... We’re being followed."

Instantly, I scanned the trees, but I saw no movement. Shifting my focus lower, I watched the bushes.

Gwen’s hand tightened on her sword, and a faint green glow radiated from my hand.

Nothing stirred.

"It might be as Beans said," I whispered. "With a group this size, I doubt anyone would be foolish enough to attack outright."

"Maybe," Gwen murmured. "But I’m not letting my guard down."

We both fell silent. Behind us, faint muttering rippled through the group.

"I can’t believe we’re stuck out here in these woods," a man muttered. "We had gold and silver back at the kingdom!"

Another man joined in. "Better to have died in our homes than in this awful place."

"Exactly," the first man added. "And the king? Weak. No surprise he couldn’t save anyone—"

"Enough, Ronald!" a woman snapped, her sharp voice cutting him off. "We’re lucky to be alive. Don’t make it worse for the rest of us."

The grumbling ceased, but the unease lingered.

I exhaled, ready to whisper to Gwen, when a gravelly voice growled from behind us.

"Hey! It’s the mammals!"

Gwen and I spun around. Emerging from the underbrush was a towering orange Basilisk-folk, gold eyes blazing with hatred.

More followed—seven in total, armed with swords and spears.

"They killed the king lizard! Kill them!" the leader hissed, pointing a jagged blade at us.

"Everyone, run!" I shouted to the group.

Screams filled the air as our companions bolted. Gwen’s sword glowed crimson as she unsheathed it, and I steadied my staff, the surge of adrenaline sharp and electric.

Without a second thought, we charged to meet them.

Four of the Basilisk-folk leaped into the sky, their swords aimed at Gwen. With swift precision, she blocked their attacks. "These jerks are pissed!" she shouted, her voice strained with effort.

As the remaining three advanced, one leaped over me, and the other two aimed their swords at me. I barely dodged both blades, their tips grazing the air on either side of me. But the third one tripped me with its tail, sending me crashing to the ground.

"I noticed!" I grunted, swinging my staff in a wide arc. It collided with the legs of two Basilisk-folk, sending them tumbling, their heads cracking against the ground. The third one quickly jumped back, giving me the chance to regain my footing.

Meanwhile, Gwen pushed back against the four attacking her, her sword glowing with intense heat. She parried their blows effortlessly and, with a swift motion, launched a fiery projectile that struck two of the Basilisk-folk, hurling them into a tree.

The remaining two tried to trap her with a pincer maneuver, but Gwen planted her sword in the ground, using it as leverage to launch herself above them. "These guys are getting on my nerves!" she growled as she evaded a wild swing, then grabbed one of their arms and flung it over the other, sending them both sprawling.

"Same here!" I called, punching my fist into the earth. Tree roots shot up from the ground, wrapping tightly around the Basilisk-folk I was fighting. Despite their desperate thrashing, the roots held them fast.

I glanced toward Gwen, who was facing the two Basilisk-folk who had just recovered from her fiery attack. She was clearly tiring, but her resolve never wavered. One of the monsters swung at her, and she expertly grabbed its sword arm, twisting it and sending the weapon flying. She followed up with a quick slash, stabbing it through the chest, then swiftly decapitating the other.

Breathing heavily, Gwen scanned the area, but before we could speak, Rubert appeared, running down the path.

I raised my hand to stop him. "Hold on, Rubert! What’s going on?"

"Ambush," he panted. "The group’s under attack."

"Hop on, Rubert!" I said to Gwen. She nodded, jumped onto his back, and he galloped off. I followed in my Celeste Elk form, sprinting through the woods as fast as I could.

When we reached the group, we found chaos. Some of the men, women, and children had been wounded, and many were crying. I quickly shifted back to human form and joined Gwen as we hurried to Beans.

"Beans! What happened?" Gwen asked urgently.

"Where were you?" Beans snapped, his face strained with worry.

"We were attacked from behind," I said, cutting him off. "A group of Basilisk-folk tried to ambush us."

Beans growled in frustration, but his anger melted into concern when Bluma walked up, her arms covered in cuts.

"Need… safety," she said calmly, placing a hand on his shoulder. He sighed, nodded, and turned back to the group.

Minutes later, we moved the survivors to a clearing. Beans and I worked quickly, tending to the wounded. Beans took care of minor cuts, while I focused on more severe injuries, offering healing where I could. As I treated a woman’s arm, she couldn’t stop crying.

Assuming it was the pain, I tried to comfort her. "You’re doing great. Almost done here. Can you tell me what happened?"

Through her sobs, she explained that as the group walked, a band of Grey Dwarves and Elves had attacked and taken the children. The rage that bubbled up inside me was almost too much to bear, but I forced a smile.

"Don’t worry," I said softly. "I will get them back."

She clutched my hand, her tears of fear turning to gratitude. "Thank you..."

After bandaging her wounds, I walked over to Gwen, who was standing guard. Her eyes narrowed as I approached, and I noticed the leaves in my hair turning dark red.

"Bushy... What’s going on?" she asked, suspicion in her voice.

I cut her off. "Out. Are you coming?"

Gwen hesitated for only a moment before nodding, quickly finding someone to take her post.

"Wait, Deta! What’s going on?" she called, catching up with me.

I didn’t answer right away. A ball of fire flared in my hand.

"Their kids were stolen by,” I balled my fist, suffocating the fire that had formed in my hand as I spat, “Filth from the Underworld," I replied flatly, cursing them.

As soon as the word came out of my mouth, Gwen shot a surprised glance at me. "You’re not kidding..."

I didn’t respond.

"Okay, let’s go." She steeled herself and followed me into the woods.

We found the place of the attack, searching for any sign of where the kidnappers had gone. After a tense moment, Gwen swung her sword, sending a wave of fire through the trees. A branch fell, and a man in a dark robe with a mask dropped to the ground.

Gwen was on him instantly, her sword pressed to his neck, while I positioned my staff threateningly at his back.

"Tell us... What happened here?" Gwen demanded, her voice low and dangerous.

The man was a member of the Dark Elves and Dwarves, and he admitted they were capturing slaves to sell in the Underworld. He provided us with the location of their camp, and, to our fury, confirmed they had seven children in their custody, with plans to send them to the Underworld by nightfall. We didn’t waste any time. We tied the man up and headed toward their camp.

Upon arrival, we saw the patrol—a mix of Elves and Dwarves—and overheard one of the Elves shouting at the captured children. Gwen’s anger flared, and she was about to charge in when I stopped her, pointing to a cave on the other side of the camp.

"That’s where they’re keeping the train," I whispered.

Gwen nodded, and we slipped toward the cave. There it was—the slave train, smaller than the one in the underworld but heavily secured. We hid as a Gray Dwarf emerged from one of the cars. As he passed, Gwen swiftly struck, decapitating him before dragging the body out of sight.

"We need to remain stealthy," I reminded her, my voice urgent.

"One less to deal with," she muttered, dragging the body behind a bush.

"Let’s sabotage the train. It’ll buy us time."

I nodded, following her inside the cave.

CHAPTER 24                                                                                                                             Hope is fragile

I followed Gwen into the dark cavern, dimly lit by mushrooms glowing faintly on the train tracks from the Underworld. The wood of the train was dark brown, almost gray. We headed straight for the metal bar connecting the two cars. Gwen unsheathed her sword, its edge glowing red-hot.

"Make sure no one sees us, Bushy," she said.

"Got it," I muttered, turning around. Gwen swung her blade, the red glow slicing through the metal, slowly cutting the bar in half.

With a chuckle, she sheathed her sword. "This should annoy them." She turned to me, a grin tugging at her lips. "Bushy, help me search for this thing."

As Gwen moved to the front cart, which was chained shut, I noticed a small box with a flap on top attached to the outside of the car. With my attention divided, Gwen struggled with the chains. I pulled the lock from my pocket and smiled, holding up the key.

She gave me an irritated glance. "What kind of idiots... Whatever. Let's see what's in here." We pried open the door to reveal several crates marked with red Dwarvish labels, reminiscent of those from the first train. A chill crawled up my spine. A rope dangled from the wall outside, passing through a hole, tied to some metal object. Glowing yellow mushrooms scattered across the cavern.

Gwen growled. "Nothing." With a swift motion, she drew her sword, its red glow cutting through the rope. A deep, thunderous roar reverberated from deeper within the cavern, and the rope retreated toward the wall.

"Shoot..."

We whirled around as a group of dark Elves and Dwarves charged us. Gwen smirked. "Well, so much for stealth."

"Yeah, now we have an excuse to kill them for stealing the kids!" I said. She dashed forward, sword blazing. As I ran after her, something cold seized my heart—crying echoed from the other cart.

I bolted toward it, desperate hope mixing with dread. The door flung open, revealing seven children, their skin bruised, their clothes torn and ragged. Chained to the walls of the car, they cowered under the weight of fear.

A gray Dwarf was looming over a little girl, threatening her with a dagger. "Shut your mouth, girl! Or else I’ll cut it off!" His laughter echoed through the car as he lunged.

Before he could strike, I stormed forward, punching him square in the face. "You monster!" I yelled as I sent him flying out of the car.

Fury burned through my veins as I conjured a small ball of fire and hurled it at him. He cried out in pain as it struck him. I transformed into my Elk form, leapt onto him, and tossed him into the air. He crashed against the far wall and crumpled to the ground.

I quickly reverted to my humanoid form and stepped toward the children, offering them a gentle smile to hide the fury welling inside. "It's going to be alright. We’ll get you back to your families, I promise. But first, I need to deal with the ones outside, okay?" They sobbed but nodded, murmuring desperately for their parents.

I met their gazes one last time before sprinting toward the camp. A group of six men was headed towards Gwen. Four drew scimitars while two set their sights on me. Upon seeing my Elk transformation, they hesitated, arming light crossbows. They fired, but the bolts bounced off harmlessly.

I didn’t waste any time. I closed the distance swiftly, impaling one with my horns. Blood spilled as he collapsed. I swung my focus to the other, who gripped his scimitar with trembling hands. Gwen’s fiery blade whistled through the air, cleaving down two attackers in one swift move. But two remained.

"You think a trick will save you?" one snarled, eyes hard with defiance.

"I’ll make it worse for you." Gwen planted her sword into the ground, then spun around, kicking one attacker down.

The scimitar fell from his grasp. Before he could rise, she snatched it and hurled it toward the other. He dodged but stepped too far, letting his own sword fall out of reach. Gwen didn’t miss the opening, running across the gap and tackling him, disarming him in an instant. She snapped his arm with brutal efficiency. He cried out, swinging his weapon uselessly as Gwen used his body against him, hurling him aside. Then, she impaled him with his own scimitar.

The last two assailants still stood, their clothes smoldering from Gwen’s fiery blade. Gwen grinned. "You’re in for a treat."

The kidnapper I engaged couldn’t cut through my stone form. Desperate, he jabbed at my leg and scored a wound. Pain shot up my limb. My vision swirled, but I didn’t falter. My horns met him again, this time hoisting him into the air before slamming him to the ground.

I cast a spell to summon stone armor to shield my leg, grateful for the protection as Gwen fought off the others. "Get out already!" she shouted, still struggling to retrieve her sword from the ground.

Together, we lifted the weapon free. "I know, Bushy! Let's go!"

We ran to the train car, where Gwen quickly began breaking the chains that bound the children. I transformed into my Elk form once more, allowing the children to climb on my back. Gwen used what chains she could to secure them before we rushed out of the cavern.

As we reached the edge of the camp, we were greeted by more enemies, weapons drawn. "Dang it..." Gwen grumbled, scowling. "Bushy, get the kids to safety! I'll hold them off!"

"I—I can't leave you!" I hesitated, my voice tightening. The weight of responsibility for the children on my back grounded me in that moment.

"Gwen…" I felt her presence even as she fought. With a grim sigh, I turned and sprinted into the woods. My legs strained beneath the load. Behind me, I heard the clash of swords and the distant roars of battle.

Beans, Bluma, and the rest of the group were preparing to leave, unaware we’d even gone. "Alright, let's move!" Beans shouted as the group gathered.

Suddenly, a rustling in the bushes caught their attention. The sight of me, transformed into my Celeste Randeth form, drew an awestruck gasp.

"Wait—what—A Randeth... They’re real?" Someone muttered in disbelief.

I turned slightly, revealing the children. Several of the group rushed forward to assist me. Beans and Bluma were at my side in seconds.

"Deta! What were you thinking? Where’s Gwen?" Beans demanded, a flicker of panic in his voice.

"She's still back there, fighting." I lowered my gaze, my heart heavy as the last child slid off my back. Turning to Bluma, I glanced up. "We have to go back…"

"Stay behind. Get the children out of here, now!" Beans urged.

"No, I can’t." I shook my head firmly, and together, we dashed back into the woods, the tension mounting as each step quickened.

"We’re too late..." My words were strained as the acrid scent of smoke reached us. The camp was engulfed in flames.

Bluma and I ran through the wreckage, frantic. "Where are they?" I shouted.

Bluma kicked aside a collapsed beam, revealing the bodies of thugs I’d killed earlier, scattered around a broken cart.

And then we found it: the shattered remnants of our battle—bloodstains on the floor, the door still half open. The train car was a mess.

I scoured the campsite, frustration mounting with each moment that passed. No traces of Gwen. No sign of any of the others. I should have stayed... I should have helped, I thought, my anger bubbling over.

I let out a shaky breath, the weight of it all pressing down on me. Without thinking, I shifted back, the form that had been a shield falling away as sadness tugged at me.

Just then, someone shouted, "Halt! Stay where you are, fiend!"

I spun to face a man in armor holding Gwen’s sword. Fury surged through me. “Where did you get that?” I demanded, my voice thick with rage.

The man scoffed. “That’s none of your concern. You’ll come with me, thug, and face the consequences for your crimes.”

My crimes... The words seared through me like fire, snapping the control I’d been clinging to. “My crimes? The only crime I see here is you holding that sword!”

I reached for my staff, gripping it tightly. “It doesn’t belong to you! You can’t keep it!”

Nearby, I spotted three large stones. With all my strength, I smacked them with my staff which made them fly at the man, one striking him squarely in the face, knocking him to the ground. I moved fast, charging forward, staff raised high above my head. The man reached for Gwen’s sword, still struggling to recover, but when he tried to shield himself, he froze—Bluma stood between us, blocking my strike.

“Deta…” she said, her voice low but firm, signaling me to halt.

I stared at her for a beat, my breath heavy with frustration and confusion, before reluctantly lowering my staff. Slowly, I reached for Gwen’s sword.

“Hey! You can’t—” The guard’s protest was cut short when Bluma swung around, placing her blade against his neck with deadly precision.

“Silence,” she commanded. Her glowing eyes pierced through him, and he fell silent.

It was a struggle for her, the words fighting to come out, but Bluma managed to explain with some effort. "Friend," she said first, then hesitated. "Sword." The new two-word sentences were harder for her, but she made them work, her gaze steady despite the difficulty.

Realizing the danger of his position, the guard spoke reluctantly “I was patrolling when a pillar of fire appeared in the woods. Dark elves and dwarves were fighting. I called for backup. We subdued some of them, including the sword’s owner. She put up a fierce fight… she’s been arrested and is being interrogated.”

I clenched my fists, restraining myself from attacking him. Bluma, calm as ever, asked, “What will happen to her?”

The guard shifted uncomfortably. "If she’s really your friend, her words won’t matter much. But with her aggression... it won’t end well"

Frustration broke free. “You idiot!” I shouted, raising the sword in anger.

Bluma shot me a sharp look before turning back to the guard. “Bring… us.”

He hesitated, no doubt intimidated by Bluma’s presence, but eventually nodded “The town is… this way…”

As we followed, I tried to steady myself. There’s a town nearby… if Gwen’s here, she’s alive… We’ll get her back…

A hand on my shoulder broke my focus. I turned to see Bluma smiling softly at me. “Gwen… return”

I nodded in gratitude. “Thank you, Bluma.”

The guard suddenly announced, “We’re here.”

As we emerged from the trees, the sight of an open prairie greeted us. In the distance, a village lay nestled in the valley, the sounds of children’s laughter carried on the breeze. As we approached the gates, the guards at the entrance greeted us.

The lead guard pointed toward the cells. “Your friend’s in here.”

Bluma’s four wary eyes scanned him.

Before we could reply, a loud crash echoed from within the prison. I laughed, my frustration easing. “I think he’s telling the truth,” I muttered, pushing the door open.

Inside, we found Gwen, shackled to the floor. But before we could move closer, she kicked one of the distracted guards at our feet, sending him sprawling.

“Gwen!” I rushed to her. She turned, anger and confusion written across her face. “What the hell are you two doing here?”

But when her eyes landed on the sword in my hand, a flicker of recognition softened her expression.

I walked over, used the sword to shatter the chains binding her. She wasted no time in reclaiming it. As the guard attempted to question us about our presence in the woods, Gwen rolled her eyes.

“Maybe next time, you could just ask?” she quipped.

I stepped in to explain, “We’re leading survivors from an attack on Sumring.” The guards exchanged looks, clearly surprised.

“If that’s the case,” one of them said, “we’ll help you find them. We’ll bring them here and see how much assistance we can offer.”

Before we could respond, a soft chuckle broke the strained silence, like a jagged knife to the chest. From the shadows of the room, a dark elf emerged, his smirk dripping with venom.

“Well, well, well… You seem to be everywhere, Randeth,” he sneered, his voice a razor-sharp whisper.

Gwen’s body locked up, her muscles stiffening, her knuckles white on the hilt of her sword. Bluma's stance shifted, every fiber of her being taut with readiness, as if preparing for an imminent strike. But for me, it was like the world slowed—my Soul Stone buzzing in my ears as I recognized him.

A cold scowl twisted across my lips. “Adam...” The name barely escaped my throat, but it was a full-on clash of shock and loathing.

A cold ripple swept through the room—the air seemed to grow thicker, charged. A pulse of pure hatred coursed through Gwen and Bluma, and I could see them trembling with every inch of rage they had buried. He shouldn’t be alive… he’s dead…

Without warning, a hairless purple tiger materialized at his side—its piercing yellow eyes glowing, its muscles rippling under its smooth, alien skin. The sight of the beast jolted us all, but it was Adam who held our full attention, his eyes glittering darkly as he scanned us.

“You do remember me...” His voice oozed with mockery, the words meant to dig under our skin.

Without hesitation, Gwen and Bluma both drew their swords in unison, ready to strike. It was as if time stopped—the air between them was taut with the promise of violence. But Adam didn’t flinch. He only laughed, that haunting sound cutting through the tension like a knife through flesh.

“See you around,” he sneered, his smug expression making every second drag like an eternity.

And then, just as quickly as he’d come, he vanished—disappearing into thin air with his tiger, leaving us with the echo of his taunting voice lingering in the room.

The silence that followed was suffocating. Gwen’s fury was palpable—her sword trembling slightly in her hand, her teeth clenched. Bluma’s gaze never wavered, locked on the spot where he had stood as if waiting for him to reappear. I stood frozen, fighting against a flood of emotions, none of them good.

Adam was supposed to be dead. He’d vanished after the massacre—never to be heard from again. The fact that he was here, standing in front of us, made every dark memory come rushing back in a cruel wave.

Gritting my teeth, I muttered under my breath, “Of course he had to be here...”

The guards exchanged glances, their curiosity piqued. “You know him?” one of them asked, his voice steady but edged with suspicion.

Gwen’s View

The moment hung heavy between us, but I didn’t have time to dwell on it as we stepped outside the village and began our way toward the camp. As we walked, I recounted the past—our brief but devastating history with Adam. The guards listened with rapt attention, but I stayed quieter, lost in my own thoughts.
        Beside me, Bluma slowed to match my pace, her gaze softening. “Are you okay?” she asked, her voice gentle, a stark contrast to the storm still raging in my chest.

I nodded quickly. “Yeah, I’m fine. I’ll have Bushy patch up my wounds later,” I said, though the strain in my voice was hard to hide—my usual fire dampened for the moment.        

Bluma’s smile didn’t fade. She didn’t push, but instead asked, “Deta, hurt the guard…”

At first, I just stared, confused. Then, my lips parted in a half-amused, half-disbelieving expression. “Hurt the gura—blah, I mean... guard!”

Bluma chuckled, and I couldn’t help but join in, a light laugh escaping me despite myself. My smile turned mischievous, eyes glinting with hidden meaning. “He was mad. You were hurt,” I said without hesitation.

Bluma’s expression shifted, teasing. “Funny. Bushy wouldn’t hurt anyone who isn’t a threat.”

I rolled my eyes at her, the corners of my mouth lifting into a grin. “Okay, sure. Bushy’s a big softie.”

Bluma’s eyebrow arched, her look playful. “Okay.”

My brow furrowed at her response, something not quite sitting right. But Bluma merely chuckled, letting the moment pass as if nothing was wrong. I shook my head, turning my focus back on the path ahead, my mind buzzing as I processed everything.

When we reached the camp, Beans was waiting with a group of people. Everyone had packed up, but the children—still in their sorry state—brought a sense of melancholy to the camp. Pain, fatigue, and coldness had taken their toll, and complaints and arguments filled the air as people scrambled for shelter. Beans looked visibly stressed, trying to figure out what to do when we emerged from the bushes behind him.

"Hey there, Beans!" I called out.

Beans turned, his face lighting up with a wide smile. "You guys made it back!" he exclaimed, then his gaze shifted to the guards behind us. "Who are these guys?"

The guards looked toward the group of arguing people and spoke up. "We are guards from the nearby village. Are these all the survivors?" Beans nodded, confirming they were.

After a few tense minutes, the group calmed down, and the guards spoke to them. "People of Sumring, we deeply apologize for the struggles you've faced with your homes being destroyed. There is a town not far from here. If you'd like, you may follow us there and stay until you can get back on your feet."

The guard looked at Beans, who smiled. Excitement spread across the group, and Beans called out, "Let's get moving, people!"

Deta’s View

We all followed the guards back to the village. Laughter and excitement replaced the earlier tension, and I glanced at Beans, his bright smile signaling relief as his people would finally have somewhere to live. Bluma walked behind him, wearing a similar smile. Gwen, on the other hand, stood off to the side, gazing into the distance.

I approached her and asked, "Something bothering you, Gwen?"

She looked at me and grinned. "Tch! Never in a million years, Bushy! I'm doing great. We can finally relax for once."

I chuckled. "Relax? I thought you enjoyed the stress of the journey."

Gwen rolled her eyes. "True, but a break every now and then doesn't hurt."

I smiled. "Wow, I never thought you'd want to stop."

Gwen chuckled, then glanced away for a moment. "Oh, Bushy..."

I looked at her, confused and concerned. "Yes?"

Before I could comprehend what was happening, she suddenly turned around, and right in front of me was a horrifying, bloodthirsty snail. I let out a scream, jumped back, and fell to the floor, causing Gwen to burst into laughter.

"Got ya!" she exclaimed, throwing the snail away and helping me up.

"What was that for?" I asked.

She gently punched my shoulder. "You need to relax. You can't get pissed off every time I prank you."

I couldn't think of a suitable response, which made her smile. Then she walked away and joined Beans and Bluma.

"What just happened?" I wondered, shaking my head. "I'll figure it out later." I smiled and followed them to the front.

After a few minutes, we finally escaped the forest and entered the town. The guards led us to a massive farm and knocked on the door of a sturdy, large building. When it opened, we were greeted by a giant Half-Orc wearing modest clothing. He looked at the guards, then at the large group of people, and asked, "What can I do for you?"

The guards explained the situation, and the Half-Orc took us to a large barn, agreeing to let the group stay there temporarily, as it was the only place large enough to accommodate everyone. Gwen, Bluma, Beans, and I stood off to the side as everyone settled down, smiling and chatting.

The Half-Orc approached us and said, "Say, how are the four of you holding up?" He smiled warmly.

I replied, "I think we're doing pretty good. And you?"

His chuckle filled the air. "I'm doing just fine... But may I ask, do I know the four of you?"

We exchanged confused glances, unable to recall who he was. He chuckled again. "Well, if not, my name is Albuquerque, but you can call me Ale."

A smile broke across my face. "Ale! It's you!" I chuckled.

This surprised him, but he quickly caught on. "So, I do know you! Now I remember! You four were those kids who tried to fight the dragon! What happened to the four of you?"

I chuckled, and Gwen spoke up, "Well, the overgrown lizard tossed us into the underworld."

Ale was shocked. "The underworld!? How did you escape?"

Beans interjected, "We managed to get a dark elf to escort us."

Gwen rolled her eyes. "That went well."

Ale looked at her curiously. "How so?"

Gwen recounted how we had been swallowed by a giant worm but found a way to escape, eventually reaching the surface. Ale was genuinely surprised.

"I see. So where did you go? Unless you crossed the sea, you couldn't have come straight here."

I shook my head. "No, actually, we went back to the kingdom and managed to lure the dragon into the underworld. But I was out of commission for about a month."

Ale's eyes narrowed as he noticed my now-flesh arm. "And other sacrifices, it looks like?"

I glanced at my hand and sighed. "Yeah, after I woke up, Sumring was invaded by its Queen. She transformed into some sort of monster and tried to kill everyone."

We fell into silence for a moment, then Ale placed his hand on my shoulder. "You tried your best. You're a good chieftain."

I smiled at him. "Thanks."

Beans then realized Rinn hadn't shown up yet and asked, "Deta, what happened to Rinn?"

I turned to Beans, and Gwen and Bluma slowly realized the same, their expressions questioning. I sighed and looked away.

"He stayed behind... to distract the Queen."

Beans and Bluma fell silent, their eyes meeting, and Gwen walked off. Ale pondered for a moment.

"Deta, right?" He looked at me and lowered himself to my eye level. "Why don't you four stay with me at my place for a while? Just until we can get these people moving in the right direction, and give you all some time to process."

I smiled gratefully. "Thank you, Ale. I think that would help."

CHAPTER 25                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  Yearning for Home

In the days that followed, we did all we could to help the town. Bluma and Gwen, known for their exceptional sword skills, were highly respected and often trained with the guards to keep themselves sharp. They even convinced me to join in on the sparring from time to time.

Beans and I, on the other hand, focused on gathering materials and helping to build or repair homes for the refugees. It was hard work, but seeing the smiles on their faces as they settled into their new homes made it all worth it. We weren’t alone in this endeavor; the townspeople came together to assist in any way they could. It was a beautiful thing to witness.

Over the course of several weeks, we managed to construct homes for some refugees, getting to know those who lived in the town: humans, Half-Elves, and even some dwarves. When we took a break, we were treated to drinks, sweets, and fruit. The refugees who decided to stay in the town even offered to help Ale on his farm, tending to the animals and fields.

As time went by, travelers and merchants passing through the town offered to take some refugees with them to the next town over. Out of the one hundred or so people we started with, only around twenty-five to fifty remained. It was heartwarming to see them find new homes and start new lives.

Many of the mothers who had lost their husbands found new people to love and help raise their children, while the fathers who had lost their wives found comfort and support from their new communities. It was a reminder that, even in the darkest times, there is always hope.

The rebuilding process wasn’t without challenges. There were times when we felt overwhelmed and exhausted, but we never lost sight of our goal. We knew that we were doing something important, and that kept us going.

About five months later, everyone had found a place to live, and even we had our own homes, which had been built as a surprise. It was around sunset when I sat on the roof of my house, constructed by the townspeople. I was wearing new clothes given to me by some refugees who had joined others in making clothing for everyone. The outfit was a light red tunic with brown trimming, paired with loose brown pants, and a belt embossed with leaves.

As the summer heat began to die down I stared into the horizon,  I sighed, and a familiar voice interrupted my thoughts. "Reminiscing about something, Leaf-Head?" It was Gwen, who had joined me on the roof with a dried piece of meat, chewing on it.

"Yeah, something like that," I replied with a chuckle.

“Well, what is it?” Gwen inquired.

I hesitated before answering. “I haven’t seen my mother for a long time now…”

Gwen swallowed and turned to me. "That's right, you do have someone waiting for you. She's probably worried about you."

I nodded. “She probably is…”

There was a moment of silence before Gwen spoke up. "You know, if you want to see her, you should go."

I turned to Gwen and asked, "Did you mean that?"

She nodded, her eyes firm. "Yeah. You've been helping everyone out here. Now that the town's built, and the refugees have a place to live, you could go home. You could also give her the soul stone."

I pulled out the soul stone, which was wrapped in a thin string around my neck. The stone glowed gold in the sunlight, and I could feel the magic within, ready to bring life to something—or someone.

“That’s true,” Gwen continued, swallowing another piece of meat. “Well, then you should go. It’s not hard to decide. Say your farewells to the people, and we’ll be off.”

I turned to her, raising an eyebrow. "We?"

"Yeah, we," she said, pointing to Beans and Bluma. "Beans and Bluma are good friends, but they came along to protect their kingdom. Now that the refugees are safe, they’ve been helping out here, but they probably won’t be able to come."

Gwen looked over at Beans and Bluma, who were chatting to each other, both wearing their repaired armor. I started to speak, "And I believe that we are now--" but then the roof tiles gave out beneath Gwen, and she began to fall. I quickly reached out with my thorn whip and caught her, gently guiding her down to the ground.

"Nice save," Gwen said, looking up at me.

"Now we’re finally even." I chuckled, thinking, Well, at least I didn’t jinx myself. But then the roof tiles beneath me cracked. "Crap," I muttered as they gave way, and I began to fall. I landed on top of Gwen with a thud, and she groaned, "Ow." I scrambled off, apologizing. "Sorry, Gwen!"

Bluma and Beans saw what happened and ran over. "Are you two okay?" Beans asked.

Gwen nodded. "Yep, just great." She looked at me with a smile. "You--"

"I owe you," I finished for her with a smile.

Beans and Bluma exchanged smiles as I told them about my plans to go home. "So, what were you two talking about?" Beans asked. Before I could respond, Gwen quickly interjected that I was thinking of leaving.

Beans and Bluma were surprised. "Oh, that's right, you have someone waiting for you, don't you?" Beans said with a smile.

I nodded, and Bluma patted my shoulder. "Go see them."

Beans agreed. "I agree. You should go see them, Deta."

I smiled at them and thanked them, asking if they could handle things while I was gone. Beans laughed and said, "Oh, don’t worry. It’s not like a dragon’s going to show up anytime soon." We all chuckled, agreeing that we’d think about things more in the morning.

After saying goodnight, we each entered our respective rooms. In mine, I looked around at the barren space, with only a dresser, a bed, and a window on the wall. But I smiled as I gazed at my new ironwood staff with a green gem at its top, a gift from one of the carpenters in town. As I lay down on my bed, I stared at the ceiling and slowly drifted off to sleep as the sun set, and the darkness of night took over the room.

My mind was trapped in a dream. I saw my home, and there was Vomete in front of me, smiling. "Deta, I'm so glad you're safe," she said, patting my back before her fingers gently brushed the Soul Stone around my neck. "Notari, my old friend…"

I looked down at the Stone. "You knew them?"

Vomete gave a weak smile, shaking her head. "Not the Randeth…" Her gaze shifted back to me, the gold in her eyes shimmering. "So, how's your new family?"

At those words, the world around us seemed to darken, shadows creeping in. I forced a smile, awkwardly. "What family?"

Suddenly, her form began to shift, her body crumbling and warping into something unrecognizable, a chaotic mass of shapes and darkness. "The one you replaced me with... You abandoned me!" Her voice twisted with the weight of accusation.

I took a step back, panic rising. "Vomete! No!" But before I could react, shadowy hands reached out from the darkness, grabbing my arms and legs, pulling me away. "Vomete! Save me!" I screamed, struggling against their grip.

But I was dragged deeper into the dark, Vomete's voice echoing faintly as she disintegrated. "You left me…" she whispered, her words fading as I was pulled into the darkness with great speed. I screamed out for her once more, tears flooding my eyes, but then I turned—and saw a giant red eye made of fire,glaring me down as I came closer to it.

I screamed as I fell in, only to jolt awake, gasping for air. I blinked, disoriented, my Soul Stone vibrating in my chest, and realized where I was. I awoke with a gasp, the remnants of the nightmare still clinging to me. The sun was shining through my window as it began to rise, its warm rays spreading across the room, slowly pulling me from the depths of the dream. I stretched, trying to shake off the lingering fear, and left my room.

As I passed by Beans and Bluma’s door, I noticed it was left open. With a quick glance down the hallway, I closed it gently and headed downstairs. In the kitchen, I found Beans munching on an apple and Bluma nibbling a piece of bread.

"Oh, hey Deta! Sleep well?" Beans asked with his mouth full.

I smiled weakly and sat down next to the window, soaking in the warm sunlight.

Beans chuckled, noticing something. "It must have been a good sleep. The leaves on your head are pretty dark green."

Before I could respond, Gwen walked down the stairs, looking disheveled, and grabbed a piece of bread.

Beans grinned, poking fun. "Seems the bed put a spell on you."

Gwen groaned, grabbing the bread. "They're too soft."

I couldn’t help but chuckle and, trying to shake off the last echoes of my nightmare, announced, "I'm going for a walk."

Heading into the woods, I smiled as the birds chirped and the sounds of nature began to wake with the day. As I walked, I ran into two village hunters. I greeted them and asked if they had any luck with their bows.

They showed me some quail they had caught. "These birds are everywhere this time of year," one of them said. "They taste pretty good, dried or roasted over the fire."

I smiled. "Well, you should enjoy it. You worked hard for it."

The men seemed proud of that, exchanging glances. "We certainly will!" one said, giving a hearty nod. "Now we best be going, or we'll miss out on some more before it gets too late in the day."

The other man chuckled. "Or our wives will have our heads." They both laughed, waved, and continued on their way.

I chuckled to myself and kept walking, the cool air of the woods surrounding me. As I moved deeper into the trees, I couldn't help but think of my home forest, with its towering oaks and birches, the small streams winding through the underbrush, and the misty mornings that always held a sense of peace.

"Things were so different back then," I muttered under my breath, my thoughts drifting back to everything that had happened over the past few months. "I left home expecting to help a little girl, and got dragged into fighting a dragon, only to fall into the underworld, then come back to save the people of a fallen kingdom?"

I smiled up at the sky, shaking my head lightly. "Almost sounds like some sort of fairytale," I said, speaking to no one but the wind. "Vomete is going to love to hear this." I chuckled softly, imagining her reaction.

As I walked deeper into the woods, my thoughts began to drift. I started to think about my home, my mother, and my friends. It had been a few months now, and I could feel a pull in my heart, a desire to return. A year had now passed since I last saw my mother, and the ache of missing her grew with each passing day.

But then my thoughts shifted to Gwen, Bluma, and Beans. We had been through so much together already, and I knew that, no matter where I went, we would continue to support each other. Still, I wondered—was I really ready to leave them behind and return to my old life? The thought of walking away from them felt heavier than I expected.

Lost in my thoughts, I wandered deeper into the woods and suddenly found myself in a clearing. The sun had risen high enough for its light to filter through the trees, casting a golden glow that made the whole area feel almost magical. The grass was still damp with dew, and small droplets of water sparkled in the sunlight. I paused, taking it all in.

The quiet beauty of the place filled me with peace. I took a deep breath of the cool, crisp air, feeling the warmth of the sun on my skin. Rabbits hopped past, squirrels darted from tree to tree, and even a family of foxes played in the distance. The woods were teeming with life, and it was all so perfect, so alive.

"The woods are always so... wonderful..." I whispered to myself, the memories rushing back of the time we were trapped in the Underworld. I remembered our small camp, the struggle to work together and find a way back to the surface.

"But it would be better if I had them with me..." I thought, feeling the conflict grow within me. Should I stay with them? The weight of that decision felt heavy in my chest, and yet, Vomete was waiting for me, too.

As I walked through the forest, the sound of a twig snapping behind me caught my attention. I turned around and saw a doe with her fawn, both moving gracefully through the underbrush. With a warm smile, I spoke softly, "Hey there, ma'am, is there something I can help you with?"

The doe paused, chuckling lightly. "Not at all, Randeth. We were just taking our morning stroll."

Realizing my mistake, I let out a soft laugh. "Oh I see, sorry for disrupting you."

"Don’t worry about it," she replied, her voice gentle. "Now, you should hurry back. I’m sure your friends are waiting for you."

With a nod, I watched her and her fawn disappear into the trees, a smile lingering on my face as I continued my walk.

When I returned to the village, I spotted Beans and Bluma leaving their house for their patrol. I waved and called out, "Hey, guys!" They turned, their smiles as bright as ever.

"Hey, Deta! What's up?" Beans asked.

I walked over, glancing toward their gear. "Are you guys off to patrol?"

Bluma gave a slight shrug. "Perhaps," she said in her usual calm tone.

Beans chuckled, then added, "Gwen’s out in the field. Maybe you should go see what she’s up to?"

I grinned. "Sounds like a plan!"

Heading over to the field, I saw Gwen and Ale talking in the distance. As I got closer, Ale waved with a big smile, and Gwen turned around in my direction.

"Hey, guys!" I greeted them. "What were you talking about?"

Ale chuckled before responding. "Gwen and I were discussing the idea of building a sparring pit in this open part of the field. It's not really being used for anything, and a sparring tournament could help lift everyone’s spirits and give them something to look forward to in the coming year."

"That sounds like a great idea!" I smiled, genuinely impressed.

Gwen gazed out into the field thoughtfully. "Yes, it does. But Bushy..." She turned to me with a playful grin. "How will we know it’s good for sparring?”

I chuckled, knowing exactly what she meant by that. Gwen and I stepped out into the open field, each of us taking a moment to stretch and warm up. I watched her grip her sword tightly, her gaze focused, determination clear in her eyes.

"You ready?" she asked, her voice steady.

I nodded, gripping my staff and getting into position. "Let's go."

We circled each other, the quiet hum of the morning air filling the space between us. Gwen took the lead with a series of quick strikes, each one coming fast and precise. I blocked them with my staff, moving quickly to keep up. When I saw an opening, I swung at her, but she nimbly dodged and countered with a slash that grazed my shoulder.

"Nice move," I said, smiling as I rubbed my shoulder. "But you're not getting past me that easily."

She smirked, twirling her sword in one hand. "We'll see about that."

Then she lunged forward again, her strikes coming faster, more intense. I blocked and parried with everything I had, but Gwen’s strength and speed were almost overwhelming. I found myself on the defensive, focusing all my energy just to keep from being overwhelmed.

Just when I thought I couldn't hold on much longer, I spotted an opening. In one swift motion, I swung my staff with all my strength. The staff connected with the side of Gwen's sword, sending it flying from her hand and skidding across the grass.

Gwen stumbled back, surprised by the force of the blow. I stepped forward, staff poised and ready.

"Looks like I won this round," I said, grinning, my heart racing.

But before I could land the finishing blow, Gwen recovered quickly, diving forward and tackling me to the ground. We both hit the grass with a thud, and for a moment, we wrestled, each of us trying to gain the upper hand. But Gwen proved to be the stronger of the two, her knee pressing into my chest as she pinned me to the ground.

"I don't think so," she said, her grin full of mischief.

I chuckled, panting for breath. "Okay, okay, you win."

We both stood up, brushing ourselves off with matching grins.

"That was a good one," Gwen said, retrieving her sword from where it had fallen. "But don't get too comfortable. I'm not going easy on you."

"I wouldn't have it any other way," I replied, twirling my staff in my hand, my heart still racing.

We resumed our fighting stances, both of us prepared for the next round. As we circled each other, I couldn't help but admire Gwen's skill. Even though I’d lost this round, it was clear she was the better fighter. I had much to learn from her.

This time, I focused more intently, trying to anticipate her moves and finding new ways to block and counter. Slowly, I started to get into the rhythm of the fight, managing to hold my ground against her flurry of strikes.

But as the minutes passed, I could tell Gwen was becoming more aggressive. She was determined to win this round, and her attacks were coming faster and harder. I struggled to keep up with her relentless assault, my muscles growing tired as she pressed on.

I gritted my teeth, trying to stay focused, but then came a moment where I misjudged her movement. She swung her sword at me again, and this time I was too slow to block. The blade caught me on the shoulder, and I winced as a sharp pain shot through my body.

"Ah!" I grunted, stepping back, my vision blurring for a moment from the intensity of the strike.

Gwen lowered her sword slightly, her eyes softening with concern. "You okay?"

I nodded, though I was clearly winded. "Yeah, just a little slow on that one. But I’m not out yet."

I stumbled backward, clutching my shoulder as Gwen advanced, a determined look in her eyes. But just as she was about to land the finishing blow, I took a deep breath and, with everything I had left, lunged forward with my staff.

The sudden movement caught her off guard. She stumbled back, her eyes widening in surprise. I didn't hesitate. Seizing the moment, I swung my staff with all my might, striking her square in the stomach and knocking the wind out of her.

Gwen doubled over, gasping for breath, as I stood over her, panting. We both paused for a moment, catching our breath, the peacefulness of the open field wrapping around us like a warm embrace. The sun’s golden light cast long shadows across the grass, a calm contrast to the intensity of our sparring.

"Let's do it again," Gwen said suddenly, her fierce determination returning to her eyes.

I grinned, the excitement of the fight still coursing through me. "You are on." I quickly healed the wound on my shoulder, ready to go again.

This time, we both charged forward without hesitation. The intensity of our fight grew, with each of us switching between offense and defense. My body was starting to ache, but I pushed through it, focusing on landing another strike. Gwen, too, seemed to be feeling the strain, but she kept up her relentless pace.

I saw an opening and charged, but Gwen, faster than I anticipated, sidestepped and drove her knee into my gut. The force of the blow knocked me backward, and I stumbled, winded.

"You okay?" she asked, a note of concern in her voice.

I nodded, gasping for breath. "Yeah, I'm good."

We continued to spar, but my movements were starting to slow, and I could feel the fatigue setting in. Gwen’s attacks were still sharp, but her movements, too, were becoming less precise as she wore herself out.

After a few more exchanges, it became clear that I wasn’t going to be able to keep up much longer. Finally, Gwen called a halt to the fight, stepping back and raising her hands.

"You did well," she said, giving me a respectful nod. "But you need to work on your endurance."

I nodded, my chest heaving as I tried to catch my breath. Even though I’d lost, a sense of pride filled me. I had lasted longer than I thought I would.

"Nice job, you two," Ale's voice came from behind us. We turned to see him walking toward us, a smile on his face. "That was quite the spar. But you should head home now. It's getting late, and it takes time to get back."

I smiled at Ale. "Fair point. It was great to see you, Ale!" He rolled his eyes playfully but smiled back.

"Ya, ya, now get!" he chuckled, waving us off.

As Gwen and I walked back, we chatted easily, the tension from the sparring session fading. But then Gwen asked, "Have you decided yet?"

I didn’t answer immediately, my thoughts still caught in the whirlwind of my decision. "Not really, no."

Gwen sighed, her voice taking on a hint of exasperation. "Of course. You know you have a problem."

I glanced at her, confused. "A problem?"

"Yes," she said, her tone soft but firm, placing a hand on my shoulder. "It's that you're thinking too hard. Just do what you need to do and stop thinking about it."

Her words were simple, but they struck me with surprising clarity. "You can't keep living in this state of indecision," she continued. "You need to make a choice and stick with it."

I nodded, realizing what she was talking about. "I know, I just don't know which choice is the right one."

Gwen stopped walking and turned to face me, her expression serious. "Bushy, there is no right or wrong choice. It's about what you want, what you need, and what will make you happy. You need to trust yourself and make a decision that feels right for you."

I looked at her, slightly surprised by her giving advice and not being blunt "But what if I make the wrong choice? What if I regret it?"

Gwen sighed and gave a soft reassuring smile. "If you make a decision that doesn't turn out the way you wanted, it's not the end of the world. You can always change your mind and try something else. The important thing is that you take action and move forward."

I nodded, taking in her words. "You're right. I need to stop second-guessing myself and take a leap of faith."

Gwen squeezed my shoulder. "Exactly."

I smiled, feeling lighter, like something had been lifted from my chest. "Thank you, Gwen. I needed to hear that."

She grinned, teasing, "Good, because never again! Can't believe you make me do the support role. Yuck!" We both laughed as we walked toward the house.

Inside, Beans and Bluma were slouched in chairs, looking exhausted. Gwen smirked at them. "Tired much?"

Beans rolled his eyes, unamused. "Haha, very funny."

Gwen chuckled. "Alright. I'm off to bed. Later." She made her way up the stairs.

"She's going to bed early," I remarked, but neither Beans nor Bluma seemed to hear. I shrugged and added, "And I think that's not a bad idea for the two of you."

That made them smile, and they nodded in agreement before heading upstairs.

I walked over to the chair by the window, sinking into it as I looked out at the fading sunlight. A cool evening breeze gently swept through the room, and I let out a quiet sigh. Should I stay? Or go…?

The next morning, when I woke up, I felt a sense of clarity I hadn’t had before. It was time to pack my bags and head back home. The decision had been gnawing at me for days, but with Gwen’s words in my heart, I knew I had to go back to Vomete and make sure she was okay, at the very least.

I gathered my clothes and folded them carefully, packing only the essentials. As I worked, memories of my time with Gwen and the others flowed through me— the laughter, the adventures, the struggles, and the moments of pure joy. They had all become treasured pieces of my life. Once I finished and had my new bag packed, everything felt right. It was time.

I stepped out of my room, my heart heavy with the thought of telling them, but I hadn’t expected to find the three of them already gathered at the bottom of the stairs, each with a bag of their own.

“Guys?” I asked, surprised.

Beans was the first to speak, grinning wide. “What? Think we were gonna let you have all the fun out there?”

Gwen followed with a smirk, her eyes glinting with mischief. “You took too long deciding, now you’re stuck with us, Leaf-head.” She shot me a grin.

A warm feeling spread through me, and I couldn’t help but smile at my friends. We hadn’t needed any words beyond that; we were in this together. We made our farewells and then stepped outside, heading toward the path that would lead us back home. Despite the uncertainty of what lay ahead, there was a sense of peace in knowing that I wasn’t walking that path alone.

CHAPTER 26                                                                                                                                                                                                                     An Empty Journey

As we began to leave town, a voice called out behind us. "Hey! Wait up!"

We stopped and turned to see a Dwarven man running toward us, holding something in his hands. Beans stepped forward, meeting him halfway.

"Is something wrong?" he asked.

The two of them began speaking in Dwarvish, their conversation unfolding in quick exchanges. As they spoke, Beans' face shifted through a range of emotions—surprise, curiosity, and something I couldn't quite place. Finally, the Dwarven man gave a respectful salute, said something we assumed was a farewell, then turned and strode back toward town.

When Beans faced us again, he was met with expectant stares. Gwen crossed her arms, one brow raised. "Care to let us in?"

He smiled, holding up the item the Dwarf had given him—a map. "He gave us this," he explained. "A map of this region. It'll help us get back to the kingdom faster."

Gwen's expression flickered with something unreadable before settling into mild surprise. "Back to the kingdom? We're actually going?"

I nodded. "The portal I used to get here is just a day's walk away."

She took that in with a slow nod, then fell into step beside us as we resumed our journey. Beans took the lead, eyes flicking between the map and the path ahead.
