As we re-entered the woods, a smile tugged at my lips. There was something so familiar about the sight of Beans scrutinizing a map while the dim light filtered through the trees.

Gwen caught my expression and tilted her head. "What's funny?"

I chuckled. "It all feels like déjà vu. Like when we were in the Underworld."

Recognition flashed across her face, and she grinned. "Yeah, I remember that. It was quite a ride."

We pressed on, weaving through towering trees and stepping over tangled roots. The forest was peaceful, filled with the soft rustle of leaves and the distant chirping of birds. Then, without warning, a deafening roar shattered the quiet.

We froze. My pulse pounded in my ears as the ground trembled beneath us. From the underbrush, two massive creatures emerged—bears, but not like any I had ever seen. Their bodies were covered in sleek feathers, and as they reared up, enormous wings unfurled, spanning over twenty feet wide.

Weapons drawn, we braced ourselves as the beasts circled, their growls vibrating through the air. For a tense moment, neither side moved. Gwen broke the silence, her gaze locked on the feathered bears.

"What do you think they want?" she asked.

I hesitated. "They're looking for their next meal."

A mischievous glint flashed in her eyes. "Well, let's not keep them waiting then!"

Bluma and Beans shifted into more aggressive stances as Gwen and I stepped forward, weapons ready. With a shared battle cry, we launched into the fight, each pair taking on one of the winged beasts.

The first bear lunged at us, a massive paw swiping toward my side. I countered with a swift strike of my staff, knocking its limb downward. The force of the impact sent its own claws raking into its leg, tripping it to the ground. Gwen seized the opening, slashing down with her sword, but the bear flared its wings and beat them with a powerful gust. The blast hurled us backward, sending me tumbling across the dirt.

With a snarl, the creature reared onto its hind legs and bellowed, "I'm going to enjoy killing you!"

I met its glare without flinching. "I'm not dying today!"

Before it could strike again, I shifted into my Celeste elk form, surging forward with antlers lowered.

Meanwhile, Bluma and Beans battled the other bear. As it swiped at Bluma, she ducked and hoisted Beans onto its back. He scrambled up to the base of its wings, dark energy coiling around his hands. The feathers beneath his grip blackened, rotting away as decay spread through the creature’s flesh.

The bear roared and reared onto its hind legs, trying to shake him off. Beans leaped free just in time, landing in a crouch.

"Bluma!" he shouted.

She was already moving. Sprinting forward, she drove her glowing white sword deep into the bear’s side. The beast howled in agony, its massive form shuddering under the force of the strike.

The Flying Bear flared its wings, forcing Bluma to dodge, but in doing so, she left Beans exposed. A powerful wing smacked into him, sending him stumbling backward. Before he could recover, the bear spun and struck him with a heavy paw, launching him off his feet. He hit the ground hard, skidding several feet away.

Bluma tightened her grip on her sword as the bear turned its attention to her, roaring loud enough to shake the trees. She held her ground, eyes locked onto the beast, ready for its next move.

I charged, but the bear let out a deafening roar and caught my antlers, using them as leverage to throw me off balance. Its jaws clamped around my neck, crushing down with terrifying force before it hurled me to the ground. Pain exploded through me as cracks splintered across my stone-like skin. The pressure was too much—I reverted to my natural form, clutching my neck in agony.

"Bushy, get up!" Gwen stood in front of me, sword drawn. Above her, the bear spread its wings and lifted off the ground. "Get up now!" she snapped.

I forced myself upright just as the beast dove toward us. Gripping my staff, I swung with all my strength, striking it square in the face. The impact sent it careening off course—straight into the other bear. The two collided midair and crashed to the ground in a tangled heap of wings and limbs.

Bluma wasted no time, sprinting toward Beans and hauling him up. Without hesitation, we followed her as she bolted northward.

"These things fly?!" Gwen shouted between breaths.

"Yes, and they're fast!" I panted.

The bears roared behind us, their massive forms lifting into the air once more. Shadows passed over us as they soared above the treetops, closing the distance at an alarming speed.

"Very fast!" I called out.

The Flying Bears caught up to us in no time, forcing Gwen to spin around and draw her glowing red sword. With a fierce swing, she sent a slash of fire hurtling toward them. The flames struck, momentarily blinding the beasts.

As they regained their sight, their heads whipped around in confusion. Growling and grunting to each other, they searched for us. One took off into the sky, while the other, its wings scorched and wounded, landed heavily on the ground. It let out a low rumble, sniffing the air, trying to catch our scent.

Bluma and Beans had taken refuge in the branches of a nearby tree, while Gwen and I crouched low behind the underbrush. The bear let out a guttural roar as it locked onto our scent and went still.

Gwen caught my eye from her hiding spot and signaled. I gave a small nod, then reached for a decent-sized rock. With careful aim, I tossed it toward a bush a little ahead of us.

The bear’s head snapped toward the rustling sound. It reared onto its hind legs and came crashing down, trampling the bush beneath its massive weight. When it found nothing there, it spun back around—only to see Gwen and me standing behind it, weapons drawn.

It let out a furious roar and charged.

Before it could reach us, Bluma and Beans dropped from the tree, plunging their weapons deep into its back and wing. The bear howled in agony, staggering under the sudden assault. Blood soaked its feathers, its movements growing sluggish.

Bluma and Beans leapt clear just as Gwen slashed her sword through the air. Another wave of fire struck the bear, igniting its feathers and forcing it into a panicked frenzy. It swung wildly, blinded by pain, but I seized the opening. With a sharp strike of my staff, I slammed its head downward, forcing it to crash onto the ground. A second blow sent it hurtling into a tree.

Gwen and Bluma didn’t hesitate. They lunged forward, driving their swords deep into its side. The bear let out one final, shuddering growl before collapsing, motionless.

After a brief moment of rest, we heard the other bear’s roar in the distance, drawing nearer. We quickly sprinted northward, eventually spotting a small cavern covered in moss. It was just big enough for us to fit, but far too small for the Flying Bear to enter.

“Get in here!” Beans called out, slipping inside first. He’d spotted the cavern before we did. Gwen and I had already passed it, so we had to quickly backtrack. Bluma was next, slipping inside just as the Flying Bear landed and charged toward us with terrifying speed.

“Crap, crap, crap!” Gwen muttered, darting inside. I hesitated, turning to look back as the bear was hot on my heels.

“Bushy!” Gwen called out, glancing behind her as the bear closed in on me.

The bear was much faster than I was. It quickly caught up, and in a panic, I veered behind a tree. The bear, too large to make the sharp turn, slowed for a moment. But that brief respite wasn’t enough—its powerful stride soon closed the distance again.

Frick! I’m gonna die! What should I do? I thought, my mind racing as the bear roared, “Stop running! It won’t save you!”

Then, an idea hit me. I made a sharp turn, transformed into my Celestial Elk form, and charged toward the cave entrance. The bear cursed, its pursuit faltering as I gained ground. My heart pounded as I approached the entrance, my hooves thundering on the ground.

Once I reached the cave, I shifted back to my natural form, sliding into the crevice just in time to avoid the bear’s grasp.

As I ventured deeper into the cavern, it opened into a large chamber, and I stumbled, falling to the ground.

“Bushy!” Gwen and the others rushed over, helping me up.

“I’m okay. I made it...” I said, catching my breath.

Beans grinned. “Good job, Deta, but you need to rest before you pass out.”

They eased me against the cave wall, and Gwen settled beside me. “Yeah, that’s probably a good idea,” I chuckled, relieved.

Bluma smiled but turned toward the entrance as the Flying-Bear roared once more. “How long?” she asked.

Beans sighed. “Maybe an hour or so before it leaves.”

I shook my head. “No, they hold grudges. We’ll have to wait until it falls asleep and try to sneak out then.”

Gwen groaned. “Of course. Well, we might as well rest.”

We all nodded in agreement and took our seats. Beans, however, began rummaging through his pack.

“Deta, could you use your magic to make some branches or something grow here?” he asked.

Smiling, I raised my hand, coaxing a cluster of roots from the ground until they reached about five feet high.

“What are you doing?” I asked, curious.

“Collecting fuel,” he explained. “If we’re stuck here overnight, we might need a fire to stay warm.”

“Let me help,” I offered, attempting to stand, but Gwen quickly pulled me back down.

“No, you’re staying right here until it’s time to leave,” she said firmly.

I frowned. “Why?”

We went back and forth for a moment before she finally asked, “Did you fix your neck?”

The question caught me off guard, but I admitted it would take a few hours.

She crossed her arms. “And you made it worse by running around.”

I sighed, knowing she was right, and slumped back against the wall in reluctant defeat.

As Beans continued gathering roots, I caught Bluma watching us, a small smile playing on her lips.

Hours passed, and night finally fell. Beans, the smallest among us, had the easiest time squeezing through the entrance. He slipped outside, returning moments later with a silent signal— the Flying-Bear was asleep.

One by one, we crept out, Bluma leading the way, followed by Gwen, and then me. The others waited patiently as I struggled to squeeze through, our height difference making it a tight fit.

Once we were all out, we quietly slipped away, careful not to wake the sleeping bear. Only when we had put a good distance between ourselves and the cave did we finally relax, smiles spreading across our faces.

“Well, that was a close one,” I chuckled.

Gwen laughed. “Pshh, please. We had him right where we wanted him. You were the one in trouble!”

Beans grinned. “Oh yeah, you were the only one struggling.”

We stifled our laughter as we joked about the danger we had just escaped. A cool breeze brushed against our faces, and I felt my body begin to relax, my eyelids growing heavy. Gwen stretched with a yawn, and Beans, mid-yawn himself, attempted to speak.

“We… gotta… stay awake,” he mumbled before shaking his head with a laugh. “We’re not out of danger yet.”

Gwen smirked. “Ten copper says you’re the first to fall asleep, Bushy.”

I grinned. “Fifteen says it’s Beans.”

Beans turned, looking appalled. “Now hold on a minute—”

We burst into laughter and continued our journey, doing our best to fight off exhaustion.

As the night wore on, we shared stories and jokes to keep ourselves entertained, but the struggle to stay awake became harder with every passing moment. The cool breeze, the rhythmic chirping of crickets, and the gentle murmur of a nearby stream worked against us, lulling us toward sleep.

Eventually, we couldn’t resist any longer. Telling ourselves it was only a short break, we settled against the trees—and before we knew it, sleep took us.

The warmth of the morning sun stirred me first. Blinking my eyes open, I found Beans and Bluma leaning against each other, sound asleep. Gwen, however, had somehow ended up collapsed on my lap.

It took a moment for my groggy brain to register what I was seeing. And when it did, I froze.

If I wake her up, would she punch me? …Probably.

Before I could decide, Gwen shifted, stirring from sleep. Panicking, I squeezed my eyes shut, hoping she’d think I was still asleep.

I felt her move—rubbing her eyes, stretching—and then, her hand brushed against my face before quickly retreating. There was a brief pause, followed by the faint swish of movement. I could only guess that she was waving a hand in front of my face, testing if I’d react.

A moment later, I heard her rummaging through her bag. Then something soft draped over me. I listened as her footsteps retreated into the woods. When I finally dared to peek, I saw a blanket covering me.

A small smile crept onto my face. The fabric was warm, soft… and faintly smelled like Gwen.

…that… is as weird as it sounded.

I found myself drifting back to sleep, only to be jolted awake when the blanket was suddenly yanked off me.

I jumped with a small yelp, my heart racing. Standing in front of me, grinning, was Gwen.

“Thought you were dead, Bushy. You’re usually one of the first to wake up,” she teased as she folded the blanket.

Blinking the sleep from my eyes, I realized I was now the last one up—a stark contrast from earlier. Beans and Bluma were already on their feet, studying the map and discussing our next move.

I chuckled. “Guess I was just really tired.” Stretching, I took a deep breath—only to pause as an unfamiliar scent reached me.

“…Do you guys smell that?” I asked, frowning.

Beans and Bluma looked up and sniffed the air.

“Oh,” Beans said, his expression shifting. “There’s a fire in the distance.” He stepped aside, pushing back the branches of a bush to reveal a clearing. Sure enough, a plume of smoke rose into the sky.

“Bluma and I figured out a way around it,” he added. “That was the direction we were heading, but we should still reach the kingdom by the end of the day.”

Although the fire made me uneasy, I smiled and nodded. “Alright, well, we should get moving. Don’t want that bear catching up to us.”

Beans chuckled. “Good point.”

Bluma smiled. “Let’s go.”

As we continued walking along the edge of the forest and the open field, we encountered minimal problems. Still, I couldn’t shake the uneasy feeling gnawing at me about the fire.

Listening closely, I let the trees whisper their knowledge. They told me a small cottage in the woods had been raided, and part of the forest was burning—but it would be fine. A rainstorm was on its way.

Curious, I asked how they knew about the storm.

We heard it through the grapevine, they replied.

I couldn't help but chuckle, and the trees joined in.

Gwen, noticing my laughter, raised an eyebrow. “Who are you even talking to, Leaf-head?”

“Oh, you know, the trees,” I said casually.

She rolled her eyes. “Oh, of course! I should’ve known!” Her sarcasm made me chuckle even more.

We walked on for a while until, in the distance, I spotted a black spire piercing the sky.

“Hey, Beans, look up,” I said, grinning as I placed a hand on his shoulder.

As he followed my gaze, his eyes widened. “I think that’s the kingdom!”

Excitement lit his face as he quickly rolled up the map and took off running. Gwen and I exchanged a smile before dashing after him.

“Race you!” Gwen grinned.

I laughed. “You’re on!”

We sprinted ahead, leaving Beans behind—but before he could protest about the unfair disadvantage of our height difference, Bluma swooped in, scooped him up, and carried him along.

Despite everything, we were smiling as we ran. Even though we knew what awaited us—the destruction, the devastation—we still allowed ourselves this fleeting moment of happiness. It meant something.

As the kingdom came into view, our pace slowed. The excitement in our chests faded into something heavier. We arrived at the stables' entrance at the back of the kingdom, catching our breath before stepping inside the city walls.

The devastation was immediate.

Small flames still smoldered in the ruins.

The grand, towering structures that once stood proud had crumbled into piles of rubble and ash. Charred buildings and shattered walls lined the streets, their remains scattered in jagged heaps. The air was thick with the acrid scent of smoke and burnt wood, and the ground beneath our feet was darkened with soot.

Everything had been reduced to little more than crumbling ruins and burnt-out shells. The once-bustling streets now stood empty and silent, the only sounds the whispering wind and the echoes of a life that no longer existed. The few surviving structures were barely standing, their walls scorched, their roofs melted by the intense heat of the fire. The grand gates that once guarded the kingdom had collapsed into twisted metal and molten stone.

As we moved deeper into the ruins, I could see the pain in Bluma’s and Beans’ faces. This was the place they had sworn to protect.

Beans let out a heavy sigh. “We should go. There’s nothing left for us here.”

He turned to Bluma, who nodded in agreement. Gwen and I shared a sorrowful glance before following them toward the kingdom’s front gates. We each took one last look back, paying silent respects to what had once been, before stepping away from the wreckage of the past.

As we walked, I hesitated before asking, “Are you two doing okay?”

To my surprise, Beans managed a small smile. “We’ll be fine. My parents are safe, the people are safe, and Bluma and I still have each other. We’ve faced worse.”

Bluma nodded. “Yes. We will be fine.”

I returned their smile, and Gwen offered her condolences.

As we continued, something caught my eye—a scorched trail stretching in the same direction we were heading. My stomach twisted.

Then, I saw it.

The flower field.

The vast meadow that lay between the kingdom and my home.

But instead of a sea of vibrant colors swaying in the wind, all I saw was devastation. A wave of shock, grief, and despair crashed over me.

Gwen must have noticed my sudden change in demeanor. “Bushy, what’s wrong—?”

Before she could finish, my body moved on its own. I shifted into my Celestial Elk form and bolted.

“Bushy!!”

Their shouts faded behind me, but I couldn’t stop. I wouldn’t stop.

The trees had told me about the raided cottage. The fire.

And now, I had to see it for myself.

After thirty minutes of running as fast as I could, the portal came into view. Gwen and the others' cries had long since faded, swallowed by the distance.

I lunged forward, shifting back into my natural form mid-air. "Exitum!" I roared. The portal flared to life, and before my feet touched the ground, I was already through—stepping straight into a nightmare.

The house was gone.

All that remained was a skeleton of blackened beams and collapsing rubble, flames still licking hungrily at the ruins. Ash choked the air, thick and acrid, burning my throat with every breath. My home—our home—was nothing but smoldering wreckage.

“Vomete!” I screamed, my voice splitting the night.

I tore through the burning wreckage, my stone skin blistering against the heat, the vines of my hair shriveling from the smoke. Embers rained down, searing my shoulders, but I didn’t stop. I couldn’t stop.

Then I saw it—a hand.

Pale stone, tangled in scorched vines, reaching from beneath a collapsed beam.

“Mom!”

I stumbled forward, my hands shaking as I grasped the burning wood and heaved. My muscles strained, my breath ragged, but I didn’t stop until the beam crashed aside.

She lay beneath it.

Her body—once strong, once full of life—was withered and broken. The vines of her hair were dry, brittle, their once-deep green reduced to crumbling black. And her chest—where her Soul Stone should have been—was empty.

“No, no, no…” I choked out, gathering her into my arms. Her stone skin was cooling, her weight unfamiliar without the steady hum of life beneath it. “Vomete, please, wake up.”

For a moment, there was nothing. Then her chest lifted, barely. A shallow, trembling breath.

“Deta…” Her voice was fragile, thinner than the wind. “You’re alive…”

“I’m here.” I brushed soot from her face, my tears streaking through the grime. “Don’t talk, save your strength—”

She weakly shook her head, a feeble hand rising to touch my cheek. “Listen to me.”

Outside, the sky finally opened, and rain poured through the shattered roof. The fire hissed in protest, steam curling through the air.

“You’ve made me proud,” she murmured. “But my time… is over.”

“No.” My grip tightened, desperate. “No, don’t say that.” I then took the soul stone around my neck and tried to put it inside her gap. Vomete grabbed my hands with her trembling ones.

A faint, broken smile. “Shh. Remember… Be kind. No matter the cost. It will light even the darkest paths.”

Her voice was fading.

“And… cherish your time. Follow your dreams… even when it hurts.”

“Vomete, please—” My voice shattered.

“You carry my love, always.” Her eyes softened, looking past me, past the ruin, toward something I couldn’t see. “Tachi’guf’s angel… they gave me you. And I thank them…”

The breath left her lips.

She stilled in my arms.

For a moment, there was nothing but the rain—dampening the last embers, washing away the soot. My chest caved in on itself, a soundless sob breaking from my throat. “No…” My voice barely made it past my lips. “Vomete!.. Mom… please…”

Footsteps. The portal shimmered behind me as Gwen and the others stepped through.

Their movements slowed as they took in the devastation. Gwen stopped first, her hand gripping the frame of the ruined doorway. Beans, for once, was silent. Bluma lingered behind them, unreadable.

“Was that… his mother?” Beans asked, voice hushed.

Gwen nodded but didn’t speak.

No one did.

I barely noticed their whispers. My world had shrunk to the weight in my arms, the cold settling into her skin.

“Go away,” I whispered. My voice cracked. “Please… just go.”

There was silence. Then—hesitant footsteps. Someone knelt beside me, only to withdraw just as quickly.

I didn’t look up, but when I finally did, Gwen was gone. In her place, beside me on the scorched floor, was a small plush. A simple, familiar creature from the underworld.

My fingers trembled as I reached for it, pressing the soft fabric to my chest. Pressing it against Vomete’s lifeless form.

The weight of everything crushed me. The memories clawed at my mind—her voice, her warmth, the way she used to hum as she combed through my vines. She had always been there. When I scraped my knees. When the nights were too dark. When I needed her most.

And now she was gone.

Her last words echoed in my mind, but they meant nothing. Not yet. The why didn’t matter. The loss was unbearable.

Whoever did this… they would pay.

But not now. Not yet.

My body finally gave in. I collapsed, lost in grief, and the world faded away.

I woke to pale morning light seeping through a smoke-stained window. Outside, the little stream trickled softly, the birds already singing. The storm had passed.

As if the world hadn’t just ended.

The air smelled of damp ash and charred wood. My vines had curled, dried at the edges, as if mourning with me. A faint breeze stirred them, carrying the last ghost of warmth from the fire.

For a moment, I just sat there, staring at nothing.

Then the memories came crashing down.

My chest ached. My fingers curled around the plush in my palm.

Whoever did this… I would find them.

But not yet.

My legs wouldn’t move. My heart was too heavy.

For now, all I could do was sit there, alone, as the echoes of her voice faded into the morning.

To Be Continued…

About the author

Caleb Jones began the creation of the world of Entine in 2016 and has been writing since 2021. Since then, he has continued to grow the world in various ways. He loves fantasy, camping, animals, and drawing. This is his debut novel, and he plans on writing more mystical Entine books.
